For those who avoid desire as if it were a pit of fire,
Who abandon craving for children and wives,
And, frightened and terrified, leave their homes. {6}
{{milestone:{label:5.24,id:UT22084-055-001-622}}}“ ‘There have been no buddhas in the past,
Nor will there be any in the future or now in the present,
Who attain the highest, most supreme enlightenment
While living inside their homes. {7}
{{milestone:{label:5.25,id:UT22084-055-001-623}}}“ ‘Casting away a kingdom like a lump of phlegm,
Longing for solitude and living in the forests,
Eliminating the kleśas and defeating the māras,
They will realize stainless, noncomposite enlightenment. {8}
{{milestone:{label:5.26,id:UT22084-055-001-624}}}“ ‘People who, with a disenchanted mind,
Leave their homes, they are superior
To those who serve, for many millions of eons,
Heroic buddhas as numerous as the Ganges sands. {9}
{{milestone:{label:5.27,id:UT22084-055-001-625}}}“ ‘People who leave their homes and practice the Dharma,
Without serving the supreme humans, the jinas,
With food, drink, and Dharma robes,
With flowers, incense, and ointments— {10}
{{milestone:{label:5.28,id:UT22084-055-001-626}}}“ ‘Those who, longing for enlightenment,
Disillusioned with the composite, and for the benefit of beings, 
Take seven steps in the direction of the forests—
They will have the superior merit.’ {11}
{{milestone:{label:5.29,id:UT22084-055-001-627}}}“Young man, King Mahābala heard what the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta said about leaving one’s home. Having heard this, he thought, ‘I have understood the Bhagavān’s teaching to mean that he does not praise the perfection of generosity, {{page:{number:31,id:UT22084-055-001-5864,folio:F.16.b}}} but gives the highest, ultimate praise to the perfection of conduct.{{note:{index293,id:UT22084-055-001-628}}} The Bhagavān has praised perfect purity, perfect celibacy, and perfect nirvāṇa.’
{{milestone:{label:5.30,id:UT22084-055-001-629}}}“He thought, ‘It is not easy to practice the unsurpassable Dharma and attain its goal while living in a home. I would decline in my practice of the unsurpassable Dharma. I shall cut off my hair and beard, wear the orange robes, and leave home for homelessness.’
{{milestone:{label:5.31,id:UT22084-055-001-630}}}“Then, young man, King Mahābala, accompanied by eighty thousand{{note:{index294,id:UT22084-055-001-631}}} brahmins and laypeople, came before the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, bowed down to his feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, and sat to one side.
{{milestone:{label:5.32,id:UT22084-055-001-632}}}“Young man, the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha, knowing the higher motivation of King Mahābala, taught this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. 
{{milestone:{label:5.33,id:UT22084-055-001-633}}}“Young man, on hearing this, King Mahābala was pleased, delighted, joyful, inspired, and happy. He shaved off his hair and beard, put on the orange robes, and with faith left home for homelessness. Having entered homelessness he learned this samādhi, and having learned it he understood it. He dedicated himself to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it. Through that root of merit, he did not fall into the lower existences for a hundred million eons. He served two hundred million buddhas and heard this samādhi from all those tathāgatas. He learned this samādhi, and having learned it he understood it. {{page:{number:32,id:UT22084-055-001-5865,folio:F.17.a}}} He dedicated himself to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it.
{{milestone:{label:5.34,id:UT22084-055-001-634}}}“Subsequently, through those roots of merit, after a hundred million eons had passed, and then another hundred thousand eons, he attained the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. He became the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha named Jñānaśūra.{{note:{index295,id:UT22084-055-001-635}}} He benefited countless beings, and afterward he passed away into perfect nirvāṇa.
{{milestone:{label:5.35,id:UT22084-055-001-636}}}“Young man, the eighty thousand people who with King Mahābala came into the presence of the Bhagavān, the Tathāgata Ghoṣadatta all heard this samādhi also and were delighted, rejoicing, and joyful. Happy and joyful, they cut off their hair and beards, wore the orange robes, and with genuine faith they left home for homelessness. Having entered homelessness they learned this samādhi, and having learned it they understood it. They dedicated themselves to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it. Through that root of merit, they did not fall into the lower existences for a hundred million eons. During all those eons, they served ten million buddhas and heard this samādhi from all those tathāgatas. They maintained this samādhi and comprehended it. They dedicated themselves to the practice of keeping it, reading it, and meditating on it. 
{{milestone:{label:5.36,id:UT22084-055-001-637}}}“Through their previous roots of merit, after two hundred million eons had passed and a further hundred thousand eons, they attained the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. They all became bhagavāns, tathāgatas, arhats, perfectly enlightened buddhas named Dṛḍhaśūra. They benefited countless beings, and afterward they passed away into perfect nirvāṇa. {{page:{number:33,id:UT22084-055-001-5866,folio:F.17.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:5.37,id:UT22084-055-001-638}}}“Therefore, young man, because of this teaching, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas cherish in this way this samādhi. They know that it is composed of the unsurpassable wisdom of omniscience.”
{{milestone:{label:5.38,id:UT22084-055-001-639}}}Then, at that time, the Bhagavān gave a detailed teaching by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha.
{{milestone:{label:5.39,id:UT22084-055-001-640}}}“I remember, countless eons ago
In the past, a supreme human, a great sage
Who benefited beings appeared in the world, 
And he was known by the name Ghoṣadatta. {12}
{{milestone:{label:5.40,id:UT22084-055-001-641}}}“The first assembly of his students
Numbered eight hundred million.{{note:{index296,id:UT22084-055-001-642}}}
The second was seven hundred million.
The third was six hundred million arhats. {13}
{{milestone:{label:5.41,id:UT22084-055-001-643}}}“All had eliminated defilements and were without kleśas.
All had attained the perfection of miraculous powers.
The lifespan was forty thousand years
And the realm was perfectly pure and beautiful. {14}
{{milestone:{label:5.42,id:UT22084-055-001-644}}}“The bodhisattvas of that protector
Were consecrated to immeasurably benefit others.
They were well established through their powers and levels.
They were near to buddhahood beneath the sacred tree.{{note:{index297,id:UT22084-055-001-645}}} {15} 
{{milestone:{label:5.43,id:UT22084-055-001-646}}}“In this Jambudvīpa there were kings
Named Dṛḍhabala and Mahābala.
One king ruled half the world,
The other was king over the other half. {16}
{{milestone:{label:5.44,id:UT22084-055-001-647}}}“The Buddha, to whom humans and devas made offerings,
Had appeared within the domain of King Mahābala.
The king gained faith in the Sugata
And attended him for a thousand years. {17}
{{milestone:{label:5.45,id:UT22084-055-001-648}}}“Many other beings, following his example,
Also honored the Tathāgata
With worldly goods and not through the Dharma.{{note:{index298,id:UT22084-055-001-649}}}
They gave many things to the śrāvakas also. {18}
{{milestone:{label:5.46,id:UT22084-055-001-650}}}“The highest of beings had this thought:
‘I shall teach the Dharma to these who desire the Dharma
So that they will all give up desire
And enter into homelessness in my teaching.’ {19}
{{milestone:{label:5.47,id:UT22084-055-001-651}}}“The highest of humans taught in verses
The practice of following the Dharma of the sugatas, {{page:{number:34,id:UT22084-055-001-5867,folio:F.18.a}}}
The endless suffering and harm of living in a home,
And that practicing the Dharma is offering to the Dharma. {20}
{{milestone:{label:5.48,id:UT22084-055-001-652}}}“When the king, the sovereign, had heard those verses,
That ruler of men contemplated entering solitude.
He thought that all who dwell at home 
Are unable to make the supreme offering to the Dharma. {21}
{{milestone:{label:5.49,id:UT22084-055-001-653}}}“He cast away the kingdom like a lump of phlegm
And together with eighty thousand persons
He came into the presence of the Jina,
Bowed to his feet, and sat before him. {22}
{{milestone:{label:5.50,id:UT22084-055-001-654}}}“The Jina, knowing what they intended,
Taught this samādhi of peace that is difficult to see.
Happy, inspired, and joyful, they were satisfied.
Pleased and delighted, they entered homelessness. {23}
{{milestone:{label:5.51,id:UT22084-055-001-655}}}“Homeless, they possessed this samādhi.
They kept it, read it, and understood it.
For two hundred million eons
They did not fall into the lower existences. {24}
{{milestone:{label:5.52,id:UT22084-055-001-656}}}“Because of those roots of merit,{{note:{index299,id:UT22084-055-001-657}}}
They all saw ten thousand million buddhas
And in the teaching of those jinas
They entered homelessness and meditated on this samādhi. {25}
{{milestone:{label:5.53,id:UT22084-055-001-658}}}“In later times they became buddhas
With infinite diligence, all named Dṛḍhaśūra.
They benefited many millions of beings
And after, like an extinguished flame, attained nirvāṇa. {26}
{{milestone:{label:5.54,id:UT22084-055-001-659}}}“The one who previously had been King Mahābala
Appeared in the world as Buddha Jñānaśūra.
He brought many billions of beings 
To enlightenment, and then attained nirvāṇa. {27}
{{milestone:{label:5.55,id:UT22084-055-001-660}}}“Therefore you who, in later times, hear and possess 
This sūtra that has been taught by the buddhas:
If you possess this treasure of the Dharma
You will quickly become a supreme human.” {28}
{{milestone:{label:5.56,id:UT22084-055-001-661}}}Conclusion of the fifth chapter, “Ghoṣadatta.” 
{{milestone:{label:6,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-6}}}Cultivating the Samādhi
Chapter 6
{{milestone:{label:6.1,id:UT22084-055-001-662}}}The Bhagavān now said to the youth Candraprabha,{{note:{index300,id:UT22084-055-001-663}}} “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should cultivate this samādhi. 
{{milestone:{label:6.2,id:UT22084-055-001-664}}}“Young man, what is the cultivation of this samādhi? {{page:{number:35,id:UT22084-055-001-5868,folio:F.18.b}}} Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas with a compassionate mind are dedicated to making offerings to the tathāgatas, whether living or passed into nirvāṇa, of Dharma robes, alms, seat and bedding, medicines for when ill, and of monastic utensils, and of flowers, incense, perfume, garlands, ointments, aromatic powders, clothing, parasols, banners, and flags, and of music and musical instruments. They dedicate that root of merit to the attainment of samādhi. They do not make offerings to a tathāgata with the hope for anything at all—not with the hope for anything they desire, nor with the hope for any enjoyment, nor with the hope for a higher existence, nor with the hope for followers—but do so with the Dharma in mind. They do not even, with that wish, perceive the Tathāgata as the dharmakāya, let alone perceiving him as the rūpakāya. 
{{milestone:{label:6.3,id:UT22084-055-001-665}}}“Young man, it is in that way that an offering is made to the tathāgatas. It is done without seeing the tathāgatas, without focusing on the self, and without any desire for the ripening of karma. Young man, if an offering made to a tathāgata is purified of those three aspects of the action, this samādhi will be attained and the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood will be quickly reached.”
{{milestone:{label:6.4,id:UT22084-055-001-666}}}At this point the Bhagavān gave a detailed teaching on the cultivation of the samādhi by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha. 
{{milestone:{label:6.5,id:UT22084-055-001-667}}}“Through offering incense to infinite wisdom
Beings will have an infinite aroma.
In ten million eons they will not go to the lower realms,
And no bad smells will come from them. {1}
{{milestone:{label:6.6,id:UT22084-055-001-668}}}“For ten million eons they will practice bodhisattva conduct 
And make offerings to ten thousand million buddhas.
The aroma of wisdom will arise so that they
Will become buddhas with the aroma of supreme conduct. {2}
{{milestone:{label:6.7,id:UT22084-055-001-669}}}“If any beings know that the incense they offer,
Those to whom they offer it, 
And the minds that offer incense {{page:{number:36,id:UT22084-055-001-5869,folio:F.19.a}}} do not exist,
The ‘concordant patience’ they have is of lesser kind. {3}
{{milestone:{label:6.8,id:UT22084-055-001-670}}}“But if a person maintains a patience that is great,{{note:{index301,id:UT22084-055-001-671}}}
Even were they cut up, for ten million eons, 
Into tiny pieces as numerous as the Ganges sands, 
Their mind will never regress. {4}
{{milestone:{label:6.9,id:UT22084-055-001-672}}}“Why is this termed ‘patience’?
And why is it called ‘concordant’? 
For what reason is it said to be ‘nonregressive’?
And why are they called ‘bodhisattvas’? {5}
{{milestone:{label:6.10,id:UT22084-055-001-673}}}“Their patience being for the selfless nature of phenomena,
Those who perceive selflessness have no kleśas.
They know that all phenomena are like space.
That, therefore, is what is termed ‘patience.’ {6}
{{milestone:{label:6.11,id:UT22084-055-001-674}}}“They train in accord with all the jinas.
Those wise ones do not practice non-Dharma.
They do not doubt the Buddha’s Dharma.
That is the patience that is ‘concordant.’ {7}
{{milestone:{label:6.12,id:UT22084-055-001-675}}}“Even if all the māras in the world transformed
Into buddhas and said to such practitioners,
‘Enlightenment is too difficult! So become a śrāvaka!’
They would not believe those words and would not regress. {8}
{{milestone:{label:6.13,id:UT22084-055-001-676}}}“If they know of the incorrect view of beings
They say, ‘This is not the path to deathlessness!’{{note:{index302,id:UT22084-055-001-677}}}
So that they reject the wrong path and are brought to the true path.{{note:{index303,id:UT22084-055-001-678}}}
That is the reason why they are called bodhisattvas.{{note:{index304,id:UT22084-055-001-679}}} {9} 
{{milestone:{label:6.14,id:UT22084-055-001-680}}}“They remain upon the path of concordant patience
And are awake through the knowledge of selflessness.
Even in a dream they do not believe 
In humans, persons, souls, or beings. {10}
{{milestone:{label:6.15,id:UT22084-055-001-681}}}“Even if as many millions of māras as there are Ganges sands
Came before them in the forms of buddhas,
And said to them that there is a soul within the body,
They would reply that it was not so and say, ‘You are not buddhas.’{{note:{index305,id:UT22084-055-001-682}}} {11} 
{{milestone:{label:6.16,id:UT22084-055-001-683}}}“Through wisdom I know that the skandhas are empty.
Because I know that, I am unaccompanied by kleśas.
In my conduct I use mere words
But within this world remain within nirvāṇa, {12}
{{milestone:{label:6.17,id:UT22084-055-001-684}}}“Just as when a man has a son born to him
And gives him a name, saying, ‘This is his name!’
But that name cannot be found anywhere.
And that name did not come from anywhere. {13}
{{milestone:{label:6.18,id:UT22084-055-001-685}}}“In that way the name ‘bodhisattva’ is given, {{page:{number:37,id:UT22084-055-001-5870,folio:F.19.b}}}
But if one seeks for this ‘bodhisattva’
That name will not be found anywhere.
One who knows that is a bodhisattva. {14}
{{milestone:{label:6.19,id:UT22084-055-001-686}}}“The bodhisattvas do not believe in the existence of a self
Any more than that a fire can burn in the middle of the ocean.
Since they have developed the aspiration for enlightenment
They have not had the view that there is a soul within.{{note:{index306,id:UT22084-055-001-687}}} {15} 
{{milestone:{label:6.20,id:UT22084-055-001-688}}}“There is no birth and there is no death
For beings, humans,{{note:{index307,id:UT22084-055-001-689}}} the descendants of Manu.
Phenomena have an empty nature, like illusions;
The tīrthikas are unable to know that. {16}
{{milestone:{label:6.21,id:UT22084-055-001-690}}}“Also those who crave for food,
Who desire and cling to alms bowls and robes,
Who are arrogant and are haughty,
They cannot understand the Buddha’s enlightenment. {17}
{{milestone:{label:6.22,id:UT22084-055-001-691}}}“The lazy who are overcome by sleepiness and dullness, 
Who have stubborn minds,{{note:{index308,id:UT22084-055-001-692}}} and are shameless,
Who have no faith in the Buddha,
They are unable to understand{{note:{index309,id:UT22084-055-001-693}}} sublime enlightenment. {18}
{{milestone:{label:6.23,id:UT22084-055-001-694}}}“The ordinary beings with incorrect behavior,
Those who do not have faith in the Dharma,
Who have no respect toward celibates,
They are unable to understand enlightenment. {19}
{{milestone:{label:6.24,id:UT22084-055-001-695}}}“Those with correct behavior, who have modesty and self-respect,
Who delight in the Dharma and the buddhas,
Who show great respect to the practitioners of celibacy,
They will attain the supreme, highest enlightenment. {20}
{{milestone:{label:6.25,id:UT22084-055-001-696}}}“Those whose conduct is performed with mindfulness,
Who sit upon their cushion with joy and delight,
With dhyāna as food and samādhi for drink,
They will attain the supreme, highest enlightenment. {21}
{{milestone:{label:6.26,id:UT22084-055-001-697}}}“Those who understand selflessness all day long,
Who are mindful of emptiness as they walk,
Who bear the beautiful aromatic flowers of the aspects of enlightenment,
Those dedicated ones will attain supreme enlightenment. {22}
{{milestone:{label:6.27,id:UT22084-055-001-698}}}“They who are skilled in bodhisattva conduct
Are not on the level of other beings,
Of śrāvakas, or of pratyekabuddhas.
Who would not aspire to that realization? {23}
{{milestone:{label:6.28,id:UT22084-055-001-699}}}“If I were to have a lifespan that continued
For as many millions of eons as there are sands in the Ganges,
I would not even be able to finish reciting the praises
Of as little of the Buddha’s wisdom as a tiny pore. {24}
{{milestone:{label:6.29,id:UT22084-055-001-700}}}“Therefore, having heard the benefits {{page:{number:38,id:UT22084-055-001-5871,folio:F.20.a}}}
That have been taught by the unsurpassable Jina,
You should quickly become instructed in this samādhi.
And then the attainment of supreme enlightenment will not be difficult.” {25}
{{milestone:{label:6.30,id:UT22084-055-001-701}}}Conclusion of the sixth chapter, “Cultivation of the Samādhi.”
{{milestone:{label:7,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-7}}}The Attainment of Patience
Chapter 7
{{milestone:{label:7.1,id:UT22084-055-001-702}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should become skilled in the wisdoms of the three kinds of patience. They should know the first patience. They should know the second patience. They should know the third patience. They should become skilled in the differences between the three kinds of patience and skilled in the differences between the wisdoms of the three kinds of patience. 
{{milestone:{label:7.2,id:UT22084-055-001-703}}}“Why is that? Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas become skilled in the differences between the three kinds of patience and become skilled in the differences between the wisdoms of the three kinds of patience, then at that time, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas will quickly attain this samādhi, and will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.
{{milestone:{label:7.3,id:UT22084-055-001-704}}}“Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood should learn this Dharma teaching on gaining the three kinds of patience. When they have learned it they should teach it widely to others. That will be of benefit to many beings, it will bring happiness to many beings, it will be a kindness to the world, it will bring fulfillment to a multitude of beings, and bring benefit and happiness to humans and devas.”{{note:{index310,id:UT22084-055-001-705}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.4,id:UT22084-055-001-706}}}Then the Bhagavān taught this Dharma discourse on gaining the three kinds of patience by chanting the following verses to the youth Candraprabha.
{{milestone:{label:7.5,id:UT22084-055-001-707}}}“Those who do not argue
Or speak unbeneficial words 
But always bring benefit and maintain the Dharma,
Such people are explained as having the first patience. {1} {{page:{number:39,id:UT22084-055-001-5872,folio:F.20.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.6,id:UT22084-055-001-708}}}“Knowing that all phenomena are like illusions,
Not having a conceptual field of experience,
And not falling from the level of increasing wisdom
Are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {2}
{{milestone:{label:7.7,id:UT22084-055-001-709}}}“Being skilled in all the paths of the sūtras,
Being wise and attracted to the Buddha’s words,
And having the infinite awareness of the sugatas’ wisdom 
Are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {3}
{{milestone:{label:7.8,id:UT22084-055-001-710}}}“Whatever Dharma taught by the Buddha they hear,
They have no doubt about the Buddha’s teachings
But aspire to the Dharma of all the jinas.
These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {4}
{{milestone:{label:7.9,id:UT22084-055-001-711}}}“They know the particular sūtra with the definitive meaning,
Such as the Sugata’s teaching on emptiness.
They know that all the Dharmas that teach 
Of beings, individuals, and persons are provisional truth. {5}
{{milestone:{label:7.10,id:UT22084-055-001-712}}}“In this world there are many tīrthikas,
But they feel no anger toward them.
They are firmly established in compassion for them.
These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {6}
{{milestone:{label:7.11,id:UT22084-055-001-713}}}“The retentions{{note:{index311,id:UT22084-055-001-714}}} become apparent to them
And they have no doubts concerning their appearance.
What they speak is in accord with the truth.
These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {7}
{{milestone:{label:7.12,id:UT22084-055-001-715}}}“The four elements of air and water,
Fire and earth may change into something else,
But they will never turn away from the enlightenment of buddhahood.
These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {8}
{{milestone:{label:7.13,id:UT22084-055-001-716}}}“Whatever skills there are in the world,
The bodhisattvas learn them all,
And no one sees anyone higher than them.
These are distinctive qualities of the first patience. {9}
{{milestone:{label:7.14,id:UT22084-055-001-717}}}“They are unwavering through the power of śamatha,
And through vipaśyanā they are like a mountain. 
Even all beings together would be unable to disturb them.
These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {10}
{{milestone:{label:7.15,id:UT22084-055-001-718}}}“In meditation they stand and talk;
Remaining in meditation they walk.
In meditation they master the perfections.
These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {11}
{{milestone:{label:7.16,id:UT22084-055-001-719}}}“In meditation they attain the five higher knowledges.
Teaching the Dharma they go to a hundred realms.
They do not lose their miraculous powers. {{page:{number:40,id:UT22084-055-001-5873,folio:F.21.a}}}
These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {12}
{{milestone:{label:7.17,id:UT22084-055-001-720}}}“They remain in that kind of samādhi of peace.
They attain certainty of the mind,
And in their meditation there is no ‘being.’
These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {13}
{{milestone:{label:7.18,id:UT22084-055-001-721}}}“With buddha wisdom they teach the Dharma
To all of the beings who are in the world,
And they are able to remember all that they have taught.
These are distinctive qualities of the second patience. {14}
{{milestone:{label:7.19,id:UT22084-055-001-722}}}“They see the lords of the worlds in all directions:
East, south, west, and north,
Above, below, and in the intermediate directions.
These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {15}
{{milestone:{label:7.20,id:UT22084-055-001-723}}}“They have a body that is the color of gold
And emanate countless manifestations,
Teaching the Dharma to many millions of beings.
These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {16}
{{milestone:{label:7.21,id:UT22084-055-001-724}}}“Each such bodhisattva appears throughout 
This buddha realm of Jambudvīpa
And is renowned also among the devas and asuras.
These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {17}
{{milestone:{label:7.22,id:UT22084-055-001-725}}}“The bodhisattvas train in accordance 
With the field of activity of the buddhas
And the conduct of the sugatas.
These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {18}
{{milestone:{label:7.23,id:UT22084-055-001-726}}}“If the beings that are in this world 
Were to recite the praises of the bodhisattvas
And they were to take great joy in that
Then they would not be trained in the Buddha’s wisdom. {19}
{{milestone:{label:7.24,id:UT22084-055-001-727}}}“If all the beings that are in this world
Were to speak badly to the bodhisattvas,
And if they were to become angry toward them,
Then they would still not be trained in the Buddha’s wisdom. {20}
{{milestone:{label:7.25,id:UT22084-055-001-728}}}“If they gain wealth it does not make them happy;
If they do not gain wealth it does not make them unhappy.
Their minds always remain like a mountain.
These are distinctive qualities of the third patience. {21}
{{milestone:{label:7.26,id:UT22084-055-001-729}}}“These three patiences are taught to be the patience regarding what is spoken,
The patience that is beneficial for contemplation and meditation,
And the patience, from listening to the Dharma, regarding birthlessness.
These trainings are the path to enlightenment.{{note:{index312,id:UT22084-055-001-730}}} {22} 
{{milestone:{label:7.27,id:UT22084-055-001-731}}}“When the bodhisattvas attain
These three unsurpassable patiences,
They see the supreme humans, the sugatas,{{note:{index313,id:UT22084-055-001-732}}}
And they give them the prophecy of their stainless enlightenment. {23} {{page:{number:41,id:UT22084-055-001-5874,folio:F.21.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.28,id:UT22084-055-001-733}}}“When they have received that prophecy
The earth shakes in six ways,
The realm is illuminated by light,
And millions of devas send down a rain of flowers. {24}
{{milestone:{label:7.29,id:UT22084-055-001-734}}}“When they have received that prophecy
Countless quintillions of beings
Develop the aspiration to enlightenment,
Thinking, ‘We also shall become jinas, worthy of offerings.’{{note:{index314,id:UT22084-055-001-735}}} {25} 
{{milestone:{label:7.30,id:UT22084-055-001-736}}}“When the bodhisattvas attain
These three unsurpassable patiences
They are not born, they do not die,
They do not pass away, and are not reborn. {26}
{{milestone:{label:7.31,id:UT22084-055-001-737}}}“When the bodhisattvas attain
These three unsurpassable patiences
They do not see beings born or dying,
But see all phenomena as remaining in the true nature. {27}
{{milestone:{label:7.32,id:UT22084-055-001-738}}}“In this way they know that they are untrue,
That phenomena are like illusions, that they are naturally empty. 
Emptiness is not born and does not die.{{note:{index315,id:UT22084-055-001-739}}}
All these phenomena are by nature empty. {28}
{{milestone:{label:7.33,id:UT22084-055-001-740}}}“Whenever someone shows them respect, 
Attending to them, honoring them, and making offerings,
They take no pleasure in it,
For they know that phenomena have an empty nature. {29}
{{milestone:{label:7.34,id:UT22084-055-001-741}}}“Toward beings who revile, threaten, or beat them,
They feel no anger, nor pride.
They only feel constant love for them,
Wishing for those beings to be liberated. {30}
{{milestone:{label:7.35,id:UT22084-055-001-742}}}“Even when beaten and cut with sticks and stones,
Those wise ones will feel no anger,
Remaining in the patience of selflessness,
And not having unyielding anger or pride. {31}
{{milestone:{label:7.36,id:UT22084-055-001-743}}}“In this way they know the lack of reality,
That phenomena are like illusions, with an empty nature.
They remain in that knowledge of phenomena
And are venerated by this world and its devas. {32}
{{milestone:{label:7.37,id:UT22084-055-001-744}}}“Even toward beings holding weapons
Who cut into pieces their body and limbs,
They would have no anger,
And their love and compassion would not diminish. {33}
{{milestone:{label:7.38,id:UT22084-055-001-745}}}“Toward such beings, while they are cutting up their body and limbs,
This is what arises in their mind:
‘Until I can bring these beings to enlightenment
I will not pass into the peace of nirvāṇa.’ {34} {{page:{number:42,id:UT22084-055-001-5875,folio:F.22.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:7.39,id:UT22084-055-001-746}}}“The bodhisattvas of great renown
Continuously meditate throughout millions of eons 
With that kind of unsurpassable power of patience,
Resting in the equanimity of the patience of selflessness. {35}
{{milestone:{label:7.40,id:UT22084-055-001-747}}}“For even more eons, as many as Ganges sand grains,
They do not accomplish benefit through the knowledge of a buddha. 
They do not reach enlightenment,
Let alone the wisdom of the tathāgatas. {36}
{{milestone:{label:7.41,id:UT22084-055-001-748}}}“Even if one were to speak for countless hundreds of eons,
It would be difficult to conclude the praises,
The endless descriptions, of the greatly renowned ones 
Who are established in the patience of selflessness. {37}
{{milestone:{label:7.42,id:UT22084-055-001-749}}}“Therefore, the one who desires supreme, unsurpassable enlightenment,
The accumulated wisdom of buddhahood,
Should meditate on the patience praised by the jinas,
And then supreme enlightenment will not be difficult to attain.” {38}
{{milestone:{label:7.43,id:UT22084-055-001-750}}}Conclusion of seventh chapter, “The Attainment of Patience.”
{{milestone:{label:8,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-8}}}Buddha Abhāva­samudgata
Chapter 8
{{milestone:{label:8.1,id:UT22084-055-001-751}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should become skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena.
{{milestone:{label:8.2,id:UT22084-055-001-752}}}“Young man, what is being skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena? Bodhisattva mahāsattvas know that all phenomena have no existence, have no essence, have no attributes, have no characteristics, have no origin, have no cessation, have no words, are empty, are primordial peace, and are pure by nature. 
{{milestone:{label:8.3,id:UT22084-055-001-753}}}“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas {{page:{number:43,id:UT22084-055-001-5876,folio:F.22.b}}} know that all phenomena have no existence, have no essence, have no attributes, have no characteristics, have no birth, have no cessation, have no words, are empty, are primordial peace, and are pure by nature, then at that time, young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas have become skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena. 
{{milestone:{label:8.4,id:UT22084-055-001-754}}}“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have become skilled in the wisdom of the nonexistent nature of all phenomena do not have desire for any form, sound, smell, taste, or touch. They do not become angry. They are never ignorant. 
{{milestone:{label:8.5,id:UT22084-055-001-755}}}“Why is that? It is because they do not see phenomena; there is no object to perceive. They do not see the phenomena of desire, the desire, or the desirer; that which angers, the anger, or one who is angry; nor that of which one is ignorant, the ignorance, or the one who is ignorant, and therefore there is no such object to perceive.
{{milestone:{label:8.6,id:UT22084-055-001-756}}}“Because there is nothing to be seen and there is no object to perceive, they have no attachment to anything in the three realms and they will quickly attain this samādhi, and quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.
“On this topic, it has been said:
{{milestone:{label:8.7,id:UT22084-055-001-758}}}“All phenomena have no existence;
They are all devoid of attributes and without characteristics,
Without birth and without cessation.
That is how you should{{note:{index316,id:UT22084-055-001-759}}} perfectly understand phenomena.
{{milestone:{label:8.8,id:UT22084-055-001-760}}}“Everything is without existence, without words,
Empty, peaceful, and primordially stainless.
The one who knows phenomena,
Young man, that one is called a buddha.
{{milestone:{label:8.9,id:UT22084-055-001-761}}}“Therefore, the revealed nature of equality
Is that all phenomena in essence have no nature.
Whoever desires the mother of the sugatas
Will attain this mother of the jinas.
{{milestone:{label:8.10,id:UT22084-055-001-762}}}“Therefore, young man, that is what you should understand through this Dharma teaching.{{note:{index317,id:UT22084-055-001-763}}}
{{milestone:{label:8.11,id:UT22084-055-001-764}}}“Young man, in the past, countless, vast, immeasurable, inconceivable, unfathomable, asaṃkhyeya eons ago, at that time, in that time, there appeared in the world the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata, who was perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata, {{page:{number:44,id:UT22084-055-001-5877,folio:F.23.a}}} a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, a buddha, and a bhagavān.
{{milestone:{label:8.12,id:UT22084-055-001-765}}}“Young man, what do you think? Why was that tathāgata named Abhāva­samudgata?{{note:{index318,id:UT22084-055-001-766}}}
“Young man, as soon as he was born he rose in the air up to the height of seven palm trees, took seven steps, and said these words: ‘All phenomena have arisen from nonexistence. From nonexistence have all phenomena arisen.’
{{milestone:{label:8.13,id:UT22084-055-001-768}}}“Young man, the sound of those words was heard in all the worlds in the trichiliocosm. It resounded and was heard by everyone from the devas on the earth up to those in Brahmā’s paradise. ‘Oh, as soon as this tathāgata was born, he rose in the air up to the height of seven palm trees, took seven steps and said the word nonexistence. Therefore he will be Abhāva­samudgata (Arisen from Nonexistence).’ Thus it was that the name Abhāva­samudgata arose, and that he was given the name Abhāva­samudgata.
{{milestone:{label:8.14,id:UT22084-055-001-769}}}“When that bhagavān attained enlightenment, the words ‘arisen from nonexistence’ sounded from the leaves of all the trees, from all the grass,{{note:{index319,id:UT22084-055-001-770}}} bushes, and forests,{{note:{index320,id:UT22084-055-001-771}}} and from the summits of all the mountains.
“Every sound in that world was heard as the words ‘arisen from nonexistence.’
{{milestone:{label:8.15,id:UT22084-055-001-773}}}“Young man, at the time, attending the teachings of the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata, there was a young prince by the name of Mahā­karuṇā­cintin, who had an excellent body and was handsome and good-looking.
{{milestone:{label:8.16,id:UT22084-055-001-774}}}“Young man, the prince went to the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata and bowed his head to the Bhagavān’s feet. He circumambulated the Bhagavān three times and then sat down. {{page:{number:45,id:UT22084-055-001-5878,folio:F.23.b}}} Then the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Abhāva­samudgata, knowing the higher motivation of Prince Mahā­karuṇā­cintin, taught him this samādhi. When he had heard this he had complete faith in it. With complete faith he shaved off his hair and beard, put on the orange robes, and with such faith left home for homelessness. Having entered homelessness he learned this samādhi. He learned it, kept it, read it, understood it, and dedicated himself to the practice of meditation on it. Through that root of merit, he did not fall into the lower existences for two hundred million eons. He served two hundred million buddhas, and he heard this samādhi from all those tathāgatas. Having heard it, he learned it and understood it. He kept it, read it, propagated it, and repeatedly meditated on it with unadulterated meditation, remaining dedicated to that practice of meditation.
{{milestone:{label:8.17,id:UT22084-055-001-775}}}“Through those roots of merit, after twenty eons had passed he appeared in the world as the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Suvicintitārtha. He ripened countless beings and benefited countless beings, and afterward, like an extinguished flame, he passed away into perfect nirvāṇa.
{{milestone:{label:8.18,id:UT22084-055-001-776}}}“Therefore, young man, this samādhi of that Dharma teaching should be cherished by bodhisattva mahāsattvas. It should be known to cause the unsurpassable perfect wisdom of buddhahood.”
{{milestone:{label:8.19,id:UT22084-055-001-777}}}Then at that time the Bhagavān gave a detailed teaching on the preceding chapter by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha:
{{milestone:{label:8.20,id:UT22084-055-001-778}}}“I remember that countless eons ago
In the past, there appeared a supreme human,
One who benefited the world, a great rishi,
And his name was Abhāva­samudgata. {1}
{{milestone:{label:8.21,id:UT22084-055-001-779}}}“As soon as he was born he rose into the air {{page:{number:46,id:UT22084-055-001-5879,folio:F.24.a}}}
And taught the nonexistence of all phenomena.
He was at that time given a corresponding name
And his words were heard throughout the trichiliocosm. {2}
{{milestone:{label:8.22,id:UT22084-055-001-780}}}“All the devas, they all called out,
‘He will be a jina named Abhāva!
As soon as he was born he took seven steps
And the Jina taught the nonexistence of phenomena.’ {3}
{{milestone:{label:8.23,id:UT22084-055-001-781}}}“When the sage became a buddha, a Dharma king,
Who taught the nature of all phenomena,
From plants, trees, bushes, mountains,{{note:{index321,id:UT22084-055-001-782}}} and rocks
There came the words ‘phenomena have no existence.’ {4}
{{milestone:{label:8.24,id:UT22084-055-001-783}}}“All the sounds there were in the world
Became the words ‘all are nonexistent.’
In that way there sounded
The words of the Guide of the World. {5}
{{milestone:{label:8.25,id:UT22084-055-001-784}}}“At that time there was a prince
Whose name had always been Karuṇāvicintin.
He had an excellent form and was handsome.
He came into the presence of that jina. {6}
{{milestone:{label:8.26,id:UT22084-055-001-785}}}“He bowed to the feet of the sage, that great being,
And respectfully circumambulated him.
In order to hear the stainless, unsurpassable Dharma
He sat there with a devout mind. {7}
{{milestone:{label:8.27,id:UT22084-055-001-786}}}“The heroic{{note:{index322,id:UT22084-055-001-787}}} Jina, knowing his aspiration,
Gave the teaching of this samādhi.
Having listened to this stainless samādhi
He quickly entered homelessness in the supreme Jina’s teaching. {8}
{{milestone:{label:8.28,id:UT22084-055-001-788}}}“Having entered homelessness he possessed, 
Read, and understood this samādhi.
For a full two hundred million eons
He did not descend to an unfortunate existence. {9}
{{milestone:{label:8.29,id:UT22084-055-001-789}}}“Through the good karma that he had made
He pleased two hundred million buddhas,
And in the presence of those jinas
He cultivated this samādhi. {10}
{{milestone:{label:8.30,id:UT22084-055-001-790}}}“He afterward became a buddha in the world
Who was always known as Sucintitārtha.
He benefited many millions of beings
And afterward attained nirvāṇa,{{note:{index323,id:UT22084-055-001-791}}} like an extinguished flame.{{note:{index324,id:UT22084-055-001-792}}} {11} 
{{milestone:{label:8.31,id:UT22084-055-001-793}}}Conclusion of the eighth chapter, “Buddha Abhāva­samudgata.”{{note:{index325,id:UT22084-055-001-794}}}
{{milestone:{label:9,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-9}}}The Patience of the Profound Dharma
Chapter 9
{{milestone:{label:9.1,id:UT22084-055-001-796}}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, {{page:{number:47,id:UT22084-055-001-5880,folio:F.24.b}}} “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood and liberate all beings from the ocean of existence should hear this king of samādhis, in which the equality of the nature of all phenomena is revealed, which is praised by all the buddhas and is the mother of the tathāgatas. They should obtain it, preserve it, understand it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others.
{{milestone:{label:9.2,id:UT22084-055-001-797}}}“Why is that? Young man, this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, has given birth to all the tathāgatas, the arhats, the perfectly enlightened buddhas; all tathāgatas, śrāvakas, and pratyekabuddhas have come from it.
{{milestone:{label:9.3,id:UT22084-055-001-798}}}“Therefore, young man, you also should obtain this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, which is praised by all the buddhas and is the mother of the tathāgatas.{{note:{index326,id:UT22084-055-001-799}}} It has been said:
{{milestone:{label:9.4,id:UT22084-055-001-800}}}“Therefore, those who wish for enlightenment and buddhahood,
And to liberate beings from the ocean of existence,
Should obtain this sūtra praised by the buddhas,
And then sublime enlightenment will not be difficult to attain.”{{note:{index327,id:UT22084-055-001-801}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.5,id:UT22084-055-001-802}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish{{note:{index328,id:UT22084-055-001-803}}} to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood should become skilled{{note:{index329,id:UT22084-055-001-804}}} in the patience of profound Dharma.{{note:{index330,id:UT22084-055-001-805}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.6,id:UT22084-055-001-806}}}“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas become skilled in the patience of profound Dharma?
“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should know that all phenomena are like illusions. {{page:{number:48,id:UT22084-055-001-5881,folio:F.25.a}}} They should know that all phenomena are like dreams, like mirages, like echoes, like optical illusions, like the moon on water, like hallucinations,{{note:{index331,id:UT22084-055-001-808}}} like reflections, and like space.
{{milestone:{label:9.7,id:UT22084-055-001-809}}}“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas know that all phenomena are like illusions,{{note:{index332,id:UT22084-055-001-810}}} they are skilled in the patience of profound Dharma. Those who have the patience of profound Dharma have no desire for any phenomenon that causes desire, have no anger toward any phenomenon that causes anger, and have no ignorance regarding any phenomenon that causes ignorance. Why is that? It is because they do not see that phenomenon; they do not perceive that phenomenon. They do not see the phenomena and they do not perceive the phenomena of that which is desired, the desire, or the desirer; that which angers, the anger, or one who is angry; nor that of which one is ignorant, the ignorance, or the one who is ignorant. Because they do not see and do not perceive those phenomena they have no desire, they have no anger, they have no ignorance, their minds do not regress, and they rest in meditation. They are without conceptual elaboration. They have crossed over to the other side. They have reached dry land. They have reached safety. They have attained freedom from fear.{{note:{index333,id:UT22084-055-001-811}}} They have correct conduct. They have knowledge. They have wisdom. They have merit. They have miraculous powers. They have memory.{{note:{index334,id:UT22084-055-001-812}}} They have intelligence. They have realization.{{note:{index335,id:UT22084-055-001-813}}} They have a sense of modesty. They have stability. They have bodhisattva conduct. They have the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy. They are unblemished.{{note:{index336,id:UT22084-055-001-814}}}{{page:{number:49,id:UT22084-055-001-5882,folio:F.25.b}}} They have nothing. They are arhats. Their defilements have ceased. They have no kleśas. They have power. Their minds are liberated. Their wisdom is liberated. They are thoroughbred stallions.{{note:{index337,id:UT22084-055-001-815}}} They are great elephants.{{note:{index338,id:UT22084-055-001-816}}} They have done what had to be done. They have accomplished what had to be accomplished. They have put down their burden. They have reached their goals. They have ended engagement with existence. They have liberated their minds through true knowledge. They are mendicants who have attained all the perfect, highest, complete powers of the mind. They are brahmins.{{note:{index339,id:UT22084-055-001-817}}} They are snātakas.{{note:{index340,id:UT22084-055-001-818}}} They are masters of the Vedas.{{note:{index341,id:UT22084-055-001-819}}} They know the Vedas.{{note:{index342,id:UT22084-055-001-820}}} They are śrotriyas.{{note:{index343,id:UT22084-055-001-821}}} They are children of the buddhas. They are children of the Śākya.{{note:{index344,id:UT22084-055-001-822}}} They have crushed the thorns.{{note:{index345,id:UT22084-055-001-823}}} They have not left the law behind.{{note:{index346,id:UT22084-055-001-824}}} They have left the trench barrier behind.{{note:{index347,id:UT22084-055-001-825}}} They have crossed over the trench barrier.{{note:{index348,id:UT22084-055-001-826}}} They have extracted the splinters.{{note:{index349,id:UT22084-055-001-827}}} They have no illness.{{note:{index350,id:UT22084-055-001-828}}} They are bhikṣus. They are free from all bondage. They have been born as humans. They are good humans. They are supreme humans. They are great humans. They are human lions.{{note:{index351,id:UT22084-055-001-829}}} They are human elephants.{{note:{index352,id:UT22084-055-001-830}}} They are human stallions.{{note:{index353,id:UT22084-055-001-831}}} They are human carthorses.{{note:{index354,id:UT22084-055-001-832}}} They are human heroes.{{note:{index355,id:UT22084-055-001-833}}} They are human strongmen.{{note:{index356,id:UT22084-055-001-834}}} They are human flowers.{{note:{index357,id:UT22084-055-001-835}}} They are human lotuses.{{note:{index358,id:UT22084-055-001-836}}} They are human white lotuses.{{note:{index359,id:UT22084-055-001-837}}} They are human tamers.{{note:{index360,id:UT22084-055-001-838}}} They are human moons.{{note:{index361,id:UT22084-055-001-839}}} They are extraordinary humans. They are stainless humans.”{{note:{index362,id:UT22084-055-001-840}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.8,id:UT22084-055-001-841}}}Then the Bhagavān, in order to give this Dharma teaching on entering the patience of profound Dharma, recited these verses:
{{milestone:{label:9.9,id:UT22084-055-001-842}}}“At one time a world appears,
And later the entire world becomes space.
As it was before, so it is afterward.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {1}
{{milestone:{label:9.10,id:UT22084-055-001-843}}}“All that there is in this world
Later dissolves into the mass of water below.
As it is below, so it is above.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {2} {{page:{number:50,id:UT22084-055-001-5883,folio:F.26.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.11,id:UT22084-055-001-844}}}“Just as in a completely cloudless sky
In an instant a mass of clouds appears—
From where did they first originate?
Know that all phenomena are like that. {3}
{{milestone:{label:9.12,id:UT22084-055-001-845}}}“If you think of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa,
His image will appear in your mind.
As he was before, so he is afterward.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {4}
{{milestone:{label:9.13,id:UT22084-055-001-846}}}“When a person sees a mass of foam
That is carried along in a river
And examines it, they see that it has no essence.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {5}
{{milestone:{label:9.14,id:UT22084-055-001-847}}}“When large drops of rain fall, 
There appear separate bubbles of water.
They vanish as they appear; the bubbles have no existence.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {6}
{{milestone:{label:9.15,id:UT22084-055-001-848}}}“When a letter is sent to another town
With news of the good or bad that has been done,
A voice does not accompany the letter.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {7}
{{milestone:{label:9.16,id:UT22084-055-001-849}}}“When a man is intoxicated from alcohol,
He perceives the ground to be spinning,
But the earth is not moving or shaking.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {8}
{{milestone:{label:9.17,id:UT22084-055-001-850}}}“A woman sees her beautified face
On the surface of a mirror or a bowl of oil.
The fool feels passion for it
And runs in search for the desired. {9}
{{milestone:{label:9.18,id:UT22084-055-001-851}}}“The face was not transferred there.
The face will never be found in the reflection,
And yet fools have desire for it.
Know that all phenomena are like that.{{note:{index363,id:UT22084-055-001-852}}} {10} 
{{milestone:{label:9.19,id:UT22084-055-001-853}}}“Just like optical illusions and fata morganas,
Just like dreams and just like illusions,
When their attributes are meditated on, their nature is empty.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {11}
{{milestone:{label:9.20,id:UT22084-055-001-854}}}“When the moon is in a clear sky,
Its reflection appears on the sea,
But the moon has not moved onto the water.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {12}
{{milestone:{label:9.21,id:UT22084-055-001-855}}}“A man who is inside a canyon{{note:{index364,id:UT22084-055-001-856}}}
Sees no one but hears the echoes
Of singing, speaking, and laughter.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {13} {{page:{number:51,id:UT22084-055-001-5884,folio:F.26.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.22,id:UT22084-055-001-857}}}“Echoes are produced
By songs, music, and weeping,
But the song that is heard does not exist.
Know that all phenomena are like that.{{note:{index365,id:UT22084-055-001-858}}} {14} 
{{milestone:{label:9.23,id:UT22084-055-001-859}}}“Although pleasures are enjoyed in a dream,
When the person awakes they are not be seen.
The fool, though, becomes attached to those pleasures. 
Know that all phenomena are like that. {15}
{{milestone:{label:9.24,id:UT22084-055-001-860}}}“A magician causes forms to appear,
Creating horses, elephants, chariots, and so on.
But though they appear they do not exist at all.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {16}
{{milestone:{label:9.25,id:UT22084-055-001-861}}}“In a young woman’s dream
She gives birth to a son and then sees him die.
She is happy when he’s born and sad when he dies.
Know that all phenomena are like that.{{note:{index366,id:UT22084-055-001-862}}} {18} 
{{milestone:{label:9.26,id:UT22084-055-001-863}}}“In the night the reflection of the moon 
Appears on clear, undisturbed water,
But it is empty of a moon and there is nothing to grasp.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {19}
{{milestone:{label:9.27,id:UT22084-055-001-864}}}“A thirsty person traveling
At noon during the summer
Sees a lake that is a mirage.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {20}
{{milestone:{label:9.28,id:UT22084-055-001-865}}}“The water that is a mirage cannot be found.
Foolish beings want to drink it,
But water that is not real cannot be drunk.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {21}
{{milestone:{label:9.29,id:UT22084-055-001-866}}}“When a person in search of its essence
Pulls apart the trunk of a green banana plant, 
They find no essence either inside or outside.
Know that all phenomena are like that. {22}
{{milestone:{label:9.30,id:UT22084-055-001-867}}}“The eyes, the ears, and the nose are unreliable.
The tongue, the body, and the mind are unreliable.
If the senses could be relied upon,
What need would there be for the path of the noble ones? {23}
{{milestone:{label:9.31,id:UT22084-055-001-868}}}“These senses are unreliable.
Their nature is material and neutral.
Therefore those who wish for the path to nirvāṇa
Must follow the path of the noble ones. {24}
{{milestone:{label:9.32,id:UT22084-055-001-869}}}“If one examines the body back into the past,
There is no body and no conception of a body.
When there is no body and no conception of a body
This is called the lineage of the noncomposite.{{note:{index367,id:UT22084-055-001-870}}} {25} 
{{milestone:{label:9.33,id:UT22084-055-001-871}}}“There are no phenomena in the phenomena of nirvāṇa,
For if it is nonexistent there could never be an existence. {{page:{number:52,id:UT22084-055-001-5885,folio:F.27.a}}}
Those who conceptualize teach existence and nonexistence,
But practicing in that way will not bring an end to suffering. {26}
{{milestone:{label:9.34,id:UT22084-055-001-872}}}“ ‘Existing,’ ‘not existing,’ and both are extremes.
‘Pure’ and ‘impure’ are also extremes.
Therefore, rejecting both extremes, 
The wise do not even remain in the middle. {27}
{{milestone:{label:9.35,id:UT22084-055-001-873}}}“ ‘Existing’ and ‘not existing’ are in conflict.
‘Pure’ and ‘impure’ are also in conflict.
When there is conflict, suffering cannot be ended.
When there is no conflict, suffering ceases.{{note:{index368,id:UT22084-055-001-874}}} {28} 
{{milestone:{label:9.36,id:UT22084-055-001-875}}}“When fools speak about remaining in mindfulness{{note:{index369,id:UT22084-055-001-876}}}
They become proud, saying, ‘I have witnessed it in my body.’{{note:{index370,id:UT22084-055-001-877}}}
But those who have witnessed it in their body have no pride;
They are those who are freed from all such pride.{{note:{index371,id:UT22084-055-001-878}}} {29} 
{{milestone:{label:9.37,id:UT22084-055-001-879}}}“When speaking of the four dhyānas,
The foolish claim they can experience dhyāna.
But those who know and realize that dhyāna 
Is without kleśas or pride reject such arrogance. {30}
{{milestone:{label:9.38,id:UT22084-055-001-880}}}“When speaking of the four truths,
The foolish say that they see the truth.
But there is no pride when the truth is seen.
The Jina taught the truth that is without pride. {31}
{{milestone:{label:9.39,id:UT22084-055-001-881}}}“Do not be proud of maintaining correct conduct. 
Do not become proud through listening to the Dharma.
When those with little wisdom become proud,
That is the root of increasing suffering. {32}
{{milestone:{label:9.40,id:UT22084-055-001-882}}}“The world’s guide, the omniscient one,
Taught that pride is the root of suffering.
To be puffed up with pride makes suffering grow;
To have no pride brings suffering to an end. {33}
{{milestone:{label:9.41,id:UT22084-055-001-883}}}“However much Dharma you have learned,
If you feel proud of your learning and let your proper conduct lapse,
Your misconduct will take you to the lower realms 
And all that great learning will not protect you. {34}
{{milestone:{label:9.42,id:UT22084-055-001-884}}}“If you feel proud of being renowned for correct conduct
And do not dedicate yourself to listening to many teachings,
When the results of your correct conduct have been used up
You will afterward experience suffering.{{note:{index372,id:UT22084-055-001-885}}} {35} 
{{milestone:{label:9.43,id:UT22084-055-001-886}}}“If you meditate on a worldly samādhi
And do not eliminate the conception of a self,
Then the kleśas will arise once more,
As happened in the samādhi practice of Udraka.{{note:{index373,id:UT22084-055-001-887}}} {36} {{page:{number:53,id:UT22084-055-001-5886,folio:F.27.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:9.44,id:UT22084-055-001-888}}}“If one examines the Dharma of selflessness,
And if after examining, one meditates,
That will be the cause resulting in the attainment of nirvāṇa.
It is impossible for peace to come from any other cause. {37}
{{milestone:{label:9.45,id:UT22084-055-001-889}}}“If a man is being attacked by bandits
And, wishing to save his life, he tries to run away
But his legs will not move and he cannot run,
He will be captured and killed{{note:{index374,id:UT22084-055-001-890}}} by the bandits. {38}
{{milestone:{label:9.46,id:UT22084-055-001-891}}}“In the same way, a stupid person without correct conduct
May try to escape from composite phenomena.
But without correct conduct he is not able to flee,
And will be killed by old age, illness, and death. {39}
{{milestone:{label:9.47,id:UT22084-055-001-892}}}“Just as many thousands of savages{{note:{index375,id:UT22084-055-001-893}}}
Do you harm in various ways,
The kleśas will in many ways,
Like savages, destroy that which is good. {40}
{{milestone:{label:9.48,id:UT22084-055-001-894}}}“Those who have understood the skandhas to be without a self,
Even if insulted or beaten, will not be dismayed.
They will not fall under the power of the kleśa demons.
Those who know emptiness will never become agitated. {41}
{{milestone:{label:9.49,id:UT22084-055-001-895}}}“Many people teach the emptiness of the skandhas 
But have not understood that selflessness;
When those who have not understood are contradicted by others,
They will be overpowered by anger and speak harsh words. {42}
{{milestone:{label:9.50,id:UT22084-055-001-896}}}“There was a man{{note:{index376,id:UT22084-055-001-897}}} who was ill and suffering physically.
For many years he could not attain freedom from his illness.
For a long time he was tormented by his illness,
And in order to be cured he went in search of a physician. {43}
{{milestone:{label:9.51,id:UT22084-055-001-898}}}“Searching and searching, again and again,
He found a skilled and wise physician
Who had compassion for him
And said, ‘Take this medicine.’ {44}
{{milestone:{label:9.52,id:UT22084-055-001-899}}}“He gave him much excellent medicine,
But the sick man didn’t take the healing medicine.
That was not the fault of the physician or the medicine;
It was the fault of the sick person. {45}
{{milestone:{label:9.53,id:UT22084-055-001-900}}}“In the same way, those who have entered homelessness in this teaching,
Who know of the strengths, the dhyānas, and the powers
But do not dedicate themselves to meditation,
Are not endeavouring in what is correct, so how could they attain nirvāṇa? {46}
{{milestone:{label:9.54,id:UT22084-055-001-901}}}“All phenomena are always empty by nature.
The heirs of the jinas have eliminated all things.
The entirety of existence has always been empty.
The emptiness of the tīrthikas is limited. {47}
{{milestone:{label:9.55,id:UT22084-055-001-902}}}“The wise do not argue with fools,
They politely avoid them; {{page:{number:54,id:UT22084-055-001-5887,folio:F.28.a}}}
Thinking, ‘They come to me with malicious intent,’
They do not engage with the Dharma of fools. {48}
{{milestone:{label:9.56,id:UT22084-055-001-903}}}“Knowing the nature and dispositions of fools,
The wise do not associate with fools.
Whenever they associate well with them
Those fools eventually turn into enemies. {49}
{{milestone:{label:9.57,id:UT22084-055-001-904}}}“The wise do not depend upon the foolish.
The wise and the foolish have different natures.
The nature of the foolish is naturally contrary,
So the wise do not have ordinary people as friends. {50}
{{milestone:{label:9.58,id:UT22084-055-001-905}}}“They may speak with words about the Dharma
But do not believe it, showing their anger and aggression.
Such is the Dharma of fools, and knowing this to be so
The wise do not rely on it. {51}
{{milestone:{label:9.59,id:UT22084-055-001-906}}}“The foolish are in accord with other fools
Like impurity with other impurities.
The wise are in accord with other wise people
Like butter{{note:{index377,id:UT22084-055-001-907}}} is with ghee. {52}
{{milestone:{label:9.60,id:UT22084-055-001-908}}}“They do not examine the faults of saṃsāra; 
They pay no attention to the ripening of karma;
They have no faith in the words of the buddhas:
Those fools will be sliced and cut into pieces. {53}
{{milestone:{label:9.61,id:UT22084-055-001-909}}}“They have obtained a human life that is difficult to obtain,
But they have not become skilled in any craft.
They have become poor without any wealth.
In order to have a livelihood they become mendicants. {54}
{{milestone:{label:9.62,id:UT22084-055-001-910}}}“Having become mendicants in this teaching of the Buddha,
They become attached to their robes and alms bowls.
They fall under the influence of bad companions,
And they do not practice the teaching of the Sugata. {55}
{{milestone:{label:9.63,id:UT22084-055-001-911}}}“They are not observant of their own conduct.
Such fools do not perceive the states of their minds.
Day and night they do not follow the discipline,
And they do not abhor the path of bad actions. {56}
{{milestone:{label:9.64,id:UT22084-055-001-912}}}“They do not restrain their body and mind.
There is nothing that they will not say. 
They are always looking for faults in others,
And criticize any mistake they make. {57}
{{milestone:{label:9.65,id:UT22084-055-001-913}}}“Such fools have attachment to food.
They know no limit to their eating.
They obtain their food through the Buddha’s merit,
But these fools do not keep that in mind. {58}
{{milestone:{label:9.66,id:UT22084-055-001-914}}}“When they find food that is delicious and pleasing,
They consume{{note:{index378,id:UT22084-055-001-915}}} it without engaging in the discipline.
For them that food becomes poison, {{page:{number:55,id:UT22084-055-001-5888,folio:F.28.b}}}
Like an unclean lotus stem{{note:{index379,id:UT22084-055-001-916}}} for an elephant calf.{{note:{index380,id:UT22084-055-001-917}}} {59} 
{{milestone:{label:9.67,id:UT22084-055-001-918}}}“The wise, the sagacious, the realized
Also eat food that is pure and pleasing, 
But they have no attachment to it.
They eat without clinging, maintaining the discipline. {60}
{{milestone:{label:9.68,id:UT22084-055-001-919}}}“The wise, sagacious, and realized
Say ‘welcome’ when the foolish come,
Bringing them closer with pleasant words,
And maintaining compassion for them; {61}
{{milestone:{label:9.69,id:UT22084-055-001-920}}}“They are kind and helpful to them.
But the foolish are happy when harm comes to the wise.
Because of such faults, the wise avoid the foolish 
And live alone like deer in the forest. {62}
{{milestone:{label:9.70,id:UT22084-055-001-921}}}“The wise, knowing these kinds of defects,
Do not associate with fools.
They think, ‘If I depend on those who have no wisdom,
There will be no higher rebirth, let alone the attainment of enlightenment.’ {63}
{{milestone:{label:9.71,id:UT22084-055-001-922}}}“The wise reach enlightenment by putting into practice
The samādhi of dwelling in love, 
Of dwelling in compassion, of acting with joy,
And with constant equanimity toward all existences. {64}
{{milestone:{label:9.72,id:UT22084-055-001-923}}}“They attain the enlightenment that is peace, free of misery.
They perceive beings afflicted by illness and aging.{{note:{index381,id:UT22084-055-001-924}}}
They have compassion toward them,
And give them the teachings of ultimate truth. {65}
{{milestone:{label:9.73,id:UT22084-055-001-925}}}“Who can know the true nature of the jinas 
And the truth of the sugatas, which is beyond description?{{note:{index382,id:UT22084-055-001-926}}}
It is they who hear this kind of Dharma
And attain the immaterial patience of the noble ones.” {66}
{{milestone:{label:9.74,id:UT22084-055-001-927}}}Conclusion of the ninth chapter, “The Patience of the Profound Dharma.”
{{milestone:{label:10,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-10}}}The Entry into the City
Chapter 10
{{milestone:{label:10.1,id:UT22084-055-001-928}}}The Bhagavān then said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, you should be someone who makes practice essential, and always trains in that way. Why is that? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who make practice essential will not even find it difficult to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, not to mention attaining this samādhi.”
{{milestone:{label:10.2,id:UT22084-055-001-929}}}Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, {{page:{number:56,id:UT22084-055-001-5889,folio:F.29.a}}} with palms placed together, bowed toward the Bhagavān and exclaimed, “Bhagavān, that teaching and instruction that the bhagavāns have taught well, presented well, and explained well to the bodhisattva mahāsattvas, the entire bodhisattva training that they have explained well and presented well is marvelous.
{{milestone:{label:10.3,id:UT22084-055-001-930}}}“Bhagavān, this is the scope of activity of the tathāgatas, not of the śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, let alone the tīrthikas.
{{milestone:{label:10.4,id:UT22084-055-001-931}}}“Bhagavān, I, too, will make practice essential, and without care for life or body I shall train as the tathāgatas have. Why is that? Bhagavān, I wish to train as the tathāgatas have. Bhagavān, I wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. Bhagavān, I wish to eliminate the evil māras. Bhagavān, I wish to free all beings from all fear and all suffering.{{note:{index383,id:UT22084-055-001-932}}} I pray that the Bhagavān will place his right hand upon my head.”
He said to the Bhagavān:
{{milestone:{label:10.5,id:UT22084-055-001-934}}}“You have an excellent body, like a clear sky. 
You are the son of wisdom, who has no body or attributes.
You are a deep ocean of qualities, and have compassion.
You who are without equal, place your hand upon my head.”{{note:{index384,id:UT22084-055-001-935}}} {i}
{{milestone:{label:10.6,id:UT22084-055-001-936}}}The Bhagavān placed upon Candraprabha’s head his right hand, which was adorned with many characteristics that were the result of many roots of merit, and which was of the color of divine gold.
{{milestone:{label:10.7,id:UT22084-055-001-937}}}As soon as the Bhagavān placed his right hand upon Candraprabha’s head, in that very instant, more indescribable than indescribably many hundred thousand quintillions of samādhi entranceways that arise from the perfection of wisdom were revealed to Candraprabha, such as the heroic,{{note:{index385,id:UT22084-055-001-938}}}the treasury of space,{{note:{index386,id:UT22084-055-001-939}}}the vajra-like,{{note:{index387,id:UT22084-055-001-940}}}the speed of the mind,{{note:{index388,id:UT22084-055-001-941}}}the revealing of all forms,{{note:{index389,id:UT22084-055-001-942}}}{{page:{number:57,id:UT22084-055-001-5890,folio:F.29.b}}}the ultimate absence of obscurations, the revealing of all tathāgatas,{{note:{index390,id:UT22084-055-001-943}}}the consecration of all emptiness,{{note:{index391,id:UT22084-055-001-944}}} and so on. Many entranceways to dhāraṇīs and liberations{{note:{index392,id:UT22084-055-001-945}}} were revealed. He attained the knowledge of the joy and happiness that is described by the noble ones, of the countless vast number of beings in the deva realms, and the scope of experience of the buddhas and bodhisattvas.
It was said:
{{milestone:{label:10.8,id:UT22084-055-001-947}}}The Bhagavān placed upon the head of the youth Candraprabha 
The hand that for many millions of eons had given away jewels,
Which was beautified by being webbed, and had markings of a vase and hook,
A knot of eternity, a wheel, a victory banner, a flag, and fishes. {ii}
{{milestone:{label:10.9,id:UT22084-055-001-948}}}Then Candraprabha, full of joy and happiness and the knowledge of the countless, vast number of beings in the deva realms, and the scope of experience of the buddhas and bodhisattvas, rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, with palms placed together, he bowed toward the Bhagavān and recited these appropriate verses of praise:
{{milestone:{label:10.10,id:UT22084-055-001-949}}}“I pay homage to you, the unsurpassable provider of freedom from fear.
I pay homage to you, a loving friend of beings who benefits others.
I pay homage to you, who possess the power of truth and the ten strengths.
I pay homage to you, who are the equal of the unequaled tathāgatas. {iii}
{{milestone:{label:10.11,id:UT22084-055-001-950}}}“I pay homage to you, the Lord who has the highest compassion. 
I pay homage to you, the hero who has subjugated the four enemies.{{note:{index393,id:UT22084-055-001-951}}}
I pay homage to you, who know the benefits of sublime diligence.
I pay homage to you, the Lord{{note:{index394,id:UT22084-055-001-952}}} who has the supreme dharmakāya. {iv}
{{milestone:{label:10.12,id:UT22084-055-001-953}}}“I will always go for refuge to you, Lord, 
The Jina who is a sun shining in the center of the vast sky of wisdom, 
Dispelling darkness with the light of love and compassion,
And who is the teacher of the extremely profound Dharma of the ultimate truth.” {v} {{page:{number:58,id:UT22084-055-001-5891,folio:F.30.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:10.13,id:UT22084-055-001-954}}}When the youth Candraprabha had recited these appropriate verses of praise to the Bhagavān, he said to him, “Bhagavān, so that you may show me your compassion I pray that you, with your saṅgha of bodhisattvas and saṅgha of bhikṣus, will assent to eat your meal tomorrow at my home.
{{milestone:{label:10.14,id:UT22084-055-001-955}}}“I pray to the Lord of men and your sons
That you eat a pure meal at my home.
Lord of sages, in order to show me your compassion,
Chief of devas, give your assent.” {vi}
{{milestone:{label:10.15,id:UT22084-055-001-956}}}The Bhagavān, because of his compassion, by remaining silent assented to eat a meal together with his saṅgha of bodhisattvas and saṅgha of bhikṣus at the home of the youth Candraprabha.
{{milestone:{label:10.16,id:UT22084-055-001-957}}}The youth Candraprabha, knowing that the Bhagavān had assented by his silence, rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, bowed his head to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, and departed from the Bhagavān’s presence.
{{milestone:{label:10.17,id:UT22084-055-001-958}}}The youth Candraprabha then went down from Vulture Peak Mountain, and at that time he perfectly adorned the entire road in between Vulture Peak Mountain and the great city of Rājagṛha.
{{milestone:{label:10.18,id:UT22084-055-001-959}}}As an offering to the Bhagavān he cleared a great, wide roadway so that it was free of grass, tree stumps, thorns, stones, pebbles, and gravel, and spread pure sand over it, so that it was as soft and pleasant to the touch as down, and made a pleasant sound. He covered it with flowers from all seasons, such as divine blue lotuses, red lotuses, night lotuses, white lotuses, water lilies, kachnar flowers, sambac jasmines, magnolias, bignonias, star jasmines, sesame flowers, ironwood flowers, and aśoka flowers. Parasols, banners, flags, flags of victory, precious arches,{{note:{index395,id:UT22084-055-001-960}}} and canopies were set up along the road. {{page:{number:59,id:UT22084-055-001-5892,folio:F.30.b}}} There were precious censers from which flowed the smoke of black agarwood.{{note:{index396,id:UT22084-055-001-961}}} Arranged in different places were dancers and performers skilled in performing divine songs, dance, and music. Beautifully adorned men, women, boys, and girls were arranged holding paṇava drums,{{note:{index397,id:UT22084-055-001-962}}} one-stringed lutes,{{note:{index398,id:UT22084-055-001-963}}} lutes, flutes, mṛdaṅga drums,{{note:{index399,id:UT22084-055-001-964}}} mukunda drums,{{note:{index400,id:UT22084-055-001-965}}} and muraja drums.{{note:{index401,id:UT22084-055-001-966}}} On both sides of the road tall palm trees were adorned with various divine jewels and a jingling network of bells made from Jambu River gold.{{note:{index402,id:UT22084-055-001-967}}} There were many hundred thousand quintillions of pillars made of precious materials, and different kinds of trees of various heights and thicknesses made from the seven jewels, and on which were arranged the leaves, flowers, and fruits of all seasons.
{{milestone:{label:10.19,id:UT22084-055-001-968}}}The road was excellently adorned in various ways.
Canopies, parasols, and flags were erected.
The sound of music was perfectly played,
And similarly there was the beautiful sound of songs. {vii}
{{milestone:{label:10.20,id:UT22084-055-001-969}}}That perfect road was excellently adorned
By many women performing dances,
Many millions of various excellent cloths,
And beautiful, excellent garlands of flowers. {viii}
{{milestone:{label:10.21,id:UT22084-055-001-970}}}“The Buddha, the moon of sages, the compassionate one 
Is coming to this pure excellent city.”
On hearing that, young Candraprabha with great faith
Perfectly adorned a great, vast road. {ix}
{{milestone:{label:10.22,id:UT22084-055-001-971}}}He spread out pure, divine sand
And scattered perfect, beautiful flowers.
He also set up precious pillars
And made the road as beautiful as a divine city. {x}
{{milestone:{label:10.23,id:UT22084-055-001-972}}}Young Candraprabha, with immense joy,
Perfectly adorned the road in various ways.
Devas, asuras, and nāgas, upon seeing it
Were astonished and cried out, “Ha ha ha!” {xi}
{{milestone:{label:10.24,id:UT22084-055-001-973}}}To the left and right of the road there were placed 
Tall, excellent, round palm trees made of Jambu River gold,
Decorated and beautified by a network 
Of numerous jingling, precious bells. {xii}
{{milestone:{label:10.25,id:UT22084-055-001-974}}}Similarly arranged were million of precious trees {{page:{number:60,id:UT22084-055-001-5893,folio:F.31.a}}}
Adorned by blossomed flowers of all seasons,
Which were beautiful adornments for that vast road,
Like a blissful park in the deva realms. {xiii}
{{milestone:{label:10.26,id:UT22084-055-001-975}}}Pillars that were made from precious materials,
With beautiful strings of beads that shone like light—
An indescribable sight, huge and vast—
Were set up and arranged on the left and right of the road. {xiv}
{{milestone:{label:10.27,id:UT22084-055-001-976}}}The Buddha, the Lord of the three worlds,
Traveled on that road to the capital city. 
That great road was adorned in that way
So that it was beautiful in every way. {xv}
{{milestone:{label:10.28,id:UT22084-055-001-977}}}On the right and left, precious censers were hung.
They were filled with black agarwood.
From all the censers there formed a cloud of smoke,
With divine, pleasant aromas of various kinds. {xvi}
{{milestone:{label:10.29,id:UT22084-055-001-978}}}The youth Candraprabha, for the sake of the Jina,
Arranged vast, incalculable ornaments of divine materials,
From the entrance to the water well of the city
Up to the king of mountains, Gṛdhrakūṭa. {xvii}
{{milestone:{label:10.30,id:UT22084-055-001-979}}}Young Candraprabha adorned the road with many different precious arrangements.{{note:{index403,id:UT22084-055-001-980}}} Then young Candraprabha descended from Vulture Peak and went to the great city of Rājagṛha, to his tall, vast, great, divine home. He reached there and he entered his home. He spent that night preparing a great amount of excellent, delicious{{note:{index404,id:UT22084-055-001-981}}} food and drink, and creating food that had a hundred flavors. Then he sprinkled well the ground in the great city of Rājagṛha and swept it clean, scattered flower petals, perfumed it with incense, put up canopies, hung ribbons and wreaths of silk, and set up parasols, banners, and flags.
{{milestone:{label:10.31,id:UT22084-055-001-982}}}In that way he made the main road of Rājagṛha up to the town free of stones, pebbles, and gravel, scattered it with various flowers, and sprinkled it with sandalwood powder. He adorned the windows, porticoes, doors,{{note:{index405,id:UT22084-055-001-983}}} roofs,{{note:{index406,id:UT22084-055-001-984}}} lattices,{{note:{index407,id:UT22084-055-001-985}}} and the crescent moons,{{note:{index408,id:UT22084-055-001-986}}} and perfumed them with sandalwood. In that way he adorned the city of Rājagṛha with countless displays {{page:{number:61,id:UT22084-055-001-5894,folio:F.31.b}}} and adorned his own house, too, with a variety of many adornments. He hung it with many precious strings of beads. He adorned it with the raiment of the Tuṣita deities and also beautified the grounds. He had many kinds of garlands and wreaths put up as adornments. He arranged a hundred thousand precious seats. In order to make offerings to the Bhagavān he placed in their center a lion throne of divine materials that surpassed the work of devas and humans. In the four directions he hung censers made of various precious materials, from which flowed the smoke of black agarwood. In that way the youth Candraprabha arranged his excellent home so that for the enjoyment of the Bhagavān there was the sound of divine songs, performances, and music; pure parasols and banners were erected; an audience of a hundred thousand devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and nonhumans thronged it; and it was filled with many various kinds of precious flowers. 
{{milestone:{label:10.32,id:UT22084-055-001-987}}}Candraprabha perfectly, extensively adorned 
His vast and excellent home.
In the center he placed a lion throne of divine materials
Where the lamp of the world would sit. {xviii}
{{milestone:{label:10.33,id:UT22084-055-001-988}}}He perfectly set out countless millions
Of extremely precious, beautiful seats
Where the saṅgha of the lamp of the world, 
The Lord of jinas, would sit. {xix}
{{milestone:{label:10.34,id:UT22084-055-001-989}}}Censers made of all kinds of precious materials,
Completely filled with agarwood,
Were hung in all directions,
And from them a beautiful aroma spread. {xx}
{{milestone:{label:10.35,id:UT22084-055-001-990}}}Candraprabha, in order to attain the ten strengths,
Spread throughout the entire excellent grounds of the house
Various kinds of beautiful, precious flowers—
A multitude of excellent, aromatic flowers. {xxi}
{{milestone:{label:10.36,id:UT22084-055-001-991}}}The sound of dancers, singers, and of music
Filled the entire excellent house with sound. 
He erected also parasols and banners {{page:{number:62,id:UT22084-055-001-5895,folio:F.32.a}}}
So that the house was intensely beautiful, like that of a deity. {xxii}
{{milestone:{label:10.37,id:UT22084-055-001-992}}}The vast excellent home of the youth Candraprabha
Was adorned by a multitude of young people.
It was filled with many nāgas, yakṣas, and asuras,
And was gazed upon by many hundreds of devas.{{note:{index409,id:UT22084-055-001-993}}} {xxiii}
