{{milestone:{label:10.38,id:UT22084-055-001-994}}}The young man Candraprabha, having adorned the great city of Rājagṛha and having perfectly beautified his own home, after the night was over, in the early morning, departed, accompanied by the music of hundreds of various kinds of instruments, with many millions of parasols, banners, and flags held high, and with an encircling vanguard of a great assembly of eight million quintillion bodhisattvas, their cupped hands filled with divine coral tree flowers. Among them were bodhisattvas with one life remaining, such as Avalokiteśvara, Mahā­sthāma­prāpta, Gandhahasti, Ratnaketu, Dundubhisvara,{{note:{index410,id:UT22084-055-001-995}}} Durabhisambhava, Mañjuśrī Kumārabhūta, Vīrasena, Subāhu, Ratnakusuma, Amoghadarśin, Maitreya, and others, accompanied by many adorned horses and elephants without riders that were being led along, with an assembly of countless people of the country, his own cupped hands filled with divine coral tree flowers; and they were accompanied by the enchanting, beautiful, harmonious sound of the laughter of the deities as they cried, “Oh, the bodhisattva’s great power! The bodhisattva’s great miracles! The bodhisattva’s great manifestations! The bodhisattva’s—a la la!”
{{milestone:{label:10.39,id:UT22084-055-001-996}}}He came out through the hot springs gateway{{note:{index411,id:UT22084-055-001-997}}} of the great city of Rājagṛha and went toward Vulture Peak Mountain, and to the Bhagavān. 
{{milestone:{label:10.40,id:UT22084-055-001-998}}}When he arrived, he bowed his head to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times,{{note:{index412,id:UT22084-055-001-999}}} sprinkled the divine coral tree flowers that filled his cupped hands over the Bhagavān, and went to sit down to one side.
{{milestone:{label:10.41,id:UT22084-055-001-1000}}}Maitreya and the other {{page:{number:63,id:UT22084-055-001-5896,folio:F.32.b}}} bodhisattva mahāsattvas bowed their heads to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated the Bhagavān three times, sprinkled the divine coral tree flowers that filled their cupped hands over the Bhagavān, and also sat down to one side.
{{milestone:{label:10.42,id:UT22084-055-001-1001}}}Then the youth, who had sat to one side, rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, with palms placed together bowed toward the Bhagavān and said, “It is midday, Bhagavān, the time to eat. If the Bhagavān considers the time has come, then together with the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, the saṅgha of bhikṣus, and the devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, rishis, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, kumbhāṇḍas, pretas, pūtanas, humans, and nonhumans who have great power, who are widely renowned for their great power and have great influence, come to the great city of Rājagṛha, as the time has come to eat the midday meal in my garden. Sugata, it is midday.{{note:{index413,id:UT22084-055-001-1002}}}
{{milestone:{label:10.43,id:UT22084-055-001-1003}}}“I have adorned well the entire, excellent city,
And similarly, Lord, my garden.
I have prepared and laid out divine food with a hundred flavors.
As it is midday, I pray to the Sugata to arise. {xxiv}
{{milestone:{label:10.44,id:UT22084-055-001-1004}}}“Supreme Rishi, you who hold the qualities of the ten strengths in your hands,
Encircled by the assembly of your sons, come to the city.
I pray that you, the illuminating sun who dispels darkness, will arise.
Bhagavān, the time has come for the midday meal in my garden. {xxv}
{{milestone:{label:10.45,id:UT22084-055-001-1005}}}“I pray that you come, with your sons, to my garden.
You will benefit an assembly of many beings.
Just as Dīpaṃkara granted a prophecy to you,
Grant me likewise a direct prophecy in this world. {xxvi}
{{milestone:{label:10.46,id:UT22084-055-001-1006}}}“When I have heard that prophecy in this world,
I will also develop a vast and perfect aspiration, 
And all these beings will become buddhas. {{page:{number:64,id:UT22084-055-001-5897,folio:F.33.a}}}
There are no unworthy beings present here. {xxvii}
{{milestone:{label:10.47,id:UT22084-055-001-1007}}}“Arise, arise, Lord who has the ten strengths.
Benefit me and come to my garden.
Just as you come to my garden,
In that way I will go to the supreme tree of enlightenment. {xxviii}
{{milestone:{label:10.48,id:UT22084-055-001-1008}}}“When I have gone to the foot of the supreme tree of enlightenment,
I will remain there unshakable and unwavering.
I will defeat with love the māras and their claws,
And just as you attained it, I, too, will attain enlightenment.” {xxix}
{{milestone:{label:10.49,id:UT22084-055-001-1009}}}Then the Bhagavān, who had known what the youth Candraprabha would request, addressed these lines of verse to him: 
{{milestone:{label:10.50,id:UT22084-055-001-1010}}}“Arise Candraprabha, son of the jinas!
Arise, you who are joyful in generosity, you supreme being!
Arise, you who have compassion and firm conduct!
Let us go to the meal!{{note:{index414,id:UT22084-055-001-1011}}} Let us proceed{{note:{index415,id:UT22084-055-001-1012}}} to your home.” {xxx}
{{milestone:{label:10.51,id:UT22084-055-001-1013}}}After speaking these lines,{{note:{index416,id:UT22084-055-001-1014}}} the Bhagavān arose from his seat. He put on his lower robe, picked up his Dharma robe and alms bowl, and with the great saṅgha of a hundred thousand bhikṣus, and accompanied by a multitude of bodhisattva mahāsattvas, he proceeded. Many hundreds of thousands of devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, rishis, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, kumbhāṇḍas, pretas, pūtanas,{{note:{index417,id:UT22084-055-001-1015}}} humans, and nonhumans made offerings to him and praised him. Through his great buddha powers, his great buddha miracles, his great buddha manifestations, and his buddha conduct he radiated many quintillions{{note:{index418,id:UT22084-055-001-1016}}} of light rays. He emanated flocks of melodious, soft, and beautiful birds of many different shapes and colors, such as geese, cranes, ruddy shelducks, swans, partridges, peacocks, rollers,{{note:{index419,id:UT22084-055-001-1017}}} parrots,{{note:{index420,id:UT22084-055-001-1018}}} mynas, cuckoos, avadavats,{{note:{index421,id:UT22084-055-001-1019}}} and snipe, so that like devas in the sky, each with its own song, they emitted the sound of music.{{note:{index422,id:UT22084-055-001-1020}}}{{page:{number:65,id:UT22084-055-001-5898,folio:F.33.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:10.52,id:UT22084-055-001-1021}}}The yakṣa lords Surūpa, Indraketu, Vikaṭa, Bakula, Pāñcika, Śākyavardhana, and many quintillions of yakṣa lords holding pestles{{note:{index423,id:UT22084-055-001-1022}}} with both hands, offered many quintillions of huge, vast censers made of various divine precious materials, with handles of beryl, sapphire, crystal, and white coral, filled with uragasāra sandalwood, gośīrṣa sandalwood, vetiver, yellow sandalwood, Malaya sandalwood, red sandalwood, agarwood, and so on, and from which smoke flowed.
{{milestone:{label:10.53,id:UT22084-055-001-1023}}}There were the superior kings of great power, renowned as having great power, from their own regions, accompanied by many divisions of perfectly adorned horses and elephants being led without their riders, chariots, and infantry,{{note:{index424,id:UT22084-055-001-1024}}} in lines marching in front, holding in their hands many streamers and precious garlands. The horses and elephants, even though they were being led along without riders, were proceeding magnificently and emitting beautiful cries.
{{milestone:{label:10.54,id:UT22084-055-001-1025}}}The Bhagavān was accompanied on his right-hand side by Brahmā, who was making offerings to him and attending upon him, and on his left-hand side by Śakra, lord of the devas, and by countless devas with great power, who were renowned for their great power, who were mighty and illustrious, and whose bodies were adorned by excellent divine crowns, ornamented anklets, earrings, bracelets, flowers on their ears, bejeweled necklaces, and flower garlands. Their forms were made visible and they were holding coral tree flowers, asters, orchids, hibiscus, amaranths, magnolias, karnikara flowers, aśoka flowers,{{note:{index425,id:UT22084-055-001-1026}}} bignonias, kachnar flowers, blue lotuses, medlar flowers,{{note:{index426,id:UT22084-055-001-1027}}}sambac jasmine, star jasmine, ironwood flowers, red lotuses, night lotuses, white lotuses, water lilies, precious garlands, precious agarwood, and precious fruit. They were playing hundreds of thousands of different kinds of musical instruments, waving millions of pieces of cloth, crying out, “Ha! Ha! Ha!” and sending down a great rain of flowers. In order to make offerings to the Bhagavān they filled the entire sky without leaving any space {{page:{number:66,id:UT22084-055-001-5899,folio:F.34.a}}} and sent down a great rain of flowers, incense, garlands, perfumes, powders, and jewels.
{{milestone:{label:10.55,id:UT22084-055-001-1028}}}The Bhagavān entered at midday the great city of Rājagṛha through the hot springs gateway. The nature of this is described in these verses:{{note:{index427,id:UT22084-055-001-1029}}}
{{milestone:{label:10.56,id:UT22084-055-001-1030}}}The Tathāgata Buddha, knowing it was time,
That hero adorned with all qualities,
Who illuminates countless realms,
The Bhagavān, the lion of men, set forth. {xxxi}
{{milestone:{label:10.57,id:UT22084-055-001-1031}}}Avalokiteśvara, Mahā­sthāma­prāpta,{{note:{index428,id:UT22084-055-001-1032}}} and Amoghadarśin;{{note:{index429,id:UT22084-055-001-1033}}}
Gandhahasti, Ratnakusuma,{{note:{index430,id:UT22084-055-001-1034}}} and Ratnabāhu;{{note:{index431,id:UT22084-055-001-1035}}}
And Ratnaketu, Durabhisambhava,{{note:{index432,id:UT22084-055-001-1036}}} Vīrasena,{{note:{index433,id:UT22084-055-001-1037}}}
And others followed in the Jina’s footsteps.{{note:{index434,id:UT22084-055-001-1038}}} {xxxii} 
{{milestone:{label:10.58,id:UT22084-055-001-1039}}}On his right was Ajita, who is named Maitraka,{{note:{index435,id:UT22084-055-001-1040}}}
Who has the wealth of infinite qualities,
Who will become the following buddha
And has completed the accumulation of merit and wisdom. {xxxiii}
{{milestone:{label:10.59,id:UT22084-055-001-1041}}}He is one who has cultivated{{note:{index436,id:UT22084-055-001-1042}}} love, rejoicing, and equanimity.
He is a great being of the Dharma who has developed compassion.
He understands the infinite qualities, the qualities of the Lord of sages.{{note:{index437,id:UT22084-055-001-1043}}} {xxxiv} 
{{milestone:{label:10.60,id:UT22084-055-001-1044}}}He followed behind{{note:{index438,id:UT22084-055-001-1045}}} the compassionate Sugata
And was followed by those{{note:{index439,id:UT22084-055-001-1046}}} who will be
Those with great realization in the Good Eon: 
The thousand buddhas less four, {xxxv}
{{milestone:{label:10.61,id:UT22084-055-001-1047}}}Who were preceded by Maitraka.
And also he who in the past, in this city of Rājagṛha,
While born in divine bodies that were like beautiful moonlight,
Made infinite offerings to jinas throughout eons, {xxxvi}
{{milestone:{label:10.62,id:UT22084-055-001-1048}}}That hero Candraprabha was also present at the front.
To the left of the one with supreme compassion
Was Mañjuśrī,{{note:{index440,id:UT22084-055-001-1049}}} along with many thousands of millions{{note:{index441,id:UT22084-055-001-1050}}}
Of heroes who have sublime qualities of miraculous powers,{{note:{index442,id:UT22084-055-001-1051}}} {xxxvii} 
{{milestone:{label:10.63,id:UT22084-055-001-1052}}}Who traveled to endless hundreds of realms.
Following him were those in the śrāvaka saṅgha:
Śārisuta,{{note:{index443,id:UT22084-055-001-1053}}} Maudgalyāyana,{{note:{index444,id:UT22084-055-001-1054}}} Kāla,
Kāśyapa, Subhūti, Nanda, and Kapphiṇa; {xxxviii}
{{milestone:{label:10.64,id:UT22084-055-001-1055}}}Bhadrikarāja,{{note:{index445,id:UT22084-055-001-1056}}} and similarly Kauṇḍinya;
Ānanda, and similarly Sthavira Rāhula;
And Svāgata, Kañcika,{{note:{index446,id:UT22084-055-001-1057}}} Pūrṇa, Udāyin,
Revata, Kauṣṭhila,{{note:{index447,id:UT22084-055-001-1058}}} Upāli, and Aniruddha. {xxxix}
{{milestone:{label:10.65,id:UT22084-055-001-1059}}}A full nine thousand{{note:{index448,id:UT22084-055-001-1060}}} of those with matted hair {{page:{number:67,id:UT22084-055-001-5900,folio:F.34.b}}}
Followed behind the śrāvaka saṅgha.
They were all mighty ascetics who knew the Vedas and the rituals,{{note:{index449,id:UT22084-055-001-1061}}}
And had mastered curses, renunciation, and beneficial incantations.{{note:{index450,id:UT22084-055-001-1062}}} {xl} 
{{milestone:{label:10.66,id:UT22084-055-001-1063}}}Self-controlled rishis with peaceful minds, 
With disciplined minds, bowing with palms together,
Followed behind the Buddha, the lamp of the world,
The lion of men, endowed with compassion, {xli}
{{milestone:{label:10.67,id:UT22084-055-001-1064}}}The liberator of thousands of beings, as he proceeded. 
Like the completely pure lord of the host of stars, 
The full moon of the last month of autumn,{{note:{index451,id:UT22084-055-001-1065}}}
The Teacher who is without equal was encircled {xlii}
{{milestone:{label:10.68,id:UT22084-055-001-1066}}}By many hundred thousands of Brahmās.
As he stepped on the threshold of the city’s gateway,
The earth and its thick forests shook.
The devas, asuras,{{note:{index452,id:UT22084-055-001-1067}}} and mahoragas {xliii}
{{milestone:{label:10.69,id:UT22084-055-001-1068}}}Scattered excellent flowers and supreme incense.{{note:{index453,id:UT22084-055-001-1069}}} {xliv} 
{{milestone:{label:10.70,id:UT22084-055-001-1070}}}The moment the Bhagavān placed his right foot, adorned by a precious wheel from the accumulation of countless roots of merit, upon the threshold of the gate, this universe of a thousand million worlds shook in six ways. It trembled, trembled strongly, and trembled intensely; it quivered, quivered strongly, and quivered intensely; it shook, shook strongly, and shook intensely; it shuddered, shuddered strongly, and shuddered intensely; it quaked, quaked strongly, and quaked intensely; the east sank and the west rose, the west sank and the east rose, the north sank and the south rose, the south sank and the north rose, the perimeter sank and the center rose, and the center sank and the perimeter rose. A great radiance shone in the world, and countless, numberless other amazing, wonderful, miraculous manifestations appeared.{{note:{index454,id:UT22084-055-001-1071}}}
The nature of this is described in these verses:
{{milestone:{label:10.71,id:UT22084-055-001-1073}}}When the Guide came to that supreme city
And placed his supreme foot upon the gateway’s threshold,
That magnificence caused this earth to shake,
And the beings in this supreme city were overjoyed. {1}
{{milestone:{label:10.72,id:UT22084-055-001-1074}}}When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold
The people who were hungry and thirsty {{page:{number:68,id:UT22084-055-001-5901,folio:F.35.a}}}
At that time became free of the need to eat or drink.
They became free of hunger and thirst. {2}
{{milestone:{label:10.73,id:UT22084-055-001-1075}}}When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold
All those people who were blind,
Deaf, and had no protector and little merit
Were all able to see and hear. {3}
{{milestone:{label:10.74,id:UT22084-055-001-1076}}}When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold
All the pretas in the realm of Yama,
Suffering greatly and eating snot and spit,
Were touched by light and became happy. {4}
{{milestone:{label:10.75,id:UT22084-055-001-1077}}}When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold
The supreme trees—the sal and the karnikara—
At the summit of crags and on mountaintops, 
They all bowed toward the Buddha. {5}
{{milestone:{label:10.76,id:UT22084-055-001-1078}}}When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold
The entire ground shook in six ways
Throughout the villages and towns as far as the ocean,
Without causing harm to anyone. {6}
{{milestone:{label:10.77,id:UT22084-055-001-1079}}}Devas, humans, kumbhāṇḍas, and rākṣasas—
Wherever beings lived, there was happiness and joy.
They developed faith in supreme, sublime enlightenment
And held a parasol for the guide of the world. {7}
{{milestone:{label:10.78,id:UT22084-055-001-1080}}}When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold,
Thousands of musical instruments sounded without being played;
Hearing the beautiful sound of music,
All beings were filled with joy. {8}
{{milestone:{label:10.79,id:UT22084-055-001-1081}}}Hundreds of thousands of trees bowed down,
And all flowers blossomed at that time.
Hundreds of thousands of devas in the sky
Made nonhuman offerings to the Jina. {9}
{{milestone:{label:10.80,id:UT22084-055-001-1082}}}When the Jina placed his foot on the gateway’s threshold,
Hundreds{{note:{index455,id:UT22084-055-001-1083}}} of bulls{{note:{index456,id:UT22084-055-001-1084}}} lowed with joy.
The kings of horses and elephants{{note:{index457,id:UT22084-055-001-1085}}} raised their bodies;
The lions, the kings of animals, roared. {10}
{{milestone:{label:10.81,id:UT22084-055-001-1086}}}The kings, the rulers, however many there were,
Came from the cardinal and intermediate directions.
When they saw the glorious majesty of the Jina,
With minds filled with joy they bowed to him. {11}
{{milestone:{label:10.82,id:UT22084-055-001-1087}}}Some praised the Lord of the World;
Some scattered a rain of flowers on the Jina;
Some placed their ten fingers together in homage,
And they cried, “Oh, the Jina, compassionate one!” {12}
{{milestone:{label:10.83,id:UT22084-055-001-1088}}}Some scattered excellent strings of pearls {{page:{number:69,id:UT22084-055-001-5902,folio:F.35.b}}}
And various ornaments that give rise to joy,
And some scattered clothing and jewels.
They developed the supreme, unequaled aspiration to enlightenment. {13}
{{milestone:{label:10.84,id:UT22084-055-001-1089}}}Some scattered excellent meshes of gold;
Some also scattered mukhaphullaka adornments. 
Some scattered excellent ornaments of gold,
And some, likewise, scattered anklets.{{note:{index458,id:UT22084-055-001-1090}}} {14} 
{{milestone:{label:10.85,id:UT22084-055-001-1091}}}Some scattered excellent bracelets,{{note:{index459,id:UT22084-055-001-1092}}}
Some scattered armlets inset with jewels,
And some aspired to enlightenment, scattering excellent 
Pieces of cloth,{{note:{index460,id:UT22084-055-001-1093}}} saying, “May we become buddhas!” {15}
{{milestone:{label:10.86,id:UT22084-055-001-1094}}}When the Lord of the World stood in the gateway,
Some people scattered golden necklaces.
Some with minds filled with faith scattered excellent crest jewels;{{note:{index461,id:UT22084-055-001-1095}}}
Some scattered networks of jewels. {16}
{{milestone:{label:10.87,id:UT22084-055-001-1096}}}Those beings who were in extreme suffering,
Tormented by many kinds of miseries,
All attained happiness through the majesty
Of the Guide, the supreme human. {17}
{{milestone:{label:10.88,id:UT22084-055-001-1097}}}Cuckoos, mynas, and peacocks,
And similarly cranes and other water birds{{note:{index462,id:UT22084-055-001-1098}}}—
All the flocks of birds were in the sky
Emitting their beautiful, perfect songs. {18}
{{milestone:{label:10.89,id:UT22084-055-001-1099}}}Desire, anger, and ignorance 
Ceased in whoever heard 
The sweet, beautiful songs
Of those flocks of joyous birds. {19}
{{milestone:{label:10.90,id:UT22084-055-001-1100}}}The millions of beings who heard that joyful sound
All attained the patience that is concordant with the Dharma.
The Sugata gave them all this prophecy:
“You will in the future become buddhas.” {20}
{{milestone:{label:10.91,id:UT22084-055-001-1101}}}At that time the kleśas did not arise, 
And everyone was respectful to the Dharma king.{{note:{index463,id:UT22084-055-001-1102}}} {21} 
{{milestone:{label:10.92,id:UT22084-055-001-1103}}}At that time, when they saw the form of the Guide’s body,{{note:{index464,id:UT22084-055-001-1104}}}
They developed the aspiration for the supreme wisdom of buddhahood.
They wondered, “When will we attain this kind of wisdom?”
And the Jina, knowing that, gave them their prophecies. {22}
{{milestone:{label:10.93,id:UT22084-055-001-1105}}}From each pore of the Sugata
There shone hundreds of thousands of light rays
And more, as many as there are sand grains in the Ganges—
It would not be possible to perceive all their attributes. {23}
{{milestone:{label:10.94,id:UT22084-055-001-1106}}}At that time, the sunlight did not shine. 
Nor was there light from jewels, fire, or the devas. {{page:{number:70,id:UT22084-055-001-5903,folio:F.36.a}}}
There was no other light at that time 
When there was the splendor of the Buddha entering the city. {24}
{{milestone:{label:10.95,id:UT22084-055-001-1107}}}When with that great assembly the Sugata proceeded on the path,
Wherever the feet of the one with the ten strengths trod
There appeared from the ground a hundred thousand lotuses
That were pure and had ten thousand million petals. {25}
{{milestone:{label:10.96,id:UT22084-055-001-1108}}}When the Guide entered the supreme city,
At that time there was no dirt or refuse.
Throughout the entire city there arose
The lovely aroma of the most fragrant incense. {26}
{{milestone:{label:10.97,id:UT22084-055-001-1109}}}The entire city and its streets were purified.
They had no stones or gravel and were sprinkled with perfume
And bestrewn with the petals of various kinds of flowers.
That is the kind of merit the one with ten strengths had. {27}
{{milestone:{label:10.98,id:UT22084-055-001-1110}}}When a hundred thousand yakṣas with ferocious minds
Saw the Buddha, the Lord of men who was like gold,
They felt an immense love for the Guide
And took refuge in the Buddha, Dharma, and Saṅgha. {28}
{{milestone:{label:10.99,id:UT22084-055-001-1111}}}All of the million millions{{note:{index465,id:UT22084-055-001-1112}}} of devas
Who had come to see the Lord of men{{note:{index466,id:UT22084-055-001-1113}}}
Let fall a rain of flowers on the Sugata.
They scattered flowers while in the middle of the sky. {29}
{{milestone:{label:10.100,id:UT22084-055-001-1114}}}The flowers scattered by humans for the Jina
Formed a parasol of flowers in the sky.
The flowers scattered by the devas
Were strewn on the ground as divine flowers. {30}
{{milestone:{label:10.101,id:UT22084-055-001-1115}}}The devas, humans, kumbhāṇḍas, and rākṣasas 
Never tired of gazing upon him.
When they saw the Lord{{note:{index467,id:UT22084-055-001-1116}}} with the ten strengths,
They were overjoyed and felt the highest delight. {31} 
{{milestone:{label:10.102,id:UT22084-055-001-1117}}}When they saw the body of the supreme being,
All beings were overjoyed and delighted;
They did not even think of the divine flowers,
Which did not seem at all wonderful.{{note:{index468,id:UT22084-055-001-1118}}} {32} 
{{milestone:{label:10.103,id:UT22084-055-001-1119}}}Brahmā upon the right of the one with ten strengths,
Śakra, the king of the devas, on his left, 
And the many millions of deities in the middle of the sky
Showed great veneration to the supreme being. {33}
{{milestone:{label:10.104,id:UT22084-055-001-1120}}}Devas and asuras encircled the Jina,
Who eclipsed all the majesty of devas and humans.
With the soles of his feet making patterns on the ground, 
The invited Bhagavān entered into the city. {34}
{{milestone:{label:10.105,id:UT22084-055-001-1121}}}His body was beautified by excellent primary signs,
Like the firmament filled with stars. {{page:{number:71,id:UT22084-055-001-5904,folio:F.36.b}}}
The Buddha shone upon the king’s road{{note:{index469,id:UT22084-055-001-1122}}}
Like the full moon in the sky. {35}
{{milestone:{label:10.106,id:UT22084-055-001-1123}}}Just as an excellent, pure, precious jewel
That is free of all impurities shines
So that a pure light goes in all directions,{{note:{index470,id:UT22084-055-001-1124}}}
In that way the Jina illuminated the entire world. {36}
{{milestone:{label:10.107,id:UT22084-055-001-1125}}}Devas and asuras encircled the Jina.
The supreme human who entered Rājagṛha
With the soles of his feet leaving patterns on the ground,
The Buddha, came to the home of the youth Candraprabha. {37}
{{milestone:{label:10.108,id:UT22084-055-001-1126}}}The supreme city was perfectly adorned,
Millions of banners had been erected,
The entire ground was anointed with the best perfumes,
And beautiful summer flowers were scattered. {38}
{{milestone:{label:10.109,id:UT22084-055-001-1127}}}When the Sugata spoke to teach
With compassion for the people in the streets,
The Jina manifested emanations
That taught to them the excellent Dharma of the Buddha. {39}
{{milestone:{label:10.110,id:UT22084-055-001-1128}}}[The Jina manifested emanations;
Bodies that were like gold were manifested. 
The Buddha, the Jina, through his emanations, 
Remained in emptiness, peace, the enlightenment of buddhahood.]{{note:{index471,id:UT22084-055-001-1129}}} {40} 
{{milestone:{label:10.111,id:UT22084-055-001-1130}}}When the hundreds of thousands of beings heard that,
They prayed for the supreme wisdom of the Buddha,
Wondering, “When will I attain this kind of wisdom?”
Knowing their thoughts, the Jina prophesied to them. {{note:{index472,id:UT22084-055-001-1131}}}{41} 
{{milestone:{label:10.112,id:UT22084-055-001-1132}}}There were those who aspired to attain
That inconceivable supreme attainment.
They had invited the Jina, the Lord of men,
And there was no limit to the offerings they made. {{note:{index473,id:UT22084-055-001-1133}}} {42} 
{{milestone:{label:10.113,id:UT22084-055-001-1134}}}There were those who developed an excellent aspiration,
Thinking, “I will tomorrow invite the compassionate one,
He who wishes to benefit beings, 
Whom it is difficult to see in saṃsāra.”{{note:{index474,id:UT22084-055-001-1135}}} {43} 
{{milestone:{label:10.114,id:UT22084-055-001-1136}}}Some who were upon the roofs
Developed the sublime, supreme aspiration to enlightenment
And they scattered divine flowers on the handsome, 
Beautifully adorned body of the one with the ten strengths. {44} 
{{milestone:{label:10.115,id:UT22084-055-001-1137}}}Some developed the supreme, highest aspiration
And scattered garlands of magnolias, 
Kachnar flowers, the scents of summer,
And wreaths of silken ribbons. {45}
{{milestone:{label:10.116,id:UT22084-055-001-1138}}}Some stood, holding excellent flowers,

They held various flowers and wreaths of silk
That they cast in the direction of the Jina with great power.{{note:{index475,id:UT22084-055-001-1139}}} {46} 
{{milestone:{label:10.117,id:UT22084-055-001-1140}}}Some scattered red lotuses, night lotuses,

Some scattered precious flowers,{{note:{index476,id:UT22084-055-001-1141}}}
And some scattered sandalwood powder. {47}
{{milestone:{label:10.118,id:UT22084-055-001-1142}}}When the Guide entered the supreme city
The wonders that appeared were uncountable,
Unequaled, impossible to describe,
And they brought many millions of beings to buddha wisdom. {48}
{{milestone:{label:10.119,id:UT22084-055-001-1143}}}Those in Avṛha, Atapa, who had seen the truth,
The devas of Sudṛśa and Sudarśana,
And those in Akaniṣṭha, who are free of desire—
They all came to see the Lord of humans. {49}
{{milestone:{label:10.120,id:UT22084-055-001-1144}}}Similarly, countless Parī­ttaśubha{{note:{index477,id:UT22084-055-001-1145}}} devas,

{{milestone:{label:10.121,id:UT22084-055-001-1147}}}Countless Apramāṇābha devas,

Came to see the Lord of the World.{{note:{index479,id:UT22084-055-001-1148}}} {51} 
{{milestone:{label:10.122,id:UT22084-055-001-1149}}}Many hundreds of thousands of Brahmā’s entourage,{{note:{index480,id:UT22084-055-001-1150}}}

{{milestone:{label:10.123,id:UT22084-055-001-1151}}}Also the Para­nirmita­vaśa­vartin{{note:{index481,id:UT22084-055-001-1152}}} devas,

{{milestone:{label:10.124,id:UT22084-055-001-1153}}}Śakra, king of the devas, and the Trāyastriṃśa{{note:{index482,id:UT22084-055-001-1154}}} devas {{note:{index483,id:UT22084-055-001-1155}}}

{{milestone:{label:10.125,id:UT22084-055-001-1156}}}Also the world guardians of the four directions

{{milestone:{label:10.126,id:UT22084-055-001-1158}}}Ailavila, the powerful king of the yakṣas,

They sent down a rain of numerous various flowers. {56}
{{milestone:{label:10.127,id:UT22084-055-001-1159}}}Also the Sadāmatta{{note:{index485,id:UT22084-055-001-1160}}} and Mālādhāra devas,

{{milestone:{label:10.130,id:UT22084-055-001-1163}}}Śambara, Bala, Vemacitra, and Rāhu,

{{milestone:{label:10.132,id:UT22084-055-001-1166}}}The nāga king Girivalgu,

{{milestone:{label:10.133,id:UT22084-055-001-1168}}}The nāga lords Padma and Mahāpadma,

{{milestone:{label:10.134,id:UT22084-055-001-1170}}}The nāga king Maṇi, filled with joy,

{{milestone:{label:10.135,id:UT22084-055-001-1171}}}Also the nāga king Anavatapta,

Came and made offerings there to the Lord of the World. {62}
{{milestone:{label:10.136,id:UT22084-055-001-1172}}}The five hundred sons of Anavatapta,
Encircled by their kindred and filled with joy,
Seeking the highest, vast wisdom,

{{milestone:{label:10.137,id:UT22084-055-001-1173}}}Similarly, the nāga king Apalāla,
Palms together, bowed to the supreme individual

{{milestone:{label:10.138,id:UT22084-055-001-1174}}}Similarly, the nāga king Mucilinda,

Holding various jewels and pearls, {{page:{number:74,id:UT22084-055-001-5907,folio:F.38.a}}}

{{milestone:{label:10.139,id:UT22084-055-001-1175}}}Similarly, the nāga king Kālika
Came before the Tathāgata.

{{milestone:{label:10.140,id:UT22084-055-001-1177}}}He{{note:{index490,id:UT22084-055-001-1178}}} felt great veneration as he thought
Of the qualities of the Tathāgata. 
Encircled by his many nāga kindred,
He recited many praises of the Guide. {67}
{{milestone:{label:10.141,id:UT22084-055-001-1179}}}Similarly, the nāga kings Nanda and Upananda—
Similarly, also, Takṣaka and Kṛṣṇagautama—
Came there gazing upon the Jina
And bowed down to the Sugata’s feet. {68}
{{milestone:{label:10.142,id:UT22084-055-001-1180}}}The nāga king Elapatra
Came weeping, encircled by a hundred nāgas.
He remembered the supreme sage Jina Kāśyapa
And saw what an unfavorable rebirth he himself had obtained. {69} 
{{milestone:{label:10.143,id:UT22084-055-001-1181}}}“Alas! I had doubts in the past.
In the past I cut down an elapatra{{note:{index491,id:UT22084-055-001-1182}}} bush,{{note:{index492,id:UT22084-055-001-1183}}}
And therefore I obtained this unfavorable rebirth.
It is not easy to know the Dharma of the Jina. {70}
{{milestone:{label:10.144,id:UT22084-055-001-1184}}}“I forsake this rebirth into a nāgī’s womb,
And this birth in an extremely detestable body.
I will realize the Dharma, the state of peace,
That the best of men realized in the Bodhimaṇḍa.” {71}
{{milestone:{label:10.145,id:UT22084-055-001-1185}}}Sāgara, the nāga cakravartin king, 
Accompanied by an entourage of thirty million nāgas,

Came in order to make offerings to the Bhagavān.{{note:{index493,id:UT22084-055-001-1186}}} {72} 
{{milestone:{label:10.146,id:UT22084-055-001-1187}}}The yakṣa of Rājagṛha who caught

{{milestone:{label:10.147,id:UT22084-055-001-1188}}}The entire domain of the king of Alakavatī{{note:{index494,id:UT22084-055-001-1189}}}

{{milestone:{label:10.148,id:UT22084-055-001-1190}}}In the same way, Kharakarṇa and Sūciromā,
The terrifying yakṣas of the forests,
And the yakṣa Gardabhaka, who lives in the snow mountains,
Had come into the presence of the self-arisen Jina.{{note:{index495,id:UT22084-055-001-1191}}} {75} 
{{milestone:{label:10.149,id:UT22084-055-001-1192}}}Indraketu, Vikaṭa, and Surūpa,

{{milestone:{label:10.150,id:UT22084-055-001-1195}}}Many with ugly, misshapen bodies,

{{milestone:{label:10.151,id:UT22084-055-001-1196}}}Gautama, Rishi Bṛhaspati, and Jahnu,

{{milestone:{label:10.152,id:UT22084-055-001-1197}}}And similarly, there were the joyous and enraptured Nārada,

{{milestone:{label:10.153,id:UT22084-055-001-1198}}}Jaimini, Vāmana,{{note:{index498,id:UT22084-055-001-1199}}} and Vaiśampāyana,

{{milestone:{label:10.154,id:UT22084-055-001-1200}}}When they saw the Rishi, the rishis were overjoyed

{{milestone:{label:10.155,id:UT22084-055-001-1201}}}The entire multitude of rishis in the world

{{milestone:{label:10.156,id:UT22084-055-001-1202}}}The garuḍas that live at the ocean’s shore

{{milestone:{label:10.157,id:UT22084-055-001-1203}}}All of the devas that dwell in Jambudvīpa,

{{milestone:{label:10.158,id:UT22084-055-001-1204}}}The countless devas of the forests

{{milestone:{label:10.159,id:UT22084-055-001-1206}}}The hundreds of devas of desert wildernesses,
All the devas of mountain peaks,

{{milestone:{label:10.160,id:UT22084-055-001-1207}}}Assemblies of devas, asuras, and nāgas,

{{milestone:{label:10.161,id:UT22084-055-001-1208}}}They made offerings to the supreme Jina
When the Guide entered the supreme city.
The kings of the devas, asuras, nāgas, and yakṣas
Could not get their fill of looking at him. {83}
{{milestone:{label:10.162,id:UT22084-055-001-1209}}}In previous existences the Lord of the World
Had made perfect offerings to the jinas of the past.
This was the ripened result of that merit.
The beings could not stop looking at the Lord of humans. {84}
{{milestone:{label:10.163,id:UT22084-055-001-1210}}}When the Jina shone light through the buddha realm,
Meru, and similarly Sumeru and Cakravāla 
The Himagiri and Gandhamādana
Could not obscure the Jina’s light. {85}
{{milestone:{label:10.164,id:UT22084-055-001-1211}}}All of the oceans in this buddha realm
At that time all became land,
And the entirety of this buddha realm
Became equally scattered with flowers. {86}
{{milestone:{label:10.165,id:UT22084-055-001-1212}}}Countless hundreds of thousands of light rays
Came from the soles of the King of Dharma’s feet.
All the beings in the hells were cooled
And, freed from suffering, experienced happiness. {87}
{{milestone:{label:10.166,id:UT22084-055-001-1213}}}The one with the ten strengths taught the Dharma
So that the sight of devas and humans was purified.
Countless hundreds of thousands of beings
All gained certainty in the Buddha’s wisdom. {88} 
{{milestone:{label:10.167,id:UT22084-055-001-1214}}}The numerous miracles manifested by the Sugata
Could not easily be described in ten million eons.
When the Guide entered the supreme city
All beings rejoiced at the Jina, the Sugata.{{note:{index500,id:UT22084-055-001-1215}}} {89} 
{{milestone:{label:10.168,id:UT22084-055-001-1216}}}These qualities of the Sugata are immeasurable.
They are the supreme human’s perfection of qualities.
They have transcended all unique qualities.
Bow your heads to the realm of the Buddha’s merit! {90}
{{milestone:{label:10.169,id:UT22084-055-001-1217}}}Conclusion of the tenth chapter, “The Entry into the City.”
{{milestone:{label:11,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-11}}}Becoming a Keeper of the Sūtra
Chapter 11
{{milestone:{label:11.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1218}}}The Bhagavān came to the street on which was the home of the youth Candraprabha, and soon arrived at the home of the youth Candraprabha. Once he had arrived, he sat on the seat prepared for him. The saṅgha of bodhisattvas and the saṅgha of bhikṣus also sat on the appropriate seats that had been arranged for each of them. 
{{milestone:{label:11.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1219}}}Then the youth Candraprabha, knowing that the Bhagavān, the saṅgha of bodhisattvas, and the saṅgha of bhikṣus were seated, {{page:{number:77,id:UT22084-055-001-5910,folio:F.39.b}}} himself presented and served a series of great offerings: numerous excellent foods, with hundreds of flavors to savor as they chewed, licked, sucked, and drank.
{{milestone:{label:11.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1220}}}When he saw that the Bhagavān had concluded his meal, which was signaled by his setting down his alms bowl,{{note:{index501,id:UT22084-055-001-1221}}} he offered for the Bhagavān’s body two lengths of cloth{{note:{index502,id:UT22084-055-001-1222}}} of the value of a trillion silver coins,{{note:{index503,id:UT22084-055-001-1223}}} and also to each of the bodhisattvas, and he offered three dharma robes to each one in the saṅgha of bhikṣus.
{{milestone:{label:11.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1224}}}Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder and, casting toward the Bhagavān a divine coral tree flower, he made offerings and uttered praises. Then, his palms placed together, he bowed toward the Bhagavān and praised him with these appropriate verses:{{note:{index504,id:UT22084-055-001-1225}}}
{{milestone:{label:11.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1226}}}“You are unborn and unceasing;
Without a body, inconceivable,
You have the perfect body and primary signs.
I pay homage to you who are an ocean of qualities. {i}
{{milestone:{label:11.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1227}}}“You are a hero who has been born from wisdom.
You possess the power of methods and strengths.
You are a buddha who is the same as space.
I pay homage to you who have perfected patience. {ii}
{{milestone:{label:11.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1228}}}“Your conduct is to remain in constant mindfulness.
The Tathāgata’s bed is joy and happiness.
Your drink is samādhi and your food is supreme dhyāna.
I pay homage to you who reside in the solitude of emptiness. {iii}
{{milestone:{label:11.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1229}}}“O Inconceivable Buddha,
The Guide for the whole world!
When the beings of this world make offerings to you
They advance toward supreme nirvāṇa.” {iv}
{{milestone:{label:11.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1230}}}Thus did he praise the one unequaled Lord, and then the youth said, with a joyous mind, “Unequaled Buddha, who has an inconceivable body, you have consumed the meal. Through this may I also become a buddha like you, the god of gods!” {{page:{number:78,id:UT22084-055-001-5911,folio:F.40.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:11.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1231}}}In that way, therefore, the youth Candraprabha provided divine food with a hundred flavors to the Bhagavān. He offered divine coral tree flowers to the Bhagavān, and praised him with appropriate verses.
{{milestone:{label:11.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1232}}}Now, placing his palms together in homage toward the Bhagavān, in his mind he addressed him with these verses: 
{{milestone:{label:11.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1233}}}“Whatever the wise bodhisattvas do,
They always follow the nature of the Dharma.
I pray to the Guide to teach what actions are performed
When those with wisdom engage in actions. {1}
{{milestone:{label:11.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1234}}}“In what way, Guide, are past lives remembered?
In what way is rebirth in a womb avoided?
In what way does the community not become divided?
In what way does one gain endless eloquence? {2}
{{milestone:{label:11.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1235}}}“You know the activities of all beings.
You have the knowledge of all phenomena.
You are the invincible, supreme human.
I have asked my questions; give me your elucidation. {3}
{{milestone:{label:11.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1236}}}“You know that nonexistence is the nature of phenomena;
You put into words that which cannot be described.
Just as a lion overpowers all jackals,{{note:{index505,id:UT22084-055-001-1237}}}
That is how the Buddha overpowers the tīrthikas. {4}
{{milestone:{label:11.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1238}}}“You know the conduct of all beings.
You have the wisdom of all phenomena.
You have wisdom without attachment, and activity that is pure.
Lord of the Dharma, elucidate those for me. {5}
{{milestone:{label:11.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1239}}}“You know the past and also the future.
You also know what is happening in the present.
You have unimpeded knowledge of the three times.
Therefore I have asked you my questions, lion of the Śākyas. {6}
{{milestone:{label:11.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1240}}}“You, Dharma king, know the true nature
That is the nature of the jinas of the three times.
You are skilled in the nature of phenomena, self-arisen one.
Therefore, ocean of wisdom, I have asked you my questions. {7}
{{milestone:{label:11.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1241}}}“You do not have any quality of error.
Therefore you have a mind of complete elimination—
You have eliminated the fetters and the rigidity of ignorance.
Lord of humans, teach me the conduct of a bodhisattva. {8}
{{milestone:{label:11.20,id:UT22084-055-001-1242}}}“You, Jina, know the characteristics of phenomena.
Teach me the characteristics of phenomena. {{page:{number:79,id:UT22084-055-001-5912,folio:F.40.b}}}
When I have understood those characteristics of phenomena 
I shall practice the conduct of enlightenment that has those characteristics. {9}
{{milestone:{label:11.21,id:UT22084-055-001-1243}}}“The conduct of beings is infinitely different.
How do they engage in practicing their conduct?
Teach to me how conduct is engaged in 
So that from your words, I may know the conduct of beings. {10}
{{milestone:{label:11.22,id:UT22084-055-001-1244}}}“Different characteristics are characteristic of the nature of phenomena.
Their essence{{note:{index506,id:UT22084-055-001-1245}}} is empty and their nature{{note:{index507,id:UT22084-055-001-1246}}} is pure.
I pray that you teach me the way of phenomena
That a bodhisattva directly perceives. {11}
{{milestone:{label:11.23,id:UT22084-055-001-1247}}}“In this there is the perfect knowledge of all phenomena.
There is skill in all the words of the teaching.
There is no doubt; all doubt and uncertainty have been cut through.
Teach me the enlightenment of buddhahood.” {12}
{{milestone:{label:11.24,id:UT22084-055-001-1248}}}The Bhagavān, knowing the thoughts that were in the mind of the youth Candraprabha, said to him, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas will attain all these qualities, and they will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, if they possess just one quality. What is that one quality? Young man, it is when the bodhisattva mahāsattvas know the nature of all phenomena. 
{{milestone:{label:11.25,id:UT22084-055-001-1249}}}“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas know the nature of all phenomena? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas know that all phenomena are nameless; they have no names. They know that all phenomena have no vocalization, they have no expression in speech, they have no letters, they have no birth, they have no cessation, they have no characteristics of cause, they have no characteristics of conditions,{{note:{index508,id:UT22084-055-001-1250}}} they are devoid of characteristics, they have the one characteristic of having no characteristics, they are devoid of attributes, they cannot be conceived of, they have no thought, and they have no mentality.” 
Then the Bhagavān taught this in the following verses:
{{milestone:{label:11.26,id:UT22084-055-001-1252}}}“The single teaching on phenomena
Is that phenomena have no characteristics.
That is the teaching of supreme wisdom
From having true, correct knowledge. {13} {{page:{number:80,id:UT22084-055-001-5913,folio:F.41.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:11.27,id:UT22084-055-001-1253}}}“The bodhisattvas who know
That teaching on phenomena
Will not cease from elucidation{{note:{index509,id:UT22084-055-001-1254}}}
Even though they teach ten million sūtras. {14}
{{milestone:{label:11.28,id:UT22084-055-001-1255}}}“Through the blessing of the Guide
The ultimate truth is known.
When the ultimate is known
There is nothing to be taught. {15}
{{milestone:{label:11.29,id:UT22084-055-001-1256}}}“Through one thing, everything is known.
Through one thing, everything is seen.
However much they teach 
They will not become proud. {16}
{{milestone:{label:11.30,id:UT22084-055-001-1257}}}“With their minds they have ascertained
The selflessness of all phenomena,
And as they are trained in teaching using terms,
They speak with words that are correct. {17}
{{milestone:{label:11.31,id:UT22084-055-001-1258}}}“Whatever sound they hear, 
They know its past.{{note:{index510,id:UT22084-055-001-1259}}}
Knowing the past{{note:{index511,id:UT22084-055-001-1260}}} of that sound 
They are not captivated{{note:{index512,id:UT22084-055-001-1261}}} by that sound. {18}
{{milestone:{label:11.32,id:UT22084-055-001-1262}}}“Just like the past{{note:{index513,id:UT22084-055-001-1263}}} of a sound,
So are the characteristics of phenomena.
Knowing phenomena to be like that
They will not be reborn in a womb. {19}
{{milestone:{label:11.33,id:UT22084-055-001-1264}}}“They know that all phenomena are unborn
And that they have no origin.
Knowing this teaching on birth{{note:{index514,id:UT22084-055-001-1265}}}
They always remember their previous lives. {20}
{{milestone:{label:11.34,id:UT22084-055-001-1266}}}“When they remember those lives
They perform their actions.
For those who perform those actions
Their community of followers remains united. {21}
{{milestone:{label:11.35,id:UT22084-055-001-1267}}}“The bodhisattvas who know
The emptiness of phenomena
Will never be without that knowledge.
It is the summit of nothingness. {22}
{{milestone:{label:11.36,id:UT22084-055-001-1268}}}“When the foolish think about
The summit of nothingness 
They continue in saṃsāra
For millions of eons. {23}
{{milestone:{label:11.37,id:UT22084-055-001-1269}}}“If they are able to understand it
Just as the Guide knows it,
Then they will have no suffering
And they will not go to the lower realms. {24}
{{milestone:{label:11.38,id:UT22084-055-001-1270}}}“All ordinary individuals
Are ignorant of this nature.
They reject this kind of Dharma 
That brings the cessation of suffering.{{note:{index515,id:UT22084-055-001-1271}}} {25} 
{{milestone:{label:11.39,id:UT22084-055-001-1272}}}“Phenomena are perceived when
No phenomena can be found.
Recognize that perception 
When that perception occurs. {26}
{{milestone:{label:11.40,id:UT22084-055-001-1273}}}“The foolish conceptualize
Through consciousness and perception. 
The wise do not become ignorant
In conceiving of phenomena. {27} {{page:{number:81,id:UT22084-055-001-5914,folio:F.41.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:11.41,id:UT22084-055-001-1274}}}“The unpolluted phenomena of emptiness
Are within the field of experience of the bodhisattvas.{{note:{index516,id:UT22084-055-001-1275}}}
This level of those who are wise
Is not within the field of experience of the foolish. {28}
{{milestone:{label:11.42,id:UT22084-055-001-1276}}}“This level of the bodhisattvas
Is that of bodhisattva practice.
It is the adornment of the Buddha’s Dharma.
It is the peace and emptiness that has been taught. {29}
{{milestone:{label:11.43,id:UT22084-055-001-1277}}}“When the bodhisattvas 
Eliminate their propensities
They remain in the family of the buddhas
And are not captured by form. {30}
{{milestone:{label:11.44,id:UT22084-055-001-1278}}}“All phenomena are without location;
They have no location that can be known.
For the one who knows this about their location,
Enlightenment is not difficult to attain. {31}
{{milestone:{label:11.45,id:UT22084-055-001-1279}}}“Generosity, conduct, learning, and patience,
And relying upon a good friend:{{note:{index517,id:UT22084-055-001-1280}}}
Those who know these activities
Will quickly attain enlightenment. {32}
{{milestone:{label:11.46,id:UT22084-055-001-1281}}}“Devas, nāgas, yakṣas, and asuras,
Mahoragas and gandharvas, will always honor them.
All the kings of the garuḍas, kinnaras, 
And rākṣasas {{note:{index518,id:UT22084-055-001-1282}}} will make offerings to them. {33}
{{milestone:{label:11.47,id:UT22084-055-001-1283}}}“Millions of buddhas will recite their praises
Continuously for many millions of eons.
It is not possible to reach the end
Of such praise for one who teaches this Dharma. {34}
{{milestone:{label:11.48,id:UT22084-055-001-1284}}}“The bodhisattvas who know emptiness
Benefit many millions of beings.
They kindly teach the Dharma to assemblies{{note:{index519,id:UT22084-055-001-1285}}}
And those who hear it are delighted and respectful.{35}
{{milestone:{label:11.49,id:UT22084-055-001-1286}}}“They gain vast knowledge
So that they see the supreme humans.
They see the beautiful display of their realms
And the lords of the worlds teach them the Dharma.{{note:{index520,id:UT22084-055-001-1287}}} {36} 
{{milestone:{label:11.50,id:UT22084-055-001-1288}}}“Know that all phenomena are like illusions;
Know that just as space is naturally empty,
Phenomena are also naturally like that.
In that way there will be no attachment in any kind of activity. {37}
{{milestone:{label:11.51,id:UT22084-055-001-1289}}}“With unimpeded wisdom, benefiting others,
Performing supreme bodhisattva conduct in the world,
With wisdom examining all phenomena,
They send emanations to other realms. {38}
{{milestone:{label:11.52,id:UT22084-055-001-1290}}}“Those emanations accomplish buddha activities.
They go naturally, just as is their nature.
The beings who remain in the aspiration to enlightenment {{page:{number:82,id:UT22084-055-001-5915,folio:F.42.a}}}
Will attain whatever goals they wish for. {39}
{{milestone:{label:11.53,id:UT22084-055-001-1291}}}“Those who are steadfastly within the buddha family 
Will always honor the buddhas.
Their bodies will shine brightly, 
Adorned by the thirty-two excellent signs. {40}
{{milestone:{label:11.54,id:UT22084-055-001-1292}}}“They will attain the conduct that is within the supreme samādhi
And an endless multitude of other benefits.
They will always have great, unshakable strength
And a majesty that outshines that of kings. {41}
{{milestone:{label:11.55,id:UT22084-055-001-1293}}}“The wise who practice the Buddha’s Dharma
Will have an excellent appearance and great beauty. 
Their merit and majesty and splendor will increase.
Their majesty will outshine even that of the devas. {42}
{{milestone:{label:11.56,id:UT22084-055-001-1294}}}“Those who steadfastly remain in the aspiration to enlightenment
Will always be friends to all beings.
There will never be any darkness 
In their teaching of the enlightenment of buddhahood. {43} 
{{milestone:{label:11.57,id:UT22084-055-001-1295}}}“The nature of phenomena is like that of space,
Inexpressible, beyond speech and words.
Those who know that supreme nature 
Will have an unceasing confidence in teaching. {44}
{{milestone:{label:11.58,id:UT22084-055-001-1296}}}“Even though they teach a hundred thousand sūtras,
They know the finest details of the past.
The wise will always have unimpeded speech,
Knowing the subtlety of the nature of phenomena. {45}
{{milestone:{label:11.59,id:UT22084-055-001-1297}}}“They will be skilled{{note:{index521,id:UT22084-055-001-1298}}} in hundreds of ways. 
They will have mastered the many kinds of words and definitions.
They have certainty in the ripening{{note:{index522,id:UT22084-055-001-1299}}} of actions and results.
They become distinctively preeminent in that way. {46}
{{milestone:{label:11.60,id:UT22084-055-001-1300}}}“They will possess unimpaired power.
They are great wise ones, the heirs of those with the ten strengths.
Knowing the subtle nature of phenomena,
They will always have a completely pure memory.{{note:{index523,id:UT22084-055-001-1301}}} {47} 
{{milestone:{label:11.61,id:UT22084-055-001-1302}}}“Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena,
They will never hear an unpleasant sound.
They always hear pleasant and melodious sounds
And their words are always pleasant. {48}
{{milestone:{label:11.62,id:UT22084-055-001-1303}}}“Because they know the very subtle nature of phenomena,
They have memory, understanding, wisdom, and realization.
Similarly, their minds are clear and unpolluted
And they teach many hundreds of sūtras. {49}
{{milestone:{label:11.63,id:UT22084-055-001-1304}}}“They are learned in the categories of letters and words.
They know many different kinds of sounds,
And they are skilled in meanings and letters. {{page:{number:83,id:UT22084-055-001-5916,folio:F.42.b}}}
They have these qualities through knowing the nature of phenomena. {50}
{{milestone:{label:11.64,id:UT22084-055-001-1305}}}“Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena
They are always attractive and charming 
To devas, humans, nāgas,{{note:{index524,id:UT22084-055-001-1306}}} and rākṣasas,
Asuras, mahoragas, and kinnaras. {51}
{{milestone:{label:11.65,id:UT22084-055-001-1307}}}“Because they know the subtle nature of phenomena
They never perceive as frightening 
The extremely terrible and flesh-devouring
Crowds of spirits, pretas, and rākṣasas. {52}
{{milestone:{label:11.66,id:UT22084-055-001-1308}}}“Those who hear the vast{{note:{index525,id:UT22084-055-001-1309}}} teaching of the wise 
Experience vast joy and their hairs stand on end.
They develop a vast attraction to the buddhas,
And gain a vast, inconceivable benefit.{{note:{index526,id:UT22084-055-001-1310}}} {53} 
{{milestone:{label:11.67,id:UT22084-055-001-1311}}}“Even by speaking for many thousands of eons
It is not possible to describe the power of the merit
That comes from memorizing this Dharma treasure of the sugatas.
It is immeasurable, infinite, and unquantifiable. {54}
{{milestone:{label:11.68,id:UT22084-055-001-1312}}}“The jinas to whom offerings have been made in the past,
The countless buddhas of the future,
And the buddhas who are present in the ten directions,
Are so by having memorized this supreme samādhi of peace. {55}
{{milestone:{label:11.69,id:UT22084-055-001-1313}}}“If a person who wishes for merit, 
With immeasurable affection for them
Serves compassionate ones with the ten strengths
For countless endless millions of eons, {56}
{{milestone:{label:11.70,id:UT22084-055-001-1314}}}“And if a second person who wishes for merit
Memorizes, during future times, 
One verse from this way of the ultimate truth,
Then the previous person’s merit will not even be a fraction of that. {57}
{{milestone:{label:11.71,id:UT22084-055-001-1315}}}“This will be the supreme offering to the buddhas.
During the future dreadful times
Hearing one of these four-line verses 
And memorizing it will be an offering to all the buddhas. {58}
{{milestone:{label:11.72,id:UT22084-055-001-1316}}}“They will always obtain the best provisions.
They will always eat the best alms of the land.{{note:{index527,id:UT22084-055-001-1317}}}
As the best senior heirs of the one with ten strengths,
They will for a long time make offerings to many jinas. {59}
{{milestone:{label:11.73,id:UT22084-055-001-1318}}}“They will also see myself here on Vulture Peak Mountain.
And I, in buddha wisdom, will thus prophesy to them.
Also, after my passing away, there will be Maitreya,{{note:{index528,id:UT22084-055-001-1319}}}
Who at that time will also prophesy to them. {60}
{{milestone:{label:11.74,id:UT22084-055-001-1320}}}“Similarly, Buddha Amitāyus also 
Has taught many other kinds of benefits:
‘All will enter my Sukhāvatī,
And go to Abhirati and see Buddha Akṣobhya.’{{note:{index529,id:UT22084-055-001-1321}}} {61} {{page:{number:84,id:UT22084-055-001-5917,folio:F.43.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:11.75,id:UT22084-055-001-1322}}}“For countless hundreds of thousands of eons 
They will never have the fear of downfalls.
In this supreme practice of bodhisattva conduct
They will always experience happiness. {62}
{{milestone:{label:11.76,id:UT22084-055-001-1323}}}“In that way it has been taught that this,
Which is preeminent, has the most excellent merit.
May I learn every single word,
And in future times be a keeper of this sūtra.”{{note:{index530,id:UT22084-055-001-1324}}} {63} 
{{milestone:{label:11.77,id:UT22084-055-001-1325}}}Conclusion of the eleventh chapter, “Becoming a Keeper of the Sūtra.”
{{milestone:{label:12,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-12}}}The Training According to the Samādhi
Chapter 12
{{milestone:{label:12.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1326}}}“Young man, those are the qualities and benefits that bodhisattvas who know the nature of all phenomena will have. They will describe the true, excellent qualities of the tathāgatas. They will not falsely say that which is untrue about the tathāgatas. Why is that? It is because they know perfectly that nature, which is the nature through which a tathāgata comes to be.{{note:{index531,id:UT22084-055-001-1327}}} They know the infinite qualities of a buddha. Why is that? Young man, the qualities of a buddha are infinite, inconceivable, beyond thought. They cannot be conceived or measured. Why is that? The mind, young man, is taught to be without a nature of its own,{{note:{index532,id:UT22084-055-001-1328}}} to be without form.{{note:{index533,id:UT22084-055-001-1329}}} Young man, that nature of the mind is also the nature of the qualities of a buddha. That nature of the qualities of a buddha is also the nature of the tathāgatas, and that is the nature of all phenomena.
{{milestone:{label:12.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1330}}}“Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who know correctly that teaching on the nature of all the qualities are, young man, called bodhisattva mahāsattvas with profound comprehension. They are skilled in emancipation. They know perfectly emancipation from the three realms. They have perfect knowledge, do not teach that which is erroneous, and do not say that which is anything other than true. {{page:{number:85,id:UT22084-055-001-5918,folio:F.43.b}}} Their conduct is in line with what they teach. They have no attachment to the three realms. They have transcended the three realms. They have transcended the level of desire, the level of form, the level of formlessness, the level of the kleśas, the level of names, and the level of language. They are skilled in the way of letters and words. They know freedom from letters.{{note:{index534,id:UT22084-055-001-1331}}} They have mastered the inexpressible Dharma. They know letters. They are skilled in letters. They are skilled in the knowledge of the categories of letters and words. They are skilled in the knowledge of the detailed categories of letters and words. They are skilled in the knowledge of the categories of all the words{{note:{index535,id:UT22084-055-001-1332}}} of the Dharma. They are skilled in the knowledge of the detailed categories of all the words{{note:{index536,id:UT22084-055-001-1333}}} of the Dharma. They are skilled in the knowledge{{note:{index537,id:UT22084-055-001-1334}}} of the presentation of all the Dharma. They are endowed with the certainty of understanding, so that all the evil māras and all the devas in their entourages cannot overcome them.” 
{{milestone:{label:12.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1335}}}At that time, when this Dharma teaching was given, ninety-eight times a hundred thousand million devas and human beings who had created the karma in previous lifetimes,{{note:{index538,id:UT22084-055-001-1336}}} had accumulated{{note:{index539,id:UT22084-055-001-1337}}} a trillion retentions,{{note:{index540,id:UT22084-055-001-1338}}} were unobscured, and had insight into the Dharma, all attained patience.{{note:{index541,id:UT22084-055-001-1339}}} The Bhagavān prophesied to them all that after four million, eight hundred thousand countless eons they would attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. He prophesied to each of them their separate names, their identical lifespans, and the individual buddha realms where they would attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. 
It was said:
{{milestone:{label:12.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1341}}}“The wise bodhisattvas who seek to attain 
The highest, supreme enlightenment,
Who are skilled in meaning and the Dharma,
Practice the nature of phenomena. {1}
{{milestone:{label:12.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1342}}}“They say nothing that is untrue 
About the unique qualities of the buddhas.
The heroes, free of all doubt,
Know the nature of the jinas. {2}
{{milestone:{label:12.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1343}}}“They know that all phenomena have but a single meaning,
And that is solely emptiness.
They do not have different meanings.
They become adept in that single meaning. {3}
{{milestone:{label:12.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1344}}}“The wise know that they are without thought, 
Are devoid of thought, and that there is no object. {{page:{number:86,id:UT22084-055-001-5919,folio:F.44.a}}}
They have eliminated without remainder 
Every conception of cessation and noncessation. {4}
{{milestone:{label:12.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1345}}}“They do not see the one with ten strengths as form,
But see the lion of men as the dharmakāya.
Neither do they conceive of attributes
Because they have eliminated all error. {5}
{{milestone:{label:12.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1346}}}“The qualities are inconceivable, beyond thought.
They have the nature of complete peace.
With this knowledge they thus see
The buddhas as the supreme among humans. {6}
{{milestone:{label:12.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1347}}}“Just as they know their own conceptions to be,
Thus they direct their understanding of everything.
All phenomena have that nature,
Which is as completely pure as space.{{note:{index542,id:UT22084-055-001-1348}}} {7}
{{milestone:{label:12.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1349}}}“Nothing arises to their conceptual mind.
They know emancipation{{note:{index543,id:UT22084-055-001-1350}}} from all phenomena.
They are liberated from the three realms
And they have no aspiration for them.{{note:{index544,id:UT22084-055-001-1351}}} {8}
{{milestone:{label:12.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1352}}}“They are those who see correctly and do not say
Anything to the contrary or any untrue words.
All the words that they speak 
Come forth through the power of the jinas. {9}
{{milestone:{label:12.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1353}}}“They transcend the level of desire,
And the levels of kleśas, form, and formlessness. 
Their minds have no attachment to phenomena.
They practice with joy, benefiting beings. {10}
{{milestone:{label:12.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1354}}}“They have transcended the level of words;
Their knowledge of language is obtained from its nature.
For however long they speak
They know those words have no basis. {11}
{{milestone:{label:12.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1355}}}“There is no activity of conceptualization;
Incorrect views have completely ceased.
Their understanding is completely assured.
It has a stability like that of space. {12}
{{milestone:{label:12.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1356}}}“Even though quintillions of māras
Come to disturb their mind,
They overcome all the māras
And do not fall under their power. {13}
{{milestone:{label:12.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1357}}}“They have rejected the net of the māras. 
They have pure, untroubled conduct.
They aspire to the bliss of dhyāna
And know the world to be empty. {14}
{{milestone:{label:12.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1358}}}“Even though it is said the world is an aggregate,
They know it to be empty,
And that all phenomena are like space,
Without birth and without cessation. {15}
{{milestone:{label:12.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1359}}}“They have forsaken the self, but not the conduct{{note:{index545,id:UT22084-055-001-1360}}}
Or listening to the teaching of the one with ten strengths.{{note:{index546,id:UT22084-055-001-1361}}}{{page:{number:87,id:UT22084-055-001-5920,folio:F.44.b}}}
They have attained perfect conduct
And will be reborn wherever they pray to be. {16}
{{milestone:{label:12.20,id:UT22084-055-001-1362}}}“They go to the buddha realms.
They see many millions of buddhas.
They have no desire for the deva realms
And they do not pray to be there. {17}
{{milestone:{label:12.21,id:UT22084-055-001-1363}}}“While they are practicing the Dharma,
Their diligence does not waver for an instant.
They are highly praised by
The buddhas in the ten directions. {18}
{{milestone:{label:12.22,id:UT22084-055-001-1364}}}“Therefore, young man, when you have received
This Dharma teaching of the samādhi,
Rejecting the profits of the intellect,
Teach this Dharma to the people. {19}
{{milestone:{label:12.23,id:UT22084-055-001-1365}}}“One who wishes for the numerous qualities
Possessed by the self-arisen buddha
Should train in this goodness
And become a buddha with the ten strengths.” {20}
{{milestone:{label:12.24,id:UT22084-055-001-1366}}}Conclusion of the twelfth chapter, “The Training According to the Samādhi.” 
{{milestone:{label:13,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-13}}}The Teaching of the Samādhi 
Chapter 13
{{milestone:{label:13.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1367}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should be skilled in teaching this samādhi.
{{milestone:{label:13.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1368}}}“Young man, what is the teaching of this samādhi? It is the true nature of all phenomena; it is equality; it is the absence of inequality; it is devoid of notions; it is devoid of concepts; it is devoid of creation; it is devoid of arising; it is devoid of production; it is devoid of cessation; it is the termination of notions, concepts, and assumptions; it is devoid of an object for the mind; it is devoid of a focus of the mind;{{note:{index547,id:UT22084-055-001-1369}}} it is the termination of designations; it is the termination of concepts from analysis; it is the termination of desire, anger, and ignorance; it is without a limited or limitless focus of the mind; it is the termination of any focus of the mind; it is the knowledge of the nature of the skandhas, dhātus, and āyatanas; it is the state of accomplishing the field of activity that is the performance of the conduct of mindfulness, understanding, comprehension, conscience, and stability; it is the level of freedom from corruptions;{{note:{index548,id:UT22084-055-001-1370}}} it is the level of peace; it is the termination of all conceptual elaboration; it is the training of all bodhisattvas; it is the field of activity of all tathāgatas; {{page:{number:88,id:UT22084-055-001-5921,folio:F.45.a}}} and it is the perfection of all good qualities.
{{milestone:{label:13.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1371}}}“Young man, that is what the teaching of samādhi is said to be. Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are established in this teaching of samādhi become inseparable from samādhi—their minds become free of delusion, they become endowed with great compassion, and they accomplish the benefit of countless beings.”
Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:
{{milestone:{label:13.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1373}}}“The level of unequaled samādhi{{note:{index549,id:UT22084-055-001-1374}}}
Is peaceful, subtle, and difficult to see.
All conceptions have been eliminated. 
Therefore it is called samādhi. {1}
{{milestone:{label:13.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1375}}}“There are no notions, there are no concepts,
There is nothing to be grasped, there is nothing to be shown,
And there is no object for the mind.
Therefore it is called samādhi. {2}
{{milestone:{label:13.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1376}}}“When in a state of meditation
There is no pride concerning any phenomenon.
That very absence of pride—
That is what is called samādhi. {3}
{{milestone:{label:13.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1377}}}“There does not exist{{note:{index550,id:UT22084-055-001-1378}}} even an atom of phenomena.
That which is called ‘an atom’ does not exist.
There are no phenomena as objects for the mind.
Therefore it is called samādhi. {4}
{{milestone:{label:13.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1379}}}“ ‘The mind has no object’
Is also itself a concept.
When there are no concepts of phenomena,
Then that is known as samādhi. {5}
{{milestone:{label:13.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1380}}}“A word indicates a meaning.
That word is not a thing.
A word is like an echo,
Like the space of the sky. {6}
{{milestone:{label:13.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1381}}}“These phenomena are not present;
There is no presence to be perceived.
The nonpresence is through the word ‘presence.’
Its nature is that there is nothing to be found. {7}
{{milestone:{label:13.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1382}}}“One says ‘going’ and ‘passing away,’
But that ‘going’ does not exist.
Through the word ‘going’ there is the absence of going. 
That is given the name samādhi. {8}
{{milestone:{label:13.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1383}}}“Saying ‘I am not meditating’ is called pride.{{note:{index551,id:UT22084-055-001-1384}}}
‘I am meditating’ is a second kind of pride.{{note:{index552,id:UT22084-055-001-1385}}}
Practicing for enlightenment without pride,{{note:{index553,id:UT22084-055-001-1386}}}
And attaining{{note:{index554,id:UT22084-055-001-1387}}} the absence of pride is the highest enlightenment.{{note:{index555,id:UT22084-055-001-1388}}} {9}
{{milestone:{label:13.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1389}}}“This unequaled equality is the level of peace;{{note:{index556,id:UT22084-055-001-1390}}}
It is śamatha and vipaśyanā,{{note:{index557,id:UT22084-055-001-1391}}} devoid of attributes.
Relying upon this peace, the level of buddhahood,
Is engaging in the meditation{{note:{index558,id:UT22084-055-001-1392}}} of samādhi. {10}
{{milestone:{label:13.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1393}}}“It is not possible through words to enter
Into the understanding of the meaning. {{page:{number:89,id:UT22084-055-001-5922,folio:F.45.b}}}
When all sounds and words are abandoned
There will be meditation without pride. {11}
{{milestone:{label:13.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1394}}}“When there is the fire of the eon’s end in this world
That fire does not burn the supreme mountain in its center, 
Just like space that has never been burned in the past,
Even though the fire burns for many hundreds of eons.{{note:{index559,id:UT22084-055-001-1395}}} {12}
{{milestone:{label:13.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1396}}}“The bodhisattvas who remain engaged
In this samādhi as it has been taught,
And know that phenomena are the same as space,
Will also not be burned by fire.{{note:{index560,id:UT22084-055-001-1397}}} {13}
{{milestone:{label:13.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1398}}}“If the buddha realm were burning
And in this samādhi they prayed
For the burning to completely cease,
Though the earth was destroyed it would be unchanged. {14}
{{milestone:{label:13.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1399}}}“They will have infinite miraculous powers.
They will travel through the air unimpeded.
The bodhisattvas will have these qualities
By remaining in samādhi just as they have been taught. {15}
{{milestone:{label:13.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1400}}}“Though one is born and though one dies, 
There is no birth and there is no death.
For the one who understands that
This samādhi will not be difficult to attain. {16}
{{milestone:{label:13.20,id:UT22084-055-001-1401}}}“The Lord of the World has taught
That there is no death and there is no birth.
Just as the Lord of the World knew that,
You should also know it through this samādhi. {17}
{{milestone:{label:13.21,id:UT22084-055-001-1402}}}“Unstained by the world,
They have no attachment to worldly phenomena.
With a body free of impediment
They go to the buddha realms. {18}
{{milestone:{label:13.22,id:UT22084-055-001-1403}}}“They constantly see in those realms
The perfect buddhas, the guides of the world.
They listen there to the Dharma
That is taught in the realms of the buddhas.{{note:{index561,id:UT22084-055-001-1404}}} {19}
{{milestone:{label:13.23,id:UT22084-055-001-1405}}}“They will never be in ignorance.
They will teach the essence of phenomena.
They always know the way of phenomena, 
Which is composed{{note:{index562,id:UT22084-055-001-1406}}} of the essence of phenomena. {20}
{{milestone:{label:13.24,id:UT22084-055-001-1407}}}“Even though they teach for ten million eons,
Their confidence in speech will not decline.
They emanate many other bodhisattvas
Who have wisdom. {21}
{{milestone:{label:13.25,id:UT22084-055-001-1408}}}“The emanated bodhisattvas
Travel from realm to realm.
They are seated, cross-legged,
Upon lotuses that have a thousand petals. {22}
{{milestone:{label:13.26,id:UT22084-055-001-1409}}}“They teach the enlightenment of buddhahood,
Wonderful dhāraṇīs and sūtras, {{page:{number:90,id:UT22084-055-001-5923,folio:F.46.a}}}
And ten million other sūtras,
While meditating peacefully in samādhi. {23}
{{milestone:{label:13.27,id:UT22084-055-001-1410}}}“They establish in irreversibility
Countless multitudes of beings,
And teach the enlightenment of buddhahood
Without their confidence in speech ever declining. {24}
{{milestone:{label:13.28,id:UT22084-055-001-1411}}}“They go to a pinnacled hall 
That is adorned with jewels
And scatter aromatic 
Flowers upon the guides. {25}
{{milestone:{label:13.29,id:UT22084-055-001-1412}}}“They also sprinkle scented 
Powders upon the guides.
They all make vast offerings
In order to attain enlightenment. {26}
{{milestone:{label:13.30,id:UT22084-055-001-1413}}}“Those countless qualities 
Are the refuge of the bodhisattvas.
When they are free of kleśas
They attain those miraculous powers. {27}
{{milestone:{label:13.31,id:UT22084-055-001-1414}}}“Because the kleśas are not created 
They are clear, pure, and bright.
The field of activity of the bodhisattvas
Is noncomposite and inviolate. {28}
{{milestone:{label:13.32,id:UT22084-055-001-1415}}}“They have perfect peace, complete peace;
They have no kleśas, and they have no misery.{{note:{index563,id:UT22084-055-001-1416}}}
They have no conceptualization, are free of conceptualization,
And have transcended conceptualization. {29}
{{milestone:{label:13.33,id:UT22084-055-001-1417}}}“This characteristic of phenomena
Is beyond the scope of words.{{note:{index564,id:UT22084-055-001-1418}}}
It is difficult{{note:{index565,id:UT22084-055-001-1419}}} to know through language{{note:{index566,id:UT22084-055-001-1420}}}
And therefore it is called samādhi. {30}
{{milestone:{label:13.34,id:UT22084-055-001-1421}}}“It is unending; it is complete peace;
It is effortless, and it cannot be shown.
The field of activity of all the buddhas
Is the completely pure summit of the truth. {31}
{{milestone:{label:13.35,id:UT22084-055-001-1422}}}“The training of all the buddhas
Is in the nature of all phenomena. 
The perfect buddhas, having trained in it,
Have reached the perfection of qualities.{{note:{index567,id:UT22084-055-001-1423}}} {32}
{{milestone:{label:13.36,id:UT22084-055-001-1424}}}“Without any concepts of the past,
Of this side and the further side,
In that way all those buddhas 
Have reached the perfection{{note:{index568,id:UT22084-055-001-1425}}} of qualities. {33}
{{milestone:{label:13.37,id:UT22084-055-001-1426}}}“Knowing the nature of phenomena
As having no coming or going,
They have reached the perfection
That is nonconceptual and effortless.” {34}
{{milestone:{label:13.38,id:UT22084-055-001-1427}}}Conclusion of the thirteenth chapter, “The Teaching of the Samādhi.” 
{{milestone:{label:14,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-14}}}The Buddha’s Smile
Chapter 14
{{milestone:{label:14.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1428}}} Then the youth Candraprabha rose from his seat, removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, {{page:{number:91,id:UT22084-055-001-5924,folio:F.46.b}}} with palms placed together he bowed toward the Bhagavān and said to him,{{note:{index569,id:UT22084-055-001-1429}}} “Bhagavān, it is marvelous that the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha has taught the equality that is the nature of all phenomena, which is the samādhi that all bodhisattvas train in.
{{milestone:{label:14.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1430}}}“Bhagavān, it was thus, in this training, that the Bhagavān trained for a long time, and accomplished the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. Bhagavān, that gives me confidence to speak.{{note:{index570,id:UT22084-055-001-1431}}} Sugata, it gives me confidence to speak.”
{{milestone:{label:14.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1432}}}The Bhagavān said, “Young man, if you think the time has come, be confident to speak.”
Since the Bhagavān had granted the youth Candraprabha this opportunity, Candraprabha spoke the following verses of praise directly to the Bhagavān.
{{milestone:{label:14.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1434}}}“You saw beings tormented by suffering,{{note:{index571,id:UT22084-055-001-1435}}}
Constantly overpowered by desire and anger,
And developed the aspiration to attain enlightenment:
‘May I become a buddha who liberates beings!’ {1}
{{milestone:{label:14.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1436}}}“Hero,{{note:{index572,id:UT22084-055-001-1437}}} for many millions of eons, constantly,
You practiced generosity, self-restraint and self-control,
Patience, correct conduct, and similarly diligence,
And your acts of generosity were vast and infinite. {2}
{{milestone:{label:14.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1438}}}“Without ever any sadness in your mind
You gave away your legs, arms, and even your life,
And similarly, without attachment you gave away 
Gold, silver, sons, wives, and your kingdom. {3}
{{milestone:{label:14.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1439}}}“Your conduct was stainless and pure.
You made a gift of yourself without ruining your conduct.
You controlled well your body, speech, and mind.
Sugata who has a self-restrained mind, I pay homage to you. {4}
{{milestone:{label:14.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1440}}}“Delighting in patience, residing on the path of patience,
Even though your body was cut into pieces you were not angered;{{note:{index573,id:UT22084-055-001-1441}}}
Through your meditation on love, milk flowed from you.
Marvelous Sugata, I pay homage to you. {5}
{{milestone:{label:14.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1442}}}“You possess the strength of the ten strengths.
With wisdom free of attachment you know all phenomena. {{page:{number:92,id:UT22084-055-001-5925,folio:F.47.a}}}
With compassion, Lord of Dharma, you benefit the world. 
Through your kindness you wish to benefit beings. {6}
{{milestone:{label:14.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1443}}}“You know emptiness and that there are no such beings,
And likewise you see that the world’s beings have lost that path.
You have realized that the nature of phenomena is selfless 
And that though you bring beings to liberation, there is no such liberation. {7}
{{milestone:{label:14.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1444}}}“With discrimination you reject all carelessness.
You have conquered the infinite, powerful māras.
Enlightened at buddhahood, you have vast, infinite wisdom.
You teach the supreme Dharma of completely pure peace. {8}
{{milestone:{label:14.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1445}}}“The sky with its moon and the stars may fall,
The earth with its mountains and towns may be destroyed,
The element of space may change into something else,
But you will never speak an untrue word. {9}
{{milestone:{label:14.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1446}}}“You have seen the suffering of beings
Who take joy in the perception of objects.
You teach the profound peace, emptiness,
In which there is no perception of objects. {10}
{{milestone:{label:14.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1447}}}“Great hero, you trained 
For countless millions of eons
In the training of nonperception,
And so you are free of error. {11}
{{milestone:{label:14.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1448}}}“Just as you have trained in the Dharma,
In that way you teach the Dharma.
Yours is not the level of foolish beings,
And neither is it the level of all the tīrthikas. {12}
{{milestone:{label:14.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1449}}}“Those who have the conception of a self,
They are unwise beings who are in error.
You know that phenomena have no self,
And so you are free of any error. {13}
{{milestone:{label:14.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1450}}}“You speak the truth, great hero;
You are established in the true Dharma.
Lord, you remain within truth, within veracity,
And you speak words that are true. {14}
{{milestone:{label:14.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1451}}}“Your conduct has been true,
Just as you have prayed for.
You have the consequence of that true conduct
And you speak words that are true. {15}
{{milestone:{label:14.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1452}}}“You have perfected true conduct.
You have trained in the summit of truth.
You have truly practiced with a true motivation.
I pay homage to you who have true wisdom. {16}
{{milestone:{label:14.20,id:UT22084-055-001-1453}}}“There is no equal to your wisdom.
Your words of wisdom illuminate.
You have attained unique wisdom.
I pay homage to you who speak words of wisdom. {17}
{{milestone:{label:14.21,id:UT22084-055-001-1454}}}“You have meditated on kindness
And become a friend to all beings. {{page:{number:93,id:UT22084-055-001-5926,folio:F.47.b}}}
