You are as unshakable as Sumeru.
You are completely stable and unwavering. {18}
{{milestone:{label:14.22,id:UT22084-055-001-1455}}}“Teacher, your following is vast. 
You have attracted these followers.
Sugata who has profound wisdom, 
Make your voice resound within this assembly. {19}
{{milestone:{label:14.23,id:UT22084-055-001-1456}}}“The voice of the Buddha is a lion’s roar.
You walk with the gait of a lion.
You defeat all the tīrthikas
Like a lion defeats jackals. {20}
{{milestone:{label:14.24,id:UT22084-055-001-1457}}}“Hero who subdues the unsubdued,
The unsubdued are subdued by you. 
They become friends who are reliable,
Inseparable, and pleasant to be with. {21}
{{milestone:{label:14.25,id:UT22084-055-001-1458}}}“You see the beings who are suffering 
Because they maintain the view of a self.{{note:{index574,id:UT22084-055-001-1459}}}
You teach the Dharma of no-self
In which there is neither like nor dislike. {22}
{{milestone:{label:14.26,id:UT22084-055-001-1460}}}“The foolish who are untrained
Take up the wrong paths.
You show them the path
That the guides have followed. {23}
{{milestone:{label:14.27,id:UT22084-055-001-1461}}}“Whoever holds to the concept of a self,
They will remain in suffering.
They do not know selflessness,
Within which there is no suffering. {24}
{{milestone:{label:14.28,id:UT22084-055-001-1462}}}“You teach the Dharma with words that are without error.
Lord of the World, you make no error.
You are one who speaks words that are never incorrect.
I pay homage to you, who bring freedom from suffering. {25}
{{milestone:{label:14.29,id:UT22084-055-001-1463}}}“In the sky there are many quintillions
Of devas, nāgas, and yakṣas.
They all feel joy in the Guide
When they hear the meaningful words of the Bhagavān. {26}
{{milestone:{label:14.30,id:UT22084-055-001-1464}}}“Your words are mild, gentle, and pleasing,
Timely, melodious, appropriate, and beloved.
You have the countless qualities of speech
That benefit and bring liberation to many beings. {27}
{{milestone:{label:14.31,id:UT22084-055-001-1465}}}“Countless hundreds of thousands of musical instruments 
Are all played melodiously and simultaneously,
But the Sugata with one word eclipses them all
With his unique, divine, beloved voice.{{note:{index575,id:UT22084-055-001-1466}}} {28}
{{milestone:{label:14.32,id:UT22084-055-001-1467}}}“Avadavats{{note:{index576,id:UT22084-055-001-1468}}} and flocks of birds{{note:{index577,id:UT22084-055-001-1469}}} with beautiful songs, 
With their beautiful songs that are pleasing to everyone—
All of the songs of these many flocks of birds{{note:{index578,id:UT22084-055-001-1470}}}
Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. {29} {{page:{number:94,id:UT22084-055-001-5927,folio:F.48.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:14.33,id:UT22084-055-001-1471}}}“Deva maidens with beautiful voices
And with melodious music and songs,
And the sound of lutes, paṭaha{{note:{index579,id:UT22084-055-001-1472}}} drums, bherī drums,{{note:{index580,id:UT22084-055-001-1473}}} and conches,
Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech.{{note:{index581,id:UT22084-055-001-1474}}} {i}
{{milestone:{label:14.34,id:UT22084-055-001-1475}}}“The songs of cuckoos, parrots, and mynas,
Of cranes, peacocks, and kinnaras—
All these beautiful, melodious sounds
Cannot equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech.{{note:{index582,id:UT22084-055-001-1476}}} {30}
{{milestone:{label:14.35,id:UT22084-055-001-1477}}}“Delightful, melodious, beautiful, enjoyable,
Exquisite, peaceful voices singing praises—
All such voices singing simultaneously
Are not as delightful as the Tathāgata’s perfect speech. {31}
{{milestone:{label:14.36,id:UT22084-055-001-1478}}}“The light from all luminous beings, 
From devas,{{note:{index583,id:UT22084-055-001-1479}}} humans, kings, and asuras,{{note:{index584,id:UT22084-055-001-1480}}}
And from all beings in the three existences,
Are eclipsed by one light ray from the Sugata. {32}
{{milestone:{label:14.37,id:UT22084-055-001-1481}}}“The Sugata’s body is like a blossomed flower
With the various adornments of all the special signs.
A pure and clear accomplishment of hundreds of merits, 
The body of the Jina shines on the entire world. {33}
{{milestone:{label:14.38,id:UT22084-055-001-1482}}}“The sound of conches and of paṇavas,{{note:{index585,id:UT22084-055-001-1483}}}
And the sound of bherī drums{{note:{index586,id:UT22084-055-001-1484}}} and kimpalas{{note:{index587,id:UT22084-055-001-1485}}}—
All those beautiful and delightful sounds
Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {34}
{{milestone:{label:14.39,id:UT22084-055-001-1486}}}“The sounds of quintillions of musical instruments,
Clear and beautiful voices like those of the devas,{{note:{index588,id:UT22084-055-001-1487}}}
And the delightful voices of male and female devas{{note:{index589,id:UT22084-055-001-1488}}}
Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice.{{note:{index590,id:UT22084-055-001-1489}}} {35}
{{milestone:{label:14.40,id:UT22084-055-001-1490}}}“Flocks of a multitude of birds—cranes, peacocks, 
Shelducks, cuckoos, geese, and snipe— 
May simultaneously sing their songs, but they 
Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice.{{note:{index591,id:UT22084-055-001-1491}}} {36}
{{milestone:{label:14.41,id:UT22084-055-001-1492}}}“The voices of nāgas, yakṣas, asuras, mahoragas,
Devendra,{{note:{index592,id:UT22084-055-001-1493}}} Brahmā, and the lords of the devas— 
All the lovely and beautiful voices in the three existences
Cannot equal a hundredth of the Buddha’s voice. {37}
{{milestone:{label:14.42,id:UT22084-055-001-1494}}}“The light of Brahmā and lords of the devas, 
The light of the sun and precious jewels,
The many different kinds of light—
All those lights are eclipsed by the brilliance of the Jina’s light.{{note:{index593,id:UT22084-055-001-1495}}} {38}
{{milestone:{label:14.43,id:UT22084-055-001-1496}}}“Your body, speech, and mind are perfectly pure.
The purity of your wisdom is unstained by the three existences. {{page:{number:95,id:UT22084-055-001-5928,folio:F.48.b}}}
Lord of men, you have the wealth of qualities, precious qualities.
Self-arisen one, through all your qualities, you are without equal.” {39}
{{milestone:{label:14.44,id:UT22084-055-001-1497}}}In that way the youth spoke those words with great joy, 
Praising the one with ten strengths, the speaker of truth.
He said, “By offering to the measureless,{{note:{index594,id:UT22084-055-001-1498}}} unquantifiable Buddha
May I also become a buddha like Śākyamuni!” {40}
{{milestone:{label:14.45,id:UT22084-055-001-1499}}}Knowing his perfect conduct, the Sugata,
The Lord of humans, the one with wisdom free of attachment, smiled.
Maitreya, the senior son of the one with ten strengths, asked him,
“For what reason did the Guide smile? {41}
{{milestone:{label:14.46,id:UT22084-055-001-1500}}}“The earth has shaken in six ways.
The devas and nāgas in the sky are filled with joy.
They are gazing at the Buddha with great delight and happiness.
I pray to the unconquerable Sugata that you elucidate this to them. {42}
{{milestone:{label:14.47,id:UT22084-055-001-1501}}}“You have a supreme being’s wisdom,
Which is not the level of the Bhagavān’s śrāvakas.
You who have pure wisdom beyond examples, wise one, 
Tell{{note:{index595,id:UT22084-055-001-1502}}} us the entire reason, Jina, why you smiled.{{note:{index596,id:UT22084-055-001-1503}}} {43}
{{milestone:{label:14.48,id:UT22084-055-001-1504}}}“You are the Śākya lion, possessor of the ten strengths, the Guide,
The chief of humans, the one who has reached the perfection of wisdom.{{note:{index597,id:UT22084-055-001-1505}}}
You have eliminated intractable desire, anger, and ignorance.
To you who shine with intense light, I ask this question: {44}
{{milestone:{label:14.49,id:UT22084-055-001-1506}}}“Seeking the supreme, highest enlightenment,
You, the Guide, practiced for millions of eons
As numerous as the grains of sand in the Ganges. 
For what reason did you show a smile? {45}
{{milestone:{label:14.50,id:UT22084-055-001-1507}}}“Seeking the supreme, highest enlightenment,
You, the Teacher, gave away your arms and legs.
You gave away sons, wives, companions, and relations.
Sage, for what reason did you show a smile? {46}
{{milestone:{label:14.51,id:UT22084-055-001-1508}}}“You gave away horses, elephants, and chariots,{{note:{index598,id:UT22084-055-001-1509}}}
Slaves, jewels, silver, and pearls.{{note:{index599,id:UT22084-055-001-1510}}}
When you practiced the sublime conduct 
There were no jewels or wealth that you did not give away. {47}
{{milestone:{label:14.52,id:UT22084-055-001-1511}}}“You have the supreme wisdom in the three existences.
You know the conduct of all beings. {{page:{number:96,id:UT22084-055-001-5929,folio:F.49.a}}}
You are skilled in knowing their natures, minds, and aspirations.
For what reason did you smile? {48}
{{milestone:{label:14.53,id:UT22084-055-001-1512}}}“Who made the offering to you, best of men?
For whom has vast merit been created? 
Who has gained that excellent conduct?
Sage, for what reason did you smile? {49}
{{milestone:{label:14.54,id:UT22084-055-001-1513}}}“The earth has shaken in six ways.
Millions of lotuses have appeared on the ground.{{note:{index600,id:UT22084-055-001-1514}}}
They shine and have millions of excellent petals.
They are the color of gold, beautiful and delightful. {50}
{{milestone:{label:14.55,id:UT22084-055-001-1515}}}“Present here are the heart sons of the Jina
Who show the greatest bodhisattva miracles. 
Many{{note:{index601,id:UT22084-055-001-1516}}} dharmabhāṇakas have gathered here.
Guide, I ask my question for their sake. {51}
{{milestone:{label:14.56,id:UT22084-055-001-1517}}}“The sound of bherī drums,{{note:{index602,id:UT22084-055-001-1518}}} conches, and gongs,{{note:{index603,id:UT22084-055-001-1519}}}
Of quintillions of instruments has resounded.
That music was heard coming from the sky,
But compared to that the Sugata’s speech is inconceivable. {52}
{{milestone:{label:14.57,id:UT22084-055-001-1520}}}“Many flocks of birds have gathered,
Cranes,{{note:{index604,id:UT22084-055-001-1521}}} geese, avadavats,{{note:{index605,id:UT22084-055-001-1522}}} and cuckoos.
They have sung their perfect, beautiful songs,
But they do not equal a fraction of the Buddha’s speech. {53}
{{milestone:{label:14.58,id:UT22084-055-001-1523}}}“Who in the past with generosity, self-restraint, and self-control
Has served well for many millions of eons? 
Who has made offerings to you, supreme among men?
For what reason did you smile? {54}
{{milestone:{label:14.59,id:UT22084-055-001-1524}}}“Who in the past, having shown you the greatest veneration, 
Asked you, supreme among men, the question,
‘How can I attain the enlightenment of buddhahood?’
For what reason did you smile? {55}
{{milestone:{label:14.60,id:UT22084-055-001-1525}}}“Those with the ten strengths in the past,
The sugatas of the present and the future,
And you, supreme among men, know all.
Therefore for the benefit of beings I ask this question. {56}
{{milestone:{label:14.61,id:UT22084-055-001-1526}}}“You know the thoughts in the minds of beings
And all beings’ infinite ways of conduct;
You know the aspirations that humans have. 
Therefore I ask this question to you, supreme among men. {57}
{{milestone:{label:14.62,id:UT22084-055-001-1527}}}“Those who are practicing the supreme conduct,
Who are adept in causes, reasons, and discipline,
They ask, ‘How does one attain the Buddha’s wisdom?’
Therefore, supreme human, I ask this question. {58}
{{milestone:{label:14.63,id:UT22084-055-001-1528}}}“There are those who meditate on the field of experience of those with the ten strengths:
The subtle Dharma that is difficult to perceive, {{page:{number:97,id:UT22084-055-001-5930,folio:F.49.b}}}
And emptiness and peace that is unequaled and inconceivable. 
For their sake, Guide, I ask you this question. {59}
{{milestone:{label:14.64,id:UT22084-055-001-1529}}}“Those who meditate on love and compassion
For all the countless beings in the world, 
Without their having the concept of beings—
Supreme human, for their sake I ask this question. {60}
{{milestone:{label:14.65,id:UT22084-055-001-1530}}}“Those who have inconceivable, unequaled wisdom,
They are never known to have any grasping. 
They have reached the perfection of the mind’s field of activity. 
Lord, it is for their sake that I ask this question. {61}
{{milestone:{label:14.66,id:UT22084-055-001-1531}}}“You have reached the perfection of conduct and wisdom’s qualities.
You have unequaled knowledge of the three times.
You will never make an error.
For what reason did you smile? {62}
{{milestone:{label:14.67,id:UT22084-055-001-1532}}}“Śāriputra, Aniruddha, and Kolita,
And the other śrāvakas of the Sugata,
Do not have that wisdom.
It is the unsurpassable field of activity of the buddhas. {63}
{{milestone:{label:14.68,id:UT22084-055-001-1533}}}“You have reached the perfection of power over all phenomena.
You have ascended through the practice of the training.
Guide, you have developed compassion.
You who know the ultimate truth, release your voice! {64}
{{milestone:{label:14.69,id:UT22084-055-001-1534}}}“You have had, in the past for many millions of eons,
The goal of being the ultimate refuge and protector,
And have inquired, supreme human, with just that intention; 
Guide, tell us the result of that today. {65}
{{milestone:{label:14.70,id:UT22084-055-001-1535}}}“Yakṣas, rākṣasas, kumbhāṇḍas, and guhyakas 
Are gazing upon the supreme among humans.
They are all respectful, their palms together in homage,
In order to listen to the elucidation from the great being. {66}
{{milestone:{label:14.71,id:UT22084-055-001-1536}}}“Many bodhisattvas with miraculous powers 
Have come from millions of buddha realms.
These senior sons, born form the minds of the sugatas,
Are all respectfully present, their palms together in homage. {67}
{{milestone:{label:14.72,id:UT22084-055-001-1537}}}“Gandhahasti with millions of bodhisattvas 
Has come into your presence from the east,
From the famous world of Akṣobhya’s realm
For this question, Lion of the Śākyas, supreme human. {68}
{{milestone:{label:14.73,id:UT22084-055-001-1538}}}“Avalokiteśvara and Mahā­sthāma­prāpta 
Have come before you with millions of bodhisattvas 
From the supreme realm of Sukhāvatī {{page:{number:98,id:UT22084-055-001-5931,folio:F.50.a}}}
For this question, Lion of the Śākyas, supreme human. {69}
{{milestone:{label:14.74,id:UT22084-055-001-1539}}}“In the past for many millions of eons
They have served countless sugatas
As numerous as the sand grains in all the oceans,
Seeking this supreme sublime wisdom. {70}
{{milestone:{label:14.75,id:UT22084-055-001-1540}}}“Mañjughoṣa is present, his palms together in homage.
He has been praised and extolled by all the buddhas.
He has reached the perfection of all good qualities
And is renowned throughout the worlds in all directions. {71}
{{milestone:{label:14.76,id:UT22084-055-001-1541}}}“They have practiced in millions of buddha realms.
It is very rare to see such beings.
They have the qualities of sons of the buddhas and excellent training, 
And are all present, with their palms together respectfully in homage. {72}
{{milestone:{label:14.77,id:UT22084-055-001-1542}}}“There is no one here other than worthy recipients.
That is what these wise ones{{note:{index606,id:UT22084-055-001-1543}}} are like,
The holders of the Dharma treasures of all teachers.
Guide, release your gentle speech.{{note:{index607,id:UT22084-055-001-1544}}} {73}
{{milestone:{label:14.78,id:UT22084-055-001-1545}}}“The jinas, the guides, the supreme humans
Have never been seen to smile without a reason. 
Grant us your supreme speech, which is like the beat of a drum.
What is the reason that we saw you smile? {74}
{{milestone:{label:14.79,id:UT22084-055-001-1546}}}“The supreme beings resound like thunder,{{note:{index608,id:UT22084-055-001-1547}}}
Geese, cuckoos, peacocks, and swans,{{note:{index609,id:UT22084-055-001-1548}}}
And they emit the melodious music of the devas. 
Liberator of beings, elucidate with your words. {75}
{{milestone:{label:14.80,id:UT22084-055-001-1549}}}“You develop kindness, you increase joy,
You teach wisdom, you eliminate ignorance,
You realize the meaning, you expand wisdom,
And you have purified for quintillions of eons. {76}
{{milestone:{label:14.81,id:UT22084-055-001-1550}}}“You have realized the nature of things with certainty,
You have taught the meaning in words that end suffering.
You have routed the teachings of all tīrthikas.
You meditate on emptiness, the absence of being, and the absence of a soul. {77}
{{milestone:{label:14.82,id:UT22084-055-001-1551}}}“You are adorned by thousands of merits.
You have practiced with hundreds of thousands of buddhas,
Are praised by hundreds of thousands of devas, 
And hundreds of thousands of Brahmās pay homage to you. {78}
{{milestone:{label:14.83,id:UT22084-055-001-1552}}}“Yakṣas, rākṣasas, and kumbhāṇḍas have faith in you. {{page:{number:99,id:UT22084-055-001-5932,folio:F.50.b}}}
You have liberated nāgas, mahoragas, and garuḍas.
You are constantly without any attachment. 
Speak the words{{note:{index610,id:UT22084-055-001-1553}}} that are the result of good actions. {79}
{{milestone:{label:14.84,id:UT22084-055-001-1554}}}“All the jinas that have passed into nirvāṇa,
Those who will live in the future, and those now present,
You know them all without impediment.
Guide, you are sublime because of all your qualities. {80}
{{milestone:{label:14.85,id:UT22084-055-001-1555}}}“This earth that supports beings, with its mountains
And oceans, has been shaken in six ways. 
The devas have thrown down flowers from the sky.
There has arisen the beautiful aroma of the incense of the devas. {81}
{{milestone:{label:14.86,id:UT22084-055-001-1556}}}“Desire, anger, and darkness of the mind have been completely eliminated.
Conduct has become completely pure and the mind has become completely pure. 
There is delight in complete peace, emptiness, and the absence of attributes.
There is the sound of the lion’s roar, the sound of the compassionate ones. {82}
{{milestone:{label:14.87,id:UT22084-055-001-1557}}}“You have the confidence of speech, and great renown.
You have perfected wisdom, the wisdom of the jinas.
Compassionate one, there is no one like you in this world.
Tell us, for what reason did you smile? {83}
{{milestone:{label:14.88,id:UT22084-055-001-1558}}}“The songs of peacocks, cuckoos, and avadavats,
And likewise the beautiful song of the partridge,{{note:{index611,id:UT22084-055-001-1559}}}
All those pleasant sounds simultaneously
Do not equal a fraction of the Sugata’s speech. {84}
{{milestone:{label:14.89,id:UT22084-055-001-1560}}}“Bherī drums, mṛdaṅgas, and similarly paṇavas;
Conches, flutes, and similarly lutes:
The simultaneous sound of a thousand instruments 
Does not equal a fraction of the Sugata’s speech. {85}
{{milestone:{label:14.90,id:UT22084-055-001-1561}}}“The divine, sublime sound of thousands of instruments
And the beautiful songs of deva maidens, 
The excellent songs that bring delightful sounds to the mind,
Do not equal a fraction of the Sugata’s speech. {86}
{{milestone:{label:14.91,id:UT22084-055-001-1562}}}“With one sound you benefit the world
As it resounds to those with different aspirations,
Each person thinking, ‘The Jina is speaking to me.’
For what reason did you smile? {87}
{{milestone:{label:14.92,id:UT22084-055-001-1563}}}“The music of the devas and the music of the nāgas,
And also the melodious music of the kinnaras,
Are never able to pacify the kleśas.
The Buddha’s speech always dispels the kleśas. {88}
{{milestone:{label:14.93,id:UT22084-055-001-1564}}}“You create joy but not joy in desire.
You create love and not a mind of anger.
You create wisdom and not a mind of stupidity. {{page:{number:100,id:UT22084-055-001-5933,folio:F.51.a}}}
The Buddha’s speech eliminates all stains. {89}
{{milestone:{label:14.94,id:UT22084-055-001-1565}}}“The sound of your voice does not go beyond your followers.
It cuts through everyone’s hundreds of doubts.
It is never too quiet nor too loud. 
The Sage’s voice teaches everyone equally and easily. {90}
{{milestone:{label:14.95,id:UT22084-055-001-1566}}}“This earth with its mountains and forests may perish,
And so may the waters of the ocean.
The moon and the sun may fall to the earth,
But the Jina’s speech will never change. {91}
{{milestone:{label:14.96,id:UT22084-055-001-1567}}}“Your voice has all the qualities of pure speech.
Your beautiful voice is a gentle lion’s roar.
Compassionate one, you have the voice of Brahmā. 
For what reason did you smile? {92}
{{milestone:{label:14.97,id:UT22084-055-001-1568}}}“You know the minds and conduct
Of all the beings in the world,
Those in the past, the future, and the present.
Tell us the reason why you smiled. {93}
{{milestone:{label:14.98,id:UT22084-055-001-1569}}}“All of the jinas, the compassionate ones,
They who have reached the perfection of power and wisdom,
The jinas whose faces are like stainless moons,
Have never smiled without a reason. {94}
{{milestone:{label:14.99,id:UT22084-055-001-1570}}}“If for millions of eons one were to describe your unequaled qualities,
Which are as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, 
One would not be able to describe them fully. 
Teach us the reason why you smiled.”{{note:{index612,id:UT22084-055-001-1571}}} {95}
{{milestone:{label:14.100,id:UT22084-055-001-1572}}}Conclusion of the fourteenth chapter, “The Buddha’s Smile.”
{{milestone:{label:15,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-15}}}The Elucidation of the Buddha’s Smile
Chapter 15
{{milestone:{label:15.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1573}}}At that time the Bhagavān spoke these appropriate verses to Bodhisattva Maitreya:
{{milestone:{label:15.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1574}}}“This youth, Candraprabha,
Has praised the Buddha with unequaled joy.
He described the unique superior qualities of the buddhas.
All the time he is reciting their praises.{{note:{index613,id:UT22084-055-001-1575}}} {1}
{{milestone:{label:15.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1576}}}“In this very city of Rājagṛha in the past 
He has seen ten thousand million buddhas.
In the presence of all those jinas 
He asked about this supreme samādhi of peace. {2}
{{milestone:{label:15.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1577}}}“He has always been my son,
Practicing this supreme bodhisattva conduct. 
He has always had the confidence of speech,
And always he has been practicing celibacy. {3} {{page:{number:101,id:UT22084-055-001-5934,folio:F.51.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:15.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1578}}}“In the very fearful future times 
You, Ajita, will be my witness.{{note:{index614,id:UT22084-055-001-1579}}}
Always remaining in a state of celibacy,
He will make this samādhi widespread. {4}
{{milestone:{label:15.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1580}}}“Those who seek entry into this sublime samādhi,
Through that path will attain enlightenment.
He will be adopted by many millions of buddhas
And he will make supreme offerings to those guides. {5}
{{milestone:{label:15.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1581}}}“I prophesy that, remaining in wisdom,
Candraprabha’s conduct will be exceptional.
In the future times there will be no obstacle
To his celibacy or to his life. {6}
{{milestone:{label:15.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1582}}}“He will know millions of buddhas as clearly
As five myrobalan plums in the palm of the hand.
And he will make offerings in the future to even more, 
As numerous as sand grains in the Ganges. {7}
{{milestone:{label:15.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1583}}}“Eight hundred million devas and nāgas, 
And seven hundred billion yakṣas,
In future times will be zealous
And make offerings to the supreme among humans. {8}
{{milestone:{label:15.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1584}}}“He will make offerings to the supreme human
And will practice this unsurpassable wisdom.
In a future time he will become a Lord of the World,
A jina by the name of Vimalaprabha.”{{note:{index615,id:UT22084-055-001-1585}}} {9}
{{milestone:{label:15.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1586}}}The young man was overjoyed
On hearing this prophecy about himself.
Candraprabha floated up to the height of seven palm trees
And remaining in the sky he made this declaration: {10}
{{milestone:{label:15.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1587}}}“O Jina, you who teach the supreme Dharma,
You have the power of a lord of liberating wisdom.
You remain in the certainty of supreme wisdom 
And cannot be defeated by adversaries. {11}
{{milestone:{label:15.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1588}}}“You have abandoned attachment and reached liberation. 
You have no attachment to existence, which is devoid of things.
You have no conceptualization whatsoever.
You have the wisdom of nonattachment toward the three existences. {12}
{{milestone:{label:15.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1589}}}“You are unstained by any conceptualization.
You are free of all conceptualized views.
You have meditated perfectly on the path that has no location.
You cannot be defeated or hindered{{note:{index616,id:UT22084-055-001-1590}}} by anyone. {13}
{{milestone:{label:15.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1591}}}“You have no residence in the three realms.
You are free from the floods{{note:{index617,id:UT22084-055-001-1592}}} and the knots.{{note:{index618,id:UT22084-055-001-1593}}}
You have cut through the bondage of the creepers of craving.{{note:{index619,id:UT22084-055-001-1594}}}{{page:{number:102,id:UT22084-055-001-5935,folio:F.52.a}}}
You are free of existence and are devoid of existence. {14}
{{milestone:{label:15.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1595}}}“You know the nonexistence that is the nature of phenomena.
You make understood in words that which cannot be described.
Just as the lion destroys the jackal,
You defeat the unwise tīrthikas. {15}
{{milestone:{label:15.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1596}}}“I have obtained today the highest treasure, 
The treasure of the Dharma taught by the Sugata.
I am freed from falling into any of the lower existences.
I will never have doubts that you are my guide. {16}
{{milestone:{label:15.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1597}}}“He placed upon my head his hand, 
Which was shining, beautiful, the color of gold. 
He gave me the consecration to be a supreme leader of humans,
With the world and its devas as witnesses.” {17}
{{milestone:{label:15.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1598}}}Conclusion of the fifteenth chapter, “The Elucidation of the Buddha’s Smile.”
{{milestone:{label:16,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-16}}}The Past
Chapter 16
{{milestone:{label:16.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1599}}}The Bhagavān then said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas thus wish to liberate all beings from all the suffering of existence. They wish to establish beings in the noble, unsurpassable bliss and joy of samādhi. Therefore they should hear this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, obtain it, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others.
{{milestone:{label:16.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1600}}}“Why is that? Young man, this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, causes one to transcend all lower existence and be freed from all illness. 
{{milestone:{label:16.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1601}}}“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas hear this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, obtain it, and meditate on it, then, young man, {{page:{number:103,id:UT22084-055-001-5936,folio:F.52.b}}} those bodhisattva mahāsattvas liberate all beings from all the sufferings of existence. They will establish them in the noble, unsurpassable bliss and joy of samādhi, this samādhi will be quickly attained, and the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood will be quickly attained.”{{note:{index620,id:UT22084-055-001-1602}}}
{{milestone:{label:16.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1603}}}Thereupon the Bhagavān, in order to teach this meaning to Candraprabha, repeated what he had previously said by explaining it in the following verses.
{{milestone:{label:16.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1604}}}“I remember that, as I was practicing in the past,
In the teaching of Sugata Siṃhadhvaja
There was a wise bhikṣu, a dharmabhāṇaka
Whose name was Brahmadatta. {1}
{{milestone:{label:16.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1605}}}“At that time I was Prince Mati.
I was tormented by the pain of an illness. 
The dharmabhāṇaka Brahmadatta 
Became my teacher at that time. {2}
{{milestone:{label:16.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1606}}}“More than five hundred physicians
Diligently sought to cure that illness, 
But they were unable to cure me of my disease.
Everyone in my family was in suffering. {3}
{{milestone:{label:16.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1607}}}“The bhikṣu heard about my illness,
And he came to me and asked about it.
Brahmadatta felt great pity for me,
And he taught me this supreme samādhi. {4}
{{milestone:{label:16.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1608}}}“When I had heard this sublime samādhi
I experienced a noble, nonworldly joy.
I understood the essential nature of phenomena
And at that time I was healed of my disease. {5}
{{milestone:{label:16.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1609}}}“That wise dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu was Dīpaṃkara
While he was practicing bodhisattva conduct,
And I was Prince Mati, who was freed from illness
Through the wisdom of the samādhi. {6}
{{milestone:{label:16.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1610}}}“Therefore, young man, in the future 
Remember past declines like that.
Tolerate the bad things the foolish will say
And keep and recite{{note:{index621,id:UT22084-055-001-1611}}} this samādhi. {7}
{{milestone:{label:16.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1612}}}“In future time, there will be many bhikṣus
Who will be covetous,{{note:{index622,id:UT22084-055-001-1613}}} malicious, and without restraint.{{note:{index623,id:UT22084-055-001-1614}}}
They will enjoy bad actions and be attached to alms bowls and robes,
And they will reject completely this samādhi. {8} {{page:{number:104,id:UT22084-055-001-5937,folio:F.53.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:16.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1615}}}“They will be unstable, distracted by their senses, and envious,
Attached to families{{note:{index624,id:UT22084-055-001-1616}}} and desiring gain.
They will always be engaged in familiarity with them
And they will reject completely{{note:{index625,id:UT22084-055-001-1617}}} this samādhi. {9}
{{milestone:{label:16.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1618}}}“They will strike with their hands and feet.
They will always engage in fun and play.
They will embrace each other and hold hands,
And will do other kinds of laypeople’s activities.{{note:{index626,id:UT22084-055-001-1619}}} {10}
{{milestone:{label:16.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1620}}}“They will have the signs of inappropriate activity.
They will always desire the daughters of others.{{note:{index627,id:UT22084-055-001-1621}}}
They will be excited and captivated by bodies,
And roam through the villages, towns, and regions. {11}
{{milestone:{label:16.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1622}}}“They will always be engaged in eating and drinking,
And similarly in dance, song, and music.
They will always be dedicated to buying and selling.
Attached to drinking, they will cast aside their shame. {12}
{{milestone:{label:16.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1623}}}“They will carry letters, engaging in inappropriate activity,
And likewise discard correct conduct and the pure path.{{note:{index628,id:UT22084-055-001-1624}}}
They will break the rules through dwelling with families,
And having broken them continue engaging in incorrect conduct. {13}{{note:{index629,id:UT22084-055-001-1625}}}
{{milestone:{label:16.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1626}}}“They will be fraudulent with weights and measures,
Always engaging in actions that the buddhas have rejected.
Through doing those actions that are sinful and defiled,
They will have bad karma and will go to the lower realms. {14}
{{milestone:{label:16.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1627}}}“They will enter homelessness, forsaking home,
Conches, gold and jewels, and great wealth;
But having entered homelessness within the Buddha’s teaching,
They will continually engage in bad actions. {15}
{{milestone:{label:16.20,id:UT22084-055-001-1628}}}“They will see wealth and grain as essential.
They will be attached to dairy cows,{{note:{index630,id:UT22084-055-001-1629}}} cattle, and carriages.
These people who do not follow the training,
Why will they have shaved their heads? {16}
{{milestone:{label:16.21,id:UT22084-055-001-1630}}}“In the past I practiced bodhisattva conduct,
Which was extremely difficult, for thousands of eons. 
I did so seeking this samādhi of peace,
But they will laugh when they hear of it. {17}
{{milestone:{label:16.22,id:UT22084-055-001-1631}}}“For a long time they will lie and will not be celibate.
Always enjoying what is harmful, they will descend to the lower realms.
They will hold up the banner of celibacy,
But will have bad conduct and what they teach will not be the Dharma. {18}
{{milestone:{label:16.23,id:UT22084-055-001-1632}}}“They will be divided against each other.
They will yearn for that which is acquired inappropriately.
They will say unpleasant things to each other,
And when they die they will go to the level of the lower existences. {19} {{page:{number:105,id:UT22084-055-001-5938,folio:F.53.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:16.24,id:UT22084-055-001-1633}}}“It will be hard to find among a hundred, a thousand,{{note:{index631,id:UT22084-055-001-1634}}}
One who has the power of patience.
Therefore there will be many who are deeply involved in quarreling.
They will explain elaborately, having rejected patience. {20}
{{milestone:{label:16.25,id:UT22084-055-001-1635}}}“They will say the words, ‘I am a bodhisattva,’ 
And those words will spread in every direction.
They will become conceited{{note:{index632,id:UT22084-055-001-1636}}} through their arrogant, false words,{{note:{index633,id:UT22084-055-001-1637}}}
But how can there be enlightenment for someone whose conduct has gone astray? {21}
{{milestone:{label:16.26,id:UT22084-055-001-1638}}}“I have never heard of, nor have I seen,
Someone whose motivation is not pure
And who has no patience for these phenomena,
Attaining enlightenment after discarding the Dharma. {22}
{{milestone:{label:16.27,id:UT22084-055-001-1639}}}“It is through fear and anxiety they will have abandoned their homes
And held firmly to the homeless life.
But having acute desires they will proceed toward destruction, 
Forsaking the way of the supreme humans. {23}{{note:{index634,id:UT22084-055-001-1640}}}
{{milestone:{label:16.28,id:UT22084-055-001-1641}}}“They will have inferior wisdom and be devoid of good qualities,
And they will always be criticizing the supreme yāna.
They will always be talking about the hundreds of faults
Of that in which they have taken refuge. {24}{{note:{index635,id:UT22084-055-001-1643}}}
{{milestone:{label:16.29,id:UT22084-055-001-1644}}}“Many will have entered homelessness because they had no livelihood. 
They will have no wish at all for the enlightenment of buddhahood.
Those foolish ones will maintain the view of a self
And become afraid when they hear of emptiness. {25}
{{milestone:{label:16.30,id:UT22084-055-001-1645}}}“They will quarrel with each other{{note:{index636,id:UT22084-055-001-1646}}}
And develop intractable evil malice.
They will say unpleasant things to each other 
And find great joy in having done bad things. {26}
{{milestone:{label:16.31,id:UT22084-055-001-1647}}}“Those who have correct conduct will have good qualities.
They will always remain loving and be skilled in patience.
They will be perfectly gentle, kind, and controlled—
Yet they will be the ones despised at that time. {27}
{{milestone:{label:16.32,id:UT22084-055-001-1648}}}“Those who have wicked minds, 
Who are dreadful, and accomplish terrible, very low actions,
Those whose conduct is not that of the Dharma and who enjoy fighting:
They will have offerings made to them at that time. {28}
{{milestone:{label:16.33,id:UT22084-055-001-1649}}}“I declare this, I know this.
Young man, if you have faith in me,
Remember this teaching by the Sugata
And never depend on those others. {29}
{{milestone:{label:16.34,id:UT22084-055-001-1650}}}“They will have strong desire and strong anger. 
They will have strong ignorance and be conceited and arrogant.
They will have unrestrained bodies and unrestrained speech
And unrestrained minds, and will descend to the lower existences. {30} {{page:{number:106,id:UT22084-055-001-5939,folio:F.54.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:16.35,id:UT22084-055-001-1651}}}“I have recited the praises of those qualities
But the bhikṣus will not practice these qualities.
Enlightenment is not attained by mere words.
For one who is dedicated to practice, enlightenment will not be difficult to attain.” {31}
{{milestone:{label:16.36,id:UT22084-055-001-1652}}}Conclusion of the sixteenth chapter, “The Past.”
{{milestone:{label:17,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-17}}}The Entranceway to the Samādhi That Is Taught by Many Buddhas
Chapter 17
{{milestone:{label:17.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1653}}}When the Bhagavān had finished speaking, the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya, who was seated there, in his mind recited this verse to the Bhagavān.{{note:{index637,id:UT22084-055-001-1654}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1655}}}“I am going, Tathāgata,{{note:{index638,id:UT22084-055-001-1656}}} to the king of mountains, 
Gṛdhrakūṭa, which is always the residence of the buddhas.
When I have gone there, lamp of the world,{{note:{index639,id:UT22084-055-001-1657}}}
I will make inconceivable offerings to you.” {i}
{{milestone:{label:17.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1658}}}The Bhagavān knew the thoughts that were in the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya’s mind, and from his own mind sent this verse to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya:
{{milestone:{label:17.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1659}}}“Go, Ajita, you who have conquered the māras,{{note:{index640,id:UT22084-055-001-1660}}}
To the king of mountains where jinas reside. 
There you will quickly accomplish 
A great unsurpassable benefit for beings.” {ii}
{{milestone:{label:17.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1661}}}So the bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya, having received in his mind that verse from the Bhagavān, paid homage to the Bhagavān in his mind and, again in his mind, circumambulated him three times. He then left the assembly and went to Gṛdhrakūṭa, the king of mountains, which has been the residence of countless buddhas, as numerous as the grains of sand in the ocean, and where there is a great caitya. 
{{milestone:{label:17.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1662}}}The moment he arrived there, for the enjoyment of the Bhagavān, he magically transformed the king of mountains to become level and vast, without any tree stumps, thorns, stones, pebbles, or gravel, and with a surrounding wall made of the seven jewels. The ground was composed of countless shining sapphire jewels and was adorned by divine adornments and jewels, all of them beyond compare, and beautified by an array of innumerable, different kinds of jewels. All the area was decorated by the clothing of Tuṣita devas, {{page:{number:107,id:UT22084-055-001-5940,folio:F.54.b}}} pervaded by the aroma of incense from a variety of censers, adorned by garlands and wreaths, scattered with various flowers; it resounded with the sound of divine music, was filled with erect and fluttering banners and flags, and over it canopies were suspended. 
{{milestone:{label:17.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1663}}}In the center of this area a divine lion throne made from the seven jewels was emanated. It was draped in cloth that was not woven, and covered with divine clothing from Tuṣita that was as soft and pleasant to the touch as down. A central awning hung above, and there were two red cushions placed upon it. It was a yojana wide and a yojana high. 
{{milestone:{label:17.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1664}}}Its beautiful footstool, made of Jambu River gold, transcended that of humans and devas. It was covered with a net of strings of pearls, and it was draped in divine, precious cottons.
{{milestone:{label:17.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1665}}}Strung upon the lion throne were strings of divine, precious bells from which came clear, beautiful, gentle sounds. In all directions there were great shining jewels. And there was emanated a precious, vast parasol, with a handle made of a great, precious jewel of stainless beryl. 
{{milestone:{label:17.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1666}}}The bodhisattva mahāsattva Maitreya now emanated an inconceivable, adorning array of various jewels on Gṛdhrakūṭa, the king of mountains, and in its entire environs. Then, in an instant, he returned to the home of the youth Candraprabha.
{{milestone:{label:17.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1667}}}Once he was back there, in his mind he paid homage to the Bhagavān, and in his mind circumambulated him three times. He then sat on his seat.
It was said:
{{milestone:{label:17.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1669}}}He manifested the mountain as a divine, vast place
With excellent, beautiful jewel flagstones— 
Inconceivable, divine, formed from the mind—
And he placed in the center a precious lion throne. {iii}
{{milestone:{label:17.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1670}}}Jinaputra Ajita also manifested 
A divine, splendid parasol that emitted delightful sounds
With great shining jewels all around,
And a handle of pure, beautiful beryl. {iv}
{{milestone:{label:17.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1671}}}Maitreya, the hero, having emanated
A variety of jewels on the mountain, 
And a precious seat that was a krośa in size, {{page:{number:108,id:UT22084-055-001-5941,folio:F.55.a}}}
In one instant returned to the house.{{note:{index641,id:UT22084-055-001-1672}}} {v} 
{{milestone:{label:17.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1673}}}Then the Bhagavān taught the Dharma to the great assembly that was like an ocean. He inspired them, he filled them with joy, and he guided them. Then he rose from his seat and departed. And with the miraculous power of a buddha he emerged through Rājagṛha’s gate of the hot springs and proceeded toward Gṛdhrakūṭa, the king of mountains. When he arrived he went to the site created by Maitreya, and having arrived there he sat upon the great lion throne that Maitreya had manifested.{{note:{index642,id:UT22084-055-001-1674}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1675}}}He was encircled by the assembly of bhikṣus, and the saṅgha of bodhisattvas gazed upon him from the front. The devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, rishis, garuḍas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and nonhumans paid homage to him. Within the ocean-like assembly, he taught the Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:17.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1676}}}Then the youth Candraprabha arrived together with a hundred thousand quintillion beings, and many millions of bodhisattva mahāsattvas who had come from other worlds. They were holding flowers, incense, and garlands; playing musical instruments and percussion; holding parasols, banners, and divine flags; and holding great garlands as offerings. 
{{milestone:{label:17.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1677}}}In order to make this offering to the Bhagavān they left the great city of Rājagṛha through the gateway of peace,{{note:{index643,id:UT22084-055-001-1678}}} and went to Gṛdhrakūṭa, to the Bhagavān. They bowed down their heads to the Bhagavān’s feet, circumambulated him three times, made a great offering to him of flowers, incense, perfume, garlands, ointments, powders, clothes, food, parasols, banners, and flags, playing music and percussion, and then they sat down in one place. In order to ask about the Dharma they sat in that place with veneration and with respect while the youth Candraprabha, kneeling on his right knee, {{page:{number:109,id:UT22084-055-001-5942,folio:F.55.b}}} with palms placed together, bowed toward the Bhagavān{{note:{index644,id:UT22084-055-001-1679}}} and said to him, “If the Bhagavān will give me an opportunity to seek answers to them, I have a few questions for the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.” 
{{milestone:{label:17.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1680}}}The Bhagavān addressed the youth Candraprabha, saying, “Young man, the Bhagavān will always give you the opportunity. Ask whatever question you wish to the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.”
{{milestone:{label:17.20,id:UT22084-055-001-1681}}}The Bhagavān having given him this opportunity, the young man Candraprabha asked, “Bhagavān, it is through possessing what qualities that bodhisattva mahāsattvas attain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena?”
The Bhagavān replied to Candraprabha, “Young man, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas possess four qualities, they will attain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. 
{{milestone:{label:17.21,id:UT22084-055-001-1683}}}“What are those four qualities? Young man, one is that bodhisattva mahāsattvas are calm, and pleasant company. They have self-restraint, and have attained a level of self-restraint such that when others abuse them or insult them, they will be patient with the abuse and the insults that are spoken, for it is their nature to have endurance; they have the view of karma, have overcome pride, and their desire is for the Dharma. Young man, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas have this first quality, they will attain this samādhi.{{note:{index645,id:UT22084-055-001-1684}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.22,id:UT22084-055-001-1685}}}“Another, young man, is that bodhisattva mahāsattvas have correct conduct. They have pure conduct, conduct that is not impaired, conduct that is free of faults, conduct that is unshakable, conduct that is unstained, conduct that has not declined, conduct that is unattached, {{page:{number:110,id:UT22084-055-001-5943,folio:F.56.a}}} conduct that is inviolate, conduct that is beyond conceptualization, conduct that is praised by the āryas, and conduct that is praised by the wise. Young man, if bodhisattva mahāsattvas have these two qualities, they will attain this samādhi.{{note:{index646,id:UT22084-055-001-1686}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.23,id:UT22084-055-001-1687}}}“Another, young man, is that bodhisattva mahāsattvas are frightened of the three realms. They are terrified of them, saddened by them,{{note:{index647,id:UT22084-055-001-1688}}} do not value them, take no delight in them,{{note:{index648,id:UT22084-055-001-1689}}} and have no attachment or clinging to them.{{note:{index649,id:UT22084-055-001-1690}}} Because they are distressed by the three realms they are dedicated to the thought, ‘I shall deliver other beings from their suffering, to somewhere other than the three realms!’ and they thus proceed to the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have these three qualities will attain this samādhi.{{note:{index650,id:UT22084-055-001-1691}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.24,id:UT22084-055-001-1692}}}“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas have faith.{{note:{index651,id:UT22084-055-001-1693}}} They insatiably seek the Dharma. They listen to many teachings. They have confidence. They long for the Dharma. They are devoted to the Dharma. They are not devoted to obtaining material gain or honors. They are not devoted to attaining success through knowledge. They think first of what will benefit others, and they teach and explain extensively to others the Dharma that they have received. They have no desire for material gain through their reputation. They think, ‘If these beings can hear this Dharma then they will proceed irreversibly to the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.’{{note:{index652,id:UT22084-055-001-1694}}} Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have these four qualities will attain this samādhi. 
{{milestone:{label:17.25,id:UT22084-055-001-1695}}}“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have these four qualities will attain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, and they will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.
{{milestone:{label:17.26,id:UT22084-055-001-1696}}}“Young man, the samādhi has been taught through this Dharma discourse by many buddhas, has been commended by many buddhas, {{page:{number:111,id:UT22084-055-001-5944,folio:F.56.b}}} has been explained by many buddhas, and has been praised{{note:{index653,id:UT22084-055-001-1697}}} by many buddhas. 
{{milestone:{label:17.27,id:UT22084-055-001-1698}}}“Young man, I have entered homelessness in the presence of many buddha bhagavāns. I heard extensively from them this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. I obtained it, asked questions about it, preserved it, recited it to others, promoted it, meditated on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgated it,{{note:{index654,id:UT22084-055-001-1699}}} and made it widely known to others.”{{note:{index655,id:UT22084-055-001-1700}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.28,id:UT22084-055-001-1701}}}Thereupon the Bhagavān taught extensively in verse what he had previously said about the samādhi doorway taught by many buddhas.
{{milestone:{label:17.29,id:UT22084-055-001-1702}}}“I remember countless, innumerable eons ago
There was a jina named Svarāṅgaghoṣa.
Tathāgata Svarāṅgaghoṣa 
Had a lifespan of six thousand years. {1}
{{milestone:{label:17.30,id:UT22084-055-001-1703}}}“After him there was a buddha,
A supreme man named Jñāneśvara.
Jñāneśvara, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of twelve thousand years. {2}
{{milestone:{label:17.31,id:UT22084-055-001-1704}}}“After Jñāneśvara there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Tejeśvara.
Tejeśvara, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of sixty-seven thousand years. {3}
{{milestone:{label:17.32,id:UT22084-055-001-1705}}}“After Tejeśvara there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Matīśvara. 
Matīśvara, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of ten million years. {4}
{{milestone:{label:17.33,id:UT22084-055-001-1706}}}“After Matīśvara there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Brahmeśvara. 
Brahmeśvara, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of fourteen thousand years.{{note:{index656,id:UT22084-055-001-1707}}} {5}
{{milestone:{label:17.34,id:UT22084-055-001-1708}}}“After Brahmeśvara there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Agnīśvara.{{note:{index657,id:UT22084-055-001-1709}}}
Agnīśvara, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of seventy-six thousand years. {6}
{{milestone:{label:17.35,id:UT22084-055-001-1710}}}“After Agnīśvara there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Brahmānana.
Brahmānana, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of seven days. {7}
{{milestone:{label:17.36,id:UT22084-055-001-1711}}}“After Brahmānana there was a buddha, {{page:{number:112,id:UT22084-055-001-5945,folio:F.57.a}}}
A jina who was named Gaṇeśvara.
Gaṇeśvara, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of a full ten million years.{{note:{index658,id:UT22084-055-001-1712}}} {8}
{{milestone:{label:17.37,id:UT22084-055-001-1713}}}“After Gaṇeśvara there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Ghoṣeśvara.
Ghoṣeśvara, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of ninety million years. {9}
{{milestone:{label:17.38,id:UT22084-055-001-1714}}}“After Ghoṣeśvara there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Ghoṣānana.
Ghoṣānana, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of a hundred million years. {10}
{{milestone:{label:17.39,id:UT22084-055-001-1715}}}“After Ghoṣānana there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Candrānana.
Candrānana, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of one day.{{note:{index659,id:UT22084-055-001-1716}}} {11}
{{milestone:{label:17.40,id:UT22084-055-001-1717}}}“After Candrānana there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Sūryānana.
Sūryānana, highest of humans,
Had a lifespan of eighteen thousand years. {12}
{{milestone:{label:17.41,id:UT22084-055-001-1718}}}“After Sūryānana there was a buddha,
Another jina who was named Brahmānana.
Brahmānana, highest of humans, [DP.138]
Had a lifespan of twenty thousand years.{{note:{index660,id:UT22084-055-001-1719}}} {13}
{{milestone:{label:17.42,id:UT22084-055-001-1720}}}“After Brahmānana there was a buddha,
A jina who was named Brahmaśrava.
Brahmaśrava, highest of humans, 
Had a lifespan of eighteen thousand years. {14}
{{milestone:{label:17.43,id:UT22084-055-001-1721}}}“In one eon these buddhas appeared
Among two hundred guides of the world.
Listen as I shall proclaim the names
Of these invincible tathāgatas:{{note:{index661,id:UT22084-055-001-1722}}} {15}
{{milestone:{label:17.44,id:UT22084-055-001-1723}}}“Anantaghoṣa and Vighuṣṭaghoṣa,
Vighuṣṭatejas and Vighuṣṭaśabda, 
Svarāvighuṣṭa and Svarārcita,
Svarāṅgaśūra and Svarāṅgaśabda, {16}
{{milestone:{label:17.45,id:UT22084-055-001-1724}}}“Jñānābala and Jñānaviśeṣaga, 
Jñānābhibhū and Jñānasamudgata, 
Jñānārcimat and Jñānābhyudgata,
Vighuṣṭajñāna and likewise Jñānaśūra, {17}
{{milestone:{label:17.46,id:UT22084-055-001-1725}}}“Brahmābala, Brahmavasu, Subrahma, 
Brahmādeva{{note:{index662,id:UT22084-055-001-1726}}} and similarly Brahmaghoṣa,
Brahmeśvara, Brahma­narendra­netra, {{page:{number:113,id:UT22084-055-001-5946,folio:F.57.b}}}
Brahmasvarāṅga, Brahmadatta,{{note:{index663,id:UT22084-055-001-1727}}} {18}
{{milestone:{label:17.47,id:UT22084-055-001-1728}}}“Tejobala, Tejavati, Sutejas, 
Tejeśvara and Tejasamudrata, 
Tejovibhu and Tejaviniścita, 
Tejasvarendra and Suvighuṣṭatejas, {19}
{{milestone:{label:17.48,id:UT22084-055-001-1729}}}“Bhīṣmabala, Bhīṣmamati, Subhīṣma,
Bhīṣmānana and Bhīṣmasamudgata,
Bhīṣmārci, Bhīṣmottara, and Bhīṣmaghoṣa—
These jinas were guides of the world. {20}
{{milestone:{label:17.49,id:UT22084-055-001-1730}}}“Gambhīraghoṣa and Śiridhāraṇa,
Viśuddha­ghoṣeśvara, Śuddhaghoṣa,{{note:{index664,id:UT22084-055-001-1731}}}
Anantaghoṣa, Suvimuktaghoṣa, 
Mārabala{{note:{index665,id:UT22084-055-001-1732}}} and Māravitrāsana, {21}
{{milestone:{label:17.50,id:UT22084-055-001-1733}}}“Sunetra, Śuddhānana, Netraśuddha, 
Viśuddhanetra and Anantanetra,
Samantanetra and Vighuṣṭanetra,
Netrābhibhu, Netrānindita, {22}
{{milestone:{label:17.51,id:UT22084-055-001-1734}}}“Dāntottara, Dānta, Sudāntacitta, 
Sudānta, Śāntendriya, Śāntamānasa, 
Śāntottara, Śāntaśirin, Praśānta, 
Śāntīya­pāraṃgata and Śāntiśūra, {23}
{{milestone:{label:17.52,id:UT22084-055-001-1735}}}“Sthitottara, Śānta, Sudāntacitta,
Sudānta, Śāntendriya, Śāntamānasa, 
Śāntottara, Śānta­śriya­jvalanta,
Śānta, Praśānteśvara, Śāntiśūra,{{note:{index666,id:UT22084-055-001-1736}}} {24}
{{milestone:{label:17.53,id:UT22084-055-001-1737}}}“Gaṇendra, Gaṇamukhya, and Gaṇeśvara,
Gaṇābhibhu, Gaṇivara, Śuddhajñānin, 
Mahāgaṇendra and Gaṇendraśūra,
And also Gaṇivara­pramocaka, {25}
{{milestone:{label:17.54,id:UT22084-055-001-1738}}}“Dharmadhvaja and similarly Dharmaketu, 
Dharmottara, Dharma­svabhāvodgata, 
Dharmabala and Sudharmaśūra, 
And Svabhāva­dharmottara­niścita. {26}
{{milestone:{label:17.55,id:UT22084-055-001-1739}}}“Also there were eight hundred million with the same name
Of Svabhāva­dharmottara­niścita.
These are the guides that appeared in two eons.
I made offerings to them for the sake of enlightenment. {27}
{{milestone:{label:17.56,id:UT22084-055-001-1740}}}“Whoever hears the name of those jinas,
Svabhāva­dharmottara­niścita,
And having heard it remembers that renowned name, {{page:{number:114,id:UT22084-055-001-5947,folio:F.58.a}}}
They will quickly attain this samādhi.” {28} 
{{milestone:{label:17.57,id:UT22084-055-001-1741}}}Then the Bhagavān, through many verses, taught extensively to the youth Candraprabha the samādhi entranceway accomplished by many buddhas in the past.{{note:{index667,id:UT22084-055-001-1742}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.58,id:UT22084-055-001-1743}}}“After inconceivable, countless eons
Following these buddhas,
There was a buddha named Narendraghoṣa, 
To whom humans and devas made offerings. {29}
{{milestone:{label:17.59,id:UT22084-055-001-1744}}}“Tathāgata Narendraghoṣa
Lived for seventy-six thousand years,
And three billion śrāvakas 
Gathered for his first assembly. {30}
{{milestone:{label:17.60,id:UT22084-055-001-1745}}}“At that time he had a shining saṅgha 
Of those who had the six higher cognitions, the three knowledges, 
Subdued senses, great powers, great miracles, 
The cessation of outflows, and who were in their last bodies. {31}
{{milestone:{label:17.61,id:UT22084-055-001-1746}}}“There was a saṅgha of bodhisattvas
Who numbered eight thousand quintillion.
They had profound understanding, fearlessness,{{note:{index668,id:UT22084-055-001-1747}}}
Great powers, and great miracles. {32}
{{milestone:{label:17.62,id:UT22084-055-001-1748}}}“They had attained the higher cognitions, eloquence,
And they had realized emptiness in everything.
They miraculously went to millions of realms 
And to even more, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. {33}
{{milestone:{label:17.63,id:UT22084-055-001-1749}}}“They came into the presence of that jina
And addressed questions to that supreme human.
They were accomplished in the sūtras and skilled in definitions. 
They were shining and moved upon the earth. {34}
{{milestone:{label:17.64,id:UT22084-055-001-1750}}}“They performed bodhisattva conduct for the benefit of beings. 
They were powerful sons of the Sugata.
They performed no bad actions through desire,
And toward them even the devas developed aspirations. {35}
{{milestone:{label:17.65,id:UT22084-055-001-1751}}}“They had no longings and were detached from the realms of existence.
They were in meditation, the field of experience of remaining in dhyāna.
They had certainty in the true meaning, and were fearless.
They maintained celibacy and were free of defilement. {36}
{{milestone:{label:17.66,id:UT22084-055-001-1752}}}“They had the confident eloquence of unceasing speech.
They were skilled in the meaning of the words and the teaching of definitions.
They were the sons of the Buddha who taught everywhere, 
And they perfectly possessed good karma. {37}
{{milestone:{label:17.67,id:UT22084-055-001-1753}}}“They maintained superior conduct throughout an infinity of eons; {{page:{number:115,id:UT22084-055-001-5948,folio:F.58.b}}}
They were always praised and extolled by the guides.
They taught the words and meaning of liberation.
They had perfectly pure conduct free of kleśas. {38}
{{milestone:{label:17.68,id:UT22084-055-001-1754}}}“They were as unstained as a lotus by water. 
They were liberated from the three realms, and were vigilant. 
They were unstained by the eight worldly concerns.
They had pure bodies and pure actions. {39}
{{milestone:{label:17.69,id:UT22084-055-001-1755}}}“They had contentment, great power, and few desires.
They were free of grasping and were established in buddha qualities.
They were a refuge and friend for all classes of beings. 
They considered practice, not words, as the essence. {40}
{{milestone:{label:17.70,id:UT22084-055-001-1756}}}“Wherever they dwelt, there they taught others.
They were adopted by all the buddhas.
They were trustworthy holders of the treasure of the jinas. 
They were terrified of the entire three realms.{{note:{index669,id:UT22084-055-001-1757}}} {41}
{{milestone:{label:17.71,id:UT22084-055-001-1758}}}“Their minds were at peace, they always had the conduct of protectors,
And they were blessed by the guides of the world.
They taught ten thousand million sūtras,
And the buddhas praised their teachings. {42}
{{milestone:{label:17.72,id:UT22084-055-001-1759}}}“They had forsaken all worldly words.{{note:{index670,id:UT22084-055-001-1760}}}
They aspired to emptiness and taught the ultimate.
They were like an ocean of good qualities; there was no end to their being praised.
Their learning was vast; they were wise and endowed with knowledge. {43}
{{milestone:{label:17.73,id:UT22084-055-001-1761}}}“If a young man were to recite their praises
Continuously for many millions of eons
He would have only uttered a small amount,
Like a drop of water from an ocean. {44}
{{milestone:{label:17.74,id:UT22084-055-001-1762}}}“At that time Narendraghoṣa
Taught this samādhi of peace, which is difficult to see.
This universe of a thousand million worlds
Was filled with devas and nāgas. {45}
{{milestone:{label:17.75,id:UT22084-055-001-1763}}}“When he taught this samādhi of peace
The ground shook in six ways.
Devas and humans as numerous as the Ganges sands
Became irreversible within the buddha’s wisdom. {46}
{{milestone:{label:17.76,id:UT22084-055-001-1764}}}“There was a human king, a sovereign 
Named Śirībala, who was very powerful.
He had five hundred sons
Who were handsome and attractive to the sight. {47}
{{milestone:{label:17.77,id:UT22084-055-001-1765}}}“The king had a harem 
Of eighty thousand million women.
The king had daughters {{page:{number:116,id:UT22084-055-001-5949,folio:F.59.a}}}
Who numbered a full four hundred billion. {48}
{{milestone:{label:17.78,id:UT22084-055-001-1766}}}“He took the eight poṣadha vows
On the full moon day of the Kārtika month,
And with the eighty thousand million others
He came before the Lord of the World. {49}
{{milestone:{label:17.79,id:UT22084-055-001-1767}}}“The king bowed down to the feet of the supreme human
And sat down before the Jina.
The supreme human knew the king’s aspiration 
And he taught this samādhi. {50}
{{milestone:{label:17.80,id:UT22084-055-001-1768}}}“When the king had heard this samādhi
He abandoned his kingdom as if it were spittle.
He renounced his beloved family and kinsmen
And entered homelessness in that jina’s teaching. {51}
{{milestone:{label:17.81,id:UT22084-055-001-1769}}}“His five hundred sons entered homelessness,
And also his harem and his daughters,
And also his other relatives,
Numbering seventy-five quintillion. {52}
{{milestone:{label:17.82,id:UT22084-055-001-1770}}}“Having entered homelessness along with his children and wives, 
He kept to the station of acquiring alms food{{note:{index671,id:UT22084-055-001-1771}}}
And steadfastly wandered in this way for eight years.
While remaining{{note:{index672,id:UT22084-055-001-1772}}} in wandering his life came to an end. {53}
{{milestone:{label:17.83,id:UT22084-055-001-1773}}}“His life having ended, that preeminent king,{{note:{index673,id:UT22084-055-001-1774}}}
Being always perfectly focused on a samādhi mind,
Was reborn into a king’s family, 
Appearing miraculously, unstained by a womb. {54}
{{milestone:{label:17.84,id:UT22084-055-001-1775}}}“Dṛḍhabala was his father’s name.
And his mother’s name was Mahāmatī.
As soon as he was born, the prince asked,
‘Is the Lord of the World present? {55}
{{milestone:{label:17.85,id:UT22084-055-001-1776}}}“ ‘The Lord of the World, who knows my mind, 
Taught to me the samādhi of peace. 
It has no causal factors, is free of causal factors,
And is the one teaching for beings in existence. {56}
{{milestone:{label:17.86,id:UT22084-055-001-1777}}}“ ‘It is the seal of the nature of all phenomena.
It is the transmission of a quintillion sūtras.
It is the unsurpassable wealth of the bodhisattvas.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {57}
{{milestone:{label:17.87,id:UT22084-055-001-1778}}}“ ‘It is the purity of the body, the purity of speech,
The purity of the mind, and the purity of view.
It transcends all objects of the mind.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {58}
{{milestone:{label:17.88,id:UT22084-055-001-1779}}}“ ‘The result of this Dharma teaching is imperishable.
It is the meditation of the supreme eightfold path.
It is the sharp wisdom of the congregation of the tathāgatas. {{page:{number:117,id:UT22084-055-001-5950,folio:F.59.b}}}
It is entering truth and constant knowledge of the Dharma.{{note:{index674,id:UT22084-055-001-1780}}} {59}
{{milestone:{label:17.89,id:UT22084-055-001-1781}}}“ ‘It is understanding the skandhas, the equality of the dhātus,
And the complete elimination of the āyatanas.
It is the direct perception of birthlessness.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {60}
{{milestone:{label:17.90,id:UT22084-055-001-1782}}}“ ‘It is discernment, the wisdom that enters peace.{{note:{index675,id:UT22084-055-001-1783}}}
It is the knowledge of the different categories of all letters.
It is transcending focusing upon the material.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {61}
{{milestone:{label:17.91,id:UT22084-055-001-1784}}}“ ‘It is the comprehension of all sounds, and the attainment of joy. 
It is the enjoyment of praising the sugatas.
It is the kindness and honesty that is the way of the āryas.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {62}
{{milestone:{label:17.92,id:UT22084-055-001-1785}}}“ ‘It is being pleasant and never frowning. 
It is being friendly and gentle with a smiling face.
It is being first to speak on seeing beings. 
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {63}
{{milestone:{label:17.93,id:UT22084-055-001-1786}}}“ ‘It is being without laziness and respecting the gurus.
It is being reverential, paying homage, and being pleasant to see.
It is being content with whatever arises, and virtuous.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {64}
{{milestone:{label:17.94,id:UT22084-055-001-1787}}}“ ‘It is having a pure livelihood and dwelling in solitary places.{{note:{index676,id:UT22084-055-001-1788}}}
It is maintaining the disciplines of mendicancy with no loss of mindfulness. 
It is being adept in the āyatanas and in the dhātus.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {65}
{{milestone:{label:17.95,id:UT22084-055-001-1789}}}“ ‘It is skill in the āyatanas, and the knowledge of the higher cognitions;
It is the elimination of the kleśas, and the level of self-subjugation.
It is the termination{{note:{index677,id:UT22084-055-001-1790}}} of all the multitudes of mantras.{{note:{index678,id:UT22084-055-001-1791}}}
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {66}
{{milestone:{label:17.96,id:UT22084-055-001-1792}}}“ ‘It transcends all the states of being in existence.
It is remembering previous lives and having no doubt in the Dharma.
It is aspiring to the Dharma and seeking to hear it.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi?{{note:{index679,id:UT22084-055-001-1793}}} {67}
{{milestone:{label:17.97,id:UT22084-055-001-1794}}}“ ‘It is a special attainment, being always engaged in meditation.
It is the knowledge of downfalls and remaining in emancipation.{{note:{index680,id:UT22084-055-001-1795}}}
It is the elimination of propensities through remaining in that emancipation. 
Does the Jina teach this samādhi?{{note:{index681,id:UT22084-055-001-1796}}} {68}
{{milestone:{label:17.98,id:UT22084-055-001-1797}}}“ ‘It is the attainment of the perfection of sharp wisdom.
It is being as unwavering and unshakable as a mountain.
It is the dhāraṇī entranceway that has the characteristic of irreversibility.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {69}
{{milestone:{label:17.99,id:UT22084-055-001-1798}}}“ ‘It is always longing for good qualities. {{page:{number:118,id:UT22084-055-001-5951,folio:F.60.a}}}
It is always{{note:{index682,id:UT22084-055-001-1799}}} avoiding bad qualities.
It is never going to the side of the kleśas.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {70}
{{milestone:{label:17.100,id:UT22084-055-001-1800}}}“ ‘The one who is wise in mastering{{note:{index683,id:UT22084-055-001-1801}}} all training,
The one who has mastered remaining in samādhi,
The one who inspires beings through knowing their thoughts
Teaches the Dharma for the supreme enlightenment of buddhahood. {71}
{{milestone:{label:17.101,id:UT22084-055-001-1802}}}“ ‘It is unique knowledge, the knowledge of births.
It is infinite knowledge, completely perfect knowledge.
It is the knowledge of the transition between all existences.
Does the Jina teach this samādhi? {72}
{{milestone:{label:17.102,id:UT22084-055-001-1803}}}“ ‘Abandoning home, aspiring to mendicancy, 
Finding no joy in the three realms, having no grasping,
And rejoicing in controlling the mind:
The supreme human teaches that Dharma. {73}
{{milestone:{label:17.103,id:UT22084-055-001-1804}}}“ ‘Having no attachment for phenomena, 
Always grasping the supreme Dharma, 
And having a stable aspiration for the ripening of karma: 
The supreme human teaches that Dharma. {74}
{{milestone:{label:17.104,id:UT22084-055-001-1805}}}“ ‘Skill in the vinaya, knowledge of the ripening of karma,
The pacification of conflict and quarrels,
Freedom from discord, the level that is free of quarrels:
The supreme human teaches that Dharma. {75}
{{milestone:{label:17.105,id:UT22084-055-001-1806}}}“ ‘Having complete patience, never having anger,
Always having skill and certainty in the Dharma,
Distinguishing between words and having the insight of wisdom:
Having developed compassion, he teaches that Dharma. {76}
{{milestone:{label:17.106,id:UT22084-055-001-1807}}}“ ‘He has taught the knowledge of the past, knowledge of the future,
The equality of the three times in the teaching of the sugatas,
And the cessation of the three aspects of an action:
That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {77}
{{milestone:{label:17.107,id:UT22084-055-001-1808}}}“ ‘The mind’s perfect stability and one-pointedness,
The body’s perfect stability as on the level of the āryas,
And at all times guarding the conduct of a mendicant:
That is the Dharma that the sage, the preeminent human, teaches. {78}
{{milestone:{label:17.108,id:UT22084-055-001-1809}}}“ ‘A pleasing sense of modesty and self-respect,
Speaking appropriate words, knowledge of the world,
The origination of phenomena, and the nature of beings:
He teaches that Dharma of the supreme, perfect enlightenment. {79}
{{milestone:{label:17.109,id:UT22084-055-001-1810}}}“ ‘Benefiting and having a sense of modesty,
Abhorring the wickedness of the mind, {{page:{number:119,id:UT22084-055-001-5952,folio:F.60.b}}}
Never abandoning the mendicant’s discipline, and begging for alms:
That is the Dharma that the supreme human teaches. {80}
{{milestone:{label:17.110,id:UT22084-055-001-1811}}}“ ‘Always maintaining a sense of modesty and self-respect,
Speaking reverently to the guru and rising to greet him,
Having overcome pride from the beginning:
That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {81}
{{milestone:{label:17.111,id:UT22084-055-001-1812}}}“ ‘That which arises from the mind is the goodness of the mind;
There is wisdom’s discrimination, and thus realization,
And the region of ignorance is always avoided:
He teaches that Dharma of supreme, perfect enlightenment. {82}
{{milestone:{label:17.112,id:UT22084-055-001-1813}}}“ ‘There is understanding of the mind, the knowledge of words, 
Being established in definitions, with certainty of meanings,
And all that is meaningless{{note:{index684,id:UT22084-055-001-1814}}} is always avoided:
That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {83}
{{milestone:{label:17.113,id:UT22084-055-001-1815}}}“ ‘Always associating with good persons
And always avoiding bad persons,
And always being attracted to and delighting in the Jina:
That is the supreme Dharma that the Jina teaches. {84}
{{milestone:{label:17.114,id:UT22084-055-001-1816}}}“ ‘The description of designations and appellations,{{note:{index685,id:UT22084-055-001-1817}}}
The continual avoidance of the suffering of saṃsāra,
And indifference to whether there is gain or no gain:
That is the supreme Dharma that the Jina teaches. {85}
{{milestone:{label:17.115,id:UT22084-055-001-1818}}}“ ‘There is no amazement if honors are gained,
There is equanimity when there are no honors,
And there is never pride when there are praises:
This is nature of the teaching that benefits the world. {86}
{{milestone:{label:17.116,id:UT22084-055-001-1819}}}“ ‘All abuse and disgrace is endured,
There is no association with any householder,
And there is no mingling with homeless mendicants:{{note:{index686,id:UT22084-055-001-1820}}}
That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {87}
{{milestone:{label:17.117,id:UT22084-055-001-1821}}}“ ‘Remaining in the Buddha’s scope of conduct,
Rejecting all that is not that conduct,
And having perfect conduct and a well-controlled mind:
That is the way of the Dharma that the Sugata teaches. {88}
{{milestone:{label:17.118,id:UT22084-055-001-1822}}}“ ‘Always rejecting the dharma of the foolish,
Rejecting all that disgraces the family of the Buddha,
Always protecting the teaching of the Buddha:
That is what the Jina, the Lord of the Dharma, teaches. {89}
{{milestone:{label:17.119,id:UT22084-055-001-1823}}}“ ‘Speaking little, pleasantly, and articulately,
Speaking good and gentle words to others,
Subjugating adversaries through the Dharma:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {90}
{{milestone:{label:17.120,id:UT22084-055-001-1824}}}“ ‘Arriving at the right time, and not the wrong time, {{page:{number:120,id:UT22084-055-001-5953,folio:F.61.a}}}
Never depending on any ordinary being,
Not being saddened on encountering suffering:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {91}
{{milestone:{label:17.121,id:UT22084-055-001-1825}}}“ ‘When seeing the poor, bringing them wealth;
When seeing those with bad conduct, feeling compassion; 
Always teaching those things that are beneficial:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {92}
{{milestone:{label:17.122,id:UT22084-055-001-1826}}}“ ‘Benefiting beings through the Dharma,
Always giving away worldly material things,
Never accumulating, never amassing:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {93}
{{milestone:{label:17.123,id:UT22084-055-001-1827}}}“ ‘Praising correct conduct and condemning bad conduct,
Being free of dishonesty and relying on those with correct conduct,
Giving away one’s possessions and not relying on wealth:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {94}
{{milestone:{label:17.124,id:UT22084-055-001-1828}}}“ ‘Providing for the guru with a higher motivation, 
Doing all that he has told one to do, 
Never ceasing from serving the dharmabhāṇaka:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {95}
{{milestone:{label:17.125,id:UT22084-055-001-1829}}}“ ‘Always being respectful and delighted, 
Remaining continually in a peaceful view,
Always being sure of one’s past conduct:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {96}
{{milestone:{label:17.126,id:UT22084-055-001-1830}}}“ ‘Always following those with correct conduct,
With skillful methods shunning{{note:{index687,id:UT22084-055-001-1831}}} concepts, 
Repelling identification and the characteristics of things:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {97}
{{milestone:{label:17.127,id:UT22084-055-001-1832}}}“ ‘Being skilled in the words produced within the sūtras,
Having certainty in the words that teach the truth,
The manifestation of the wisdom of liberation:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {98}
{{milestone:{label:17.128,id:UT22084-055-001-1833}}}“ ‘Speaking words that are never contradictory, 
Skillful in the certainty of what is taught,{{note:{index688,id:UT22084-055-001-1834}}}
And using words that will not be doubted:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching.{{note:{index689,id:UT22084-055-001-1835}}} {i}
{{milestone:{label:17.129,id:UT22084-055-001-1836}}}“ ‘Always relying on the Dharma of emptiness,
Maintaining fearlessly the power of correct conduct,
And applying equality through remaining in samādhi:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {99}
{{milestone:{label:17.130,id:UT22084-055-001-1837}}}“ ‘Not wishing to attain intellectual knowledge, 
Keeping the mind free from hypocrisy, 
And rejecting the creation of any view:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {100} {{page:{number:121,id:UT22084-055-001-5954,folio:F.61.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.131,id:UT22084-055-001-1838}}}“ ‘Supreme confidence in speech and sublime retention,
The limitless radiance of wisdom, 
And correct eloquence with the power of mantra:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {101}
{{milestone:{label:17.132,id:UT22084-055-001-1839}}}“ ‘Meditation on the path through this doorway of correct conduct,{{note:{index690,id:UT22084-055-001-1840}}}
Excellent practice, instruction, and conduct,{{note:{index691,id:UT22084-055-001-1841}}}
And teaching that follows practicing the teaching:{{note:{index692,id:UT22084-055-001-1842}}}
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {102}
{{milestone:{label:17.133,id:UT22084-055-001-1843}}}“ ‘The appropriate patience that is praised by the buddhas,
The maintenance of patience that avoids bad actions,
And eliminating ignorance by being established in knowledge:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {103}
{{milestone:{label:17.134,id:UT22084-055-001-1844}}}“ ‘The level of yoga{{note:{index693,id:UT22084-055-001-1845}}} that is based upon wisdom,
The mastery of yoga through entering enlightenment,
The continual reliance on good beings:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {104}
{{milestone:{label:17.135,id:UT22084-055-001-1846}}}“ ‘It is the constant avoidance of unrestrained practitioners,{{note:{index694,id:UT22084-055-001-1847}}}
It is the level of buddhahood taught by tathāgatas,
And it is rejoiced in by all who are wise:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {105}
{{milestone:{label:17.136,id:UT22084-055-001-1848}}}“ ‘It is rejected by the foolish and ignorant.
It is not the level{{note:{index695,id:UT22084-055-001-1849}}} of the numerous śrāvakas,{{note:{index696,id:UT22084-055-001-1850}}}
And it is always obtained by the bodhisattvas:
That is the nature of the Jina’s teaching. {106}
{{milestone:{label:17.137,id:UT22084-055-001-1851}}}“ ‘It is realized{{note:{index697,id:UT22084-055-001-1852}}} by the tathāgatas.
It is offered to and honored by the devas.
It is rejoiced in by a hundred billion Brahmās.
Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {107}
{{milestone:{label:17.138,id:UT22084-055-001-1853}}}“ ‘Thousands of nāgas always pay homage to it,
And so do garuḍas, yakṣas, and kinnaras.
It is the supreme enlightenment taught by the Jina.
Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {108}
{{milestone:{label:17.139,id:UT22084-055-001-1854}}}“ ‘It is always obtained by those who are wise.
It is the perfect attainment of the best, supreme wealth.
It is the supreme nonmaterial medicine of wisdom. 
Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {109}
{{milestone:{label:17.140,id:UT22084-055-001-1855}}}“ ‘It is wisdom’s treasure of unceasing eloquence.
Ten million sūtras are contained within it. 
It is accurate knowledge, the complete knowledge of the three realms.
Is the Jina teaching this samādhi? {110}
{{milestone:{label:17.141,id:UT22084-055-001-1856}}}“ ‘It is a boat that crosses to the other shore,
It is a ship that crosses a great river, {{page:{number:122,id:UT22084-055-001-5955,folio:F.62.a}}}
And it increases fame and garlands of praises 
For those to whom this samādhi of peace is taught. {111}
{{milestone:{label:17.142,id:UT22084-055-001-1857}}}“ ‘Those who teach this samādhi of peace
Are praised by all the tathāgatas,
Extolled by the chiefs among humans,
And unceasingly commended by bodhisattvas. {112}
{{milestone:{label:17.143,id:UT22084-055-001-1858}}}“ ‘It is the teaching of love to end bad actions.
It is the level of compassion’s equanimity. 
It is the comfort of the greatly famed ones{{note:{index698,id:UT22084-055-001-1859}}}
For the ones to whom this samādhi is taught. {113}
{{milestone:{label:17.144,id:UT22084-055-001-1860}}}“ ‘It is the practice of the teaching of the lion’s roar.
It originates from the supreme wisdom of buddhahood.
It is the seal of the nature of all phenomena.
This is the samādhi taught by the guides. {114}
{{milestone:{label:17.145,id:UT22084-055-001-1861}}}“ ‘It brings the attainment of omniscient wisdom,
It is the conduct of those established in enlightenment,
And it also terrifies the army of the māras.
This is the samādhi of peace taught by the Jina. {115}
{{milestone:{label:17.146,id:UT22084-055-001-1862}}}“ ‘This knowledge{{note:{index699,id:UT22084-055-001-1863}}} is the protection that is based in the Dharma.
It is the supreme protection in the midst of enemies. 
It is the subjugation of adversaries through the Dharma:
This is the samādhi of peace taught by the Jina.{{note:{index700,id:UT22084-055-001-1864}}} {116}
{{milestone:{label:17.147,id:UT22084-055-001-1865}}}“ ‘This is the teaching of the level of eloquence.
It is the strengths, the liberations, and likewise the powers,
And it is the eighteen unique qualities of a buddha:
That is the practice of this samādhi, this peace. {117}
{{milestone:{label:17.148,id:UT22084-055-001-1866}}}“ ‘It is seeking the ten strengths,
It is the omen of the coming of buddha wisdom,
