It is the buddhadharma taught by the supreme being,
And it is the teaching that compassionately benefits the world. {118}
{{milestone:{label:17.149,id:UT22084-055-001-1867}}}“ ‘It is possessed by the sons of the buddhas.
It is the path taught for those who seek enlightenment.
It is rejoiced in by the offspring of the sugatas
When they hear this samādhi of peace that is difficult to see. {119}
{{milestone:{label:17.150,id:UT22084-055-001-1868}}}“ ‘It is the complete wisdom of buddhahood.
It is what the wise bodhisattva seeks. 
One with a pure mind, clear and unblemished,{{note:{index701,id:UT22084-055-001-1869}}}
Practices the peace of this samādhi. {120}
{{milestone:{label:17.151,id:UT22084-055-001-1870}}}“ ‘One who has a pure body like that of the jinas,
Who has the knowledge of liberation, the vision of liberation, 
And who is never afflicted by the bondage of desire,
Practices this excellent samādhi. {121} {{page:{number:123,id:UT22084-055-001-5956,folio:F.62.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:17.152,id:UT22084-055-001-1871}}}“ ‘One who is not on the level of anger and is free of ignorance,
In whom wisdom has arisen{{note:{index702,id:UT22084-055-001-1872}}} and who seeks liberation,{{note:{index703,id:UT22084-055-001-1873}}}
In whom knowledge has developed and ignorance is destroyed,
Practices the peace of this samādhi. {122}
{{milestone:{label:17.153,id:UT22084-055-001-1874}}}“ ‘This samādhi of peace is taught to the meditator
For whom liberation is central, and is fulfilled by this teaching.
The one with the sight of the faultless buddhas
Practices the peace of this samādhi. {123}
{{milestone:{label:17.154,id:UT22084-055-001-1875}}}“ ‘The clairvoyance that reveals many realms,
The miraculous powers that reveal infinite buddhas,
And dhāraṇī is also not difficult to attain
For the one who practices this samādhi. {124}
{{milestone:{label:17.155,id:UT22084-055-001-1876}}}“ ‘The senses are pacified in this state of enlightenment.
There is the revelation of infinite blessings,
And subtle, vast, and pure wisdom
For the one who practices this samādhi. {125}
{{milestone:{label:17.156,id:UT22084-055-001-1877}}}“ ‘For the one who has not heard this samādhi of peace,
Practice without self-restraint will bring no realization, 
And as all the words will have been subverted,
No understanding will be possible from speech. {126}
{{milestone:{label:17.157,id:UT22084-055-001-1878}}}“ ‘This is known by wise bodhisattvas 
Just as taught by the Lord of Dharma. 
There is faultless realization of peace
For the one who practices this samādhi. {127}
{{milestone:{label:17.158,id:UT22084-055-001-1879}}}“ ‘For the one who practices this samādhi
With diligent application, having possession of it,
Constantly serving it, and perfectly keeping it,
There will be cessation of suffering and the end of rebirth. {128}
{{milestone:{label:17.159,id:UT22084-055-001-1880}}}“ ‘It has been taught that all phenomena are birthless,
As are all the existences of beings. 
Is the Jina teaching this samādhi
Of the greatly famous, supremely wise buddhas?’ {129}
{{milestone:{label:17.160,id:UT22084-055-001-1881}}}“A full eighty-eight trillion beings 
Heard these verses recited by the prince,
Attained the patience that corresponded to those words,
And were established in irreversible progress toward buddha wisdom. {130}
{{milestone:{label:17.161,id:UT22084-055-001-1882}}}“Dṛḍhabala said to the prince,
‘The Lord of the World is still present.
I have a question for you, my son: 
Where did you hear of this samādhi?’ {131}
{{milestone:{label:17.162,id:UT22084-055-001-1883}}}“The prince said to the king, ‘Listen! {{page:{number:124,id:UT22084-055-001-5957,folio:F.63.a}}}
During one eon I have seen 
A quintillion buddhas, honored them all, 
And asked them for this samādhi of peace. {132}
{{milestone:{label:17.163,id:UT22084-055-001-1884}}}“ ‘And for another ninety-four{{note:{index704,id:UT22084-055-001-1885}}} eons,
And for a thousand quintillion eons,
I remember all my births wherever they were, 
And I was never born from a womb. {133}
{{milestone:{label:17.164,id:UT22084-055-001-1886}}}“ ‘Then I meditated upon this samādhi.
I listened correctly to the teaching of those jinas.
Having heard it I had longing for what had been described.
Free from uncertainty I embraced enlightenment. {134}
{{milestone:{label:17.165,id:UT22084-055-001-1887}}}“ ‘I questioned whatever bhikṣus
Had understood this samādhi.
I venerated them respectfully
As if they were benefactors of the world. {135}
{{milestone:{label:17.166,id:UT22084-055-001-1888}}}“ ‘When I received even one verse from them
I practiced that teaching properly 
And considered them to be teachers,
Venerating them with the respect shown to buddhas. {136}
{{milestone:{label:17.167,id:UT22084-055-001-1889}}}“ ‘Whenever someone questioned me
About my understanding of this samādhi,
Even in dreams I had no doubts
That I would become a jina, a guide of the world. {137}
{{milestone:{label:17.168,id:UT22084-055-001-1890}}}“ ‘I respectfully attended 
To senior, middle, and junior bhikṣus.
With that respect my renown increased,
As did my merit, fame, and qualities.{{note:{index705,id:UT22084-055-001-1891}}} {138}
{{milestone:{label:17.169,id:UT22084-055-001-1892}}}“ ‘I had no desire for conflict or quarrels.
At that time, I had few desires.
Those who do bad actions are reborn in certain existences.
Those who do good actions are reborn in other existences. {139}
{{milestone:{label:17.170,id:UT22084-055-001-1893}}}“ ‘One hears unpleasant words from those
Who, without restraint, act inappropriately.
At that time I became the lord of my own actions. 
The karma that is created is never lost. {140}
{{milestone:{label:17.171,id:UT22084-055-001-1894}}}“ ‘I did not at that time become absorbed in anger.
I maintained the power of patience, which is praised by the buddhas.
The guides have always praised patience;
Attaining enlightenment is not difficult for those who practice patience. {141}
{{milestone:{label:17.172,id:UT22084-055-001-1895}}}“ ‘I continually had correct conduct
And established others in correct conduct.
I always spoke the praises of correct conduct, {{page:{number:125,id:UT22084-055-001-5958,folio:F.63.b}}}
And what I spoke at that time was praiseworthy. {142}
{{milestone:{label:17.173,id:UT22084-055-001-1896}}}“ ‘I was always speaking the praises of solitude.
I always maintained correct conduct.
I established others in the poṣadha vows
And I introduced them to enlightenment. {143}
{{milestone:{label:17.174,id:UT22084-055-001-1897}}}“ ‘I established them in celibacy,
I introduced them to the meaning of the Dharma,
And I awoke them to the path to enlightenment, 
For which they had endless devotion.{{note:{index706,id:UT22084-055-001-1898}}} {144}
{{milestone:{label:17.175,id:UT22084-055-001-1899}}}“ ‘I remember an eon in the past 
When there was the jina Svarāṅgaghoṣa.{{note:{index707,id:UT22084-055-001-1900}}}
I took a vow in his presence
To have the power of patience at all times. {145}
{{milestone:{label:17.176,id:UT22084-055-001-1901}}}“ ‘I remained faithful to that vow
For eight hundred and forty million years.
Although Māra reviled and abused me,
My mind remained unshakable. {146}
{{milestone:{label:17.177,id:UT22084-055-001-1902}}}“ ‘Māra put me to the test, 
And discovered my love and patience to be enduring.
And with faith{{note:{index708,id:UT22084-055-001-1903}}} he bowed down to my feet,
And I established five hundred beings on the path to supreme enlightenment. {147}
{{milestone:{label:17.178,id:UT22084-055-001-1904}}}“ ‘At all times I was free of avarice 
And always praised generosity.
I became wealthy, possessing many riches
And was a benefactor in times of famine. {148}
{{milestone:{label:17.179,id:UT22084-055-001-1905}}}“ ‘I pay homage to any monks
Who possess this samādhi,
Who recite it and teach it. 
They all become supreme men. {149}
{{milestone:{label:17.180,id:UT22084-055-001-1906}}}“ ‘Because of that unsurpassable karma
I saw many buddhas, many lords of the world.
I entered into homelessness in the teachings of those jinas
And I always became a wise dharmabhāṇaka. {150}
{{milestone:{label:17.181,id:UT22084-055-001-1907}}}“ ‘I was always engaged in the discipline of a mendicant.
I always remained in the solitude of forests.
I never gave the appearance of spirituality in order to obtain food.
I was content with whatever I obtained. {151}
{{milestone:{label:17.182,id:UT22084-055-001-1908}}}“ ‘At all times I was free of envy.
I had no attachment to a family.
Attachment to family causes envy.
Without envy I remained in the pleasant forests. {152}
{{milestone:{label:17.183,id:UT22084-055-001-1909}}}“ ‘At all times I had loving-kindness. {{page:{number:126,id:UT22084-055-001-5959,folio:F.64.a}}}
When I was abused I did not become angry.
As I was always kind, the garland of fame
Of my compassion spread in the four directions. {153}
{{milestone:{label:17.184,id:UT22084-055-001-1910}}}“ ‘I was always content, with few desires.
I was dedicated to mendicancy in solitary places. 
I never abandoned begging for alms.
I remained unwaveringly committed to mendicancy. {154}
{{milestone:{label:17.185,id:UT22084-055-001-1911}}}“ ‘I always had faith and belief. 
I always had great belief in the Buddha’s teaching.
I obtained many benefits from having belief. 
I became attractive with faultless faculties. {155}
{{milestone:{label:17.186,id:UT22084-055-001-1912}}}“ ‘I practiced whatever I taught.
I always valued practice above all else.
As I valued practice above all else,
Devas and nāgas believed in me and honored me. {156}
{{milestone:{label:17.187,id:UT22084-055-001-1913}}}“ ‘There are also numerous other qualities,
Other than these that I have described. 
They should always be trained in by the wise ones
Who wish for the enlightenment of buddhahood. {157}
{{milestone:{label:17.188,id:UT22084-055-001-1914}}}“ ‘I remember the greatest number of hardships
That I practiced through numerous eons,{{note:{index709,id:UT22084-055-001-1915}}}
So numerous{{note:{index710,id:UT22084-055-001-1916}}} I am unable to describe them.{{note:{index711,id:UT22084-055-001-1917}}}
I will now go{{note:{index712,id:UT22084-055-001-1918}}} into the presence of the Sugata.’ {158}
{{milestone:{label:17.189,id:UT22084-055-001-1919}}}“That wise bodhisattva with sharp wisdom
At that moment attained the five higher cognitions.
Through miraculous power he came before the Jina, 
Accompanied by eight hundred million beings. {159}
{{milestone:{label:17.190,id:UT22084-055-001-1920}}}“Dṛḍhabala was extremely pleased,
And, accompanied by one billion six hundred million beings,
He came into the presence of the Buddha,
Bowed down to his feet, and sat before him. {160}
{{milestone:{label:17.191,id:UT22084-055-001-1921}}}“Knowing the aspiration of that king,
The Lord of humans taught this samādhi.
When the king had heard that samādhi
He renounced his kingdom and entered homelessness. {161}
{{milestone:{label:17.192,id:UT22084-055-001-1922}}}“Homeless, he meditated on this samādhi,
And he recited it and taught it.
After sixty eons had passed
He became a jina named Padmottara. {162}
{{milestone:{label:17.193,id:UT22084-055-001-1923}}}“The one billion six hundred million beings 
Who had come with the king into the presence of the Jina
Also heard this samādhi, {{page:{number:127,id:UT22084-055-001-5960,folio:F.64.b}}}
And with the highest joy they entered homelessness. {163}
{{milestone:{label:17.194,id:UT22084-055-001-1924}}}“Homeless, they possessed this samādhi,
And recited it and taught it.
After six trillion eons had passed
They all reached supreme enlightenment in the same eon. {164}
{{milestone:{label:17.195,id:UT22084-055-001-1925}}}“They all had the name Ananta­jñānanottara.
They were buddhas to whom devas and humans made offerings.
Each of those supreme humans liberated as many beings
As there are grains of sand in the Ganges. {165}
{{milestone:{label:17.196,id:UT22084-055-001-1926}}}“I was King Śirībala.{{note:{index713,id:UT22084-055-001-1927}}}
The practitioners of this supreme bodhisattva conduct,
Those who were my five hundred sons,
Are these guardians of the Dharma. {166}
{{milestone:{label:17.197,id:UT22084-055-001-1928}}}“The one who was my mother 
Was Māyādevī{{note:{index714,id:UT22084-055-001-1929}}} in this time. 
My four hundred billion daughters 
All entered nirvāṇa. {{note:{index715,id:UT22084-055-001-1930}}} {166b}
{{milestone:{label:17.198,id:UT22084-055-001-1931}}}“The king who was named Dṛḍhabala, 
The powerful cakravartin with many treasures,
Became King Śuddhodana{{note:{index716,id:UT22084-055-001-1932}}} in this age,
And has been my father in various lifetimes.{{note:{index717,id:UT22084-055-001-1933}}} {166c}
{{milestone:{label:17.199,id:UT22084-055-001-1934}}}“Thus have I for ten billion eons
Exercised diligence that is free of laziness.
The pure yearning for this samādhi
Brings the accomplishment of supreme enlightenment. {167}
{{milestone:{label:17.200,id:UT22084-055-001-1935}}}“Therefore, young man, those bodhisattvas
Who wish to meditate{{note:{index718,id:UT22084-055-001-1936}}} on this samādhi
Should exercise diligence, regardless of risks to their lives,
And always follow, young man, my example.” {168}
{{milestone:{label:17.201,id:UT22084-055-001-1937}}}Conclusion of the seventeenth chapter, “The Entranceway to the Samādhi That Is Taught by Many Buddhas.” {{note:{index719,id:UT22084-055-001-1938}}}
{{milestone:{label:18,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-18}}}The Entrustment of the Samādhi 
Chapter 18
{{milestone:{label:18.1,id:UT22084-055-001-1939}}}The Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, in that way know that there are four beneficial qualities possessed by bodhisattva mahāsattvas who obtain this samādhi, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, and make it widely known to others.
{{milestone:{label:18.2,id:UT22084-055-001-1940}}}“What are those four beneficial qualities? They will be unsurpassable in merit, they will be undefeatable by opponents, they will have unlimited wisdom, and they will have unending confidence of speech. 
{{milestone:{label:18.3,id:UT22084-055-001-1941}}}Young man, you should know{{note:{index720,id:UT22084-055-001-1942}}} that bodhisattva mahāsattvas {{page:{number:128,id:UT22084-055-001-5961,folio:F.65.a}}} who obtain this samādhi, study it, keep it, read it out loud, disseminate it, teach it, chant it, and make it widely known to others will possess these four beneficial qualities.”
The Bhagavān then recited these verses:
{{milestone:{label:18.4,id:UT22084-055-001-1944}}}“Throughout time they will be 
Unsurpassable in merit
Through attaining this samādhi of peace.
That is the range of activity of all the buddhas. {1}
{{milestone:{label:18.5,id:UT22084-055-001-1945}}}“Throughout time these heroes 
Will be protected by merit,
Practicing supreme, pure, 
Unique bodhisattva conduct. {2}
{{milestone:{label:18.6,id:UT22084-055-001-1946}}}“There will be no adversary
Whatsoever who can harm them.
They will, throughout time,
Be in the care of the buddhas. {3}
{{milestone:{label:18.7,id:UT22084-055-001-1947}}}“Throughout time their wisdom 
Will be immeasurable.
Their confidence will be eternal
Through their possessing this state of peace. {4}
{{milestone:{label:18.8,id:UT22084-055-001-1948}}}“They will have an eternally unsurpassable accumulation of merit.
They will have most excellent bodhisattva conduct.
They will not be attacked by adversaries,
Having come into possession of this samādhi of supreme peace. {5}
{{milestone:{label:18.9,id:UT22084-055-001-1949}}}“They will have vast and sharp wisdom 
And thus will have eternal confidence and pure sight.
Those wise ones will always have
The power of memory and the power of retention. {6}
{{milestone:{label:18.10,id:UT22084-055-001-1950}}}“The meaningful words that they teach
Will be most beautiful to the minds of the wise.
Many beings with wisdom will know 
This supreme peaceful samādhi that is taught. {7}
{{milestone:{label:18.11,id:UT22084-055-001-1951}}}“They will obtain perfect, excellent Dharma robes, 
Bedding, invitations, and hard and soft food.
The ones who possess this supreme samādhi of peace
Will be very youthful and handsome. {8}
{{milestone:{label:18.12,id:UT22084-055-001-1952}}}“They will see many buddhas, lords of worlds,
And make unequaled offerings to those guides.
In seeking this supreme samādhi of peace
They will encounter no impediment. {9}
{{milestone:{label:18.13,id:UT22084-055-001-1953}}}“They will be in the presence of the lords of worlds
And made happy by hundreds of beautiful verses. {{page:{number:129,id:UT22084-055-001-5962,folio:F.65.b}}}
Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace
They will never experience decline. {10}
{{milestone:{label:18.14,id:UT22084-055-001-1954}}}“A Lord of the World will be present before them
With the beautiful primary and secondary signs of the body.
Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace
There will be no decline in their wisdom. {11}
{{milestone:{label:18.15,id:UT22084-055-001-1955}}}“They will never be disheartened.
They will always be wealthy and never poor.
Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace
There will be no attachment in their mind. {12}
{{milestone:{label:18.16,id:UT22084-055-001-1956}}}“They will never have an unfavorable existence.
They will be world rulers, cakravartin kings.
Having gained this supreme samādhi of peace
Their kingdoms will always be happy. {13}
{{milestone:{label:18.17,id:UT22084-055-001-1957}}}“They will have vast wisdom free of uncertainty
Through unceasing teachings for hundreds of eons.
Having heard this samādhi, this level of peace,
Constant, they will follow whatever has been taught. {14}
{{milestone:{label:18.18,id:UT22084-055-001-1958}}}“Though one were to describe the benefits of the ten strengths
Throughout countless, endless millions of eons, 
One would not have spoken of even a fraction of them.
It would be like taking a drop of water from the ocean.” {15}
{{milestone:{label:18.19,id:UT22084-055-001-1959}}}At that time the young man, with great joy,
Stood up and paid homage with his palms together.
Joyfully standing before the one with the ten strengths
He uttered these inspired words: {16}
{{milestone:{label:18.20,id:UT22084-055-001-1960}}}“Inconceivable great hero,
Lord of the World, illuminator,
These benefits have been taught to me
By you, the Lord of humans. {17}
{{milestone:{label:18.21,id:UT22084-055-001-1961}}}“Compassionate one who wishes to bring benefit,
Great hero, pray tell me,
Who, in the future,
Will listen to this samādhi?” {18}
{{milestone:{label:18.22,id:UT22084-055-001-1962}}}The one with a voice like the avadavat’s song,
The Teacher who had taught this to him,
The Bhagavān, who had unimpeded wisdom,
Answered him with these words: {19}
{{milestone:{label:18.23,id:UT22084-055-001-1963}}}“Listen, young man, and I will explain
That which is the highest practice.
Those who follow the Dharma
Will be the ones who listens to this sūtra. {20}
{{milestone:{label:18.24,id:UT22084-055-001-1964}}}“They will make offerings to the lords of humans;
They will seek the wisdom of buddhahood.
Developing a loving mind,
They will listen to this sūtra. {21} {{page:{number:130,id:UT22084-055-001-5963,folio:F.66.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:18.25,id:UT22084-055-001-1965}}}“Those who have the qualities of mendicancy{{note:{index721,id:UT22084-055-001-1966}}}
And the qualities of austerity,{{note:{index722,id:UT22084-055-001-1967}}}
And who maintain this practice,
Will be ones who listen to this sūtra. {22}
{{milestone:{label:18.26,id:UT22084-055-001-1968}}}“They will not listen to this sūtra 
When it is in the hands of those whose acts are evil,
Nor of those who have lost their correct conduct
Regarding the teaching of the lords of worlds. {23}
{{milestone:{label:18.27,id:UT22084-055-001-1969}}}“They will hear it when in the hands
Of the celibates, the heroes,
Those who have a mind free of craving
And who have been consecrated by the buddhas. {24}
{{milestone:{label:18.28,id:UT22084-055-001-1970}}}“In future times they will hear 
This sūtra when it is in the hands
Of those who have served the buddhas,
The lords of the world, in the past. {25}
{{milestone:{label:18.29,id:UT22084-055-001-1971}}}“Those who in previous lifetimes
Have been tīrthikas
Will experience no joy
When they hear this sūtra. {26}
{{milestone:{label:18.30,id:UT22084-055-001-1972}}}“Those who have entered homelessness
In my teaching in order to have a livelihood 
Will be under the power of gain and honor,
And they will criticize each other. {27}
{{milestone:{label:18.31,id:UT22084-055-001-1973}}}“Many bhikṣus with unrestrained senses,
Who covet the wives of others, 
Who wish for gain and have poor conduct,
Will have no faith in this sūtra. {28}
{{milestone:{label:18.32,id:UT22084-055-001-1974}}}“Those who do not intend to attain 
Merit for buddhahood or to attain dhyāna,
And who maintain the conception of a self,
Will have no faith in this sūtra. {29}
{{milestone:{label:18.33,id:UT22084-055-001-1975}}}“In future times there will be those
Who are intent on the result of worldly dhyānas.
They will eat the alms food of arhats 
And criticize the enlightenment of buddhahood. {30}
{{milestone:{label:18.34,id:UT22084-055-001-1976}}}“One who rejects this sūtra
Will have greater bad karma
Than someone who destroys 
All the caityas in this Jambudvīpa. {31}
{{milestone:{label:18.35,id:UT22084-055-001-1977}}}“One who rejects this sūtra
Will have greater bad karma
Than someone who kills as many arhats
As there are grains of sand in the Ganges. {32}
{{milestone:{label:18.36,id:UT22084-055-001-1978}}}“Who among you has the fortitude
To teach this sūtra
In the dreadful future time
When the Dharma is ruined?”{{note:{index723,id:UT22084-055-001-1979}}} {33} 
{{milestone:{label:18.37,id:UT22084-055-001-1980}}}The young man stood up, weeping,
And at that time spoke to the Jina.
This heart-born son of the Buddha 
Roared thus this lion’s roar: {34} {{page:{number:131,id:UT22084-055-001-5964,folio:F.66.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:18.38,id:UT22084-055-001-1981}}}“In the dreadful time in future
When the Buddha has passed away,
Without concern for my life or body
I will spread this sūtra widely. {35}
{{milestone:{label:18.39,id:UT22084-055-001-1982}}}“I will endure 
The false talk of fools 
And, Guide, I will undergo
Their abuse and threats. {36}
{{milestone:{label:18.40,id:UT22084-055-001-1983}}}“I shall cleanse myself of whatever bad actions
I have done in the past
And any maliciousness 
Toward other bodhisattvas.” {37} 
{{milestone:{label:18.41,id:UT22084-055-001-1984}}}The Buddha, who was the color of gold,
Placed his hand upon Candraprabha’s head.
The Tathāgata, who had a gentle voice,
The Teacher, then said to him, {38}
{{milestone:{label:18.42,id:UT22084-055-001-1985}}}“I give you my blessing.
Young man, in the future
There will be no obstacle to your celibacy
Nor will there be to your life.” {39}
{{milestone:{label:18.43,id:UT22084-055-001-1986}}}Eight hundred dharmabhāṇakas 
Who were present stood up and said,
“In future times we also
Will be holders of this sūtra.” {40}
{{milestone:{label:18.44,id:UT22084-055-001-1987}}}Eight hundred million
Devas, nāgas, and yakṣas stood up,
And another six trillion,
And said to the guide of the world, {41}
{{milestone:{label:18.45,id:UT22084-055-001-1988}}}“Guide, in future times
We will protect
These bhikṣus who
Stood up today.” {42}
{{milestone:{label:18.46,id:UT22084-055-001-1989}}}When this sūtra was taught,
Through the blessing of the Teacher,
Buddha realms shook, in numbers
Equal to the Ganges sands. {43}
{{milestone:{label:18.47,id:UT22084-055-001-1990}}}The Lord of the World sent
To all those shaken buddha realms
Emanations of the Buddha
Who taught the Dharma there. {44}
{{milestone:{label:18.48,id:UT22084-055-001-1991}}}In each of those realms
Countless millions of beings 
Were established in the wisdom of buddhahood
When they had heard that Dharma. {45}
{{milestone:{label:18.49,id:UT22084-055-001-1992}}}In those buddha realms 
Nine hundred million devas{{note:{index724,id:UT22084-055-001-1993}}}
Developed the aspiration to enlightenment
And scattered flowers on the Buddha. {46}
{{milestone:{label:18.50,id:UT22084-055-001-1994}}}The Lord of men prophesied that 
After eight hundred million eons
They would all, within the same eon, 
Become guides of the world.{{note:{index725,id:UT22084-055-001-1995}}} {47} 
{{milestone:{label:18.51,id:UT22084-055-001-1996}}}Bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs,
Upāsakas and upāsikās— {{page:{number:132,id:UT22084-055-001-5965,folio:F.67.a}}}
Seven hundred and sixty million beings— 
All heard this sūtra. {48}
{{milestone:{label:18.52,id:UT22084-055-001-1997}}}The Lord of humans{{note:{index726,id:UT22084-055-001-1998}}} prophesied 
That they would see as many guides of the world
As there are grains of sand in the Ganges
While practicing bodhisattva conduct. {49}
{{milestone:{label:18.53,id:UT22084-055-001-1999}}}“They will make offerings to them all,
Seeking the wisdom of enlightenment,
And here and there they will hear 
This unsurpassable sūtra. {50}
{{milestone:{label:18.54,id:UT22084-055-001-2000}}}“They will make unsurpassable offerings 
To Buddha Maitreya.
They will possess the highest Dharma
And they will go to Sukhāvatī. {52}{{note:{index727,id:UT22084-055-001-2001}}}
{{milestone:{label:18.55,id:UT22084-055-001-2002}}}“There they will make offerings 
To the stainless buddha,
The Tathāgata Amitāyus,
For the sake of supreme enlightenment. {53}
{{milestone:{label:18.56,id:UT22084-055-001-2003}}}“Having heard this unsurpassable sūtra
They will not go in future 
To the lower existences 
For seventy-three{{note:{index728,id:UT22084-055-001-2004}}} countless eons. {54}
{{milestone:{label:18.57,id:UT22084-055-001-2005}}}“Those who in future times
Listen to this unsurpassable sūtra,
And keep it and read it,{{note:{index729,id:UT22084-055-001-2006}}}
Will all be honoring{{note:{index730,id:UT22084-055-001-2007}}} me. {55}
{{milestone:{label:18.58,id:UT22084-055-001-2008}}}“I make this declaration{{note:{index731,id:UT22084-055-001-2009}}}
To all those who are standing before me.
I bestow this enlightenment gained{{note:{index732,id:UT22084-055-001-2010}}} with difficulty.” {56}
{{milestone:{label:18.59,id:UT22084-055-001-2011}}}Conclusion of the eighteenth chapter, “The Entrustment of the Samādhi.”
{{milestone:{label:19,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-19}}}The Teaching of the Inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha
Chapter 19
{{milestone:{label:19.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2012}}}The Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas, having heard the inconceivable and measureless benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, through wishing not to be fearful, wishing not to be terrified, and not to be gripped by terror, will become learned in the teaching of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Aspire to the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Be wise in asking questions about the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Be wise in seeking the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. Do not be fearful, do not be terrified, and do not be gripped by terror on hearing the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha.” {{page:{number:133,id:UT22084-055-001-5966,folio:F.67.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:19.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2013}}}The youth Candraprabha placed his palms together, bowed toward the Bhagavān, and asked him, “Bhagavān, in this way how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas aspire to the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, become wise in asking questions about the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, become wise in seeking the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, and not be fearful, not be terrified, and not be gripped by terror on hearing the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha?”
{{milestone:{label:19.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2014}}}The Bhagavān replied to the youth Candraprabha, “Those bodhisattva mahāsattvas who listen to and hear this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, and obtain it, understand it, keep it, read it out loud, disseminate it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others, will become wise in the teaching of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. They will aspire to the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, they will become wise in asking questions about the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, and will not be fearful, will not be terrified, and will not be gripped by terror on hearing the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha.”{{note:{index733,id:UT22084-055-001-2015}}}
{{milestone:{label:19.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2016}}}“After the youth Candraprabha had been taught by the Bhagavān these words on accomplishing the benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, he again heard from the Bhagavān countless, innumerable verses{{note:{index734,id:UT22084-055-001-2017}}} describing the benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena; and it was at that time that the youth Candraprabha attained this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena.{{note:{index735,id:UT22084-055-001-2018}}}
{{milestone:{label:19.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2019}}}Innumerable, countless bodhisattva mahāsattvas attained the great, higher cognitions. {{page:{number:134,id:UT22084-055-001-5967,folio:F.68.a}}} Countless beings also developed the motivation that is directed toward great compassion. 
{{milestone:{label:19.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2020}}}This universe of a thousand million worlds shook in six ways. It trembled, trembled strongly, and trembled intensely; it quivered, quivered strongly, and quivered intensely; it shook, shook strongly, and shook intensely; it shuddered, shuddered strongly, and shuddered intensely; it quaked, quaked strongly, and quaked intensely; the east sank and the west rose, the west sank and the east rose, the north sank and the south rose, the south sank and the north rose, the perimeter sank and the center rose, and the center sank and the perimeter rose. An immeasurable radiance shone in the universe. There fell a great rain of divine incense. Devas and their sons gathered in order to listen to the Dharma. High in the sky they heard the innumerable verses on the benefits of the qualities that come from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. All the devas and their sons felt pleased, delighted, thrilled, joyous, happy, and glad, and they emitted cries of joy{{note:{index736,id:UT22084-055-001-2021}}} and laughter. They let fall a great rain of divine flowers of various kinds. They played many thousands of trillions of divine musical instruments. And they proclaimed the following words together as one voice:
{{milestone:{label:19.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2022}}}“Aho!{{note:{index737,id:UT22084-055-001-2023}}} We have obtained something that is excellent to obtain. We have heard the innumerable verses on the benefits of the qualities from the Bhagavān. Bhagavān, just as the bodhisattva mahāsattva, the youth Candraprabha, attained this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, we also, Bhagavān, will all together at the same time attain this samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena.” {{page:{number:135,id:UT22084-055-001-5968,folio:F.68.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:19.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2024}}}At the time when the Bhagavān was teaching the Dharma on Vulture Peak Mountain to the assembly that was like an ocean, the gandharva{{note:{index738,id:UT22084-055-001-2025}}} Pañcaśikha, in order to honor and serve him, descended from the sky accompanied by the sound of five hundred musical instruments, and remained before the Bhagavān.
{{milestone:{label:19.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2026}}}The gandharva Pañcaśikha thought, “Just as I{{note:{index739,id:UT22084-055-001-2027}}} render service and honor in Sudharma before the devas of Trāyastriṃśa and Śakra, the lord of the devas, by singing them songs, in that same way I shall sing in order to make an offering to the god of gods, the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.”
{{milestone:{label:19.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2028}}}Then the gandharva Pañcaśikha stood up before the Bhagavān holding a lute, the body of which was made of beryl. He was accompanied by the music{{note:{index740,id:UT22084-055-001-2029}}} of five hundred other gandharvas{{note:{index741,id:UT22084-055-001-2030}}} holding musical instruments. 
{{milestone:{label:19.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2031}}}The Bhagavān thought, “I shall perform a miracle so that the youth Candraprabha will attain skill in the realization of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha, so that he will not waver from the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, and so that I may manifest the gandharva Pañcaśikha’s skill in singing and playing the lute.”
{{milestone:{label:19.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2032}}}Then the Bhagavān performed that miracle, and through the power of the Buddha the five hundred instruments were played excellently. From that excellent playing there came the sound of the inconceivable meaning, which was united{{note:{index742,id:UT22084-055-001-2033}}} with the true nature. And these verses of the realization of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha were sung:{{note:{index743,id:UT22084-055-001-2034}}}
{{milestone:{label:19.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2035}}}“Within the breadth of one hair there are as many buddhas
As the number of grains of sand in the Ganges.
And those jinas have as many buddha realms, too,
Each one separate and with distinct characteristics. {1}
{{milestone:{label:19.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2036}}}“Within the breadth of one hair there are the five kinds of beings:
The beings in hell, those who are animals, {{page:{number:136,id:UT22084-055-001-5969,folio:F.69.a}}}
Those in the realm of Yama, the devas, and humans,
Without overlapping or being squeezed.{{note:{index744,id:UT22084-055-001-2037}}} {2}
{{milestone:{label:19.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2038}}}“Within that space there are the lakes and oceans,
All rivers, and similarly ponds and springs,
Without overlapping or being squeezed.
In that way the Buddha’s Dharma is inconceivable. {3}
{{milestone:{label:19.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2039}}}“Within that space there are numerous mountains: 
Cakravāla, Meru, and Sumeru,
Mucilinda and Mahāmucilinda,
Vindhya, Gṛdhrakūṭa, and Himavat. {4}
{{milestone:{label:19.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2040}}}“Within that space there are the terrible hells,
The horrible Tāpana and Pratāpana.
Those who have fallen into those hells
Experience the sensation of suffering. {5}
{{milestone:{label:19.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2041}}}“Within that space there are divine palaces,
Twelve{{note:{index745,id:UT22084-055-001-2042}}} yojanas in size and beautiful.{{note:{index746,id:UT22084-055-001-2043}}}
Within them there are many thousands of devas{{note:{index747,id:UT22084-055-001-2044}}}
Who experience bliss in divine pleasures. {6} 
{{milestone:{label:19.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2045}}}“Within that space there are the births of buddhas.
There is illumination from the teaching of those who know the world.
Those{{note:{index748,id:UT22084-055-001-2046}}} who have not trained in pure conduct 
And who have no wisdom will not see them. {7}
{{milestone:{label:19.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2047}}}“Within that space they hear the words,
‘The Dharma has ceased, the Guide has passed away.’
Within that space there are some who hear,
‘The Guide lives and he teaches the Dharma.’ {8}
{{milestone:{label:19.21,id:UT22084-055-001-2048}}}“Within that space there are some who perceive
That they live for countless years.
Within that space there are those whose time is ending.
They hear the words, ‘You have not long to live.’ {9}
{{milestone:{label:19.22,id:UT22084-055-001-2049}}}“Within that space there are some who have the perception, 
Believing what their mind perceives,
Of seeing and making offerings to sugatas{{note:{index749,id:UT22084-055-001-2050}}} and pleasing the buddhas.
Yet there is no arising and no making of offerings. {10}
{{milestone:{label:19.23,id:UT22084-055-001-2051}}}“A man dreams he is in a house
Experiencing the bliss of sensory pleasures. 
When he awakes he does not see those pleasures.{{note:{index750,id:UT22084-055-001-2052}}}
He knows that it was a dream. {11}
{{milestone:{label:19.24,id:UT22084-055-001-2053}}}“In that way, what is seen, heard, thought, or known,{{note:{index751,id:UT22084-055-001-2054}}}
All of this is unreal, like a dream.
The one who has attained the samādhi
Will know this nature of phenomena. {12}
{{milestone:{label:19.25,id:UT22084-055-001-2055}}}“For people such as this there is no pleasure or displeasure.
They are always perfectly happy in the world. {{page:{number:137,id:UT22084-055-001-5970,folio:F.69.b}}}
Those who delight in vast forests
Become perfectly happy mendicants. {13}
{{milestone:{label:19.26,id:UT22084-055-001-2056}}}“Those who have no thought of ‘mine,’
Those who have abandoned all attachments,
Wander in the world like rhinoceroses 
And roam like the wind through the air. {14}
{{milestone:{label:19.27,id:UT22084-055-001-2057}}}“Meditation on the path, the development of wisdom,
The emptiness and selflessness of all phenomena:
He who meditates on these Dharmas
Will have unending confidence. {15}
{{milestone:{label:19.28,id:UT22084-055-001-2058}}}“The people in the world whose minds have no attachment,
They are perfectly happy in this world.
Their minds are always like the wind,
Knowing no attachment to pleasure or displeasure. {16}
{{milestone:{label:19.29,id:UT22084-055-001-2059}}}“It is suffering to be with that which is unpleasant;
It is suffering to be separated from that which is pleasant.
Finally abandoning both of these,
Those happy people delight in the Dharma. {17}
{{milestone:{label:19.30,id:UT22084-055-001-2060}}}“The one who has attachment on hearing this Dharma,
And animosity on hearing that which is not Dharma,
Goes astray through conceit and pride,
And overpowered by pride, experiences suffering. {18}
{{milestone:{label:19.31,id:UT22084-055-001-2061}}}“Those who remain in equanimity
Are always free of arrogance and depression.
When faced with the pleasant and the unpleasant
They always have a liberated mind. {19}
{{milestone:{label:19.32,id:UT22084-055-001-2062}}}“Those who maintain perfectly pure correct conduct,
Who remain always in inconceivable dhyāna
And delight in the peace of the forests,
Will never know the arising of doubts. {20}
{{milestone:{label:19.33,id:UT22084-055-001-2063}}}“Those who engage in that which is unreal,
The fools who are always enjoying sensory pleasures 
Like vultures attracted to a corpse,
They always fall under the power of Namuci.”{{note:{index752,id:UT22084-055-001-2064}}} {21} 
{{milestone:{label:19.34,id:UT22084-055-001-2065}}}When these verses had been created through the sound of the lutes,{{note:{index753,id:UT22084-055-001-2066}}} the youth Candraprabha attained skill in the realization of the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha; the gandharva Pañcaśikha attained the patience that was in accord with that sound; countless beings, both devas and humans, developed the aspiration to the highest, complete enlightenment; {{page:{number:138,id:UT22084-055-001-5971,folio:F.70.a}}} and countless beings were benefitted.
{{milestone:{label:19.35,id:UT22084-055-001-2067}}}Conclusion of the nineteenth chapter, “The Teaching of the Inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha.”
{{milestone:{label:20,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-20}}}Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja
Chapter 20
{{milestone:{label:20.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2068}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this Dharma teaching of entering great compassion and wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood quickly should rely upon all roots of merit, training, qualities, and completely pure conduct.
{{milestone:{label:20.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2069}}}“Bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have few involvements, avoid bad companions, rely on kalyāṇamitras, have an inquiring nature, unrelentingly seek the Dharma, have the Dharma as their goal, desire the Dharma, delight in the Dharma, obtain the Dharma, and practice the Dharma in accord with the Dharma will, young man, develop great compassion for beings and will develop the aspiration for the highest, complete enlightenment. 
{{milestone:{label:20.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2070}}}“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this Dharma teaching of entering great compassion and wish to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood quickly should be diligent, without regard for life or body, and should continuously seek kalyāṇamitras who teach this Dharma teaching of entering great compassion, and unwaveringly serve them, rely upon them, and honor them. 
{{milestone:{label:20.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2071}}}“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who with a higher motivation seek kalyāṇamitras should hear from them the Dharma teaching of entering great compassion, and should obtain it, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, {{page:{number:139,id:UT22084-055-001-5972,folio:F.70.b}}} promulgate it, and make it widely known to others. They should, with joy and veneration, perceive as the Teacher the person from whom they hear this Dharma teaching on entering great compassion.
{{milestone:{label:20.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2072}}}“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas search for kalyāṇamitras, and respect them and serve them without weariness, at that time, young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas easily attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood and they obtain this Dharma teaching on easily entering great compassion. 
{{milestone:{label:20.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2073}}}“Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas should constantly seek for kalyāṇamitras as if their head or clothing were on fire, and unwaveringly attend upon them, serve them, and venerate them. 
{{milestone:{label:20.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2074}}}“Why is that? Young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, not even to speak of this Dharma teaching on entering great compassion, depends upon kalyāṇamitras.
{{milestone:{label:20.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2075}}}“Therefore, young man, you should always practice by thinking, ‘I will not weary of seeking kalyāṇamitras, venerating them, and serving them.’ ”
{{milestone:{label:20.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2076}}}Thereupon the Bhagavān, in order to make clear this Dharma teaching on entering great compassion, gave the youth Candraprabha the teaching that had been given in the past in detail in the form of the following verses:{{note:{index754,id:UT22084-055-001-2077}}}
{{milestone:{label:20.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2078}}}“Many incalculable, innumerable, 
Inconceivable millions of eons in the past,
There was the highest of humans,
The Guide named Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja. {1}
{{milestone:{label:20.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2079}}}“He taught this samādhi of peace
In which there is no human, soul, or person:
‘All phenomena are like the moon on water,
Illusions, bubbles, mirages, and lightning. {2}
{{milestone:{label:20.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2080}}}“ ‘There is no human, no descendant of Manu, to be found {{page:{number:140,id:UT22084-055-001-5973,folio:F.71.a}}}
Who goes to the next world when his time has come to an end. 
However, the karma that has been created will not disappear,
But will give corresponding black or white results. {3}
{{milestone:{label:20.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2081}}}“ ‘This is the excellent doorway of the way of logic, 
The subtle, difficult-to-see realm of experience of the jinas.
The Bhagavān knows the enlightenment of buddhahood 
In which there are there no words or letters to be found. {4}
{{milestone:{label:20.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2082}}}“ ‘Vast retention and the accumulation of wisdom
Come from a hundred thousand trillion sūtras.
The Bhagavān teaches the samādhi
That is the field of experience of a hundred thousand trillion buddhas. {5} 
{{milestone:{label:20.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2083}}}“ ‘This frees the sick from their illness.
It is the wealth accomplished by bodhisattvas.
It is praised and extolled by all buddhas;
A hundred thousand trillion devas make offerings to it. {6}
{{milestone:{label:20.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2084}}}“ ‘It is condemned by all foolish beings,{{note:{index755,id:UT22084-055-001-2085}}}
And the tīrthikas always reject it.
It is the supreme wealth of conduct that is praised by the buddhas. 
It is as undefiled as lightning in the sky. {7}
{{milestone:{label:20.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2086}}}“ ‘Those who make offerings to millions of jinas
Are wise in the practice of generosity and correct conduct,
Have forsaken their previous bad companions,
And have an unsurpassable inheritance of wealth.’{{note:{index756,id:UT22084-055-001-2087}}} {8} 
{{milestone:{label:20.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2088}}}“There was present a bhikṣu, a dharmabhāṇaka, 
A celibate who was the heart son of the Sugata.
When he had heard this benevolent Dharma,
He developed the aspiration to be a guide of the world.{{note:{index757,id:UT22084-055-001-2089}}} {9} 
{{milestone:{label:20.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2090}}}“The Guide, Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja,
Said to the dharmabhāṇaka,
‘Bhikṣu, develop the supreme, difficult-to-attain
Motivation for the highest enlightenment. {10}
{{milestone:{label:20.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2091}}}“ ‘Maintain the conduct that is like a precious jewel,
Always depend on favorable friends,
Never depend on friends whose actions are evil
And before long you will attain buddha wisdom.’ {11}
{{milestone:{label:20.21,id:UT22084-055-001-2092}}}“The one who developed the aspiration to enlightenment
In the presence of Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja
Became a supreme dharmabhāṇaka,
A celibate who was the heart son of the Sugata.”{{note:{index758,id:UT22084-055-001-2093}}} {12} 
{{milestone:{label:20.22,id:UT22084-055-001-2094}}}Conclusion of the twentieth chapter, “Indra­ketu­dhvaja­rāja.” {{page:{number:141,id:UT22084-055-001-5974,folio:F.71.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:21,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-21}}}The Past
Chapter 21
{{milestone:{label:21.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2095}}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should entertain no misgivings about all the teachings on the root of merits, the training, and the qualities.{{note:{index759,id:UT22084-055-001-2096}}} They should have few involvements, avoid bad companions, rely on kalyāṇamitras, have an inquiring nature, unrelentingly seek the Dharma, have the Dharma as their goal, desire the Dharma, delight in the Dharma, obtain the Dharma, and practice the Dharma in accord with the Dharma. They should perceive every buddha and bodhisattva as the teacher. They should with joy and veneration perceive as the teacher the person from whom they hear this Dharma teaching.
{{milestone:{label:21.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2097}}}“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who adopt and follow this Dharma teaching of entertaining no misgivings about all the teachings on the root of merits, the training, and the qualities will quickly display unending confidence of speech. They will accomplish{{note:{index760,id:UT22084-055-001-2098}}} the inconceivable Dharma of the Buddha. They will realize the profound Dharma of the Buddha. They will be like a light that dispels the darkness of perplexity, uncertainty, and doubt of the people of the world and the devas.”
{{milestone:{label:21.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2099}}}Then at that time, in order to relate this Dharma teaching of entertaining no misgivings about all the teachings on the root of merits, the training, and the qualities, he spoke to the youth Candraprabha these verses that told of the past.{{note:{index761,id:UT22084-055-001-2100}}}
{{milestone:{label:21.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2101}}}“In the past, in this world named Jambudvīpa,{{note:{index762,id:UT22084-055-001-2102}}}
There were two excellent sons{{note:{index763,id:UT22084-055-001-2103}}} who were not heedless. 
They entered homelessness in the teaching of a sugata,
And dwelt like rhinoceroses in a grove of trees. {1}
{{milestone:{label:21.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2104}}}“They had miraculous powers and had attained the four dhyānas,
They were very learned and skilled in composing poetry and texts, {{page:{number:142,id:UT22084-055-001-5975,folio:F.72.a}}}
They had mastered levitating up into the air,
And they could travel freely through the sky. {2}
{{milestone:{label:21.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2105}}}“They were engaged in conversation
In that cool grove of trees
That was filled with a variety of beautiful flowers
And attended by flocks of varieties of birds. {3}
{{milestone:{label:21.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2106}}}“A king who was pursuing a deer
Heard their voices and entered that grove.
The monarch saw the two dharmabhāṇakas 
And with the greatest joy he approached them. {4} 
{{milestone:{label:21.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2107}}}“They addressed each other agreeably
And the king sat down before them.
The king’s multitudinous army
Of sixty quintillion soldiers approached. {5}
{{milestone:{label:21.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2108}}}“Then both of those dharmabhāṇakas 
Said to the king, ‘Listen, Kṣatriya!{{note:{index764,id:UT22084-055-001-2109}}}
It is very difficult to reach supreme buddhahood.
Monarch, always be careful! {6}
{{milestone:{label:21.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2110}}}“ ‘Life is always passing and never stays.
It passes as quickly as a mountain stream.
From the torment of illness, misery, and aging
You have no other refuge than good actions.{{note:{index765,id:UT22084-055-001-2111}}} {7} 
{{milestone:{label:21.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2112}}}“ ‘Supreme king,{{note:{index766,id:UT22084-055-001-2113}}} be a protector of the Dharma.
Guard the teaching of the one with ten strengths
In this utterly terrible time of degeneration.
Remain on the side of Dharma, supreme king!’ {8}
{{milestone:{label:21.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2114}}}“Thus the wise ones at that time
Gave much advice to that sovereign,
Following which the monarch, with the other six quintillions,{{note:{index767,id:UT22084-055-001-2115}}}
Developed the aspiration to enlightenment. {9}
{{milestone:{label:21.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2116}}}“When the supreme king had heard the Dharma,
He was joyful, very happy, and enraptured
With those who had spoken it so gently and pleasantly, 
And bowed down to their feet before departing. {10}
{{milestone:{label:21.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2117}}}“Under that king there were many other bhikṣus
Who desired gain and who entered homes.
When he saw how dissimilar was their conduct 
The king did not show them respect. {11}
{{milestone:{label:21.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2118}}}“The teacher of the teaching had passed away
And this was the time of the latter years.
There were very few worthy recipients in Jambudvīpa,
And there were present many who were without self-control. {12}
{{milestone:{label:21.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2119}}}“The many bhikṣus, who were desirous and greedy,
Yearned for acquisitions, held the view of objective reality, {{page:{number:143,id:UT22084-055-001-5976,folio:F.72.b}}}
And had fallen away from the Sugata’s teaching, 
At that time repeatedly urged the king to action. {13}
{{milestone:{label:21.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2120}}}“ ‘You must kill those two dharmabhāṇakas. 
They are tīrthikas who are teaching nihilism.
Among those who have adopted that practice for a long time
There are none who have attained nirvāṇa. {14}
{{milestone:{label:21.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2121}}}“ ‘They deny karma, they deny ripening;
Those imposters teach that there are no skandhas.
Your Majesty, banish them from the land
And then the Dharma will remain for a long time.’ {15}
{{milestone:{label:21.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2122}}}“When he had listened to what they had to say, 
The elephant-like king became distrustful.
‘I shall kill these two dharmabhāṇakas.
I must not leave them alone, for that would be harmful.’{{note:{index768,id:UT22084-055-001-2123}}} {16} 
{{milestone:{label:21.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2124}}}“The king was attended by a goddess{{note:{index769,id:UT22084-055-001-2125}}}
Who had practiced with him in a previous lifetime.
She was wise and had benefited him for a long time,
And at this time she said to the sovereign king, {17}
{{milestone:{label:21.21,id:UT22084-055-001-2126}}}“ ‘Kṣatriya,{{note:{index770,id:UT22084-055-001-2127}}} do not think in this way
Because of what bad associates have said.
Do not kill{{note:{index771,id:UT22084-055-001-2128}}} those two wise dharmabhāṇakas 
Because of what bad associates have said. {18}
{{milestone:{label:21.22,id:UT22084-055-001-2129}}}“ ‘Lord of men, do you not remember even a little
Of what they said to you in the forest grove?
In this perfectly terrible time of degeneration, 
Remain on the side of Dharma, elephant-like king!’ {{note:{index772,id:UT22084-055-001-2130}}} {19} 
{{milestone:{label:21.23,id:UT22084-055-001-2131}}}“The king, inspired by those true words,
Did not abandon the teachings of the jinas.{{note:{index773,id:UT22084-055-001-2132}}}
But the king had a cruel brother
Who was persuaded by those around him.{{note:{index774,id:UT22084-055-001-2133}}} {19b–20a}{{note:{index775,id:UT22084-055-001-2134}}}
{{milestone:{label:21.24,id:UT22084-055-001-2135}}}“They told him, ‘The king, your brother, is wicked;
He has no joy in being alive.{{note:{index776,id:UT22084-055-001-2136}}}
Those two bhikṣus possess dreadful spells.
With those spells they can fly through the sky.{{note:{index777,id:UT22084-055-001-2137}}} {20} 
{{milestone:{label:21.25,id:UT22084-055-001-2138}}}“ ‘Having heard this we have come to you,
To tell you all that has occurred.
Quickly kill those dreadful magicians,
Or afterward you will be filled with regret.’ {21}
{{milestone:{label:21.26,id:UT22084-055-001-2139}}}“Then the king’s brother{{note:{index778,id:UT22084-055-001-2140}}} put on his armor,
Under the influence of those bad associates.
The king’s brother, encircled by his entire army,
Came to the forest where the two bhikṣus dwelt. {22}
{{milestone:{label:21.27,id:UT22084-055-001-2141}}}“The nāgas and yakṣas that lived in that forest
Knew the intention of the king’s dreadful, cruel brother {{page:{number:144,id:UT22084-055-001-5977,folio:F.73.a}}}
And hurled upon them a rain of bricks and stones
That killed the king’s brother and his army. {23}
{{milestone:{label:21.28,id:UT22084-055-001-2142}}}“See how the life of the king’s cruel brother came to an end
Because he listened to what bad associates said.
Those who were angry at the dharmabhāṇakas 
Took rebirth sixty times in the Avīci hell. {24}
{{milestone:{label:21.29,id:UT22084-055-001-2143}}}“Those numerous bhikṣus who believed in reality
And drove the kṣatriya king to action
Experienced the sufferings of hell
For countless billons of rebirths. {25}
{{milestone:{label:21.30,id:UT22084-055-001-2144}}}“The goddess who influenced the king
And protected the dharmabhāṇakas 
Saw buddhas as numerous as sand grains in ten million Ganges, 
Made offerings to them, and engaged in practice. {26}
{{milestone:{label:21.31,id:UT22084-055-001-2145}}}“The multitudinous six quintillion men,
Who with the king had heard the Dharma 
And developed the aspiration to enlightenment,
Became buddhas in numerous different realms. {27}
{{milestone:{label:21.32,id:UT22084-055-001-2146}}}“Their lifespans were many millions of eons. 
They had inconceivable, unequaled wisdom.
They all taught this excellent samādhi,
And then those supreme humans passed into nirvāṇa. {28}
{{milestone:{label:21.33,id:UT22084-055-001-2147}}}“Having heard this unsurpassable teaching 
On the accumulation of correct conduct, purity, qualities, and wisdom, 
You must practice intently, without distraction,
And quickly attain the wisdom of buddhahood.{{note:{index779,id:UT22084-055-001-2148}}} {29} 
{{milestone:{label:21.34,id:UT22084-055-001-2149}}}“Look upon us, you tathāgatas in the ten directions,
Who have peaceful minds and compassionate, loving eyes.
You are the refuge and protection for all beings.
Send down your rain of Dharma upon the world.{{note:{index780,id:UT22084-055-001-2150}}} {30} 
{{milestone:{label:21.35,id:UT22084-055-001-2151}}}“Do not think that those two young men,
Those perfect sons,{{note:{index781,id:UT22084-055-001-2152}}} were anyone else:
Dīpaṃkara was at that time one of them,
And I was the second dharmabhāṇaka. {30a}
{{milestone:{label:21.36,id:UT22084-055-001-2153}}}“At that time Maitreya was the king{{note:{index782,id:UT22084-055-001-2154}}}
Who listened favorably to the Dharma.
And you, young man, at that time, 
Were the wise goddess who wished to help. {30b}
{{milestone:{label:21.37,id:UT22084-055-001-2155}}}“At that time, Devadatta 
Was the king’s brother, 
Influenced by the acquisitive bhikṣus {{page:{number:145,id:UT22084-055-001-5978,folio:F.73.b}}}
Who said, ‘Kill those two dharmabhāṇakas.’ ” {30c}
{{milestone:{label:21.38,id:UT22084-055-001-2156}}}Conclusion of the twenty-first chapter, “The Past.”
{{milestone:{label:22,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-22}}}The Teaching on the Body
Chapter 22
{{milestone:{label:22.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2157}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should have no attachment to their life or body. Why is that? Because, young man, beings accomplish bad actions due to attachment to their lives and bodies.{{note:{index783,id:UT22084-055-001-2158}}}
{{milestone:{label:22.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2159}}}“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have no attachment to their life and body will not even find it difficult to attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, not to mention this samādhi. Therefore, young man, have no attachment to your life and body. That is how you should practice.”
It was said concerning this:
{{milestone:{label:22.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2161}}}“Foolish beings always unceasingly
Have strong attachment to the putrid body. 
Grasping at life, and for the sake of happiness,
The unwise always commit bad actions. {i}
{{milestone:{label:22.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2162}}}Those who do not know attachment
To body and life, which have no essence,
Will defeat the armies of Māra
And realize enlightenment at the foot of the Bodhi tree. {ii}
{{milestone:{label:22.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2163}}}Those who have attachment to these two things—
The body that is empty and selfless,
And life, which is like a dream or a fleeting dewdrop—
Those people will go to hell when they die. {iii}
{{milestone:{label:22.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2164}}}Conclusion of the twenty-second chapter, “The Teaching on the Body.”{{note:{index784,id:UT22084-055-001-2165}}}
{{milestone:{label:23,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-23}}}The Teaching on the Tathāgata’s Body 
Chapter 23
{{milestone:{label:23.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2166}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should not know the Tathāgata to be the rūpakāya.{{note:{index785,id:UT22084-055-001-2167}}} Why is that? It is because the Buddha Bhagavān manifests because of the dharmakāya and does not manifest because of the rūpakāya. {{page:{number:146,id:UT22084-055-001-5979,folio:F.74.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:23.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2168}}}“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas whose wish is to aspire to the body of the tathāgata, who wish to know the body of the tathāgata, should obtain this samādhi, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with dedication to the practice of meditation, and make it widely known to others. 
{{milestone:{label:23.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2169}}}“Young man, the body of the tathāgata{{note:{index786,id:UT22084-055-001-2170}}} is taught to be one meaning,{{note:{index787,id:UT22084-055-001-2171}}} with the understanding that it arises from a hundred merits. It arises from the Dharma.{{note:{index788,id:UT22084-055-001-2172}}} It is without attributes. It is devoid of all attributes. It is profound.{{note:{index789,id:UT22084-055-001-2173}}} It is immeasurable. It is an immeasurable phenomenon.{{note:{index790,id:UT22084-055-001-2174}}} It has the nature of the absence of attributes.{{note:{index791,id:UT22084-055-001-2175}}} It is free of all attributes.{{note:{index792,id:UT22084-055-001-2176}}} It is unwavering.{{note:{index793,id:UT22084-055-001-2177}}} It has no location. It completely has the nature of space. It is invisible. It transcends the scope of the eye’s vision. That should be known as the dharmakāya.{{note:{index794,id:UT22084-055-001-2178}}}
{{milestone:{label:23.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2179}}}“It is inconceivable. It is beyond the level of thought. It is unaffected by bliss or suffering. It transcends all conceptual elaboration.{{note:{index795,id:UT22084-055-001-2180}}} It has no location,{{note:{index796,id:UT22084-055-001-2181}}} because it transcends the scope of the words of those who aspire to the wisdom of buddhahood. It is the quintessence{{note:{index797,id:UT22084-055-001-2182}}} because it transcends desire. It is indivisible because it transcends anger.{{note:{index798,id:UT22084-055-001-2183}}} It is stable because it transcends the scope of ignorance. It is taught through the teaching of emptiness. It is unborn because it transcends birth.{{note:{index799,id:UT22084-055-001-2184}}} It is ‘permanent’ in terms of words, and terminology is empty.{{note:{index800,id:UT22084-055-001-2185}}} It is undifferentiated because it is nirvāṇa.{{note:{index801,id:UT22084-055-001-2186}}} It is ‘nirvāṇa’{{note:{index802,id:UT22084-055-001-2187}}} because of a word. It is ‘peace’ because of speaking.{{note:{index803,id:UT22084-055-001-2188}}} There is equality in terms of conventional appellations.{{note:{index804,id:UT22084-055-001-2189}}} There are appellations in terms of ultimate truth. There is ultimate truth through correct speech.{{note:{index805,id:UT22084-055-001-2190}}}
{{milestone:{label:23.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2191}}}“It is calmness, the absence of anguish.{{note:{index806,id:UT22084-055-001-2192}}} It is groundless,{{note:{index807,id:UT22084-055-001-2193}}} and cannot be comprehended.{{note:{index808,id:UT22084-055-001-2194}}} There is no end to its description.{{note:{index809,id:UT22084-055-001-2195}}}
{{milestone:{label:23.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2196}}}“Young man, it arises from training in the great, higher cognitions, and it is known as the tathāgatakāya.” 
Thereupon, the Bhagavān spoke these verses: {{page:{number:147,id:UT22084-055-001-5980,folio:F.74.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:23.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2198}}}“Someone who wishes to know 
This body of the Lord of the World{{note:{index810,id:UT22084-055-001-2199}}}
Should meditate on this samādhi,
And then they will know the Buddha’s body.{{note:{index811,id:UT22084-055-001-2200}}} {1} 
{{milestone:{label:23.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2201}}}“A buddha’s body is born from merit.{{note:{index812,id:UT22084-055-001-2202}}}
It{{note:{index813,id:UT22084-055-001-2203}}} is pure and it is brilliant.
It is the same as space;
There is no difference between them. {2}
{{milestone:{label:23.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2204}}}“The characteristics of a buddha
Are the same as those of enlightenment.
The characteristics of the body
Are the same as those characteristics. {3}
{{milestone:{label:23.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2205}}}“The body has enlightenment’s characteristics 
And a buddha realm has the same.
The strengths, liberations, and dhyānas
Are all also a single characteristic. {4}
{{milestone:{label:23.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2206}}}“That is the nature of the emergence 
Of the buddhas, of the lords of worlds.
There is no being who with physical eyes
Is able to see their bodies. {5}
{{milestone:{label:23.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2207}}}“There are many who declare,
‘I have seen the guide of the world.
He is the color of gold and his body
Illuminates the entire world.’ {6}
{{milestone:{label:23.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2208}}}“This body that is seen,
Beautified by characteristics,
Is a manifestation through the power
Of the blessing of the buddhas. {7}
{{milestone:{label:23.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2209}}}“The Buddha’s body is displayed
As having a height and a width,
But that body cannot be measured, 
And therefore it is inconceivable. {8}
{{milestone:{label:23.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2210}}}“If the Buddha’s body could be measured
And found to be of a certain size,
Then the Teacher would be the same
As a deva or a human. {9}
{{milestone:{label:23.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2211}}}“That characteristic is the ripening 
Of a mind in meditation.
There will be pure, radiant names-and-form
That have that characteristic. {10} 
{{milestone:{label:23.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2212}}}“There is no being whatsoever
Who has meditated on this samādhi of peace
It is in that way that the Lord of the World 
Has practiced for millions of eons. {11}
{{milestone:{label:23.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2213}}}“I have developed this samādhi
Through a multitude of good qualities.
Because of the vastness of that samādhi 
My body cannot be seen. {12}
{{milestone:{label:23.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2214}}}“As is someone’s mind, 
So are their names-and-form;
The mind that has no nature of its own
Has names-and-form with that characteristic. {13}
{{milestone:{label:23.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2215}}}“Those who have a gross perception
Of names-and-form,
Their inharmonious perception {{page:{number:148,id:UT22084-055-001-5981,folio:F.75.a}}}
Gives rise to a mind that is gross. {14}
{{milestone:{label:23.21,id:UT22084-055-001-2216}}}“Those who have a subtle perception
Within their names-and-form
Will have a mind that is radiant
And without attachment to names-and-form. {15} 
{{milestone:{label:23.22,id:UT22084-055-001-2217}}}“I remember that in my previous lives
During seven countless eons,
The three bad perceptions{{note:{index814,id:UT22084-055-001-2218}}}
Never arose in me at any time. {16}
{{milestone:{label:23.23,id:UT22084-055-001-2219}}}“My mind has been undefiled
For countless millions of eons.
I bring benefit to beings
And my body is not visible. {17}
{{milestone:{label:23.24,id:UT22084-055-001-2220}}}“The one whose mind 
Is liberated from existents
Will never again be
Connected with existents. {18}
{{milestone:{label:23.25,id:UT22084-055-001-2221}}}“My consciousness is liberated
Completely from all things.
I know the nature of the mind,
So that henceforth wisdom will arise. {19}
{{milestone:{label:23.26,id:UT22084-055-001-2222}}}“My emanations proceed
To thousands of millions of realms.
There they benefit beings
Though there is no body to be found. {20}
{{milestone:{label:23.27,id:UT22084-055-001-2223}}}“Without characteristics, without attributes,
It is the same as space.
My body is indescribable.
It is taught to be difficult to understand. {21}
{{milestone:{label:23.28,id:UT22084-055-001-2224}}}“The dharmakāya, the great hero,
Is a body born from the Dharma.
The Jina cannot be made known
By means of the rūpakāya. {22}
{{milestone:{label:23.29,id:UT22084-055-001-2225}}}“Māra will find no opportunity
To cause harm to the one 
Who has felt joy on hearing 
These words that have been taught. {23} 
{{milestone:{label:23.30,id:UT22084-055-001-2226}}}“Those who have heard the profound Dharma
And have not been frightened by it,
Will not even for the sake of their lives
Forsake the enlightenment of buddhahood. {24}
{{milestone:{label:23.31,id:UT22084-055-001-2227}}}“They will know the truth that is taught
In thousands of millions of sūtras.
They will be a light for the world
Wherever it is that they will go.{{note:{index815,id:UT22084-055-001-2228}}} {25} 
{{milestone:{label:23.32,id:UT22084-055-001-2229}}}“Young man, the body of the Tathāgata is not easily known through attributes or actions. It is blue, or is colored blue, or is like blue, or shines with blue light; or it is yellow, or is colored yellow, or is like yellow, or shines with yellow light; or it is red, or is colored red, or is like red, {{page:{number:149,id:UT22084-055-001-5982,folio:F.75.b}}} or shines with red light; or it is white, or is colored white, or is like white, or shines with white light; or it is madder, or is colored madder, or is like madder, or shines with madder light; or it is crystal, or is crystal-colored, or is like crystal, or shines with crystal light; or it is fire, or is fire-colored, or is like fire, or shines with fire light; or it is distilled ghee, or is ghee-colored, or is like ghee, or shines with ghee-colored light; or it is gold, or is gold-colored, or is like gold, or shines with golden light; or it is beryl, or is beryl-colored, or is like beryl, or shines with beryl light; or it is lightning, or is lightning-colored, or is like lightning, or shines with lightning’s light; or it is Brahmā, or is Brahmā-colored, or is like Brahmā, or shines with Brahmā’s light; or it is a deva, or is deva-colored, or is like a deva, or shines with a deva’s light. It is not easy to know it.
{{milestone:{label:23.33,id:UT22084-055-001-2230}}}“Young man, in that way the body of the tathāgata is pure. It cannot be conceived of through attributes, and so it is taught to be inconceivable. It cannot be conceived of{{note:{index816,id:UT22084-055-001-2231}}} through any attribute, and so it is taught to be inconceivable. It cannot be conceived of through external appearances. It is immeasurable. The beings and devas of this world cannot easily grasp its extent even through the perfect rūpakāya.”{{note:{index817,id:UT22084-055-001-2232}}}
The Bhagavān then spoke these verses:
{{milestone:{label:23.34,id:UT22084-055-001-2234}}}“All the particles in the world
And all that can be conceived of as dust,
And all the water that is in springs, 
Lakes, ponds, and the ocean— {26}
{{milestone:{label:23.35,id:UT22084-055-001-2235}}}“One may ask how many particles there are, 
But one can never find the end.
Even if, with the tip of a hair, one could measure out 
How much water there is in an ocean,{{note:{index818,id:UT22084-055-001-2236}}} {26–27} 
{{milestone:{label:23.36,id:UT22084-055-001-2237}}}“Even that could not be taught 
As an analogy for the Lord of the World.
There are countless drops of water {{page:{number:150,id:UT22084-055-001-5983,folio:F.76.a}}}
And it is the same for atoms, {27}
{{milestone:{label:23.37,id:UT22084-055-001-2238}}}“But I see that even a single sentient being 
Has far more numerous
Aspirations and motivations
That are developed at numerous times.{{note:{index819,id:UT22084-055-001-2239}}} {28} 
{{milestone:{label:23.38,id:UT22084-055-001-2240}}}“Yet even the aspirations of all beings
Are not adequate as an analogy
For those qualities of the body
That I have indicated. {29}
{{milestone:{label:23.39,id:UT22084-055-001-2241}}}“One cannot{{note:{index820,id:UT22084-055-001-2242}}} through{{note:{index821,id:UT22084-055-001-2243}}} attributes and actions 
Know the appearance of these kinds
Of qualities{{note:{index822,id:UT22084-055-001-2244}}} of a buddha,
And that is my distinctive characteristic. {30}
{{milestone:{label:23.40,id:UT22084-055-001-2245}}}“The buddhas are devoid of attributes.
They are the manifestation of the dharmakāya.
They are profound and immeasurable,
And therefore the buddhas are inconceivable. {31}
{{milestone:{label:23.41,id:UT22084-055-001-2246}}}“The inconceivable buddha body 
Of a buddha is also inconceivable. 
Those bodies are inconceivable. 
They are the manifestation of the dharmakāya. {32}
{{milestone:{label:23.42,id:UT22084-055-001-2247}}}“The mind is incapable of conceiving
The bodies of the buddhas.
One cannot, therefore, obtain 
The measure of such a body. {33}
{{milestone:{label:23.43,id:UT22084-055-001-2248}}}“Those immeasurable qualities 
I have practiced for ten million eons.
Therefore have I accomplished
A body that is inconceivable and radiant, too. {34}
{{milestone:{label:23.44,id:UT22084-055-001-2249}}}“There is no being that can grasp it
Or that can obtain its measure.
In that way the body of a buddha
Is inconceivable and immeasurable. {35}
{{milestone:{label:23.45,id:UT22084-055-001-2250}}}“Because the qualities are immeasurable 
There is no measure that can be conceived for them.{{note:{index823,id:UT22084-055-001-2251}}}
Because the qualities are not conceived
The buddha also is inconceivable. {36} 
{{milestone:{label:23.46,id:UT22084-055-001-2252}}}“The measured is taught to be a conception;
The measureless is nonconceptual.
That which is not conceived is without conception;
Therefore the buddha is inconceivable. {37}
{{milestone:{label:23.47,id:UT22084-055-001-2253}}}“Just as space is limitless
And no one is able to measure it,
Likewise a buddha’s body
Is just the same as space. {38}
{{milestone:{label:23.48,id:UT22084-055-001-2254}}}“Those who thus know the body 
Of the buddhas are the progeny of the jinas.
They will also become buddhas,
Inconceivable lords of worlds.” {39}
{{milestone:{label:23.49,id:UT22084-055-001-2255}}}Conclusion of the twenty-third chapter, “The Teaching on the Tathāgata’s Body.”{{note:{index824,id:UT22084-055-001-2256}}}
{{milestone:{label:24,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-24}}}The Inconceivable Tathāgata 
Chapter 24
{{milestone:{label:24.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2257}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, {{page:{number:151,id:UT22084-055-001-5984,folio:F.76.b}}} “Young man, aspiring bodhisattva mahāsattvas think, ‘How can I make manifest the four discernments? What are these four? They are the discernment of meaning, the discernment of phenomena, the discernment of definitions, and the discernment of eloquence. I shall manifest these four!’ On having this thought, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should obtain this samādhi, understand it, preserve it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, and make it widely known to others.
{{milestone:{label:24.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2258}}}“Young man, what is the discernment of phenomena? 
“Young man, however many words there can be for forms, the tathāgata has that many appellations for them.{{note:{index825,id:UT22084-055-001-2260}}} It is the same for sensation, identification, mentation; and, young man, for consciousnesses. Young man, in that way there are infinite, endless, inconceivably numerous{{note:{index826,id:UT22084-055-001-2261}}} words for forms, and the tathāgata, too has inconceivably numerous appellations for them. It is the same for sensation, identification, mentation, and, young man, for consciousnesses: there are infinite, endless, inconceivably numerous words for them, and the tathāgata, too has inconceivably numerous appellations for them.{{note:{index827,id:UT22084-055-001-2262}}}
{{milestone:{label:24.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2263}}}“Young man, there are countless faults in those composite phenomena; there are also countless benefits in nirvāṇa, and the tathāgata, too, has that many countless appellations. Young man, as numerous as are the names for nirvāṇa, the tathāgata has that many appellations. {{page:{number:152,id:UT22084-055-001-5985,folio:F.77.a}}} Thus, young man, there are countless names of nirvāṇa, and the tathāgata, too, has that many appellations. 
{{milestone:{label:24.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2264}}}“Young man, the tathāgata has spoken of four kinds of appellations that are inconceivably numerous because it is not easy to state that there is an end to them. What are these four? They are the inconceivably numerous appellations in regard to the composite, the inconceivably numerous appellations for sounds, the inconceivably numerous appellations for kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous appellations for purification. Young man, those are the tathāgata’s four kinds of inconceivably numerous appellations. Young man, those four, the tathāgata’s inconceivably numerous appellations, are taught to be inconceivably numerous as it is not easy to state that there is an end to them. To understand what those four are, they should be taught in detail. 
{{milestone:{label:24.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2265}}}“Young man, there are the four ways of the bodhisattvas. What are the four ways? They are the inconceivably numerous ways of the composite, the inconceivably numerous ways of teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous ways of the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous ways of purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2266}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of reasoning.{{note:{index828,id:UT22084-055-001-2267}}} What are the four kinds of reasoning? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of reasoning concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2268}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of doorways. What are the four kinds of doorways? They are the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous doorways concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2269}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of elucidation. What are the four kinds of elucidation? {{page:{number:153,id:UT22084-055-001-5986,folio:F.77.b}}} They are the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous elucidations concerning purification. Those are the four. 
{{milestone:{label:24.49,id:UT22084-055-001-2321}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of the result. What are the four kinds of knowledge of the result? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the result concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the result concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the result concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the result concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.50,id:UT22084-055-001-2322}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of ignorance. What are the four kinds of knowledge of ignorance? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of ignorance concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of ignorance concerning teaching the composite, {{page:{number:161,id:UT22084-055-001-5994,folio:F.81.b}}} the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of ignorance concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of ignorance concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.51,id:UT22084-055-001-2323}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of suffering. What are the four kinds of knowledge of suffering?
