They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of suffering concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of suffering concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of suffering concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of suffering concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.52,id:UT22084-055-001-2324}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of unhappiness. What are the four kinds of knowledge of unhappiness? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of unhappiness concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of unhappiness concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of unhappiness concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of unhappiness concerning purification. Those are the four. 
{{milestone:{label:24.53,id:UT22084-055-001-2325}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of poverty. What are the four kinds of knowledge of poverty? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of poverty concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of poverty concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of poverty concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of poverty concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.54,id:UT22084-055-001-2326}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of birth. What are the four kinds of knowledge of birth? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of birth concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of birth concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of birth concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of birth concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.55,id:UT22084-055-001-2327}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of inner knowledge. What are the four kinds of inner knowledge? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of inner knowledge concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of inner knowledge concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of inner knowledge concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of inner knowledge concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.56,id:UT22084-055-001-2328}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of external knowledge. What are the four kinds of external knowledge? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of external knowledge concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of external knowledge concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of external knowledge concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of external knowledge concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.57,id:UT22084-055-001-2329}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of modesty. What are the four kinds of knowledge of modesty? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of modesty concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of modesty concerning teaching the composite, {{page:{number:162,id:UT22084-055-001-5995,folio:F.82.a}}} the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of modesty concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of modesty concerning purification. Those are the four. 
{{milestone:{label:24.58,id:UT22084-055-001-2330}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of truth. What are the four kinds of knowledge of truth? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of truth concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of truth concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of truth concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of truth concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.59,id:UT22084-055-001-2331}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of existence. What are the four kinds of knowledge of existence? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existence concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existence concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existence concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existence concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.60,id:UT22084-055-001-2332}}} “Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of existents. What are the four kinds of knowledge of existents? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existents concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existents concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existents concerning the kleśas, {{page:{number:163,id:UT22084-055-001-5996,folio:F.82.b}}} and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of existents concerning purification. Those are the four.
{{milestone:{label:24.61,id:UT22084-055-001-2333}}} “Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of the individual. What are the four kinds of knowledge of the individual? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of the individual concerning purification. Those are the four. 
{{milestone:{label:24.62,id:UT22084-055-001-2334}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of knowledge of apprehensions. What are the four kinds of knowledge of apprehensions? They are the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning teaching the composite, the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning the kleśas, and the inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions concerning purification. Those are the four.
“Young man, those are the four inconceivably numerous kinds of knowledge of apprehensions that are taught to be inconceivably numerous. It is not easy to state an end to them.
{{milestone:{label:24.63,id:UT22084-055-001-2336}}}“Young man, the bodhisattvas have four kinds of retention. What are the four kinds of retention? The first retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite composites. The second retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite sounds. The third retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite kleśas. The fourth retention is of what is known concerning the teaching of all infinite purifications. Those are the four retentions. The four retentions are those.
{{milestone:{label:24.64,id:UT22084-055-001-2337}}}“So it is in these ways that there is the discernment of phenomena through knowing phenomena. 
“The discernment of meaning is the meaning in the knowledge of phenomena. {{page:{number:164,id:UT22084-055-001-5997,folio:F.83.a}}}
“The discernment of definitions is delight{{note:{index840,id:UT22084-055-001-2340}}} in the knowledge of phenomena. 
{{milestone:{label:24.65,id:UT22084-055-001-2341}}}“Young man, the discernment of eloquence is teaching terminology, explaining, expounding,{{note:{index841,id:UT22084-055-001-2342}}} clarifying,{{note:{index842,id:UT22084-055-001-2343}}} disseminating,{{note:{index843,id:UT22084-055-001-2344}}} analyzing, differentiating, proclaiming,{{note:{index844,id:UT22084-055-001-2345}}} having unimpeded speech, having unalloyed{{note:{index845,id:UT22084-055-001-2346}}} speech, not being mute,{{note:{index846,id:UT22084-055-001-2347}}} not stammering,{{note:{index847,id:UT22084-055-001-2348}}} and speaking without loss of confidence in relation to the knowledge of phenomena.”
Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:
{{milestone:{label:24.66,id:UT22084-055-001-2350}}}“As numerous as are the knowledges of the Buddha,
There are that many designations for forms.
As numerous as are the designations for forms,
There are that many appellations of forms.{{note:{index848,id:UT22084-055-001-2351}}} {1}
{{milestone:{label:24.67,id:UT22084-055-001-2352}}}“As numerous as are the appellations of forms,
There are that many names for conduct.
As numerous as are the names for conduct,
There are that many names of buddhas. {2}
{{milestone:{label:24.68,id:UT22084-055-001-2353}}}“As numerous as are the names of buddhas,
There are that many names of beings.
I know{{note:{index849,id:UT22084-055-001-2354}}} whatever number of names 
Even one single being has. {3}
{{milestone:{label:24.69,id:UT22084-055-001-2355}}}“The names for conduct, names of buddhas,
And names of beings are equal 
To the infinity of names and appellations 
That I have previously taught. {4}
{{milestone:{label:24.70,id:UT22084-055-001-2356}}}“As numerous as are the faults in the composite,
There are that many qualities{{note:{index850,id:UT22084-055-001-2357}}} in nirvāṇa.
I have taught as many analogies
As there are qualities of the buddhas. {5}
{{milestone:{label:24.71,id:UT22084-055-001-2358}}}“As numerous as are the motivations
That I have taught beings to have,
There are that many light rays
From a single hair of a Lord of the World. {6}
{{milestone:{label:24.72,id:UT22084-055-001-2359}}}“As numerous as are the names
And aspirations of all beings,
A lord of humans has even more 
Qualities of the aspects of his speech. {7}
{{milestone:{label:24.73,id:UT22084-055-001-2360}}}“The names of all beings that have been taught
To be those of one being
Are the names of one being
That have been taught to be those of all beings. {8}
{{milestone:{label:24.74,id:UT22084-055-001-2361}}}“The Buddha has taught 
This engagement with discernment.{{note:{index851,id:UT22084-055-001-2362}}}
Infinite names have been taught 
For the sake of the bodhisattvas. {9}
{{milestone:{label:24.75,id:UT22084-055-001-2363}}}“Those who wish to teach in some way
The endless millions of sūtras {{page:{number:165,id:UT22084-055-001-5998,folio:F.83.b}}}
Should recite this sūtra
And teach it with full confidence. {10}
{{milestone:{label:24.76,id:UT22084-055-001-2364}}}“They should teach in the middle of an assembly
Millions of sūtras without impediment.
They should teach the Dharma in the way 
That space is without any limit. {11}
{{milestone:{label:24.77,id:UT22084-055-001-2365}}}“In that way the bodhisattvas, 
The pure beings, the protectors,
Having taken up this sūtra
Will become endowed with wisdom. {12}
{{milestone:{label:24.78,id:UT22084-055-001-2366}}}“Through the way this path is taught
By those who have faith,
That is how wisdom grows,
Like a tree on a snow mountain.” {13}
{{milestone:{label:24.79,id:UT22084-055-001-2367}}}Conclusion of the twenty-fourth chapter, “The Inconceivable Tathāgata.” 
{{milestone:{label:25,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-25}}}Engaging in Discernment
Chapter 25
{{milestone:{label:25.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2368}}}“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas who practice that discernment of phenomena, who view phenomena as phenomena, attain the highest, complete enlightenment?
“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who practice that discernment of phenomena, who view phenomena as phenomena, do not perceive enlightenment as other than form. They do not approach enlightenment as other than form. They do not seek enlightenment as other than form. They do not attain enlightenment as other than form. They do not inspire beings to an enlightenment that is other than form. They do not see a tathāgata as other than form. They see a tathāgata in this way: ‘The Tathāgata is the fearlessness that is the nature of form.’ They do not see the tathāgata as other than form, as other than the nature of form. They do not see the nature of form as other than the tathāgata. The nature of that which is called form and that of the tathāgata are nondual. The bodhisattva mahāsattvas who see in that way are engaging in the discernment of phenomena. 
{{milestone:{label:25.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2370}}}“In that same way they do not perceive enlightenment as other than sensation, {{page:{number:166,id:UT22084-055-001-5999,folio:F.84.a}}} other than identification, other than mentation, or other than consciousness. They do not approach enlightenment as being other than consciousness. They do not seek enlightenment as other than consciousness. They do not attain enlightenment as other than consciousness. They do not inspire beings to an enlightenment that is other than consciousness. They do not see a tathāgata as other than consciousness. They see a tathāgata in this way: ‘The Tathāgata is the fearlessness that is the nature of consciousness.’ They do not see the tathāgata as other than consciousness, as other than the nature of consciousness. They do not see the nature of consciousness as other than the tathāgata. The nature of that which is called consciousness and that of the tathāgata are nondual. The bodhisattva mahāsattvas who see in that way are engaging in the discernment of phenomena.”{{note:{index852,id:UT22084-055-001-2371}}}
Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:
{{milestone:{label:25.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2373}}}“Enlightenment is taught through form; 
Form is taught through enlightenment. 
Through these dissimilar words 
The highest of Dharma is taught. {1}
{{milestone:{label:25.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2374}}}“The highest form is taught through words;
Its nature is profound.
Form and enlightenment are the same:
There is no difference that can be found. {2}
{{milestone:{label:25.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2375}}}“Nirvāṇa is profound 
And it is taught through words,{{note:{index853,id:UT22084-055-001-2376}}}
Yet nirvāṇa is not to be found
And words are not to be found. {3}
{{milestone:{label:25.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2377}}}“Both words and nirvāṇa,
Neither of them are to be found.
Thus nirvāṇa has been taught
In terms of empty phenomena. {4}
{{milestone:{label:25.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2378}}}“Nirvāṇa is not to be found
In saying ‘passed into nirvāṇa.’
There is no development of phenomena.
It is afterward just as it was before. {5}
{{milestone:{label:25.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2379}}}“All phenomena are by nature
Exactly the same as nirvāṇa. {{page:{number:167,id:UT22084-055-001-6000,folio:F.84.b}}}
That is known by those dedicated to renunciation,
By those engaged in the Buddha’s teachings. {6}
{{milestone:{label:25.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2380}}}“Some say, ‘I have seen the Guide,
For I saw the Buddha’s body.’ 
But it is not possible for anyone
To see me because of my rūpakāya. {7}
{{milestone:{label:25.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2381}}}“The known nature of form,
That is the characteristic of form.
When the nature of form is known,
Then my body is revealed.{{note:{index854,id:UT22084-055-001-2382}}} {8}
{{milestone:{label:25.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2383}}}“In that way I know the characteristics 
Of phenomena, of the five skandhas.
Knowing that nature of phenomena, 
I remain in the dharmakāya. {9}
{{milestone:{label:25.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2384}}}“I teach the Dharma to beings
Without departing from the dharmakāya.{{note:{index855,id:UT22084-055-001-2385}}}
But the qualities of the buddhas
Cannot be expressed in words. {10}
{{milestone:{label:25.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2386}}}“Those who do not know this way
Listen to the Buddha’s words
And then merely say with words,
‘I have seen the Guide of humans.’ {11}
{{milestone:{label:25.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2387}}}“Whoever casts off all conceptual identification
Brings to an end the identification of existence.
Whoever has a conceptual identification of words
Will never be able to see the Teacher. {12}
{{milestone:{label:25.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2388}}}“Whoever knows emptiness
As the characteristic of form
Will not say that emptiness 
Is other than the nature of form.
Whoever knows form,
Knows emptiness.{{note:{index856,id:UT22084-055-001-2389}}} {13}
{{milestone:{label:25.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2390}}}“Whoever knows emptiness
As the characteristic of form
Will overcome and defeat
Tens of millions of māras.{{note:{index857,id:UT22084-055-001-2391}}} {14}
{{milestone:{label:25.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2392}}}“Whoever knows form,
Knows emptiness.
Whoever knows emptiness,
Knows nirvāṇa.{{note:{index858,id:UT22084-055-001-2393}}} {15}
{{milestone:{label:25.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2394}}}“Those who do not know this way,
Those who conceptualize, are lost.{{note:{index859,id:UT22084-055-001-2395}}}
They conceive of the unreal as being real 
And the real as being unreal.{{note:{index860,id:UT22084-055-001-2396}}} {16}
{{milestone:{label:25.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2397}}}“They are deceived by acquisitions through reputation{{note:{index861,id:UT22084-055-001-2398}}}
And wander far{{note:{index862,id:UT22084-055-001-2399}}} from my teaching.
They maintain the conception of a result
And lose all their wealth of mendicancy. {17}
{{milestone:{label:25.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2400}}}“Those who are lazy and lacking in diligence, 
Who do not maintain the aspect of conduct,
They will stand up and state, {{page:{number:168,id:UT22084-055-001-6001,folio:F.85.a}}}
‘That is not the teaching of the Buddha!’ {18}
{{milestone:{label:25.21,id:UT22084-055-001-2401}}}“Some of them will declare,
‘We are enlightened!’
But they will be uncontrolled, untrained,
And disrespectful to each other. {19}
{{milestone:{label:25.22,id:UT22084-055-001-2402}}}“They will delight in words
And have no stability in the Dharma.
They will have that kind of aspiration,
Desiring what is gained through reputation. {20}
{{milestone:{label:25.23,id:UT22084-055-001-2403}}}“They will be motivated to have a following. 
They will delight in acquisition.
They will be overpowered by arrogance and carelessness.
Their goal will be gain and honors. {21}
{{milestone:{label:25.24,id:UT22084-055-001-2404}}}“Based upon gains and honors
They will desire the intellect’s accomplishments. 
They will build temples and stūpas.
Their interest will be in the women of families. {22}
{{milestone:{label:25.25,id:UT22084-055-001-2405}}}“They will depend upon their perception.
They will dwell in craving and desire.
They will be within the realm of Māra
And they will do the work of laypeople. {23}
{{milestone:{label:25.26,id:UT22084-055-001-2406}}}“Their desire will be like the flames of a fire.
They will give teachings to laypeople.
They will enter into their homes
And they will corrupt those families. {24}
{{milestone:{label:25.27,id:UT22084-055-001-2407}}}“The laypeople will come to think of them
As their teachers.
They will take up residence with them
And they will corrupt their sons and daughters. {25}
{{milestone:{label:25.28,id:UT22084-055-001-2408}}}“They will treat with kindness 
Those who give them food and drink,
And they will think of those people’s wives
And daughters as their own wives.{{note:{index863,id:UT22084-055-001-2409}}} {26}
{{milestone:{label:25.29,id:UT22084-055-001-2410}}}“Laymen will not be as attracted
To their own wives 
As the mendicants will be 
Attracted to the wives of others. {27}
{{milestone:{label:25.30,id:UT22084-055-001-2411}}}“There are the trainings{{note:{index864,id:UT22084-055-001-2412}}} that I have taught
To the laymen who wear white clothing.{{note:{index865,id:UT22084-055-001-2413}}}
At that time, those bhikṣus
Will not even have those trainings. {28}
{{milestone:{label:25.31,id:UT22084-055-001-2414}}}“They will make offerings to me
With bherī drums,{{note:{index866,id:UT22084-055-001-2415}}} conches, and mṛdaṅga drums.{{note:{index867,id:UT22084-055-001-2416}}}
The offerings that are superior
Will not be included in their practices. {29}
{{milestone:{label:25.32,id:UT22084-055-001-2417}}}“When they who have very poor conduct
See those who are maintaining correct conduct
They will say, one to another,
‘They are the same as us.’ {30}
{{milestone:{label:25.33,id:UT22084-055-001-2418}}}“When those with bad conduct and wicked behavior 
Hear correct conduct being praised,
They will stand up and state,
‘That is not the Buddha’s teaching.’ {31} {{page:{number:169,id:UT22084-055-001-6002,folio:F.85.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:25.34,id:UT22084-055-001-2419}}}“They will be devoid of shame.
They will have lost the wealth of the mendicant.
They will debate with words that are false
And reject the enlightenment of buddhahood.{{note:{index868,id:UT22084-055-001-2420}}} {32}
{{milestone:{label:25.35,id:UT22084-055-001-2421}}}“They who have wicked minds
Will reject the Buddha’s teaching.
They will cast aside the Dharma
And they will dwell in the Avīci hell. {33}
{{milestone:{label:25.36,id:UT22084-055-001-2422}}}“Those who have that kind of conduct
Will neither hear me nor see me.
Those who follow the Dharma of fools
Will not attain{{note:{index869,id:UT22084-055-001-2423}}} the wisdom of buddhahood.{{note:{index870,id:UT22084-055-001-2424}}} {34}
{{milestone:{label:25.37,id:UT22084-055-001-2425}}}“They will be hypocrites
Who will deceive by saying,
‘I know everything about that. 
That wisdom is within me.’ {35}
{{milestone:{label:25.38,id:UT22084-055-001-2426}}}“If I were to teach them for an eon
Their confusion would still be vast.
They do no more than make
Promises to be bodhisattvas.{{note:{index871,id:UT22084-055-001-2427}}} {36}
{{milestone:{label:25.39,id:UT22084-055-001-2428}}}“They will be young men
Whose bad behavior is incessant. 
You should not in the future
Be associated{{note:{index872,id:UT22084-055-001-2429}}} with them. {37}
{{milestone:{label:25.40,id:UT22084-055-001-2430}}}“Should you speak with them or converse,
Treat them with respect;
Honor them without being disheartened,
In order to attain the highest enlightenment. {38}
{{milestone:{label:25.41,id:UT22084-055-001-2431}}}“You should ask their age,
And if they are your senior
Show them respect
And bow your head to their feet. {39}
{{milestone:{label:25.42,id:UT22084-055-001-2432}}}“Do not look at their errors,
But see the essence of enlightenment.
Do not feel anger toward them
But always have a loving mind. {40}
{{milestone:{label:25.43,id:UT22084-055-001-2433}}}“If you see an error of theirs 
Do not mention that fault.
Whatever karma they create
The corresponding result will come to them. {41}
{{milestone:{label:25.44,id:UT22084-055-001-2434}}}“Have a smiling face that is like the moon
For both the seniors and the novices.
You should always speak sincerely,
Gently, and without pride. {42}
{{milestone:{label:25.45,id:UT22084-055-001-2435}}}“You should help them in adopting
Dharma robes and receiving alms.
You should keep in your mind the thought,
‘They are all going to become buddhas.’{{note:{index873,id:UT22084-055-001-2436}}} {43}
{{milestone:{label:25.46,id:UT22084-055-001-2437}}}“If they request from you
The gift of the Dharma,
First you should say to them,
‘I do not have much learning.’{{note:{index874,id:UT22084-055-001-2438}}} {44}
{{milestone:{label:25.47,id:UT22084-055-001-2439}}}“You should speak in this way: {{page:{number:170,id:UT22084-055-001-6003,folio:F.86.a}}}
‘Brother, wise scholar, 
How can I say anything
In front of such a great being?’ {45}
{{milestone:{label:25.48,id:UT22084-055-001-2440}}}“Do not speak too hastily.
Examine the one who would be the recipient.
If you know that he is a worthy recipient
Teach him even if he has not requested it. {46}
{{milestone:{label:25.49,id:UT22084-055-001-2441}}}“If you see that there are many present
Among your followers who have bad conduct 
You should not teach them austerity, 
But instead you should praise generosity.{{note:{index875,id:UT22084-055-001-2442}}} {47}
{{milestone:{label:25.50,id:UT22084-055-001-2443}}}“If they have few desires
And maintain pure conduct,
Have a loving mind
And speak to them of austerity. {48}
{{milestone:{label:25.51,id:UT22084-055-001-2444}}}“If there are many with correct conduct
Who have restrained bad desires, 
When that aspect has been attained
Then you should praise correct conduct. {49}
{{milestone:{label:25.52,id:UT22084-055-001-2445}}}“First you should know your students,
And if they are known to be pure
Then teach to them every one 
Of the virtuous qualities that there are. {50}
{{milestone:{label:25.53,id:UT22084-055-001-2446}}}“Always praise and teach
Generosity, conduct, patience, 
Diligence, meditation, and learning,
Contentment, few desires, and austerity.{{note:{index876,id:UT22084-055-001-2447}}} {51}
{{milestone:{label:25.54,id:UT22084-055-001-2448}}}“Living in solitary places, practicing meditation,{{note:{index877,id:UT22084-055-001-2449}}}
And abandoning living among many people 
Should be praised by you
As the doorway to the power of retention.{{note:{index878,id:UT22084-055-001-2450}}} {52}
{{milestone:{label:25.55,id:UT22084-055-001-2451}}}“They should have perfect conduct
By staying in solitary places. 
They should have perfect generosity
Through remaining in seclusion. {53}
{{milestone:{label:25.56,id:UT22084-055-001-2452}}}“Maintaining the aspect of conduct,
They should become very learned. 
Those who seek for this samādhi
Should make offerings to the Buddha’s relics. {54}
{{milestone:{label:25.57,id:UT22084-055-001-2453}}}“Those who seek this peaceful samādhi
Should make offerings to the Buddha
With parasols, banners, and flags,
And with incense, garlands, and ointments. {55}
{{milestone:{label:25.58,id:UT22084-055-001-2454}}}“Without being indolent or disheartened,
They should offer to the Buddha’s relics
Delightful music, 
United with song. {56}
{{milestone:{label:25.59,id:UT22084-055-001-2455}}}“For the highest enlightenment{{note:{index879,id:UT22084-055-001-2456}}}
They should offer to the Lord 
As much incense, garlands, parasols,
Clothing, and powders as there are. {57}
{{milestone:{label:25.60,id:UT22084-055-001-2457}}}“For the sake of this peaceful samādhi, {{page:{number:171,id:UT22084-055-001-6004,folio:F.86.b}}}
All the immeasurable, inconceivable 
Offerings that there can be 
They should make to all the buddhas.{{note:{index880,id:UT22084-055-001-2458}}} {58}
{{milestone:{label:25.61,id:UT22084-055-001-2459}}}“Those who seek unimpeded wisdom, 
Who are without attachment,
Give the highest wisdom of buddhahood,
Equally shared for all beings. {59}
{{milestone:{label:25.62,id:UT22084-055-001-2460}}}“I, too, having become unattached,
And seeking this peaceful samādhi,
Made inconceivable offerings
To the buddhas of the past. {60}
{{milestone:{label:25.63,id:UT22084-055-001-2461}}}“It is difficult to attain the appearance of the buddhas.
It is difficult to attain birth as a human.
It is difficult to attain faith in the teachings,
And to become a mendicant. {61}
{{milestone:{label:25.64,id:UT22084-055-001-2462}}}“One whose mind is dedicated to enlightenment
Is one who pleases the Buddha.{{note:{index881,id:UT22084-055-001-2463}}}
Do not deviate from that commitment,
But remain within that practice. {62}
{{milestone:{label:25.65,id:UT22084-055-001-2464}}}“One who maintains this sūtra
During the time of destruction
Should quickly gain eloquence
And continue its teaching. {63}
{{milestone:{label:25.66,id:UT22084-055-001-2465}}}“For someone who has wished to hear it,
There is an inconceivable accumulation of merit
In possessing just one verse,
Let alone obtaining the entire sūtra. {64}
{{milestone:{label:25.67,id:UT22084-055-001-2466}}}“For even if as many beings as there are in a kalpa
Were diligently to make offerings
To all the beings who have attained enlightenment,
And do so continuously with veneration, {65}
{{milestone:{label:25.68,id:UT22084-055-001-2467}}}“All the merit from the latter
Will come not even to a sixteenth part
Of the merit from possessing 
Just one verse of this samādhi. {66}
{{milestone:{label:25.69,id:UT22084-055-001-2468}}}“One who hears this samādhi
Will be free of uncertainty.
I know these inconceivable benefits
Through my wisdom of buddhahood.” {67}
{{milestone:{label:25.70,id:UT22084-055-001-2469}}}Conclusion of the twenty-fifth chapter, “Engaging in Discernment.”
{{milestone:{label:26,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-26}}}Rejoicing 
Chapter 26
{{milestone:{label:26.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2471}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should be skillful in methods. {{page:{number:172,id:UT22084-055-001-6005,folio:F.87.a}}}{{note:{index882,id:UT22084-055-001-2470}}}
{{milestone:{label:26.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2472}}}“Young man, in what way should bodhisattva mahāsattvas be skillful in methods? For that, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas focus their minds upon all beings. Those bodhisattva mahāsattvas rejoice in whatever roots of merit and accumulations of merit all beings have. Three times every day and three times every night they rejoice in whatever roots of merit and accumulations of merit all beings have, and the roots of merit and accumulation of merit that come from their taking omniscience as the focus of their aspiration they donate to all beings.
{{milestone:{label:26.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2473}}}“Young man, because those bodhisattva mahāsattva possess the accumulation of merit that comes from being skillful in methods, they will quickly attain this samādhi, and they will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.”
{{milestone:{label:26.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2474}}}Thereupon the Bhagavān spoke these verses:
“Three times a day and three times a night
I develop the aspiration to enlightenment 
And rejoice in the entirety of the merit accumulated
By all these beings who are my family. {1}
{{milestone:{label:26.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2476}}}“I rejoice in those who have pure conduct,
Who will do nothing bad even to save their lives.
I rejoice in whatever merit is possessed
By bodhisattvas with perfect aspiration. {2}
{{milestone:{label:26.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2477}}}“I rejoice in those who have faith in the Buddha, 
Faith in the Dharma, and also the Saṅgha.
I rejoice in those who make offerings to the Sugata
Because of their desire for enlightenment.{{note:{index883,id:UT22084-055-001-2478}}} {3}
{{milestone:{label:26.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2479}}}“I rejoice in those who develop the aspiration
For the highest, supreme, unsurpassable enlightenment,
Doing so with great understanding, for the sake of beings,
And so that the lineage of enlightenment will remain.{{note:{index884,id:UT22084-055-001-2480}}} {i}
{{milestone:{label:26.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2481}}}“I rejoice in the bodhisattvas overwhelmed by compassion
Who give away their wealth, grain, and jewels,
Their queens, sons, and daughters,
Their vast kingdoms, and even their own flesh.{{note:{index885,id:UT22084-055-001-2482}}} {ii}
{{milestone:{label:26.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2483}}}“I rejoice in those who give away their own bodies
With joyful minds for the sake of beings,
Having trained in the training of skillful methods {{page:{number:173,id:UT22084-055-001-6006,folio:F.87.b}}}
And subdued their bodies through meditation on wisdom.{{note:{index886,id:UT22084-055-001-2484}}} {iii}
{{milestone:{label:26.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2485}}}“I rejoice in those who live in the forest, 
Always alone and solitary like a rhinoceros,
Always with pure livelihood and few activities, 
Without acting hypocritically for the sake of reputation. {6}
{{milestone:{label:26.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2486}}}“I rejoice in those who have no entanglements,
Who have no envy or yearning for a home,
Who are always terrified of the three realms
And act without attachment to the world. {7}
{{milestone:{label:26.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2487}}}“I rejoice in those who are without complication 
And are saddened by every rebirth into existence.
This samādhi will not be difficult to attain
For those who do not dispute but have peaceful minds. {8}
{{milestone:{label:26.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2488}}}“I rejoice in those who see the harmfulness of crowds,
Who avoid every kind of disagreement, 
Who live in solitude, dwelling at the foot of trees,
And who are heirs of the sugatas focused upon liberation. {9}
{{milestone:{label:26.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2489}}}“I rejoice in those who live in solitude,
Neither praising themselves nor criticizing others.
I rejoice in those who are not careless
But careful in the Buddha’s teaching. {10}
{{milestone:{label:26.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2490}}}“That carefulness is the very root 
Of all the qualities of the aspects of enlightenment. 
This samādhi is not difficult to attain
For any heirs of the Buddha who are always careful. {11}
{{milestone:{label:26.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2491}}}“The teaching of the Sugata is a treasure that has been found.
Attaining homelessness is a second treasure.
The attainment of faith is a third treasure.
This samādhi is a fourth treasure. {12}
{{milestone:{label:26.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2492}}}“On learning of emptiness, of the field of activity of the buddhas,
If it is not rejected, that is a treasure that has been found.
Endless eloquence is a treasure that has been found,
And any dhāraṇī is a supreme treasure. {13}
{{milestone:{label:26.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2493}}}“That carefulness is the very root 
Of all the virtuous qualities that have been proclaimed,
And of correct conduct, learning, giving, and patience.
The Sugata has taught that it is a treasure that has been found. {14}
{{milestone:{label:26.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2494}}}“For those who are careful in the Buddha’s teaching,
For those who have perfect aspirations, {{page:{number:174,id:UT22084-055-001-6007,folio:F.88.a}}}
This samādhi will not be difficult to obtain.
They are established in the Buddha’s teaching.” {15}
{{milestone:{label:26.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2495}}}Conclusion of the twenty-sixth chapter, “Rejoicing.”
{{milestone:{label:27,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-27}}}The Benefits of Generosity
Chapter 27
{{milestone:{label:27.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2496}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, as it has been said, ‘Be careful,’ you, young man, should consequently train in that way. Why is that? Because, young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are careful, the highest, complete enlightenment is not difficult to attain, let alone this samādhi.
{{milestone:{label:27.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2497}}}“Young man, in what way should bodhisattva mahāsattvas be careful? For that, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas should have perfectly pure conduct. Young man, in what way should bodhisattva mahāsattvas have perfectly pure conduct? For that, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have perfectly pure conduct, never separating from an all-knowing mind, should practice the six perfections. Listen, for I shall teach you their benefits.
{{milestone:{label:27.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2498}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who aspire to generosity. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] the kleśa of avarice is overcome; [2] their minds are constantly devoted to generosity; [3] from the ordinary wealth of the populace they obtain what is essential; [4] they are reborn into a wealthy family, and as soon as they are born they have a mind that aspires to generosity;{{note:{index887,id:UT22084-055-001-2499}}} [5] they are beloved by the fourfold assembly; [6] they enter the assembly without fear or lack of confidence; [7] verses that praise their greatness spread to the cardinal and intermediate directions; [8] they have soft and youthful arms and legs; [9] they stand on feet with level soles;{{note:{index888,id:UT22084-055-001-2500}}} and [10] they are never apart from kalyāṇamitras {{note:{index889,id:UT22084-055-001-2501}}} until they are seated at the Bodhimaṇḍa. {{page:{number:175,id:UT22084-055-001-6008,folio:F.88.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:27.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2502}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who aspire to generosity.”
It was said:
{{milestone:{label:27.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2504}}}“Avarice is overcome.
Their generosity increases.
They are those who obtain the essentials
And are reborn into a wealthy family. {1}
{{milestone:{label:27.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2505}}}“As soon as they are born
There is generosity in their minds.
They are beloved by beings,
Both the laity and mendicants. {2}
{{milestone:{label:27.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2506}}}“They enter the assembly
Fearlessly and confidently.
Their renown spreads
Through the villages and towns. {3}
{{milestone:{label:27.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2507}}}“They have soft arms and legs 
That they gain without difficulty.
They obtain kalyāṇamitras,
Both buddhas and śrāvakas. {4}
{{milestone:{label:27.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2508}}}“They never have an avaricious mind;
Their minds always delight in generosity.
They are beloved by millions of beings.
Those are the benefits of being without avarice. {5}
{{milestone:{label:27.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2509}}}“They are reborn into a family with great wealth.
At birth they have minds that delight in generosity.
They obtain the essentials and choose the time of passing away.
Those are the benefits of being without avarice. {6}
{{milestone:{label:27.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2510}}}“Fearlessly they enter an assembly.
Their renown spreads in all directions.
They always have soft arms and legs.
Those are the benefits of being without avarice. {7}
{{milestone:{label:27.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2511}}}“It is not difficult for them to obtain kalyāṇamitras.
They also see buddhas and śrāvakas.
Seeing them, they make offerings to them with faith.
Those are the benefits of being without avarice.” {8}
{{milestone:{label:27.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2512}}}Conclusion of the twenty-seventh chapter, “The Benefits of Generosity.”
{{milestone:{label:28,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-28}}}The Teaching on Correct Conduct
Chapter 28
{{milestone:{label:28.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2513}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from perfectly pure, correct conduct. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they devote{{note:{index890,id:UT22084-055-001-2514}}} themselves to wisdom and perfect it; [2] they follow the example of the buddhas; [3] they do not criticize the wise; [4] they do not waver from their vows; [5] they maintain their practice; [6] they turn away{{note:{index891,id:UT22084-055-001-2515}}} from saṃsāra; [7] they are led to attain nirvāṇa;{{note:{index892,id:UT22084-055-001-2516}}} [8] they live without faults arising; {{page:{number:176,id:UT22084-055-001-6009,folio:F.89.a}}} [9] they attain samādhi; and [10] they will never be poor.{{note:{index893,id:UT22084-055-001-2517}}}
{{milestone:{label:28.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2518}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have perfectly pure, correct conduct.” 
It was said concerning this:
{{milestone:{label:28.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2520}}}“They bring wisdom to perfection,
Follow the example of the buddhas,
Do not criticize those who are wise,
And they are always without fear. {1}
{{milestone:{label:28.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2521}}}“They do not waver from their vows,
They maintain their practice,
They are led to attain nirvāṇa, 
And they turn away from saṃsāra. {2}
{{milestone:{label:28.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2522}}}“They live without faults arising,
They quickly attain samādhi,
They will not be poor,
And they maintain correct conduct. {3}
{{milestone:{label:28.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2523}}}“Their wisdom will be perfected,
And they follow the example of the buddhas.
They never make criticisms of the wise,
And thus their conduct is completely pure. {4}
{{milestone:{label:28.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2524}}}“The wise ones never waver from their vows.
The heroic ones{{note:{index894,id:UT22084-055-001-2525}}} maintain their practice.
Seeing the many faults of saṃsāra
They go toward nirvāṇa. {5}
{{milestone:{label:28.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2526}}}“There are no faults{{note:{index895,id:UT22084-055-001-2527}}} that arise in their minds;
Thus, they maintain the strength of correct conduct,
And quickly attain an immaculate{{note:{index896,id:UT22084-055-001-2528}}} samādhi.
Those are the benefits of pure, correct conduct.” {6}
{{milestone:{label:28.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2529}}}Conclusion of the twenty-eighth chapter, “The Teaching on Correct Conduct.”
{{milestone:{label:29,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-29}}}Ten Benefits
Chapter 29
{{milestone:{label:29.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2530}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from maintaining patience and being kind. {{page:{number:177,id:UT22084-055-001-6010,folio:F.89.b}}} What are these ten? They are: [1] they are not burned by fire; [2] they are not slain by weapons; [3] they are not affected by poison; [4] they do not drown in water; [5] the devas protect them; [6] they attain a body adorned by the primary signs of a great being; [7] all the doorways to their rebirth in lower existences are closed; [8] it is not difficult for them to be reborn in the paradise of Brahmā; [9] they are happy day and night; and [10] their physical sensations of comfort and pleasure are never lost. 
{{milestone:{label:29.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2531}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from maintaining patience and being kind.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2533}}}“They are not burned by fire,
They are not killed by weapons,
They are not affected by poison,
They do not drown in water, {1}
{{milestone:{label:29.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2534}}}“They are protected by devas,
They have the thirty-two primary signs,
And the lower existences are closed to them.
Those are the benefits of patience. {2}
{{milestone:{label:29.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2535}}}“The state of Brahmā and the state of Śakra
Are not difficult for them to attain.
They always dwell in happiness
And have inconceivable pleasure. {3}
{{milestone:{label:29.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2536}}}“They are not slain by fire or weapons;
They are not killed by poison or drowning.
They are protected by devas, nāgas, and yakṣas.
Those are the benefits of maintaining kindness. {4}
{{milestone:{label:29.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2537}}}“Their bodies will have the thirty-two primary signs.
They will not fall into the lower existences,
And at death they will be reborn in the realm of Brahmā.
Those are the benefits of maintaining patience. {5}
{{milestone:{label:29.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2538}}}“They have happiness day and night.
Their bodies will have pleasurable sensations.
They will have the power of patience and bliss.
Those wise ones will always have a tranquil mind. {6}
{{milestone:{label:29.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2539}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from taking up diligence. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] it is difficult to approach their level;{{note:{index897,id:UT22084-055-001-2540}}} [2] they attain the state of being cared for by the buddhas; [3] they will be cared for by the devas; [4] they maintain the Dharma they have received; [5] they obtain the Dharma they have not previously received; [6] they attain the lineage of samādhis;{{note:{index898,id:UT22084-055-001-2541}}} [7] they have few illnesses; [8] they digest their food well; [9] they are like lotuses; and [10] they are not like pestles.{{note:{index899,id:UT22084-055-001-2542}}}
{{milestone:{label:29.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2543}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from taking up diligence.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2545}}}“It is difficult to approach their level.{{note:{index900,id:UT22084-055-001-2546}}}
They are without idleness.{{note:{index901,id:UT22084-055-001-2547}}}
The devas protect them.
They quickly{{note:{index902,id:UT22084-055-001-2548}}} see the buddhas. {7}
{{milestone:{label:29.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2549}}} “Their prayers are fulfilled,{{note:{index903,id:UT22084-055-001-2550}}}
They attain the lineage of samādhis,
And they do not become ill.{{note:{index904,id:UT22084-055-001-2551}}}{{page:{number:178,id:UT22084-055-001-6011,folio:F.90.a}}}
Those are the benefits of diligence.{{note:{index905,id:UT22084-055-001-2552}}} {8–9}{{note:{index906,id:UT22084-055-001-2553}}}
{{milestone:{label:29.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2554}}}“They digest pleasurably, without harm,
That which they eat and drink. {10} 
They gradually develop
Like a blue lotus in the middle of water.{{note:{index907,id:UT22084-055-001-2555}}}
{{milestone:{label:29.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2556}}}“In that way the bodhisattvas
Develop through good qualities. {11}
The days and the nights
Pass fruitfully for them.{{note:{index908,id:UT22084-055-001-2557}}}
{{milestone:{label:29.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2558}}}“The Tathāgata who has engaged in diligence,
Gaining accomplishments for numerous eons, 
Has taught to the bodhisattvas 
These benefits of possessing diligence. {12}
{{milestone:{label:29.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2559}}}“Those who engage in diligence
Are in the care of the jinas.
The devas, too, make aspirations for them.
They will soon attain the Buddha’s enlightenment. {13}
{{milestone:{label:29.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2560}}}“What they have learned will never diminish,
And they give many other Dharma teachings.
Their confidence of speech increases immensely.
Those are the benefits of engaging in diligence. {14}
{{milestone:{label:29.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2561}}}“They will quickly attain the lineage of samādhis.
They will never become ill.
Whatever food they eat
They will comfortably digest completely. {15}
{{milestone:{label:29.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2562}}}“Day and night the good qualities
Of their powerful diligence increase.
Through the power of this diligence,
Before long they will attain enlightenment. {16}
{{milestone:{label:29.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2563}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from being devoted to meditation. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they maintain their bodhisattva conduct; [2] they engage in the field of that conduct;{{note:{index909,id:UT22084-055-001-2564}}} [3] they live free from anguish; [4] their sensory faculties are protected;{{note:{index910,id:UT22084-055-001-2565}}} [5] they experience pleasure;{{note:{index911,id:UT22084-055-001-2566}}} [6] they are separated from desire; [7] they have insatiability for meditation; [8] they are free from the domain of Māra; [9] they are established in the domain of the Buddha; and [10] they ripen the state of liberation. 
{{milestone:{label:29.21,id:UT22084-055-001-2567}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from being devoted to meditation.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.22,id:UT22084-055-001-2569}}}“They are never without bodhisattva conduct,
As they are established in bodhisattva conduct.
The yogins practice the field of that conduct, 
And reject that which is not the field of that conduct. {17}
{{milestone:{label:29.23,id:UT22084-055-001-2570}}}“They live without anguish.
Their senses hidden and bound,
They experience pleasure. {{page:{number:179,id:UT22084-055-001-6012,folio:F.90.b}}}
Their field of conduct is practicing meditation. {18}
{{milestone:{label:29.24,id:UT22084-055-001-2571}}}“They are without desire, or the craving of desire.
They abide in the bliss of meditation.
They are free from the domain of Māra
And dwell in the Buddha’s domain. {19}
{{milestone:{label:29.25,id:UT22084-055-001-2572}}}“This is the particular quality of the yogins:
That they delight in being alone in the forest.
They bring liberation to fruition.
Those are the ten aspects. {20}
{{milestone:{label:29.26,id:UT22084-055-001-2573}}}“The bodhisattvas remain in bodhisattva conduct
And they reject everything that is not that conduct.
They reject that which is not the field of that conduct and remain in that which is.
Those are the benefits of endeavoring in samādhi. {21}
{{milestone:{label:29.27,id:UT22084-055-001-2574}}}“They never experience anguish.
They reach the state of higher bliss.
Both their body and mind become blissful.
These are the benefits of endeavoring in meditation.{{note:{index912,id:UT22084-055-001-2575}}} {22}
{{milestone:{label:29.28,id:UT22084-055-001-2576}}}“They live secretly in solitary places. 
They never have any distractions.
Thus their bodies are in isolation
And they attain happiness free of desires. {23}
{{milestone:{label:29.29,id:UT22084-055-001-2577}}}“They are unstained by desires and have no kleśas.
Thus they are free from the domain of Māra
And are established in the domain of the tathāgatas.
They bring their liberation to fruition. {24}
{{milestone:{label:29.30,id:UT22084-055-001-2578}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from engaging in wisdom. What are these ten? They are: [1] they give away all their possessions without becoming proud that they are pure; [2] they have immaculate, correct conduct without forming an attachment to that conduct; [3] they maintain the power of patience without maintaining the conceptualization that there are beings; [4] they take up diligence in isolation from body and mind;{{note:{index913,id:UT22084-055-001-2579}}} [5] in meditating they meditate with a non-abiding meditation; [6] they are invincible to the māras; [7] they are unshakable to all adversaries;{{note:{index914,id:UT22084-055-001-2580}}} [8] they attain illumination regarding all engagement with the composite;{{note:{index915,id:UT22084-055-001-2581}}} [9] they engage in vast great compassion for all beings, and have no aspiration for the level of the śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas;{{note:{index916,id:UT22084-055-001-2582}}}{{page:{number:180,id:UT22084-055-001-6013,folio:F.91.a}}} and [10] they enter into the dhyānas, samādhis, and samāpattis of the buddhas.{{note:{index917,id:UT22084-055-001-2583}}}
{{milestone:{label:29.31,id:UT22084-055-001-2584}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from engaging in wisdom.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.32,id:UT22084-055-001-2586}}}“The heroic ones give away all their possessions
But do not become proud that they are pure.
They keep their correct conduct immaculate
But they form no attachment to that. {25}
{{milestone:{label:29.33,id:UT22084-055-001-2587}}}“The wise ones meditate on patience
But have expelled the conceptualization of beings.
They are those who engage in diligence
But in isolation from body and mind. {26}
{{milestone:{label:29.34,id:UT22084-055-001-2588}}}“They are those who cultivate meditation, 
But without abiding and independent;
They are invincible to the māras.
Those are the qualities of those who have wisdom. {27}
{{milestone:{label:29.35,id:UT22084-055-001-2589}}}“They are unshakable 
To every adversary
And have obtained the illumination of saṃsāra.
Those are the qualities of wisdom. {28}
{{milestone:{label:29.36,id:UT22084-055-001-2590}}}“They have attained great compassion
Toward all beings.
They never have an aspiration
For the wisdom of the śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha. {29}
{{milestone:{label:29.37,id:UT22084-055-001-2591}}}“They are not proud of being pure through giving away all their possessions.
They have immaculate correct conduct but have no attachment to conduct.
They meditate on patience but have no conceptualization of beings.
Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom. {30}
{{milestone:{label:29.38,id:UT22084-055-001-2592}}}“They engage in diligence but in isolation.{{note:{index918,id:UT22084-055-001-2593}}}
They meditate without being bound, without fixation.
They are wise{{note:{index919,id:UT22084-055-001-2594}}} and are invincible to Māra.{{note:{index920,id:UT22084-055-001-2595}}}
Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom. {31}
{{milestone:{label:29.39,id:UT22084-055-001-2596}}}“They are unshakable to adversaries.{{note:{index921,id:UT22084-055-001-2597}}}
They have discovered the shallowness{{note:{index922,id:UT22084-055-001-2598}}} of the composite,
And they have vast compassion for beings.
Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom. {32}
{{milestone:{label:29.40,id:UT22084-055-001-2599}}}“They never give rise to an aspiration to be
A pratyekabuddha or śrāvaka,
And thus they are established in the qualities of a buddha.
Those are the benefits of being devoted to wisdom.{{note:{index923,id:UT22084-055-001-2600}}} {33}
{{milestone:{label:29.41,id:UT22084-055-001-2601}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas from becoming very learned. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they do not create kleśas;{{note:{index924,id:UT22084-055-001-2602}}} [2] they do not develop malice;{{note:{index925,id:UT22084-055-001-2603}}}{{page:{number:181,id:UT22084-055-001-6014,folio:F.91.b}}} [3] they expose doubts; [4] they make views accurate; [5] they shun the wrong paths; [6] they are established on the true path; [7] they have reached the doorway to deathlessness; [8] they are close to enlightenment; [9] they are a light for beings; and [10] they have no fear of the lower existences. 
{{milestone:{label:29.42,id:UT22084-055-001-2604}}} “Young man, those are the ten benefits for the bodhisattva mahāsattvas from becoming very learned.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.43,id:UT22084-055-001-2606}}}“These are taught to be the ten benefits
From becoming very learned
Just as they are known 
By the Tathāgata, the Buddha. {34}
{{milestone:{label:29.44,id:UT22084-055-001-2607}}}“They know the two aspects
Of the kleśas and of purification.
They reject the kleśas
And follow{{note:{index926,id:UT22084-055-001-2608}}} the path of purification. {35}
{{milestone:{label:29.45,id:UT22084-055-001-2609}}}“The wise ones reject doubts
And develop accurate views.
They shun the wrong path
And follow the correct path. {36}
{{milestone:{label:29.46,id:UT22084-055-001-2610}}}“They are at the door to deathlessness
And they are close to enlightenment.
They are a light for beings
And they are not afraid of the lower existences. {37}
{{milestone:{label:29.47,id:UT22084-055-001-2611}}}“They know the numerous properties of having the kleśas,
And in the same way they know the aspect of purification.
They completely reject the kleśas
And train in the supreme quality of purification. {38}
{{milestone:{label:29.48,id:UT22084-055-001-2612}}}“They expose the doubts of all beings.
They have a view that is always accurate.
They shun the wrong path
And are always upon the true path of peace. {39}
{{milestone:{label:29.49,id:UT22084-055-001-2613}}}“They are always beside the doorway to deathlessness;
They are always close to stainless enlightenment.
They have become a light to all the multitudes of beings
And they have no fear of the lower existences. {40}
{{milestone:{label:29.50,id:UT22084-055-001-2614}}}“Young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are intent on giving the Dharma, there are ten benefits that come from giving the Dharma. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they reject that which should not be done; [2] they engage in that which should be done; [3] they follow the Dharma of a worthy person; [4] they purify buddha realms; [5] they reach the Bodhimaṇḍa; [6] they give away material things; [7] they overcome the kleśas; {{page:{number:182,id:UT22084-055-001-6015,folio:F.92.a}}} [8] they give their portion{{note:{index927,id:UT22084-055-001-2615}}} to all beings; [9] they meditate on love toward those on whom their minds are focused; and [10] they attain happiness in this life. 
{{milestone:{label:29.51,id:UT22084-055-001-2616}}}“Young man, for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are intent on giving the Dharma, those are the ten benefits that come from giving the Dharma.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.52,id:UT22084-055-001-2618}}}“Those who give the supreme gift,
The gift of the Dharma, are not misers.
The Lord of the World has taught
That they will have ten benefits. {41}
{{milestone:{label:29.53,id:UT22084-055-001-2619}}}“They reject all that should not be done;
The wise ones engage in what should be done.
They obtain the Dharma of a worthy person
And maintain a motivation of generosity. {42}
{{milestone:{label:29.54,id:UT22084-055-001-2620}}}“They purify a buddha realm.{{note:{index928,id:UT22084-055-001-2621}}}
Their realm is inconceivable.{{note:{index929,id:UT22084-055-001-2622}}}
They are always on the Bodhimaṇḍa,{{note:{index930,id:UT22084-055-001-2623}}}
Which is the result of giving the Dharma. {43}
{{milestone:{label:29.55,id:UT22084-055-001-2624}}}“They give away all material things.
They follow the king of the Dharma. 
For those who have overcome the kleśas,
Enlightenment is not hard to attain. {44}
{{milestone:{label:29.56,id:UT22084-055-001-2625}}}“With a loving mind they give
Their portion to all beings.
They are those who have no envy,
And they have a happiness higher than that of humans. {45}
{{milestone:{label:29.57,id:UT22084-055-001-2626}}}“They are learned people who reject what should not be done.
They are wise people who are always doing what should be done.
They always follow the Dharma of great beings.
They are learned people who always give the gift of the Dharma. {46}
{{milestone:{label:29.58,id:UT22084-055-001-2627}}}“Their realm is one that is always pure.
They increase those qualities that are aspects of enlightenment.
They are always close to the Bodhimaṇḍa.
Those are the benefits of giving the Dharma. {47}
{{milestone:{label:29.59,id:UT22084-055-001-2628}}}“They have no kleśas, and give material things away.
They know the characteristics of things.
They are liberated from all attachment.
They never have any impediments. {48}
{{milestone:{label:29.60,id:UT22084-055-001-2629}}}“They have a wise one’s mind. 
They wish for all beings to be happy. 
They have loving minds free of envy,
And in this life their happiness is not little. {49}
{{milestone:{label:29.61,id:UT22084-055-001-2630}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who dwell in emptiness. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they dwell in the dwelling of the Buddha;{{note:{index931,id:UT22084-055-001-2631}}}{{page:{number:183,id:UT22084-055-001-6016,folio:F.92.b}}} [2] their meditation is nondwelling;{{note:{index932,id:UT22084-055-001-2632}}} [3] they are not intent on rebirth;{{note:{index933,id:UT22084-055-001-2633}}} [4] they have no clinging to conduct;{{note:{index934,id:UT22084-055-001-2634}}} [5] they do not criticize superior beings; [6] they live in an appropriate manner; [7] they do not conceptualize the objects of perception;{{note:{index935,id:UT22084-055-001-2635}}} [8] they remain detached;{{note:{index936,id:UT22084-055-001-2636}}} [9] they do not disparage the buddhas;{{note:{index937,id:UT22084-055-001-2637}}} and [10] they possess the Dharma.{{note:{index938,id:UT22084-055-001-2638}}}
{{milestone:{label:29.62,id:UT22084-055-001-2639}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who dwell in emptiness.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.63,id:UT22084-055-001-2641}}}“The yogins dwell in that which is
The dwelling of the lords of men
And the field of activity of all the buddhas,
Without the conception of a life. {50}
{{milestone:{label:29.64,id:UT22084-055-001-2642}}}“Without dependence on any existence
They never give up the superior dhyāna.
Having seen the nature of phenomena
They have no intention of being reborn. {51}
{{milestone:{label:29.65,id:UT22084-055-001-2643}}}“Those who have no clinging to conduct
Will not be dependent on conduct.{{note:{index939,id:UT22084-055-001-2644}}}
They do not criticize in any way
Another superior being{{note:{index940,id:UT22084-055-001-2645}}} who is without defilement.{{note:{index941,id:UT22084-055-001-2646}}} {52}
{{milestone:{label:29.66,id:UT22084-055-001-2647}}}“They live in an appropriate manner
And are not known to quarrel.
The yogins do not conceptualize things
But live always detached. {53}
{{milestone:{label:29.67,id:UT22084-055-001-2648}}}“They do not disparage the Buddha
Even for the sake of their life.
While remaining in the emptiness of phenomena
They are fearlessly visible in their body. {54}
{{milestone:{label:29.68,id:UT22084-055-001-2649}}}“They teach the Dharma with veneration 
For the inconceivable enlightenment of buddhahood
Of all the lords of the worlds,
And they have no doubt in the Dharma of the Buddha. {55}
{{milestone:{label:29.69,id:UT22084-055-001-2650}}}“The dwelling place of the supreme individuals,
The level not that of the many kinds of tīrthika, 
There where there is no being, soul, or person:
That is where the bodhisattvas dwell.{{note:{index942,id:UT22084-055-001-2651}}} {56}
{{milestone:{label:29.70,id:UT22084-055-001-2652}}}“They have no dwelling whatsoever.
They remain in the bliss of nondwelling dhyāna.{{note:{index943,id:UT22084-055-001-2653}}}
They see that phenomena have no self, no being,
And they do not give rise to the concept of creation. {57}
{{milestone:{label:29.71,id:UT22084-055-001-2654}}}“They understand the nature of phenomena.
They have no dependence even on conduct.
They do not conceive of themselves as pure because of conduct,
And always have faith in the buddhas.{{note:{index944,id:UT22084-055-001-2655}}} {58}
{{milestone:{label:29.72,id:UT22084-055-001-2656}}}“They meditate on the empty nature of all phenomena
And they are never in any way inappropriate. {{page:{number:184,id:UT22084-055-001-6017,folio:F.93.a}}}
They possess the pure Dharma of the tathāgatas
And do not disparage the guides. {59}
{{milestone:{label:29.73,id:UT22084-055-001-2657}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who remain intently in meditative seclusion. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] their minds are unpolluted; [2] they remain careful; [3] they keep the Buddha in mind; [4] they have faith in bodhisattva conduct;{{note:{index945,id:UT22084-055-001-2658}}} [5] they have no uncertainty concerning wisdom;{{note:{index946,id:UT22084-055-001-2659}}} [6] they have gratitude toward the buddhas;{{note:{index947,id:UT22084-055-001-2660}}} [7] they do not abandon{{note:{index948,id:UT22084-055-001-2661}}} the Dharma; [8] they maintain vows perfectly; [9] they have attained the level of self-discipline; and [10] they have the direct perception of the four discernments. 
{{milestone:{label:29.74,id:UT22084-055-001-2662}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who remain intently in meditative seclusion.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.75,id:UT22084-055-001-2664}}}“Their minds are unpolluted.
They have rejected all carelessness.
They maintain carefulness.
Their field of activity is meditative seclusion. {60}
{{milestone:{label:29.76,id:UT22084-055-001-2665}}}“They have faith in the buddhas, having heard
Of the conduct of the Lord of the World. 
The yogins have no doubt concerning wisdom,
The inconceivable wisdom of the buddhas. {61}
{{milestone:{label:29.77,id:UT22084-055-001-2666}}}“They have gratitude toward the buddhas,
And have no doubt concerning the Dharma of the buddhas.
They maintain their vows perfectly,
And have attained the level of self-discipline. {62}
{{milestone:{label:29.78,id:UT22084-055-001-2667}}}“They have attained discernment.
They delight in being alone in the forest.
They have forsaken gain and honors,
And their field of activity is meditative seclusion. {63}
{{milestone:{label:29.79,id:UT22084-055-001-2668}}}“Their minds are unpolluted.
They have forsaken all carelessness.
They are great beings who are always careful.
Those are the benefits of being dedicated to samādhi. {64}
{{milestone:{label:29.80,id:UT22084-055-001-2669}}}“They keep in mind the buddhas, the supreme humans,
And they have faith in their supreme conduct.
They do not doubt the wisdom of the tathāgatas.
Those are the benefits of being dedicated to samādhi. {65}
{{milestone:{label:29.81,id:UT22084-055-001-2670}}}“They always have gratitude toward the buddhas.
They do not forsake the Dharma even for the sake of their life.
At all times they keep their vows perfectly.
Those are the benefits of being dedicated to samādhi. {66}
{{milestone:{label:29.82,id:UT22084-055-001-2671}}}“They have attained the level of self-discipline. {{page:{number:185,id:UT22084-055-001-6018,folio:F.93.b}}}
They quickly attain the direct perception of discernment.
They speak with the unceasing confidence of speech.
They teach millions and billions of sūtras. {67}
{{milestone:{label:29.83,id:UT22084-055-001-2672}}}“They quickly attain the enlightenment of buddhahood.
They protect the teaching of the Guide.
They defeat all who are adversaries.
They extensively propagate the enlightenment of buddhahood. {68}
{{milestone:{label:29.84,id:UT22084-055-001-2673}}}“When those bodhisattvas pass away,
They go to the realm of Sukhāvatī.
They hear the highest Dharma from Amitāyus
And attain the acceptance of the nonorigination of phenomena. {69} 
{{milestone:{label:29.85,id:UT22084-055-001-2674}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are dedicated to solitude. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they have few activities; [2] they have gone far from busy crowds; [3] they have no quarrels; [4] they have no harm; [5] they do not increase defilements;{{note:{index949,id:UT22084-055-001-2675}}} [6] they do not create any cause for disputes; [7] they have perfectly peaceful conduct; [8] they maintain perfect self-restraint; [9] their minds are prepared for liberation; and [10] they quickly manifest liberation. 
{{milestone:{label:29.86,id:UT22084-055-001-2676}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who are dedicated to solitude.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.87,id:UT22084-055-001-2678}}}“They always have few activities.
They have gone far from busy crowds.
They have no quarrels.
They live alone in the forest. {70}
{{milestone:{label:29.88,id:UT22084-055-001-2679}}}“Without an intention to cause harm
They do not increase their defilements.
They have no cause for disputes.
Those are the qualities of living in a forest. {71}
{{milestone:{label:29.89,id:UT22084-055-001-2680}}}“They are peaceful in their conduct.
They restrain their body, speech, and mind.
They are prepared for liberation;
They will quickly reach liberation. {72}
{{milestone:{label:29.90,id:UT22084-055-001-2681}}}“They are yogins who always have few activities.
They have shunned the many faults of busy gatherings.
The yogins{{note:{index950,id:UT22084-055-001-2682}}} do not ever quarrel.
Those are the qualities of living in a solitary place. {73}
{{milestone:{label:29.91,id:UT22084-055-001-2683}}}“When they have become saddened by the composite,
They never harbor any longing for the world,
And they do not increase their defilements.
The ones who live in a forest gain these benefits. {74}
{{milestone:{label:29.92,id:UT22084-055-001-2684}}}“There never arises in them a cause for disputes. {{page:{number:186,id:UT22084-055-001-6019,folio:F.94.a}}}
They live in solitude, delighting in peace.
Their body, speech, and mind are restrained.
The ones who live in solitude will have many qualities. {75}
{{milestone:{label:29.93,id:UT22084-055-001-2685}}}“They are prepared for liberation.
They will quickly attain the peace of liberation.
They dwell in the forest and are close to liberation.
Those who dwell in solitude will have all these qualities. {76}
{{milestone:{label:29.94,id:UT22084-055-001-2686}}}“Young man, there are ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who live by receiving alms in the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy. What are the ten benefits? They are: [1] they have no desire for a reputation; [2] they have no desire for fame; [3] they have no desire for honors or gains; [4] they remain within the four noble families;{{note:{index951,id:UT22084-055-001-2687}}} [5] they have no hypocrisy or boasting; [6] they do not praise themselves; [7] they do not criticize others; [8] they engage with households without aversion or attachment;{{note:{index952,id:UT22084-055-001-2688}}} [9] they give the Dharma without expectation of a reward;{{note:{index953,id:UT22084-055-001-2689}}} and [10] the Dharma they teach while remaining in the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy will be remembered. 
{{milestone:{label:29.95,id:UT22084-055-001-2690}}}“Young man, those are the ten benefits for bodhisattva mahāsattvas who live by receiving alms in the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy.” 
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.96,id:UT22084-055-001-2692}}}“They have no desire for a reputation.
They do not wish for fame.
Those who remain in the disciplines of mendicancy
Are indifferent to gain and loss. {77}
{{milestone:{label:29.97,id:UT22084-055-001-2693}}}“They do not abandon the noble family.
They have no hypocrisy or boastfulness.
They do not praise themselves
And they do not criticize others. {78}
{{milestone:{label:29.98,id:UT22084-055-001-2694}}}“They have no attachment or aversion,
And teach the Dharma with no thought of reward.
The words they speak will be remembered.
Recipients of alms will have those qualities.{{note:{index954,id:UT22084-055-001-2695}}} {79}
{{milestone:{label:29.99,id:UT22084-055-001-2696}}}“They do not seek reputation, fame, or gain.
They remain within the four noble families.
The wise ones are neither hypocritical nor boastful. 
Those are the qualities of dedication to mendicancy. {80}
{{milestone:{label:29.100,id:UT22084-055-001-2697}}}“They do not praise themselves or criticize others.
They are not upset when spoken to harshly.
They are not delighted when they hear themselves praised. {{page:{number:187,id:UT22084-055-001-6020,folio:F.94.b}}}
Recipients of alms will have that contentment.{{note:{index955,id:UT22084-055-001-2698}}} {81}
{{milestone:{label:29.101,id:UT22084-055-001-2699}}}“They give the gift of the Dharma without thought of reward.
They do not search for fame or gain.
The words they speak will be remembered.
Those are the benefits that come from dedication to mendicancy. {82}
{{milestone:{label:29.102,id:UT22084-055-001-2700}}}“Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who dwell in solitude while maintaining those qualities of the Dharma will obtain the treasure of the buddhas, they will obtain the treasure of the Dharma, they will obtain the treasure of wisdom, and they will obtain the treasure of knowing the past, the future, and the present.
{{milestone:{label:29.103,id:UT22084-055-001-2701}}}“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the buddhas? Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who practice alone, who dwell in solitude, will attain the five higher cognitions. What are the five higher cognitions? They are divine sight, divine hearing, the knowledge of others’ minds, remembering past lives, and possessing miraculous powers. Young man, those are the five higher cognitions that are obtained. Through divine vision, which transcends human vision, the countless, innumerable buddha bhagavāns in the eastern direction are seen. In the same way the countless, innumerable buddha bhagavāns in the southern, western, and northern directions are seen. They constantly have this vision of the buddhas. Young man, in that way the bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the buddhas.
{{milestone:{label:29.104,id:UT22084-055-001-2702}}}“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the Dharma? The bodhisattva mahāsattvas hear with their divine hearing the Dharma that is taught by those buddha bhagavāns in the ten directions. They are constantly hearing the Dharma. Young man, in that way the bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of the Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:29.105,id:UT22084-055-001-2703}}}“Young man, how do the bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of wisdom? Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have that wisdom obtain the entire Dharma. They do not forget anything that they have obtained, and teach the Dharma to beings, {{page:{number:188,id:UT22084-055-001-6021,folio:F.95.a}}} knowing what will be beneficial for any one person. Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of wisdom.
{{milestone:{label:29.106,id:UT22084-055-001-2704}}}“Young man, how do bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of knowing the past, the future, and the present? Through the higher cognitions they gain the knowledge of the minds and conduct of all beings in the past, the future, and the present. Young man, in that way bodhisattva mahāsattvas obtain the treasure of knowing the past, the future, and the present.
{{milestone:{label:29.107,id:UT22084-055-001-2705}}}“Young man, in brief, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who maintain the qualities of the Dharma in that way will obtain the entire Dharma of the buddhas. This level is not reached by śrāvakas or pratyekabuddhas, let alone any adversary of the Dharma.”
On this topic, it was said:
{{milestone:{label:29.108,id:UT22084-055-001-2707}}}“The wise ones who remain in solitude
Will quickly attain the treasure of the buddhas, 
The treasure of the Dharma, the treasure of wisdom, 
The treasure of the past, and the five higher cognitions.”{{note:{index956,id:UT22084-055-001-2708}}} {83} 
{{milestone:{label:29.109,id:UT22084-055-001-2709}}}Conclusion of the twenty-ninth chapter, “Ten Benefits.”
{{milestone:{label:30,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-30}}}Tejaguṇarāja
Chapter 30
{{milestone:{label:30.1,id:UT22084-055-001-2710}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, you should train in this way, thinking, ‘I will abandon even the pleasures of the kingship of a divine cakravartin and enter homelessness.’
{{milestone:{label:30.2,id:UT22084-055-001-2711}}}“Young man, having entered homelessness you should maintain the disciplines of mendicancy, live in solitude, and develop perfect mildness and patience.
{{milestone:{label:30.3,id:UT22084-055-001-2712}}}“Young man, you should apply yourself diligently, as if your hair and clothes were on fire, and listen to the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, learn it, understand it, keep it, recite it to others, promote it, proclaim it, chant it, meditate on it with unadulterated meditation, promulgate it, and make it widely known to others.
{{milestone:{label:30.4,id:UT22084-055-001-2713}}}“Young man, you should always, like a rhinoceros, dwell without a companion in the forest.”{{note:{index957,id:UT22084-055-001-2714}}}{{page:{number:189,id:UT22084-055-001-6022,folio:F.95.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:30.5,id:UT22084-055-001-2715}}}Thereupon the Bhagavān, in order to explain this topic,{{note:{index958,id:UT22084-055-001-2716}}} gave a detailed teaching on this episode from the past by chanting the following verses to the youth Candraprabha:
{{milestone:{label:30.6,id:UT22084-055-001-2717}}}“I remember many hundreds of eons ago
There was a guide of limitless renown.
Multitudes of humans, devas, and nāgas made offerings to him.
He was a jina named Tejaguṇarāja. {1}
{{milestone:{label:30.7,id:UT22084-055-001-2718}}}“During that time there formed a community
Of a hundred and sixty million bhikṣus with higher cognitions,
Who had completely attained the power of the discernments, 
Who practiced the austerity of the disciplines of mendicancy, and who had peaceful minds. {2}
{{milestone:{label:30.8,id:UT22084-055-001-2719}}}“At that time there were in this Jambudvīpa
One billion seven hundred and sixty million towns,
And each of them was five yojanas wide,
And was particularly supreme, made of the seven precious materials. {3}
{{milestone:{label:30.9,id:UT22084-055-001-2720}}}“At that time, all of those perfect towns
Were adorned by many hundreds of parks,
And all those parks were adorned 
With fresh flowers and fruit, like massed clouds. {4}
{{milestone:{label:30.10,id:UT22084-055-001-2721}}}“Those perfect parks were adorned
With various beautiful trees with edible fruits—
Covered with jackfruits, mangos, rose apples, and breadfruit,
And with hundreds of karnikara, magnolia, and puṇṇaga trees. {5}
{{milestone:{label:30.11,id:UT22084-055-001-2722}}}“At that time, flocks of birds in banyan trees would sing—
Hundreds of cuckoos, avadavats, and peacocks,
And flocks of many other birds were heard:
The songs of parrots,{{note:{index959,id:UT22084-055-001-2723}}} partridges, and snipes. {6}
{{milestone:{label:30.12,id:UT22084-055-001-2724}}}“There was the supreme sound of the songs of bees and partridges
That equaled that of Dhṛtarāṣṭra,{{note:{index960,id:UT22084-055-001-2725}}} the king of geese.
They had bright, multicolored bodies, brilliant with great hues,
And sang delightful, beautiful, charming songs. {7}
{{milestone:{label:30.13,id:UT22084-055-001-2726}}}“At that time, there were gatherings of these birds,
There were the songs of avadavats, peacocks, and parrots,{{note:{index961,id:UT22084-055-001-2727}}}
Cuckoos, mynas, and a variety of other birds—
Various kinds of songs from many birds. {8}
{{milestone:{label:30.14,id:UT22084-055-001-2728}}}“They dwelt in those hundreds of parks
Where there were the blossoms of karnikara, 
Gardenia, aśoka, and kachnar trees,
As well as red lotuses, blue lotuses, night lotuses, and white lotuses. {9}
{{milestone:{label:30.15,id:UT22084-055-001-2729}}}“They were beautified by lotus flower ponds 
That were adorned by a hundred thousand lotuses.
There were beautiful, exquisite lotus ponds {{page:{number:190,id:UT22084-055-001-6023,folio:F.96.a}}}
Adorned by the fragrance of the most delightful scents. {10}
{{milestone:{label:30.16,id:UT22084-055-001-2730}}}“At that time, the king in this Jambudvīpa
Was the lord of men whose name was Dṛdhadatta.
He had five hundred sons
Who were handsome and beautiful to see. {11}
{{milestone:{label:30.17,id:UT22084-055-001-2731}}}“At that time the kingdom was peaceful and happy,
Free of calamities, and filled with joy and peace.
Jambudvīpa was adorned by many flowers.
It was identical to a paradise, with no difference. {12}
{{milestone:{label:30.18,id:UT22084-055-001-2732}}}“At that time there was a jina, one with the ten strengths,
Without bad actions, who taught this supreme samādhi:
‘The beings within existence are like dreams.
There is no one who is born and no one who dies. {13}
{{milestone:{label:30.19,id:UT22084-055-001-2733}}}“ ‘There is no being to be found, and no soul,{{note:{index962,id:UT22084-055-001-2734}}} or person.{{note:{index963,id:UT22084-055-001-2735}}}
These phenomena are like dreams{{note:{index964,id:UT22084-055-001-2736}}} or a plantain tree;{{note:{index965,id:UT22084-055-001-2737}}}
Like illusions, the same as lightning in the sky;
Like the moon on water, the same as a mirage.{{note:{index966,id:UT22084-055-001-2738}}} {14}
{{milestone:{label:30.20,id:UT22084-055-001-2739}}}“ ‘There is no person who dies in this world,
Who departs and goes to another world.
But the karma that has been created is not destroyed.
It will ripen as good and bad results within saṃsāra. {15}
{{milestone:{label:30.21,id:UT22084-055-001-2740}}}“ ‘It is neither eternal nor is it annihilated.
There is no accumulation or presence of karma,
Yet if it has been created there is no way to avoid encountering it,
While that which is created by others will not be experienced. {16}
{{milestone:{label:30.22,id:UT22084-055-001-2741}}}“ ‘There is no passing away or returning.
There is no existence of all things, yet neither are they nonexistent.
There is no pure engagement with the locus of a view.
There is no conduct of beings and no engagement with peace. {17}
{{milestone:{label:30.23,id:UT22084-055-001-2742}}}“ ‘The conduct of the sugatas, the qualities of the jinas,
