See stainless buddhas who have minds of perfect peace,
Praise those lords of the worlds with hundreds of verses,
And obtain the peace of this stainless samādhi. {164}
{{milestone:{label:33.170,id:UT22084-055-001-3199}}}“They will make unequaled offerings to those guides{{note:{index1099,id:UT22084-055-001-3200}}}
Who have perfect, great fame and are supreme among humans and devas,
And they will cast aside the kingdom like spittle,
And pure, perfectly pure, will practice celibacy. {165}
{{milestone:{label:33.171,id:UT22084-055-001-3201}}}“They will enter homelessness in the Sage’s teaching
And obtain the peace of this stainless samādhi. {{page:{number:219,id:UT22084-055-001-6052,folio:F.110.b}}}
They will have friendly speech with gentle words,
And become empowered and wise in teaching{{note:{index1100,id:UT22084-055-001-3202}}} a million sūtras. {166}
{{milestone:{label:33.172,id:UT22084-055-001-3203}}}“Having attained this samādhi they will teach it to many beings:
Empty and without attributes, the perfect attainment of peace, 
The perfect and unimpeded practice of the Dharma of complete peace,
The empty nature that is constant, stainless peacefulness. {167}
{{milestone:{label:33.173,id:UT22084-055-001-3204}}}“They have profound realization, continuous endless realization,
A vast realization, a realization that is incalculably beneficial.
Having attained profound peace, this samādhi,
They will become an illumination for all worlds. {168}
{{milestone:{label:33.174,id:UT22084-055-001-3205}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
They will be continually pure in celibacy,
Unsullied, always free of the kleśas,
And lead millions of other beings to be the same. {169}
{{milestone:{label:33.175,id:UT22084-055-001-3206}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
They will have exceedingly sharp wisdom, supreme wisdom;
They will gain an ocean of learning and always have infinite understanding,
Virtuous speech, excellent understanding, and knowledge of the instructions. {170}
{{milestone:{label:33.176,id:UT22084-055-001-3207}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
They will gain skill in works and skill in the arts,
Skill in healing and likewise skill in herbs.
In everything they will be constant and perfect. {171}
{{milestone:{label:33.177,id:UT22084-055-001-3208}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
They will be perfect and completely skilled 
In poetry, treatises, comedy, music, song, and dance, 
Always becoming masters of these in this world. {172}
{{milestone:{label:33.178,id:UT22084-055-001-3209}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
Such people will be those who always have a retinue.
They will not cause division, but will always keep harmonious unity
And practice the supreme, highest, peaceful bodhisattva conduct. {173}
{{milestone:{label:33.179,id:UT22084-055-001-3210}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
Those wise people will never have
Sorrow, pain, or mental anguish,
And will at all times be free of illness. {174}
{{milestone:{label:33.180,id:UT22084-055-001-3211}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
In this human world they will not have any illness,
No physical pain, nor likewise mental pain,
No toothache, and similarly no headache. {175} {{page:{number:220,id:UT22084-055-001-6053,folio:F.111.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:33.181,id:UT22084-055-001-3212}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
They will never have any illness occur:
None of the various sicknesses of the mortal world,
Whether physical illness or likewise mental illness. {176}
{{milestone:{label:33.182,id:UT22084-055-001-3213}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
They will never have the many different kinds of afflictions,
Whether they are the various kinds of mental afflictions
Or the various kinds of physical illnesses. {177}
{{milestone:{label:33.183,id:UT22084-055-001-3214}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
Just as space, the air, is undefiled,
Has a pure nature, and is vast{{note:{index1101,id:UT22084-055-001-3215}}} and bright,
In the same way their minds will be completely pure. {178}
{{milestone:{label:33.184,id:UT22084-055-001-3216}}}“Having attained this peace, this stainless samādhi,
Just as moonlight, and likewise sunlight, too,
Are pure, ungraspable, and radiant,
In the same way their minds will be bright. {179}
{{milestone:{label:33.185,id:UT22084-055-001-3217}}}“Just as it is not easy, using pigments,
To paint various forms in the air,
In the same way it is not easy to create pictures in the minds{{note:{index1102,id:UT22084-055-001-3218}}}
Of those who remain in this stainless samādhi of peace. {180}
{{milestone:{label:33.186,id:UT22084-055-001-3219}}}“Just as the wind blows in the four{{note:{index1103,id:UT22084-055-001-3220}}} directions,
Going in every direction without impediment,
Their continuum of mind is like the wind,
Moving unimpeded, without attachment,{{note:{index1104,id:UT22084-055-001-3221}}} throughout the world. {181}
{{milestone:{label:33.187,id:UT22084-055-001-3222}}}“One may be able to catch the wind with a net,
One may be able to bind the wind with a noose,
But it is not so easy to know the mind of someone
Who has meditated on this stainless samādhi of peace. {182}
{{milestone:{label:33.188,id:UT22084-055-001-3223}}}“One may be able to catch a reflection on water,
And obtain from it a bowl of sesame oil,
But it is not so easy to know the mind of someone
Who has meditated on this stainless samādhi of peace. {183}
{{milestone:{label:33.189,id:UT22084-055-001-3224}}}“Someone may be able to catch in their hands
The lightning that flashes from the thundering clouds,
But it is not so easy to know the extent of the mind of someone
Who has meditated on this stainless samādhi of peace.{{note:{index1105,id:UT22084-055-001-3225}}} {184} {{page:{number:221,id:UT22084-055-001-6054,folio:F.111.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:33.190,id:UT22084-055-001-3226}}}“One may be able to know the languages of all beings,
The beings in the buddha realms in the ten directions, 
But it is not so easy to know the heights of the mind 
Of bodhisattvas who have attained this samādhi. {185}
{{milestone:{label:33.191,id:UT22084-055-001-3227}}}“When they have attained this stainless samādhi of peace
They will have no kleśas and be undefiled.
Those who have attained this samādhi of peace
Will never again have attachment{{note:{index1106,id:UT22084-055-001-3228}}} to the three existences.{{note:{index1107,id:UT22084-055-001-3229}}} {186}
{{milestone:{label:33.192,id:UT22084-055-001-3230}}}“Having attained this stainless samādhi of peace,
They have no longing for objects of desire, no longing for forms;{{note:{index1108,id:UT22084-055-001-3231}}}
They have no longing for women and have unconfused minds.
They are peaceful, completely peaceful, and undefiled. {187}
{{milestone:{label:33.193,id:UT22084-055-001-3232}}}“Having attained this stainless samādhi of peace,
They have no longing for sons, no longing for daughters;
They have no longing for a wife, and no longing for attendants.
Their conduct is peaceful and they are undefiled. {188}
{{milestone:{label:33.194,id:UT22084-055-001-3233}}}“They have no longing for gold and no longing for wealth.
They have no longing for higher rebirth and no attachment to money and jewels. 
They have completely pure minds and are free of thought.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {189}
{{milestone:{label:33.195,id:UT22084-055-001-3234}}}“They do not practice celibacy for a higher rebirth.{{note:{index1109,id:UT22084-055-001-3235}}}
The wise are not generous out of yearning for a higher rebirth;
Bodhisattvas are generous because they desire enlightenment.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {190}
{{milestone:{label:33.196,id:UT22084-055-001-3236}}}“Those who accomplish this stainless samādhi
Do not practice asceticism in order to have a kingdom,
Nor in order to become sovereign over the three existences.
They benefit many beings because they long for enlightenment. {191}
{{milestone:{label:33.197,id:UT22084-055-001-3237}}}“They have no longing for songs and no longing for dance,
They have no longing for incense{{note:{index1110,id:UT22084-055-001-3238}}} and no longing for drink,
And they have no longing for food and no longing for clothes.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {i}{{note:{index1111,id:UT22084-055-001-3239}}}
{{milestone:{label:33.198,id:UT22084-055-001-3240}}}“They have no longing for eyes and no longing for ears, 
They have no longing for a nose and no longing for a tongue,
And they have no longing for a body and no longing for a mind.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {ii}
{{milestone:{label:33.199,id:UT22084-055-001-3241}}}“They have no longing for home and no longing for the forest, {{page:{number:222,id:UT22084-055-001-6055,folio:F.112.a}}}
They have no longing for a monastery and no longing for a village,
And they have no longing for a region and no longing for a town.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {iii}
{{milestone:{label:33.200,id:UT22084-055-001-3242}}}“They have no longing for generosity and no longing for conduct,
They have no longing for patience and no longing for diligence,
And they have no longing for meditation and no longing for wisdom.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {iv}
{{milestone:{label:33.201,id:UT22084-055-001-3243}}}“They have no longing for being and no longing for life,
They have no longing for the Buddha and no longing for the Dharma,
And they have no longing for the Saṅgha and no longing for enlightenment.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {v}
{{milestone:{label:33.202,id:UT22084-055-001-3244}}}“They have no longing for existence and no longing for nonexistence,
They have no longing for the middle way and no longing for the extremes,
And they have no longing for everything and no longing for nothing.
That is the uniqueness of this attainment of samādhi. {vi}
{{milestone:{label:33.203,id:UT22084-055-001-3245}}}“When they have attained this stainless samādhi of peace,
Desire can never cause them harm.
Those who yearn for women have confused minds 
And they know that this is the nature of desire. {192}
{{milestone:{label:33.204,id:UT22084-055-001-3246}}}“When they have attained this stainless samādhi of peace,
Anger can never cause them harm.
The wise ones destroy malice; 
Through love they completely overcome anger.{{note:{index1112,id:UT22084-055-001-3247}}} {193}
{{milestone:{label:33.205,id:UT22084-055-001-3248}}}“Ignorance can never cause them harm;
Wisdom eliminates ignorance and stupidity.
They attain measureless wisdom free of darkness.
These qualities from attaining samādhi are measureless. {194}
{{milestone:{label:33.206,id:UT22084-055-001-3249}}}“Desire is always overcome by repulsiveness.{{note:{index1113,id:UT22084-055-001-3250}}}
Anger is constantly defeated by love.
Wisdom cuts through ignorance, the net of the kleśas. 
Those who have attained samādhi are majestic to the whole world. {195}
{{milestone:{label:33.207,id:UT22084-055-001-3251}}}“Sleep can never cause them harm.
They eliminate the various subsidiary kleśas.
They are undefiled and liberated.
These qualities from attaining samādhi are measureless. {196}
{{milestone:{label:33.208,id:UT22084-055-001-3252}}}“Desire can never cause harm
To the bodhisattvas who possess this samādhi. {{page:{number:223,id:UT22084-055-001-6056,folio:F.112.b}}}
They delight always in generosity:
They give away their possessions and give happiness. {197}
{{milestone:{label:33.209,id:UT22084-055-001-3253}}}“The bodhisattvas who possess this samādhi
Possess power that is beyond compare.
At all times they are in the possession of strength.
There is no one who is their equal in the world. {198}
{{milestone:{label:33.210,id:UT22084-055-001-3254}}}“They become cakravartins in this world.
They come to Jambudvīpa as the sovereign of humans 
And many beings make offerings to them,
And in particular they attain the unique wisdom free of darkness. {199}
{{milestone:{label:33.211,id:UT22084-055-001-3255}}}“Such bodhisattvas become the leaders in a special, jewellike family.{{note:{index1114,id:UT22084-055-001-3256}}}
They have great wealth and are lords over many people.{{note:{index1115,id:UT22084-055-001-3257}}}
They have horses, elephants, and perfect chariots to ride upon.
They have abundant gold and precious jewels.{{note:{index1116,id:UT22084-055-001-3258}}} {200}
{{milestone:{label:33.212,id:UT22084-055-001-3259}}}“Those who have faith in the supreme wisdom of the Buddha,
They are called the jewellike families in Jambudvīpa.
They are born there into special, jewellike families 
And they benefit a multitude of their kin. {201}
{{milestone:{label:33.213,id:UT22084-055-001-3260}}}“They carefully engender faith in those
Who are of families in Jambudvīpa who have no faith.
They bring a multitude of beings to aspire to enlightenment, 
And they become self-arisen buddhas, supreme jinas. {202}
{{milestone:{label:33.214,id:UT22084-055-001-3261}}}“They attain unequaled, highest enlightenment
And turn the unequaled Dharma wheel in buddha realms.{{note:{index1117,id:UT22084-055-001-3262}}}
Those who then know that Dharma wheel
Will all remain in the birthlessness of phenomena. {203}
{{milestone:{label:33.215,id:UT22084-055-001-3263}}}“The bodhisattvas will perform many activities.
Beings will constantly make offerings to them.
They will constantly accomplish unequaled benefit.
They will remove the darkness from the eyes of beings. {204}
{{milestone:{label:33.216,id:UT22084-055-001-3264}}}{205}{{note:{index1118,id:UT22084-055-001-3265}}}
{{milestone:{label:33.217,id:UT22084-055-001-3266}}}“The bodhisattvas, joyous, with loving minds
And unstained, will become buddhas.
Wherever those bodhisattvas are present
They will create an immeasurable benefit for beings. {206}
{{milestone:{label:33.218,id:UT22084-055-001-3267}}}“They will protect correct conduct and have matchless celibacy.
They will meditate on samādhi for many endless eons. {{page:{number:224,id:UT22084-055-001-6057,folio:F.113.a}}}
They will constantly have certainty in dhyāna and liberation.
Those bodhisattvas will be the sons of the buddhas. {207}
{{milestone:{label:33.219,id:UT22084-055-001-3268}}}“They always practice the bases of miraculous powers,
And they go to various infinite realms.
They listen to the Dharma taught by the sugatas
And, having the power of retention, they remember everything. {208}
{{milestone:{label:33.220,id:UT22084-055-001-3269}}}“Those bodhisattvas who have the power of retention
Teach endless, countless sūtras.
Those bodhisattvas who have the power of retention
Accomplish countless benefits for beings. {209}
{{milestone:{label:33.221,id:UT22084-055-001-3270}}}“They know the deaths and rebirths 
And the coming and going of beings,
What kind of actions they do,
And the ripening of their karma. {210}
{{milestone:{label:33.222,id:UT22084-055-001-3271}}}“In that transference of karma 
There are not even atoms to be found. 
Those greatly famous bodhisattvas
Know, too, that this is so. {211}
{{milestone:{label:33.223,id:UT22084-055-001-3272}}}“Emptiness is the supreme
Dwelling of the great beings.
They establish countless millions
Of beings in the great yāna. {212}
{{milestone:{label:33.224,id:UT22084-055-001-3273}}}“When they are teaching 
They have no concept of beings.
The bodhisattvas teach
Without engaging in phenomena. {213}
{{milestone:{label:33.225,id:UT22084-055-001-3274}}}“When they teach the Dharma
There is no apprehending of an object.
They reside in emptiness,
Established in enduring wisdom. {214}
{{milestone:{label:33.226,id:UT22084-055-001-3275}}}“When someone has been taught this samādhi,
In which all the teachers reside,
No conceptions arise in him, 
He naturally has no conceptions about women. {215}
{{milestone:{label:33.227,id:UT22084-055-001-3276}}}“When conceptions of women have ceased,
He sits at the Bodhimaṇḍa. 
Once he has sat at the Bodhimaṇḍa
The conceptions of Māra cease. {216}
{{milestone:{label:33.228,id:UT22084-055-001-3277}}}“The wise one does not see
Māra{{note:{index1119,id:UT22084-055-001-3278}}} and Māra’s army,{{note:{index1120,id:UT22084-055-001-3279}}}
And neither does he see
The three daughters of Māra. {217}
{{milestone:{label:33.229,id:UT22084-055-001-3280}}}“Once he is seated upon the Bodhimaṇḍa,
All his conceptions are eliminated.
Once all his conceptions are eliminated 
This entire world is shaken. {218}
{{milestone:{label:33.230,id:UT22084-055-001-3281}}}“So, too, are all the worlds in the ten directions {{page:{number:225,id:UT22084-055-001-6058,folio:F.113.b}}}
With their Sumerus and their oceans,
And this is known 
By all the beings in the ten directions.{{note:{index1121,id:UT22084-055-001-3282}}} {219}
{{milestone:{label:33.231,id:UT22084-055-001-3283}}}“This shaking of the world
Is the miracle of the bodhisattva;
It is shaken six times 
When he attains supreme enlightenment. {220}
{{milestone:{label:33.232,id:UT22084-055-001-3284}}}“All the composite phenomena there are,
And all the noncomposite phenomena—
All phenomena are understood
That are taught by the word phenomena.{{note:{index1122,id:UT22084-055-001-3285}}} {221}
{{milestone:{label:33.233,id:UT22084-055-001-3286}}}“There is nothing there to be understood,
And that lion’s roar arises.
Knowing this process of arising, 
He becomes an illuminating buddha. {222}
{{milestone:{label:33.234,id:UT22084-055-001-3287}}}“Phenomena appear dependently.
Phenomena are produced dependently.
The wise ones know the entirety 
Of the dependence of phenomena. {223}
{{milestone:{label:33.235,id:UT22084-055-001-3288}}}“They know the development of all phenomena.
They have complete understanding through emptiness.
They have wisdom concerning states of existence. 
They have complete understanding of all phenomena. {224}
{{milestone:{label:33.236,id:UT22084-055-001-3289}}}On seeking for these states of existence,
The bodhisattva does not find them.
That is the same as the inconceivable knowledge 
Of all the buddhas concerning states of existence. {225}
{{milestone:{label:33.237,id:UT22084-055-001-3290}}}“The one who has that complete knowledge
Knows all states of existence.{{note:{index1123,id:UT22084-055-001-3291}}}
Knowing the characteristic of the true Dharma,
He brings to an end all illusions.{{note:{index1124,id:UT22084-055-001-3292}}} {226}
{{milestone:{label:33.238,id:UT22084-055-001-3293}}}“Knowing the characteristic of the true Dharma,
He gazes upon all the realms.
Having gazed upon all the realms,
He seats himself at the Bodhimaṇḍa.{{note:{index1125,id:UT22084-055-001-3294}}} {i}
{{milestone:{label:33.239,id:UT22084-055-001-3295}}}“Having sat at the Bodhimaṇḍa,
There is the sound of the lion’s roar,
Which thus resounds throughout 
Countless, innumerable millions of realms. {227}
{{milestone:{label:33.240,id:UT22084-055-001-3296}}}“All those greatly renowned buddha heroes
Also cause those realms to shake.
The leader of beings guides beings
In the way that they are to be guided. {228}
{{milestone:{label:33.241,id:UT22084-055-001-3297}}}“Having reached the highest enlightenment,
He rises from the Bodhimaṇḍa.
He guides the countless, innumerable beings
Who are to be guided. {229}
{{milestone:{label:33.242,id:UT22084-055-001-3298}}}“Then the Buddha emanates
Infinite buddha emanations.
These buddha emanations{{note:{index1126,id:UT22084-055-001-3299}}} go
To thousands of millions of realms.{{note:{index1127,id:UT22084-055-001-3300}}} {230}
{{milestone:{label:33.243,id:UT22084-055-001-3301}}}“They lead countless millions 
Of beings to the highest enlightenment. {{page:{number:226,id:UT22084-055-001-6059,folio:F.114.a}}}
He teaches the supreme Dharma
For the benefit of all beings. {231}
{{milestone:{label:33.244,id:UT22084-055-001-3302}}}“That kind of great wisdom
Is the inconceivable wisdom of a buddha.
Therefore develop the aspiration,
The supreme aspiration to enlightenment.{{note:{index1128,id:UT22084-055-001-3303}}} {232}
{{milestone:{label:33.245,id:UT22084-055-001-3304}}}“Develop veneration for those with the highest qualities:
The Buddha, the Dharma, and the Saṅgha,
And the heroes, the bodhisattvas,
Who seek for the highest enlightenment. {233}
{{milestone:{label:33.246,id:UT22084-055-001-3305}}}“Without becoming disheartened,
Venerate them unflaggingly,
And become before long
An illuminating buddha. {234}
{{milestone:{label:33.247,id:UT22084-055-001-3306}}}“Those bodhisattvas who come here
From thousands of realms
See the lamp of the world
Teaching the supreme Dharma. {235}
{{milestone:{label:33.248,id:UT22084-055-001-3307}}}“Those great heroes throw down
Great jewels for the Guide,
And in order to attain enlightenment
They cast down coral tree flowers. {236}
{{milestone:{label:33.249,id:UT22084-055-001-3308}}}“They adorn this realm,
The highest buddha realm.
All of the ten directions{{note:{index1129,id:UT22084-055-001-3309}}}
Are covered with networks of jewels. {237}
{{milestone:{label:33.250,id:UT22084-055-001-3310}}}“They string up flags
And erect millions of banners, 
And they adorn this realm
With endless adornments. {238}
{{milestone:{label:33.251,id:UT22084-055-001-3311}}}“They create countless, beautiful
Pinnacled halls with balconies,{{note:{index1130,id:UT22084-055-001-3312}}}
Upper chambers,{{note:{index1131,id:UT22084-055-001-3313}}} and towers{{note:{index1132,id:UT22084-055-001-3314}}}
Adorned with every jewel. {239}
{{milestone:{label:33.252,id:UT22084-055-001-3315}}}“They create palaces with crescents,
Round windows and aviaries,
Incense, banners, and vases,{{note:{index1133,id:UT22084-055-001-3316}}}
And adorned with many jewels. {240}
{{milestone:{label:33.253,id:UT22084-055-001-3317}}}“The aroma{{note:{index1134,id:UT22084-055-001-3318}}} of incense 
Spreads through this buddha realm.{{note:{index1135,id:UT22084-055-001-3319}}}
That delightful incense
Pervades a billion{{note:{index1136,id:UT22084-055-001-3320}}} realms. {241}
{{milestone:{label:33.254,id:UT22084-055-001-3321}}}“When it has spread through them 
A rain of incense falls.
Those who smell that incense
Become buddhas, guides. {242}
{{milestone:{label:33.255,id:UT22084-055-001-3322}}}“They cast away the pain{{note:{index1137,id:UT22084-055-001-3323}}} of desire.
They do not have anger and craving.{{note:{index1138,id:UT22084-055-001-3324}}}
The net of ignorance{{note:{index1139,id:UT22084-055-001-3325}}} is destroyed
And all darkness comes to an end. {243}
{{milestone:{label:33.256,id:UT22084-055-001-3326}}}“There they attain the miraculous powers, 
And the strengths, powers, and aspects of enlightenment. {{page:{number:227,id:UT22084-055-001-6060,folio:F.114.b}}}
They attain the dhyānas and the liberations
And become worthy of offerings. {244}
{{milestone:{label:33.257,id:UT22084-055-001-3327}}}“Fifty million{{note:{index1140,id:UT22084-055-001-3328}}} beautiful 
Seats are arranged,
Draped with millions{{note:{index1141,id:UT22084-055-001-3329}}} of cloths 
And nets of jewels.{{note:{index1142,id:UT22084-055-001-3330}}} {245}
{{milestone:{label:33.258,id:UT22084-055-001-3331}}}“The bodhisattvas, the famous heroes,
Are gathered there upon those seats.{{note:{index1143,id:UT22084-055-001-3332}}}
They shine with the primary signs
And also with the secondary signs. {246}
{{milestone:{label:33.259,id:UT22084-055-001-3333}}}“This entire buddha realm
Is adorned by trees made of jewels.
There are emanated ponds that are filled
With water that has the eight qualities. {247}
{{milestone:{label:33.260,id:UT22084-055-001-3334}}}“Those on the banks of those pools
Who drink from their waters 
Are freed from all craving 
And become worthy of veneration by the world. {248}
{{milestone:{label:33.261,id:UT22084-055-001-3335}}}“In other realms, too,
Bodhisattvas gather.
They praise the Buddha, 
The lion of the Śākyas, the protector. {249}
{{milestone:{label:33.262,id:UT22084-055-001-3336}}}“Those who hear that praise
Become guides of the worlds.
Here I have described 
This sūtra’s inconceivable benefits. {250}
{{milestone:{label:33.263,id:UT22084-055-001-3337}}}“Countless millions of lotuses
Are emanated, which have
Petals made of gold,
And pericarps of uragasāra.{{note:{index1144,id:UT22084-055-001-3338}}} {251}
{{milestone:{label:33.264,id:UT22084-055-001-3339}}}“They have stems{{note:{index1145,id:UT22084-055-001-3340}}} of beryl,
They have leaves{{note:{index1146,id:UT22084-055-001-3341}}} of crystal,
They have stamens of emerald,{{note:{index1147,id:UT22084-055-001-3342}}}
And have beautifully appeared. {252}
{{milestone:{label:33.265,id:UT22084-055-001-3343}}}“They have an inconceivable aroma
That they continuously emit. 
The inconceivable aroma of the lotuses
Fills millions of realms.{{note:{index1148,id:UT22084-055-001-3344}}} {i}
{{milestone:{label:33.266,id:UT22084-055-001-3345}}}“Those who smell that aroma
That they delightfully emanate
Will have delight in their minds
And all their illnesses will cease. {253}
{{milestone:{label:33.267,id:UT22084-055-001-3346}}}“Desire, anger, and ignorance
Will cease without trace.
When those three faults have ceased in them 
They will be buddhas who bestow happiness. {254}
{{milestone:{label:33.268,id:UT22084-055-001-3347}}}“From them are emitted sounds,
Countless numbers of the word buddha.
And from them also the words 
dharma and saṅgha emanate everywhere, {255}
{{milestone:{label:33.269,id:UT22084-055-001-3348}}}“And also the words emptiness, 
Absence of attributes, and absence of aspiration.
The progress of the numerous millions of beings 
Who hear them becomes irreversible. {256} {{page:{number:228,id:UT22084-055-001-6061,folio:F.115.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:33.270,id:UT22084-055-001-3349}}}“These words that are emanated 
Also reach millions of realms.
They establish countless millions 
Of beings in this buddha wisdom. {257}
{{milestone:{label:33.271,id:UT22084-055-001-3350}}}“The birds that are peacocks,{{note:{index1149,id:UT22084-055-001-3351}}}
Avadavats, and partridges
Also sing out a word,
The unsurpassable word buddha. {258}
{{milestone:{label:33.272,id:UT22084-055-001-3352}}}“The birds that are snipes,
Mynas, cranes, and cuckoos 
Also sing out a word,
The inconceivable{{note:{index1150,id:UT22084-055-001-3353}}} word dharma.{{note:{index1151,id:UT22084-055-001-3354}}} {i}
{{milestone:{label:33.273,id:UT22084-055-001-3355}}}“The birds that are parrots, geese, 
Ducks, shelducks, and swans 
Also sing out a word,
The unsurpassable word saṅgha. {ii}
{{milestone:{label:33.274,id:UT22084-055-001-3356}}}“All the birds that there are
In the deva or the human worlds
Are continuously singing 
Praises of the Three Jewels. {iii}
{{milestone:{label:33.275,id:UT22084-055-001-3357}}}“Trees made of jewels
Are manifested in this realm.
Those delightful jewel trees
Are uniquely beautiful. {259}
{{milestone:{label:33.276,id:UT22084-055-001-3358}}}“On all those trees are hung
Every kind of ornament.
They have manifested in this realm 
Through the power of the Buddha.{{note:{index1152,id:UT22084-055-001-3359}}} {260}
{{milestone:{label:33.277,id:UT22084-055-001-3360}}}“This display does not exist
Anywhere in any realm. 
This unique, superior sight
Is not to be seen in this realm.{{note:{index1153,id:UT22084-055-001-3361}}} {261}
{{milestone:{label:33.278,id:UT22084-055-001-3362}}}“This is what has been taught
By the Śākya lion, the protector.
The greatly famed bodhisattvas
Have no doubt in that wisdom. {262}
{{milestone:{label:33.279,id:UT22084-055-001-3363}}}“They comprehend that highest point.
Their way is inconceivable.
Their wisdom increases 
Like an ocean into which rivers flow. {263}
{{milestone:{label:33.280,id:UT22084-055-001-3364}}}“They have no final end. 
It is like drinking an ocean.
This is the inconceivable way 
Of the bodhisattvas that has been taught. {264}
{{milestone:{label:33.281,id:UT22084-055-001-3365}}}“The greatly famed bodhisattvas,
The heroes, are at the highest point.
They give forth aspects of speech 
That are as numerous as the Ganges sands. {265}
{{milestone:{label:33.282,id:UT22084-055-001-3366}}}“There is such inconceivable speech
But the bodhisattvas have no pride.{{note:{index1154,id:UT22084-055-001-3367}}}
They have eliminated pride
And are near to enlightenment, {266}
{{milestone:{label:33.283,id:UT22084-055-001-3368}}}“They will not ruin their correct conduct
Even for the sake of their life.
The bodhisattvas are resolute {{page:{number:229,id:UT22084-055-001-6062,folio:F.115.b}}}
And behave immaculately. {267}
{{milestone:{label:33.284,id:UT22084-055-001-3369}}}“They do not become ruined
By any concept of desire.
They have eliminated all conceptions
And they have countless samādhis. {268}
{{milestone:{label:33.285,id:UT22084-055-001-3370}}}“They practice them while in meditation 
Yet have no attachment to those samādhis.
They have no clinging, they are attentive,
And they have no attachment to the world. {269}
{{milestone:{label:33.286,id:UT22084-055-001-3371}}}“When they leave this world
They go to Sukhāvatī.
When they have arrived there
They see Buddha Amitābha. {270}
{{milestone:{label:33.287,id:UT22084-055-001-3372}}}“Those bodhisattva heroes
Are adorned by the primary signs.
They have reached the domain of the five higher cognitions,
Great wisdom,{{note:{index1155,id:UT22084-055-001-3373}}} and the retentions. {271}
{{milestone:{label:33.288,id:UT22084-055-001-3374}}}“They go to millions of realms
And bow down to the feet of the buddhas.
Shining, they travel 
To countless buddha realms. {272}
{{milestone:{label:33.289,id:UT22084-055-001-3375}}}“They have eliminated all faults
And are purified of all kleśas.
With the kleśas completely eradicated
They are one lifetime from becoming a jina. {273}
{{milestone:{label:33.290,id:UT22084-055-001-3376}}}“They will not go to the lower realms.
From that realm of humans
All rebirth into the lower realms 
Has been eradicated in that realm. {274}
{{milestone:{label:33.291,id:UT22084-055-001-3377}}}“Do not doubt what has been revealed
Concerning that protector, 
The Lord of the World, Amitābha, 
And you will go to Sukhāvatī.{{note:{index1156,id:UT22084-055-001-3378}}} {275}
{{milestone:{label:33.292,id:UT22084-055-001-3379}}}“A woman who has faith on hearing
The praise of this precious sūtra{{note:{index1157,id:UT22084-055-001-3380}}}
Will soon become a superior wise man
Who miraculously goes to billions of realms. {276}
{{milestone:{label:33.293,id:UT22084-055-001-3381}}}“Many offerings of innumerable kinds, 
Offered continuously to supreme beings
Within the appearance of a quintillion realms,
Cannot equal a fraction of a loving mind. {277}
{{milestone:{label:33.294,id:UT22084-055-001-3382}}}“Those who always practice correct conduct and samādhi,
And also countless dhyānas and liberations,
Who always practice emptiness devoid of attributes—
They will soon become sugatas in the world. {278}
{{milestone:{label:33.295,id:UT22084-055-001-3383}}}“The bodhisattvas who maintain the aggregate of correct conduct
Make the greatest, most special offering to me.
Those who maintain the aspiration to enlightenment in the time of degeneration
Are continuously making an offering to all the buddhas.{{note:{index1158,id:UT22084-055-001-3384}}} {279} {{page:{number:230,id:UT22084-055-001-6063,folio:F.116.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:33.296,id:UT22084-055-001-3385}}}“The bodhisattvas in the dreadful time of degeneration 
Who protect this supreme Dharma{{note:{index1159,id:UT22084-055-001-3386}}} taught by the sugatas,
Are my offspring and protectors of the Dharma in the later times.{{note:{index1160,id:UT22084-055-001-3387}}}
They have been entrusted by ten billion buddhas.” {280}
{{milestone:{label:33.297,id:UT22084-055-001-3388}}}Conclusion of the thirty-third chapter, “The Benefits of Possessing the Sūtra.” 
{{milestone:{label:34,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-34}}}Kṣemadatta
Chapter 34
{{milestone:{label:34.1,id:UT22084-055-001-3389}}} Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha,{{note:{index1161,id:UT22084-055-001-3390}}} “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should abide in the absence of attributes and be dedicated to making vast offerings to a present tathāgata or to the stūpa of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa.
{{milestone:{label:34.2,id:UT22084-055-001-3391}}}“Young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas should develop an aspiration focused upon all beings as they wish for this samādhi. And, wishing to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, they should abide in the absence of attributes, without aspiration for the ripening of karma, and use even their own body and life to perform vast actions of making offerings to a present tathāgata or to the stūpa of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa. 
{{milestone:{label:34.3,id:UT22084-055-001-3392}}}“With their mind and attention focused on compassion; with a loud, clear voice, elevated and pleasant; and with especially noble vocabulary and a continuity of words they should teach extensively to others, propagate, and explain the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. Why is that? Because, young man, this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena, is the basis and root of the entire Dharma.
{{milestone:{label:34.4,id:UT22084-055-001-3393}}}“Young man, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas who have great compassion {{page:{number:231,id:UT22084-055-001-6064,folio:F.116.b}}} and diligently rely on methods are dedicated to making vast offerings to a present tathāgata or to the stūpa of a tathāgata who has passed into nirvāṇa, they should teach extensively to others this king of samādhis, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena. 
{{milestone:{label:34.5,id:UT22084-055-001-3394}}}“At that time, young man, those bodhisattva mahāsattvas should abide in the doorways to liberation that are emptiness, the absence of attributes, and the absence of aspiration, and should not apprehend any phenomenon whatsoever. The bodhisattva mahāsattvas who abide in the practice of the samādhi that is free of apprehending will abide in all aspirations. Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who abide in all aspirations will fulfill all the aspirations of all beings, will quickly attain this samādhi, and will quickly attain the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood.{{note:{index1162,id:UT22084-055-001-3395}}}
{{milestone:{label:34.6,id:UT22084-055-001-3396}}}“Young man, you should understand this through the following teaching. 
{{milestone:{label:34.7,id:UT22084-055-001-3397}}}“Young man, in the past, uncountable, vast, immeasurable, inconceivable, innumerable countless eons ago,{{note:{index1163,id:UT22084-055-001-3398}}} at that time and in those days, there appeared in the world the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta, who was perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata, a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, a buddha, and a bhagavān.
{{milestone:{label:34.8,id:UT22084-055-001-3399}}}“Young man, the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha Ghoṣadatta established countless, innumerable beings in the cessation of defilements, in arhatship, and having established them in that state, he passed into nirvāṇa. He also established countless, innumerable beings in irreversible progress toward the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood and then passed into nirvāṇa. {{page:{number:232,id:UT22084-055-001-6065,folio:F.117.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:34.9,id:UT22084-055-001-3400}}}“Young man, at that time and in those days,{{note:{index1164,id:UT22084-055-001-3401}}} in Jambudvīpa there was a king named Śrīghoṣa. In order to make offerings to the Tathāgata who had passed into nirvāṇa he built eighty-four quintillion stūpas that contained the relics of the Tathāgata and he presented eighty-four quintillion lights to each of those stūpas. In the same way he offered eighty-four quintillion musical instruments, percussion instruments, flowers, incense offerings, perfumes, garlands, ointments, powders, robes, parasols, banners, and flags to each of those stūpas.
{{milestone:{label:34.10,id:UT22084-055-001-3402}}}“Young man, in that way King Śrīghoṣa made offerings to the stūpas that contained the relics of the Tathāgata. Then he gathered eighty quintillion bodhisattvas and dedicated himself to making offerings of all the most pleasing necessities to those bodhisattvas.
{{milestone:{label:34.11,id:UT22084-055-001-3403}}}“Every one of all those bodhisattva mahāsattvas was a dharmabhāṇaka. They had uninterrupted eloquence, the attainment of samādhi, and the attainment of unimpeded retention. They were teachers of the pure Dharma, and had attained the perfection of the supreme powers of a bodhisattva.
{{milestone:{label:34.12,id:UT22084-055-001-3404}}}“Young man, at that time, within that assembly there was a bodhisattva mahāsattva{{note:{index1165,id:UT22084-055-001-3405}}} named Kṣemadatta. He was a young boy with black hair, in the first stage of youth. He had become a youth who did not indulge in desires, but was a young celibate, who had been keeping the vow for a year.
{{milestone:{label:34.13,id:UT22084-055-001-3406}}}“Young man, at that time, King Śrīghoṣa made a request to that great assembly of bodhisattvas. He made a request to those bodhisattva mahāsattvas that he might, combining the six perfections, accomplish the great retention of the bodhisattva piṭaka, skill in methods, and unimpeded power and guidance. {{page:{number:233,id:UT22084-055-001-6066,folio:F.117.b}}} That evening he lit a quintillion lights before the stūpas that contained the relics of the Tathāgata. He also swept clean the circumambulation walkway, moistened and washed it, scattered flowers upon it, and arranged various seats. King Śrīghoṣa then came there accompanied by his harem and the people of the villages, towns, and regions. Holding musical instruments, percussion instruments, cymbals, flowers, incense, perfumes, garlands, ointments, powders, robes, parasols, banners, and flags, they made offerings to the stūpa, which contained the relics of the Tathāgata. Afterwards, in order to hear the Dharma, accompanied by his harem of queens, he ascended to the roof of the palace. Gatherings of devas and humans also assembled in order to hear the Dharma. 
{{milestone:{label:34.14,id:UT22084-055-001-3407}}}“The bodhisattva Kṣemadatta saw them and the lights from the numerous quintillions of offered lamps that shone as one pervading radiance. Knowing that many devas and humans had assembled in order to hear the Dharma, he thought, ‘I have entered the Mahāyāna, and because I now long for this samādhi I shall make an offering to the Tathāgata. It will be such an offering to the Tathāgata that it will amaze the worlds of devas, humans, and asuras, and bring them joy, delight, pleasure, and happiness, and they will obtain the light of the Dharma. I shall make an offering that will surpass all the offerings made to the Tathāgata by King Śrīghoṣa and amaze King Śrīghoṣa, his harem of queens, and his attendants, and bring them joy, delight, pleasure, and happiness.’ {{page:{number:234,id:UT22084-055-001-6067,folio:F.118.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:34.15,id:UT22084-055-001-3408}}}“The bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta was joyful and happy, and knowing that the great assembly of people had gathered to hear the Dharma, that evening he sat in front of the Tathāgata’s stūpa, bound his right hand in cotton, and immersed it in sesame oil. Having immersed it in sesame oil he set it alight. 
{{milestone:{label:34.16,id:UT22084-055-001-3409}}}“At this point the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta developed the supreme intention. He developed the supreme intention for the highest, complete enlightenment and, seeking complete enlightenment, although his right hand was burning brightly, his mind and the expression of his face remained unchanged. 
{{milestone:{label:34.17,id:UT22084-055-001-3410}}}“Young man, as the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta’s right hand burned brightly, and was transformed into a single flame, at that time this great earth shook. The light from his burning right hand made that of the many quintillions of offering lamps seem dark, and its great illumination spread in all directions, its radiance illuminating and pervading every direction.
{{milestone:{label:34.18,id:UT22084-055-001-3411}}}“He became joyful and happy, and with a gentle and pleasing voice, a uniquely superior vocabulary, and a continuity of words and letters, he taught{{note:{index1166,id:UT22084-055-001-3412}}} the samādhi, the revealed equality of the nature of all phenomena so that the entire assembly understood it in detail. 
{{milestone:{label:34.19,id:UT22084-055-001-3413}}}“The one thousand two hundred Trāyastriṃśa devas assembled there to listen to the Dharma were made joyous and happy and made various divine offerings. The apsarases engaged in singing divine songs.{{note:{index1167,id:UT22084-055-001-3414}}}
{{milestone:{label:34.20,id:UT22084-055-001-3415}}}“King Śrīghoṣa, who was keeping the eight poṣadha vows, was in the middle of his harem of queens, with his court before him, seated on the roof of his palace. He saw that the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta’s hand was burning and outshining all other lights, {{page:{number:235,id:UT22084-055-001-6068,folio:F.118.b}}} creating a brightness that transcended the lights of devas and the lights of humans.
{{milestone:{label:34.21,id:UT22084-055-001-3416}}}“He thought, ‘This bodhisattva mahāsattva has attained great higher cognition,’ and felt intense joy, faith, veneration, and reverence for the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta. Supported by his great accumulation of merit and roots of merit he leapt from the roof of the palace, together with his harem of eighty queens. He leapt because of his joy on having seen the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta.
{{milestone:{label:34.22,id:UT22084-055-001-3417}}}“Because of the roots of merit that were produced by his veneration, he and his retinue were caught by devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, and mahoragas. After they had been caught by devas, nāgas, yakṣas, gandharvas, asuras, garuḍas, kinnaras, and mahoragas, King Śrīghoṣa and his retinue, even though they had jumped from a building that was a hundred thousand cubits high, were physically unharmed, mentally unharmed, and were not unnerved.
{{milestone:{label:34.23,id:UT22084-055-001-3418}}}“King Śrīghoṣa extended both his hands, and together with the great assembly of people saw the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta’s hand on fire and burning brightly. All of them cried out loudly and wailed. Then the king, together with the great assembly of people, weeping and shedding tears, came before the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta.
{{milestone:{label:34.24,id:UT22084-055-001-3419}}}“Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta saw King Śrīghoṣa, and having seen him asked, ‘Great king, why are you and this great assembly of people here before me crying out loudly, wailing, sorrowful, and weeping?’ {{page:{number:236,id:UT22084-055-001-6069,folio:F.119.a}}}
“King Śrīghoṣa spoke these verses to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Kṣemadatta: 
{{milestone:{label:34.25,id:UT22084-055-001-3421}}}“ ‘These beings have cried out{{note:{index1168,id:UT22084-055-001-3422}}}
Because they have seen that Kṣemadatta, 
The one with great wisdom, the learned one, 
The dharmabhāṇaka, has lost a limb. {1}
{{milestone:{label:34.26,id:UT22084-055-001-3423}}}“ ‘Seeing that this body 
That emits this brilliant light
Has had a hand destroyed,
I also feel great suffering. {2}
{{milestone:{label:34.27,id:UT22084-055-001-3424}}}“ ‘The light from your burning hand
Has shone into the ten directions.
The divine light you have emitted
Has obscured the light of these lamps. {3}
{{milestone:{label:34.28,id:UT22084-055-001-3425}}}“ ‘This earth has been shaken
And you are not disheartened.
There arose in me the thought,
“That is no ordinary wise man.” {4}
{{milestone:{label:34.29,id:UT22084-055-001-3426}}}“ ‘I leapt a hundred thousand cubits
From the roof of my palace, 
Together with my harem of queens,
But my body was not harmed. {5}
{{milestone:{label:34.30,id:UT22084-055-001-3427}}}“ ‘How excellent your wonderful wisdom!
How excellent your unsurpassable mind!
How excellent your dedicated diligence!
How excellent your great aspiration! {6}
{{milestone:{label:34.31,id:UT22084-055-001-3428}}}“ ‘Your hand{{note:{index1169,id:UT22084-055-001-3429}}} is burning
But you are not disturbed.
You are happy and joyous
And again teach the Dharma. {7}
{{milestone:{label:34.32,id:UT22084-055-001-3430}}}“ ‘Worthy friend, you are as beautiful
As the moon that is full,
Or the sun high in the sky,
Or Sumeru, the king of mountains. {8}
{{milestone:{label:34.33,id:UT22084-055-001-3431}}}“ ‘Wise one, may I also 
Fulfill such a prayer!
Rejecting my care for the body
I will accomplish benefit for beings. {9}
{{milestone:{label:34.34,id:UT22084-055-001-3432}}}“ ‘I delight in joy for the Dharma;
My happiness in that is inconceivable.
That you have lost a limb
Causes me the highest suffering.’ {10}
{{milestone:{label:34.35,id:UT22084-055-001-3433}}}“Kṣemadatta, through devas and nāgas,
Made offerings to the king
And he spoke these verses 
With infinite confidence: {11}
{{milestone:{label:34.36,id:UT22084-055-001-3434}}}“ ‘Someone who has no hand
Is not the one who lacks a limb;
Someone who has no correct conduct
Is the one who is lacking a limb. {12}
{{milestone:{label:34.37,id:UT22084-055-001-3435}}}“ ‘This putrid{{note:{index1170,id:UT22084-055-001-3436}}} body of mine
I have offered to the tathāgatas,
The inconceivable recipients of offerings,
The ones to whom offerings should be made by all the world. {13} {{page:{number:237,id:UT22084-055-001-6070,folio:F.119.b}}}.
{{milestone:{label:34.38,id:UT22084-055-001-3437}}}“ ‘Seeking the wisdom of buddhahood
I offer to the lords of the worlds
Infinite billion-world universes
Entirely filled with jewels. {14}
{{milestone:{label:34.39,id:UT22084-055-001-3438}}}“ ‘There are these material offerings 
But there are other inconceivable offerings.
Those who know that phenomena are empty
Give away their bodies and their lives. {15}
{{milestone:{label:34.40,id:UT22084-055-001-3439}}}“ ‘I shall speak words of truth.
Great king, listen to me!
All the people gathered here,
Understand the meaning of these verses! {16}
{{milestone:{label:34.41,id:UT22084-055-001-3440}}}“ ‘If it is true that I will become a buddha,
One who is revered by the world,
May that truth cause this earth
To shake in six ways!’ {17}
{{milestone:{label:34.42,id:UT22084-055-001-3441}}}“He spoke those words
And the earth shook.
Millions of devas were overjoyed,
Amazed, and astonished. {18}
{{milestone:{label:34.43,id:UT22084-055-001-3442}}}“The joyous devas and humans 
Developed the aspiration for enlightenment.
Immeasurable, incalculable numbers
Were established in the supreme yāna. {19}
{{milestone:{label:34.44,id:UT22084-055-001-3443}}}“The benefit accomplished 
By the bhikṣu Kṣemadatta
Is the unending and inconceivable engagement
With the wisdom of the buddhas. {20}
{{milestone:{label:34.45,id:UT22084-055-001-3444}}}“ ‘If it is true that this phenomenon
That is called “hand” does not exist,
Then may that truth cause my hand
To be instantly restored as it was before! {21}
{{milestone:{label:34.46,id:UT22084-055-001-3445}}}“ ‘If it is true that this phenomenon
Called “Kṣemadatta” does not exist,
Though one seeks for it in the ten directions,
It will be not be found, because it is empty. {22}
{{milestone:{label:34.47,id:UT22084-055-001-3446}}}“ ‘Whatever sound arises, 
Know it to be empty.
Sound is like an echo:
Know phenomena to be like that. {23}
{{milestone:{label:34.48,id:UT22084-055-001-3447}}}“ ‘When there is fearlessness,
Emptiness is fully comprehended.
Through those words of truth
May the entire world not be burned! {24}
{{milestone:{label:34.49,id:UT22084-055-001-3448}}}“ ‘May all the beings in the three existences,
The devas and the humans,
All rest in a state of meditation
Because of the brilliance of omniscience. {25}
{{milestone:{label:34.50,id:UT22084-055-001-3449}}}“ ‘All the misfortunes 
That devas and humans have,
May they all come to cessation
Through the brilliance of irreversibility!’ {26}
{{milestone:{label:34.51,id:UT22084-055-001-3450}}}“After Kṣemadatta spoke those verses 
His hand grew back, {{page:{number:238,id:UT22084-055-001-6071,folio:F.120.a}}}
And Kṣemadatta’s body became
Adorned by the primary signs. {27}
{{milestone:{label:34.52,id:UT22084-055-001-3451}}}“Ten thousand million devas
Who were residing in the sky
Threw down at that moment
Coral tree flowers upon the bhikṣu. {28}
{{milestone:{label:34.53,id:UT22084-055-001-3452}}}“Those divine flowers
Filled up this world.
A quintillion apsarases
Engaged in performing songs. {29}
{{milestone:{label:34.54,id:UT22084-055-001-3453}}}“When Kṣemadatta
Emitted these words,
Ten thousand million buddhas
Witnessed this miracle. {30}
{{milestone:{label:34.55,id:UT22084-055-001-3454}}}“In each of their realms
They made his great fame known
To their bhikṣus and bhikṣuṇīs,
Upāsakas and upāsikās:{{note:{index1171,id:UT22084-055-001-3455}}} {31}
{{milestone:{label:34.56,id:UT22084-055-001-3456}}}“ ‘This bhikṣu Kṣemadatta
Is wise and has great might.
He burned his hand in order to gain
The wisdom of buddhahood.’ {32}
{{milestone:{label:34.57,id:UT22084-055-001-3457}}}“Thousands of realms,
As numerous as the Ganges sands,
Were illuminated by that lamp, 
Which was like the fire at an eon’s end. {33}
{{milestone:{label:34.58,id:UT22084-055-001-3458}}}“All the realms became filled 
With flowers and sandalwood{{note:{index1172,id:UT22084-055-001-3459}}} powder,
Up to kneeheight
From the ground.{{note:{index1173,id:UT22084-055-001-3460}}} {34}
{{milestone:{label:34.59,id:UT22084-055-001-3461}}}“Jewels and flowers of every kind
Filled the buddha realm.
Nāgas brought down a rain of pearls
As an offering to Kṣemadatta. {35}
{{milestone:{label:34.60,id:UT22084-055-001-3462}}}“This realm became adorned
By a display of every kind of jewel. 
Jewels and pearls were spread out
As an offering to Kṣemadatta. {36}
{{milestone:{label:34.61,id:UT22084-055-001-3463}}}“Devas, nāgas, and yakṣas,
kinnaras {{note:{index1174,id:UT22084-055-001-3464}}} and mahoragas,
As numerous as the Ganges sands,
Were established in the highest enlightenment.” {37}
{{milestone:{label:34.62,id:UT22084-055-001-3465}}}The Śākya lion, the Buddha,
Was on Vulture Peak Mountain.
In front of his assembly of bhikṣus
The Jina roared this lion’s roar: {38}
{{milestone:{label:34.63,id:UT22084-055-001-3466}}}“It is I who was Kṣemadatta
And Ajita was Śrīghoṣa.
For ten thousand million eons
I practiced the bodhisattva conduct. {39}
{{milestone:{label:34.64,id:UT22084-055-001-3467}}}“Countless women, 
The moment they saw
Bhikṣu Kṣemadatta,
Ceased being women.{{note:{index1175,id:UT22084-055-001-3468}}} {40}
{{milestone:{label:34.65,id:UT22084-055-001-3469}}}“The Lord of humans prophesied
That they would not return
But that they all would become
Self-arisen guides of the world.{{note:{index1176,id:UT22084-055-001-3470}}} {41} {{page:{number:239,id:UT22084-055-001-6072,folio:F.120.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:34.66,id:UT22084-055-001-3471}}}“The wise who have heard this sūtra,
The teaching on the disciplines of mendicancy, {{note:{index1177,id:UT22084-055-001-3472}}}
Should have no cherishing for the body
And should study well this Dharma.” {42}
{{milestone:{label:34.67,id:UT22084-055-001-3473}}}Conclusion of the thirty-fourth chapter, “Kṣemadatta.”{{note:{index1178,id:UT22084-055-001-3474}}}
{{milestone:{label:35,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-35}}}Jñānāvatī 
Chapter 35
{{milestone:{label:35.1,id:UT22084-055-001-3475}}}Then the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who wish for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, should plant roots of merit and apply themselves to practicing generosity through the Dharma or generosity through material things. 
{{milestone:{label:35.2,id:UT22084-055-001-3476}}}“Those bodhisattva mahāsattvas should dedicate that generosity through four prayers of dedication. 
{{milestone:{label:35.3,id:UT22084-055-001-3477}}}“What are the four dedication prayers? The first dedication prayer is: ‘I plant{{note:{index1179,id:UT22084-055-001-3478}}} the roots of merit of this generosity so that I may attain skills in methods, those skills in methods by which the buddha bhagavāns attained the highest, complete enlightenment of buddhahood.’
{{milestone:{label:35.4,id:UT22084-055-001-3479}}}“The second dedication prayer is: ‘I plant the roots of merit of this generosity so that I may listen to those skills in methods from kalyāṇamitras, remember them, understand them, possess them, and recite them, and so that I will always be in the company of those kalyāṇamitras who will attain the highest, complete enlightenment of buddhahood.’
{{milestone:{label:35.5,id:UT22084-055-001-3480}}}“The third dedication prayer is: ‘I plant the roots of merit of this generosity so that all may obtain the requisites that sustain life in the world, and so that these requisites may come together for me.’{{note:{index1180,id:UT22084-055-001-3481}}}
{{milestone:{label:35.6,id:UT22084-055-001-3482}}}“The fourth dedication prayer is: ‘I plant the roots of merit of this generosity so that I may attain an existence in which I take care of beings, taking care of them in two ways: taking care of them through the Dharma and taking care of them through material things.’
{{milestone:{label:35.7,id:UT22084-055-001-3483}}}“Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas dedicate those roots of merit through those four prayers of dedication. {{page:{number:240,id:UT22084-055-001-6073,folio:F.121.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:35.8,id:UT22084-055-001-3484}}}“Moreover, young man, bodhisattva mahāsattvas who yearn for this samādhi, and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, whether they are homeless renunciants or householders, should sincerely{{note:{index1181,id:UT22084-055-001-3485}}} serve, provide for,{{note:{index1182,id:UT22084-055-001-3486}}} and attend upon a bodhisattva mahāsattva who has correct conduct, good qualities, and wisdom.{{note:{index1183,id:UT22084-055-001-3487}}} If that bodhisattva mahāsattva bhikṣu who possesses this samādhi were to become ill, afflicted by a powerful illness, then they should eagerly cure him of the illness with their own flesh and blood. Young man, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas who with the perfect higher motivation yearn for this samādhi and wish to attain quickly the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood should fearlessly and confidently{{note:{index1184,id:UT22084-055-001-3488}}} give even their own flesh and blood so that the dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu will be healed from his illness. 
“Young man, this is how that teaching is to be understood.
{{milestone:{label:35.9,id:UT22084-055-001-3490}}}“Young man, in a past countless eon—numerous, incalculable, countless eons ago—at that time and in those days, there was a tathāgata, an arhat, a perfectly enlightened buddha perfect in wisdom and conduct, a sugata, a knower of the world, an unsurpassable guide who tamed beings, a teacher of devas and humans, the Bhagavān Buddha Acintya­praṇidhāna­viśeṣa­samudgata­rāja who had appeared in the world. 
{{milestone:{label:35.10,id:UT22084-055-001-3491}}}“Young man, before the end of the day on which he attained the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood, he manifested incalculable, innumerable buddha emanations and guided countless beings, establishing them in the arhathood in which all outflows have ceased, {{page:{number:241,id:UT22084-055-001-6074,folio:F.121.b}}} and he established countless beings in irreversible progress toward the highest, complete enlightenment. And then, before that day had ended, he passed into nirvāṇa.
{{milestone:{label:35.11,id:UT22084-055-001-3492}}}“The Dharma of that Bhagavān who had passed into nirvāṇa remained for a hundred thousand quintillion years.
{{milestone:{label:35.12,id:UT22084-055-001-3493}}}“Young man, in the last five hundred years before the Dharma of Bhagavān Acintya­praṇidhāna­viśeṣa­samudgata­rāja finally came to an end, there were many bhikṣus who held the view of objective existence. They had no yearning, no aspiration for a sūtra like this and opposed it and attacked it. They harmed and even killed the bhikṣus who possessed this sūtra. They had attachment to gain and honor and therefore they killed thousands of bhikṣus who possessed a sūtra like this.
{{milestone:{label:35.13,id:UT22084-055-001-3494}}}“Young man, at that time and in those days, King Jñānabala ruled over Jambudvīpa. He possessed the Dharma and had appeared because of his perfect prayers in previous lifetimes. 
{{milestone:{label:35.14,id:UT22084-055-001-3495}}}“Young man, at that time and in those days, in this Jambudvīpa there was a bhikṣu named Bhūtamati who possessed this sūtra. That dharmabhāṇaka went to the king’s palace and became a kalyāṇamitra who was altruistic, was compassionate, and wished to benefit others. The king never tired of gazing upon him and always longed to see him. He came to him for teaching and for discussions on the Dharma. He honored him, asked him questions, obtained answers, and was able to understand what was spoken. 
{{milestone:{label:35.15,id:UT22084-055-001-3496}}}“That dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu was wise in the behavior,{{note:{index1185,id:UT22084-055-001-3497}}} conduct, aspirations, natures, and propensities of beings. He knew the extent of the powers, strengths, and diligence of beings. He was wise in natures and propensities.{{note:{index1186,id:UT22084-055-001-3498}}} He was wise in implying the truth. He was also wise in giving answers without implied meaning. He had profound eloquence and was wise in the ways of guiding all beings. He spoke sincerely.{{note:{index1187,id:UT22084-055-001-3499}}} His face was free of frowns. {{page:{number:242,id:UT22084-055-001-6075,folio:F.122.a}}} He remained in a state of greatness of mind. He was dedicated to great compassion. He could not be defeated by any opponent. 
{{milestone:{label:35.16,id:UT22084-055-001-3500}}}“Young man, at that time and in those days, King Jñānabala’s daughter was sixteen years old and she was beautiful, attractive, and charming. She had a lovely complexion, and was magnificent. Her name was Jñānāvatī. The bhikṣu Bhūtamati was her ācārya. He taught her the virtuous qualities, extolled them, delighted in them, and made her develop them.
{{milestone:{label:35.17,id:UT22084-055-001-3501}}}“Young man, at that time and in those days, the dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu developed widespread, black erysipelas on both his thighs, which did not respond to treatment and had no known cure, so that the physicians gave up trying to heal him. King Jñānabala with his harem, sons, daughters, and attendants, on learning that the bhikṣu was ill, wept and shed tears. 
{{milestone:{label:35.18,id:UT22084-055-001-3502}}}“Eighty thousand women, the inhabitants of the cities and towns, the people of the kingdom, the people of the market towns and the regions, the astrologers, ministers, and prime ministers, and the doorkeepers and attendants, hearing that the bhikṣu was ill, wept and shed tears and cried, ‘May this bhikṣu not die!’
{{milestone:{label:35.19,id:UT22084-055-001-3503}}}“Young man, at that time and in those days, the goddess of King Jñānabala’s family since ancient times, who was always by his side, instructed the king in a dream, saying, ‘Great king, if fresh, unspoiled human blood{{note:{index1188,id:UT22084-055-001-3504}}} is applied to this bhikṣu’s erysipelas, and if fresh, untarnished human flesh is prepared with various flavors and given to him to eat, then this bhikṣu will be cured of his illness.’
{{milestone:{label:35.20,id:UT22084-055-001-3505}}}When that night had passed and King Jñānabala awoke from his sleep he entered his harem and he described the dream to his harem, saying, ‘This is the kind of dream that I have had.’ {{page:{number:243,id:UT22084-055-001-6076,folio:F.122.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:35.21,id:UT22084-055-001-3506}}}“Young man, none of the women in the harem, the king’s wives, had the fortitude to provide that remedy for the bhikṣu. 
{{milestone:{label:35.22,id:UT22084-055-001-3507}}}“Princess Jñānāvatī also dreamed that kind of dream. When she awoke, she went into the harem and described the dream to her circle of mothers, but none of the women had the fortitude to provide that remedy for the bhikṣu. 
{{milestone:{label:35.23,id:UT22084-055-001-3508}}}“Then Princess Jñānāvatī became happy, delighted, thrilled, joyful, pleased, and glad, and made this resolution: ‘In that case I shall cut from myself the remedy, and as instructed will give him the fresh blood and fresh flesh. I am the youngest and least within the royal household, and my body, speech, and mind are untarnished. I seek untarnished wisdom, and therefore I shall offer my flesh and blood to the untarnished dharmabhāṇaka, so that I may heal this bhikṣu of his illness!’
{{milestone:{label:35.24,id:UT22084-055-001-3509}}}“Then Princess Jñānāvatī returned to her own dwelling and, taking up a sharp knife and with her mind focused on the Dharma, she cut flesh from her own thigh. She prepared it, adding various excellent flavors. Bringing the blood, too, she went to her ācārya{{note:{index1189,id:UT22084-055-001-3510}}} and, seated before King Jñānabala, she applied the blood onto the black erysipelas and nourished the bhikṣu with the well-prepared meal.
{{milestone:{label:35.25,id:UT22084-055-001-3511}}}“Then the bhikṣu, not knowing, unaware, and unsuspecting, ate that food. As soon as he had eaten it, the bhikṣu’s illness completely vanished and he was entirely cured of his illness. Freed from pain and happy, he taught the Dharma so that twelve hundred beings from among the harem and the assembled people from the land, towns, and countryside developed the aspiration to highest, complete enlightenment. 
“King Jñānabala then recited these verses to his daughter: {{page:{number:244,id:UT22084-055-001-6077,folio:F.123.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:35.26,id:UT22084-055-001-3513}}}“ ‘Daughter, from where did you obtain this blood?
And from where did you obtain this human flesh?
Daughter, by your preparing this food
The dharmabhāṇaka has become healthy. {1}
{{milestone:{label:35.27,id:UT22084-055-001-3514}}}“ ‘Was it from someone slain or who had died that you obtained
This flesh prepared with various flavors? 
Daughter, where did you obtain this blood
That has freed him from this evil sickness?’ {2}
{{milestone:{label:35.28,id:UT22084-055-001-3515}}}“The daughter listened to her father’s words
And Jñānāvatī then addressed him.
With no despondency, she spoke these words:
‘Listen, father, to what I have to say. {3}
{{milestone:{label:35.29,id:UT22084-055-001-3516}}}“ ‘I too, father, had the dream
That was sent by the goddess.
Lord of the World, listen to me,
And understand its true meaning. {4}
{{milestone:{label:35.30,id:UT22084-055-001-3517}}}“ ‘That goddess said to me
That whoever gives to the bhikṣu
The flesh and blood of a human
Will cure him of his evil illness. {5}
{{milestone:{label:35.31,id:UT22084-055-001-3518}}}“ ‘I arose from my bed
And I entered the harem.
I then related my dream
To my superiors, my mothers. {6}
{{milestone:{label:35.32,id:UT22084-055-001-3519}}}“ ‘I asked the servants who among them
Would be able to do this,
To make perfectly delicious
Human blood and flesh? {7}
{{milestone:{label:35.33,id:UT22084-055-001-3520}}}“ ‘If that food is given to him
And if the blood is applied,
The bhikṣu will be freed
From this black erysipelas. {8}
{{milestone:{label:35.34,id:UT22084-055-001-3521}}}“ ‘If we do not use this method,
If we do not apply this remedy,
This bhikṣu will soon die
Because of this illness that he has. {9}
{{milestone:{label:35.35,id:UT22084-055-001-3522}}}“ ‘What being in the three existences
Would not give their flesh and blood?{{note:{index1190,id:UT22084-055-001-3523}}}
What wise ones on seeing this
Would hold fast to their body? {10}
{{milestone:{label:35.36,id:UT22084-055-001-3524}}}“ ‘Though I told the harem of this,
Not even one woman said she would give.
The bhikṣu is beloved and he is beloved by me,
So I gave him my flesh and blood for the sake of enlightenment. {11}
{{milestone:{label:35.37,id:UT22084-055-001-3525}}}“ ‘Those who seek enlightenment, peace, and freedom from misery
Have no devotion to their body or dependence on it;
Of themselves they cherish not even an atom,
And are not saddened to give themselves away. {12}
{{milestone:{label:35.38,id:UT22084-055-001-3526}}}“ ‘When the harem heard those words, {{page:{number:245,id:UT22084-055-001-6078,folio:F.123.b}}}
They were all perplexed.
None of them had the fortitude
To take on such an act. {13}
{{milestone:{label:35.39,id:UT22084-055-001-3527}}}“ ‘Then I developed the intention
That I would provide the food for the bhikṣu,
Cutting off pieces of my own flesh
And using for lotion my own blood. {14}
{{milestone:{label:35.40,id:UT22084-055-001-3528}}}“ ‘I cut into my own thighs
And obtained the flesh and blood.
I myself cooked the pieces of flesh
And added various flavorings. {15}
{{milestone:{label:35.41,id:UT22084-055-001-3529}}}“ ‘In the presence of my father
I gave to the sick bhikṣu
The meal of human flesh
And the lotion of blood. {16}
{{milestone:{label:35.42,id:UT22084-055-001-3530}}}“ ‘Lord of men, listen to my words!
Sovereign, there not being any human flesh,
I cut the flesh from my own thighs,
And having cooked it gave it to the dharmabhāṇaka. {17}
{{milestone:{label:35.43,id:UT22084-055-001-3531}}}“ ‘It was for the sake of the highest enlightenment
That I accomplished this great purpose with my body.
The bhikṣu is cured and returned to health
And I have created immeasurable merit.’ {18}
{{milestone:{label:35.44,id:UT22084-055-001-3532}}}“The king inquired of his daughter,
‘How did you cut the flesh from your body?
Daughter, when you engaged in creating this remedy,
Did you not suffer from physical pain?’ {19}
{{milestone:{label:35.45,id:UT22084-055-001-3533}}}“The wise and fearless princess replied to him,
‘King, lord of the earth, listen!
Having listened, understand correctly
The inconceivable ripening of karma. {20}
{{milestone:{label:35.46,id:UT22084-055-001-3534}}}“ ‘Father, through having done bad actions,
Beings fall into dreadful hell.
They lose their flesh, and again have flesh. 
See the inconceivable result of actions! {21}
{{milestone:{label:35.47,id:UT22084-055-001-3535}}}“ ‘Through bad karma they have no flesh or blood,
And in an instant they again have flesh and blood.
Therefore, needless to say that, because of good karma,
Through aspiration flesh and blood will be created. {22}
{{milestone:{label:35.48,id:UT22084-055-001-3536}}}“ ‘I had no pain when I cut my flesh. 
When the blood flowed I did not become dizzy.
Even if I were to cut off all of my flesh,
The body of the Dharma would have no wound or cut. {23}
{{milestone:{label:35.49,id:UT22084-055-001-3537}}}“ ‘Feeling perfect joy in the Dharma,
I cut the flesh to be given from my thighs.
I had no suffering because of the wounds, {{page:{number:246,id:UT22084-055-001-6079,folio:F.124.a}}}
And my body became as it was before. {24}
{{milestone:{label:35.50,id:UT22084-055-001-3538}}}“ ‘Father, just like a fig-tree flower is only seen
A few times in many millions of eons,
This dharmabhāṇaka is just like that, 
Seen rarely in this Jambudvīpa. {25}
{{milestone:{label:35.51,id:UT22084-055-001-3539}}}“ ‘Just as humans never tire of gazing
Upon shining Jambu River gold,
Devas and humans never tire of gazing
In that way upon this dharmabhāṇaka. {26}
{{milestone:{label:35.52,id:UT22084-055-001-3540}}}“ ‘Just as a thirsty man is freed from thirst
When he drinks clear water,
In the same way wise dharmabhāṇakas 
Free beings of thirst with the nectar of Dharma. {27}
{{milestone:{label:35.53,id:UT22084-055-001-3541}}}“ ‘This my flesh and blood that I bestowed 
Upon the bhikṣu who was afflicted by illness 
Eliminated the dharmabhāṇaka’s erysipelas,
And I thus respectfully rendered homage to the Buddha. {28}
{{milestone:{label:35.54,id:UT22084-055-001-3542}}}“ ‘I gave of my own flesh
To the learned one with correct conduct,
Who is a holder of this supreme samādhi.
May I obtain from him this Dharma! {29}
{{milestone:{label:35.55,id:UT22084-055-001-3543}}}“ ‘Just as the fragrant aroma of the incense 
Of yellow sandalwood and red sandalwood{{note:{index1191,id:UT22084-055-001-3544}}}
Spreads throughout the ten directions,
So, too, does the aroma of the dharmabhāṇaka. {30}
{{milestone:{label:35.56,id:UT22084-055-001-3545}}}“ ‘Just as Meru is seen from every direction,
And seeing its beauty brings joy
And it illuminates, shining in all directions,
In that way the dharmabhāṇaka is like Meru. {31}
{{milestone:{label:35.57,id:UT22084-055-001-3546}}}“ ‘Just as when a wise man rebuilds
A stūpa that has fallen into ruin, 
His having faith in that stūpa
Is the cause for it to be rebuilt, {32}
{{milestone:{label:35.58,id:UT22084-055-001-3547}}}“ ‘Likewise, this stūpa of the Dharma was ill
And I cured it by applying blood.
With veneration for the Dharma, with my own flesh
I have lit the lamp for Jambudvīpa. {33}
{{milestone:{label:35.59,id:UT22084-055-001-3548}}}“ ‘If this bhikṣu had passed away,
The words of this samādhi would have been 
Forever silenced for the beings in this world.
By healing him, this samādhi will be obtained. {34}
{{milestone:{label:35.60,id:UT22084-055-001-3549}}}“ ‘This bhikṣu is a protector of the whole world,
And gives sight to the blind world.
With the king of medicines he even heals
Desire, anger, and ignorance. {35} {{page:{number:247,id:UT22084-055-001-6080,folio:F.124.b}}}
{{milestone:{label:35.61,id:UT22084-055-001-3550}}}“ ‘He always has a mind that is vast,
The extent of his conduct is immeasurable,
He is learned in words and their definite meaning,
And he cannot be defeated by opponents. {36}
{{milestone:{label:35.62,id:UT22084-055-001-3551}}}“ ‘I have no fear that I will fall into lower realms,
And I will not again become a woman
Throughout thousands of millions of eons,
As I have performed a supreme service for the dharmabhāṇaka.’ ” {37}
{{milestone:{label:35.63,id:UT22084-055-001-3552}}}At this point, the Bhagavān said to the youth Candraprabha, “Therefore, young man, when the princess had heard this Dharma of the bodhisattva, which is marvelous, wonderful, and very difficult to practice, in order to serve the sick dharmabhāṇaka for whom there was no medicine, she used her own flesh and blood to heal him. Even the gift of just one finger will be a service to the stūpa of the Dharma for beings.” 
{{milestone:{label:35.64,id:UT22084-055-001-3553}}}Thereupon the Bhagavān gave a detailed teaching on that account of the past by chanting the following extensive verses to the youth Candraprabha:{{note:{index1192,id:UT22084-055-001-3554}}}
{{milestone:{label:35.65,id:UT22084-055-001-3555}}}“The one who makes an offering of a single toe
Gains excellent merit that is millions of times greater
Than that from offering to the guides 
Jewels filling buddha realms as numerous as the Ganges sands. {38}
{{milestone:{label:35.66,id:UT22084-055-001-3556}}}“After that girl had passed away
She saw ten thousand million buddhas.
She entered homelessness in all their teachings
And obtained the supreme peace of this samādhi. {39}
{{milestone:{label:35.67,id:UT22084-055-001-3557}}}“When all those supreme humans
Had passed into nirvāṇa
As bodhisattvas,{{note:{index1193,id:UT22084-055-001-3558}}} unafflicted,
She always maintained homelessness. {40}
{{milestone:{label:35.68,id:UT22084-055-001-3559}}}“She practiced celibacy within the teachings
Of the tathāgata Dīpaprabha.{{note:{index1194,id:UT22084-055-001-3560}}}
Never again reverting to being a woman,
She became a dharmabhāṇaka bhikṣu. {41}
{{milestone:{label:35.69,id:UT22084-055-001-3561}}}“Maitreya was Jñānabala, the ruler of men, 
Who always maintained the supreme Dharma.
Dīpaṃkara was that dharmabhāṇaka,
And I was then that princess. {42}
{{milestone:{label:35.70,id:UT22084-055-001-3562}}}“Akṣobhya, when he was practicing bodhisattva conduct,
Was at that time the ancient goddess of the family,
Who was the attendant of sovereign Jñānabala
And revealed the dream to the king.{{note:{index1195,id:UT22084-055-001-3563}}} {i} {{page:{number:248,id:UT22084-055-001-6081,folio:F.125.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:35.71,id:UT22084-055-001-3564}}}“Because of my longing for this samādhi,
Avoiding all wickedness
I served that dharmabhāṇaka
With my flesh and my blood. {43}
{{milestone:{label:35.72,id:UT22084-055-001-3565}}}“Those who wept when they saw the bhikṣu
Afflicted by the agony of his illness
Became irreversible in their progress in all their lifetimes
And were never reborn into the lower existences. {44}
{{milestone:{label:35.73,id:UT22084-055-001-3566}}}“They never had illness of the eyes,
No illness of the head, no illness of the ears,
No illness of the nose, no illness of the tongue,
And never any illness of the teeth. {45}
{{milestone:{label:35.74,id:UT22084-055-001-3567}}}“Those who attended the sick monk 
Became always very attractive,
Their bodies shining with splendor and majesty,
Adorned by the vivid thirty-two signs of hundreds of merits. {46}
{{milestone:{label:35.75,id:UT22084-055-001-3568}}}“They have entered homelessness in my teaching
And in future times when the supreme enlightenment is vanishing
They will obtain the treasure of the tathāgatas, 
And see ten thousand million buddhas. {47}
{{milestone:{label:35.76,id:UT22084-055-001-3569}}}“Having obtained this supreme enlightenment,
They will always keep it and venerate it.
And having accomplished great benefit for beings,
They will see the supreme human, Akṣobhya. {48}
{{milestone:{label:35.77,id:UT22084-055-001-3570}}}“When they have heard this unsurpassable conduct
They will attain the superior, unworldly joy.
When they hear of my past conduct
They will make vast offerings to the buddhas. {49}
{{milestone:{label:35.78,id:UT22084-055-001-3571}}}“When wise bhikṣus with correct conduct are seen
They should always be served with sincerity.
Forsaking harshness and anger,{{note:{index1196,id:UT22084-055-001-3572}}}
Always serve the bhikṣu dharmabhāṇakas. {50}
{{milestone:{label:35.79,id:UT22084-055-001-3573}}}“Forsaking aggression and wrath,
Make offerings to my sons, the protectors of the Dharma.
Do not be blind for many millions of eons 
And fall into the lower existences and experience suffering. {51}
{{milestone:{label:35.80,id:UT22084-055-001-3574}}}“Those who are malicious toward each other 
Will not be protected by correct conduct, or by learning. 
They will not be protected by dhyāna or by solitude,
Nor by generosity or offering to buddhas.” {52}
{{milestone:{label:35.81,id:UT22084-055-001-3575}}}Conclusion of the thirty-fifth chapter, “Jñānāvatī.”
{{milestone:{label:36,id:UT22084-055-001-chapter-36}}}Supuṣpacandra
Chapter 36
{{milestone:{label:36.1,id:UT22084-055-001-3576}}}Then at that time Brother Ānanda rose from his seat, {{page:{number:249,id:UT22084-055-001-6082,folio:F.125.b}}} removed his robe from one shoulder, and, kneeling on his right knee, with palms placed together he bowed toward the Bhagavān and made this request: “If the Bhagavān will give me an opportunity to seek answers to them, I have a few questions for the Bhagavān, the tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha.” 
{{milestone:{label:36.2,id:UT22084-055-001-3577}}}The Bhagavān addressed Brother Ānanda, saying, “That is why, Ānanda, I am seated upon this seat. Ask whatever question you wish to the Tathāgata, the arhat, the perfectly enlightened Buddha, and I shall gratify you with answers to each and every question you have asked.”
{{milestone:{label:36.3,id:UT22084-055-001-3578}}}Brother Ānanda then said to the Bhagavān: “Bhagavān, I have been given the opportunity. Sugata, I have been given the opportunity to receive answers to my questions.”
{{milestone:{label:36.4,id:UT22084-055-001-3579}}}So Brother Ānanda, having received the Bhagavān’s permission, sat upon a seat before the Bhagavān and asked him, “Bhagavān, what is the cause and what are the factors whereby when bodhisattva mahāsattvas are practicing infinite bodhisattva conduct, they do not regress from enlightenment even if their hands are cut off, their feet are cut off, their ears are cut off, their noses are cut off, their eyes are gouged out, their heads are cut off, their bodies are cut up, and their limbs are cut off, or they experience various other kinds of suffering? What is the cause and what are the factors for that?”
The Bhagavān replied to Brother Ānanda, “Ānanda, in order to truly accomplish the highest, complete enlightenment, I experienced every kind of suffering. You know and remember this, so what made you decide to ask the Tathāgata this question? {{page:{number:250,id:UT22084-055-001-6083,folio:F.126.a}}}
{{milestone:{label:36.5,id:UT22084-055-001-3581}}}“Ānanda, as an analogy, if there were a person who was on fire from his feet to the crown of his head, burning so that he was a single flame, and someone else were to come up to him and say, ‘Oh, you sir, while you are still burning, should encounter, be provided with, delight in, enjoy, and indulge in the five sensory pleasures!’ what would he think? Would that person, while he was still burning, encounter, be provided with, delight in, enjoy, and indulge in the five sensory pleasures?”
“No, Bhagavān, he would not,” replied Ānanda.
{{milestone:{label:36.6,id:UT22084-055-001-3583}}}The Bhagavān continued, “Ānanda, consider whether that person, while still burning, could encounter, be provided with, delight in, enjoy, and indulge in the five sensory pleasures. The tathāgata, while practicing bodhisattva conduct in the past, was not happy or joyful on seeing beings suffering and in poverty in the three lower existences.
{{milestone:{label:36.7,id:UT22084-055-001-3584}}}“Ānanda, when bodhisattva mahāsattvas of the past were practicing bodhisattva conduct, they had perfect correct conduct, faultless correct conduct, pure correct conduct, unalloyed correct conduct, immaculate correct conduct, unwavering correct conduct, unshakable correct conduct, imperturbable correct conduct, resolute correct conduct, sincere correct conduct, trustworthy correct conduct, honest correct conduct, correct conduct that was faithful to the vows they had taken, and correct conduct that benefits beings. That is the kind of correct conduct they had.
{{milestone:{label:36.8,id:UT22084-055-001-3585}}}“Ānanda, the bodhisattva mahāsattvas of the past who were practicing infinite bodhisattva conduct did not regress if their hands were cut off, did not regress if their feet were cut off, {{page:{number:251,id:UT22084-055-001-6084,folio:F.126.b}}} did not regress if their ears were cut off, did not regress if their noses were cut off, did not regress if their eyes were gouged out or their heads were cut off, and did not regress if their body or limbs were severed. Even if they experienced various kinds of suffering, they quickly attained the highest, complete enlightenment of perfect buddhahood. 
{{milestone:{label:36.9,id:UT22084-055-001-3586}}}“Ānanda, you should understand this through the following teaching:
